To investigate the&nbsp;<a title="Blood libel" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Blood_libel">blood libel</a>, Emperor Frederick II held a special conference of Jewish converts to Christianity at which the converts were questioned about Jewish ritual practice. Letters inviting prominent individuals to the conference still survive. At the conference, the converts stated unequivocally that Jews do not harm Christian children or require blood for any rituals. In 1236 the Emperor published these findings and in 1247&nbsp;<a title="Pope Innocent IV" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pope_Innocent_IV">Pope Innocent IV</a>, the Emperor's enemy, also denounced accusations of the&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Ritual murder" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ritual_murder">ritual murder</a>&nbsp;of Christian children by Jews. In 1272, the papal repudiation of the&nbsp;<a title="Blood libel" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Blood_libel">blood libel</a>&nbsp;was repeated by&nbsp;<a title="Pope Gregory X" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pope_Gregory_X">Pope Gregory X</a>, who also ruled that thereafter any such testimony of a Christian against a Jew could not be accepted unless it is confirmed by another Jew. Unfortunately, these proclamations from the highest sources were not effective in altering the beliefs of the Christian majority and the libels continued.</dd>
</dl>
<dl>
<dt>1236</dt>
<dd><a class="mw-redirect" title="Crusade" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Crusade">Crusaders</a>&nbsp;attack Jewish communities of&nbsp;<a title="Anjou" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Anjou">Anjou</a>&nbsp;and&nbsp;<a title="Poitou" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Poitou">Poitou</a>&nbsp;and attempt to baptize all the Jews. Those who resisted (est. 3,000) were slaughtered.</dd>
</dl>
<dl>
<dt>1236</dt>
<dd>A Jew and a Christian fisherman get into a heated argument about prices, which turns physical. It ends when the Jew deals a devastating blow to the Gentile's head which leads to his death. This enrages the local Christian population, who attack the Jewish quarter of Narbonne. Don Aymeric, the governor of Narbonne prevents a massacre and restores all stolen Jewish property to their rightful owner.<sup id="cite_ref-70" class="reference"></sup></dd>
</dl>
<dl>
<dt>1240</dt>
<dd>Duke Jean le Roux expels Jews from&nbsp;<a title="Brittany" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Brittany">Brittany</a>.</dd>
</dl>
<dl>
<dt>1240</dt>
<dd><a title="Disputation of Paris" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Disputation_of_Paris">Disputation of Paris</a>.&nbsp;<a title="Pope Gregory IX" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pope_Gregory_IX">Pope Gregory IX</a>&nbsp;puts&nbsp;<a title="Talmud" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Talmud">Talmud</a>&nbsp;on trial on the charges that it contains&nbsp;<a title="Blasphemy" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Blasphemy">blasphemy</a>&nbsp;against&nbsp;<a title="Jesus" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jesus">Jesus</a>&nbsp;and&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Blessed Virgin Mary" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Blessed_Virgin_Mary">Mary</a>&nbsp;and attacks on the Church.</dd>
</dl>
<dl>
<dt>1241</dt>
<dd>A pogrom against the Jews of Frankfurt takes place after conflicts over Jewish-Christian marriages and the enforced baptism of interfaith couples. 180 Jews are killed as a result and 24 agree to be baptized. This became known as the&nbsp;<em>Judenschlacht</em>&nbsp;(German for&nbsp;<em>Slaughter of the Jews</em>).</dd>
</dl>
<dl>
<dt>1241</dt>
<dd>In England, first of a series of royal levies against Jewish finances, which forced the Jews to sell their debts to non-Jews at cut prices.</dd>
</dl>
<dl>
<dt>1242</dt>
<dd>24 cart-loads of hand-written Talmudic manuscripts burned in the streets of Paris.</dd>
</dl>
<dl>
<dt>1242</dt>
<dd><a title="James I of Aragon" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/James_I_of_Aragon">James I of Aragon</a>&nbsp;orders Jews to listen to conversion sermons and to attend churches. Friars are given power to enter synagogues uninvited.</dd>
</dl>
<dl>
<dt>1243</dt>
<dd>The first ever accusation of&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Host Desecration" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Host_Desecration">Host Desecration</a>. The entire Jewish population of&nbsp;<a title="Beelitz" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Beelitz">Beelitz</a>&nbsp;was burned at the stake after being accused of torturing Jesus and the spot it happened was named "Judenberg."</dd>
</dl>
<dl>
<dt>1243</dt>
<dd>11 Jews are tortured to death following a blood libel in&nbsp;<a title="Kitzingen" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kitzingen">Kitzingen</a>&nbsp;Germany.</dd>
</dl>
<dl>
<dt>1244</dt>
<dd><a title="Pope Innocent IV" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pope_Innocent_IV">Pope Innocent IV</a>&nbsp;orders&nbsp;<a title="Louis IX of France" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Louis_IX_of_France">Louis IX of France</a>&nbsp;to burn all Talmud copies.</dd>
</dl>
<dl>
<dt>1249</dt>
<dd><a class="mw-redirect" title="Alphonse of Poitiers" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Alphonse_of_Poitiers">Alphonse of Poitiers</a>&nbsp;orders the expulsion of all Jews in&nbsp;<a title="Poitou" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Poitou">Poitou</a>.</dd>
</dl>
<dl>
<dt>1250</dt>
<dd><a class="mw-redirect" title="Saragossa" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Saragossa">Saragossa</a>&nbsp;Spain: death of a choirboy&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Saint Dominguito del Val" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Saint_Dominguito_del_Val">Saint Dominguito del Val</a>&nbsp;prompts&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Ritual murder" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ritual_murder">ritual murder</a>&nbsp;accusation. His sainthood was revoked in the 20th century but reportedly a chapel dedicated to him still exists in the&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Seo de San Salvador" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Seo_de_San_Salvador">Cathedral of Saragossa</a>.</dd>
</dl>
<dl>
<dt>1253</dt>
<dd><a title="Henry III of England" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Henry_III_of_England">Henry III of England</a>&nbsp;introduces harsh anti-Jewish laws.</dd>
</dl>
<dl>
<dt>1254</dt>
<dd>Louis IX expels the Jews from France, their property and synagogues confiscated. Most move to Germany and further east, however, after a couple of years, some were readmitted back.</dd>
</dl>
<dl>
<dt>1255</dt>
<dd>Henry III of England sells his rights to the Jews (regarded as royal "chattels") to his brother Richard for 5,000 marks.</dd>
</dl>
<dl>
<dt>1257</dt>
<dd>The&nbsp;<a title="Badge of shame" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Badge_of_shame">Badge of shame</a>&nbsp;is imposed locally on the&nbsp;<a title="Italian Jews" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Italian_Jews">Italian Jews</a>.</dd>
</dl>
<dl>
<dt>1260</dt>
<dd>Mongols are defeated and Syria is brought under Mamluk rule. Anti-Jewish laws are once again decreed, and Jewish life becomes a lot more restricted in the Levant.</dd>
</dl>
<dl>
<dt>1260</dt>
<dd>Jews are banned from ascending above the 7th step on the&nbsp;<a title="Cave of the Patriarchs" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cave_of_the_Patriarchs">Cave of the Patriarchs</a>. This ban would last 700 years.</dd>
</dl>
<dl>
<dt>1260</dt>
<dd><a title="Thomas Aquinas" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Thomas_Aquinas">Thomas Aquinas</a>&nbsp;publishes&nbsp;<em><a title="Summa contra Gentiles" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Summa_contra_Gentiles">Summa Contra Gentiles</a></em>, a summary of Christian faith to be presented to those who reject it. The Jews who refuse to convert are regarded as "deliberately defiant" rather than "<a class="mw-redirect" title="Invincibly ignorant" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Invincibly_ignorant">invincibly ignorant</a>".</dd>
</dl>
<dl>
<dt>1263</dt>
<dd><a title="Disputation" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Disputation">Disputation</a>&nbsp;of&nbsp;<a title="Barcelona" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Barcelona">Barcelona</a>.</dd>
</dl>
<dl>
<dt>1264</dt>
<dd><a title="Pope Clement IV" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pope_Clement_IV">Pope Clement IV</a>&nbsp;assigns Talmud censorship committee.</dd>
</dl>
<dl>
<dt>1264</dt>
<dd><a title="Simon de Montfort, 6th Earl of Leicester" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Simon_de_Montfort,_6th_Earl_of_Leicester">Simon de Montfort</a>&nbsp;inspires massacre of Jews in London.</dd>
</dl>
<dl>
<dt>1265</dt>
<dd>German-Jewish convert&nbsp;<a title="Abraham of Augsburg" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Abraham_of_Augsburg">Abraham of Augsburg</a>&nbsp;publicly assails Christianity, severs the heads of crucifix figurines and is sentenced to&nbsp;<a title="Torture" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Torture">torture</a>&nbsp;and&nbsp;<a title="Death by burning" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Death_by_burning">death by burning</a>.</dd>
</dl>
<dl>
<dt>1267</dt>
<dd>In a special session, the&nbsp;<a title="Vienna" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vienna">Vienna</a>&nbsp;city council forces Jews to wear&nbsp;<em><a class="mw-redirect" title="Judenhut" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Judenhut">Pileum cornutum</a></em>&nbsp;(a cone-shaped headdress, prevalent in many medieval illustrations of Jews). This distinctive dress is an addition to&nbsp;<a title="Yellow badge" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Yellow_badge">Yellow badge</a>&nbsp;Jews were already forced to wear. Christians are not permitted to attend Jewish ceremonies.</dd>
</dl>
<dl>
<dt>1267</dt>
<dd>Synod of&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Breslau" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Breslau">Breslau</a>&nbsp;orders Jews to live in a segregated quarter.</dd>
</dl>
<dl>
<dt>1267</dt>
<dd>After an accusation from an old woman that the Jews had bought a Christian child from her to kill, the entire Jewish community of&nbsp;<a title="Pforzheim" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pforzheim">Pforzheim</a>&nbsp;face massacres and expulsion. Rabbi Samuel ben Yaḳar ha-Levi, Rabbi Isaac ben Eliezer and Rabbi Abraham ben Gershom commit suicide to escape the cruel torture they feared.</dd>
</dl>
<dl>
<dt>1275</dt>
<dd>King&nbsp;<a title="Edward I of England" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Edward_I_of_England">Edward I of England</a>&nbsp;passes the&nbsp;<a title="Statute of the Jewry" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Statute_of_the_Jewry">Statute of the Jewry</a>&nbsp;forcing Jews over the age of seven to wear an identifying&nbsp;<a title="Yellow badge" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Yellow_badge">yellow badge</a>, and making usury illegal, in order to seize their assets. Scores of English Jews are arrested, 300 hanged and their property goes to the Crown. In 1280 he orders Jews to be present as&nbsp;<a title="Dominican Order" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dominican_Order">Dominicans</a>&nbsp;preach conversion. In 1287 he arrests heads of Jewish families and demands their communities pay ransom of 12,000 pounds.</dd>
</dl>
<dl>
<dt>1276</dt>
<dd>Massacre in&nbsp;<a title="Fez" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fez">Fez</a>&nbsp;to kill all Jews stopped by intervention of the Emir</dd>
</dl>
<dl>
<dt>1278</dt>
<dd>The Edict of&nbsp;<a title="Pope Nicholas III" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pope_Nicholas_III">Pope Nicholas III</a>&nbsp;requires compulsory attendance of Jews at conversion sermons.</dd>
</dl>
<dl>
<dt>1279</dt>
<dd>Synod of Ofen: Christians are forbidden to sell or rent&nbsp;<a title="Real estate" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Real_estate">real estate</a>&nbsp;to or from Jews.</dd>
</dl>
<dl>
<dt>1282</dt>
<dd>John Pectin,&nbsp;<a title="Archbishop of Canterbury" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Archbishop_of_Canterbury">Archbishop of Canterbury</a>, orders all London synagogues to close and prohibits Jewish physicians from practicing on Christians.</dd>
</dl>
<dl>
<dt>1283</dt>
<dd><a title="Philip III of France" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Philip_III_of_France">Philip III of France</a>&nbsp;causes mass migration of Jews by forbidding them to live in the small rural localities.</dd>
</dl>
<dl>
<dt>1283</dt>
<dd>10 Jews are slain in&nbsp;<a title="Mainz" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mainz">Mainz</a>&nbsp;after claims of blood libel.</dd>
</dl>
<dl>
<dt>1285</dt>
<dd><a title="Blood libel" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Blood_libel">Blood libel</a>&nbsp;in&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Munich, Germany" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Munich,_Germany">Munich, Germany</a>&nbsp;results in the death of 68 Jews. 180 more Jews are burned alive at the synagogue.</dd>
</dl>
<dl>
<dt>1287</dt>
<dd>A 16-year-old boy is found dead in the Rhine. Immediately the Jews of&nbsp;<a title="Oberwesel" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Oberwesel">Oberwesel</a>&nbsp;are accused of killing the boy. Over 40 men, women and children were killed by rioters as a response.</dd>
</dl>
<dl>
<dt>1287</dt>
<dd>Jews are arrested and accused of coin clippage. Even without evidence, the whole community is convicted and expelled.</dd>
</dl>
<dl>
<dt>1288</dt>
<dd>The Jewish population of&nbsp;<a title="Troyes" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Troyes">Troyes</a>&nbsp;is accused of ritual murder. 13 Jewish martyrs are burned at the stake, sacrificing themselves to spare the rest of the community.</dd>
</dl>
<dl>
<dt>1288</dt>
<dd>104 Jews in&nbsp;<a title="Bonn" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bonn">Bonn</a>,&nbsp;<a title="Germany" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Germany">Germany</a>&nbsp;are killed during a pogrom.</dd>
</dl>
<dl>
<dt>1289</dt>
<dd>Jews are expelled from&nbsp;<a title="Gascony" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gascony">Gascony</a>&nbsp;and&nbsp;<a title="Anjou" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Anjou">Anjou</a>.</dd>
</dl>
<dl>
<dt>1290</dt>
<dd><a title="Edict of Expulsion" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Edict_of_Expulsion">Edict of Expulsion</a>:&nbsp;<a title="Edward I of England" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Edward_I_of_England">Edward I</a>&nbsp;expels all Jews from&nbsp;<a title="England" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/England">England</a>, allowing them to take only what they could carry, all the other property became the&nbsp;<a title="The Crown" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/The_Crown">Crown</a>'s. Official reason: continued practice of&nbsp;<a title="Usury" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Usury">usury</a>.</dd>
</dl>
<dl>
<dt>1290</dt>
<dd>A Jewish man named Jonathan and his wife are accused of&nbsp;<a title="Host desecration" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Host_desecration">stabbing the wafer to torture Jesus</a>. They are both burned at the stake, their house is destroyed and replaced with a chapel.</dd>
</dl>
<dl>
<dt>1290</dt>
<dd>The Jews of&nbsp;<a title="Baghdad" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Baghdad">Baghdad</a>&nbsp;are massacred.</dd>
</dl>
<dl>
<dt>1290</dt>
<dd>18 July&nbsp;<a title="Edward I of England" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Edward_I_of_England">Edward I of England</a>&nbsp;issues&nbsp;<a title="Edict of Expulsion" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Edict_of_Expulsion">Edict of Expulsion</a>, decreeing all Jews to be expelled from England.</dd>
</dl>
<dl>
<dt>1291</dt>
<dd><a title="Philip IV of France" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Philip_IV_of_France">Philip the Fair</a>&nbsp;publishes an ordinance prohibiting the Jews to settle in France.</dd>
</dl>
<dl>
<dt>1291</dt>
<dd>Jewish physician and grand&nbsp;<a title="Vizier" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vizier">vizier</a>&nbsp;<a title="Sa'ad al-Dawla" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sa%27ad_al-Dawla">Sa'ad al-Dawla</a>&nbsp;is killed by Muslims who felt it a degradation to have a Jew placed over them.&nbsp;<a title="Persian Jews" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persian_Jews">Persian Jews</a>&nbsp;suffer a long-period of violent persecution by the Muslim population.</dd>
</dl>
<dl>
<dt>1292</dt>
<dd>Forced conversion and expulsion of the&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Italian Jewish" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Italian_Jewish">Italian Jewish</a>&nbsp;community.</dd>
</dl>
<dl>
<dt>1298</dt>
<dd>Accusations of&nbsp;<a title="Host desecration" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Host_desecration">Host desecration</a>&nbsp;against the&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="German Jews" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/German_Jews">German Jews</a>. More than 140 Jewish communities face forced conversions.</dd>
</dl>
<dl>
<dt>1298</dt>
<dd>During the civil war between&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Adolf, King of Germany" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Adolf,_King_of_Germany">Adolph of Nassau</a>&nbsp;and&nbsp;<a title="Albert I of Germany" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Albert_I_of_Germany">Albrecht of Austria</a>, German knight&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Rintfleisch-Pogrom" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Rintfleisch-Pogrom">Rintfleisch</a>&nbsp;claims to have received a mission from heaven to exterminate "the accursed race of the Jews". Under his leadership, the mob goes from town to town destroying Jewish communities and massacring about 100,000 Jews, often by mass burning at stake. Among 146 localities in Franconia, Bavaria and Austria are R&ouml;ttingen (20 April), W&uuml;rzburg (24 July), Nuremberg (1 August).</dd>
</dl>
<h2><span id="Fourteenth_century" class="mw-headline">Fourteenth century</span></h2>
<dl>
<dt>1301</dt>
<dd>Riots break out in&nbsp;<a title="Egypt" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Egypt">Egypt</a>, which are encouraged by the Mamluks. Many Jews are forcibly converted to Islam, including the entire Jewish population of&nbsp;<a title="Bilbeis" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bilbeis">Bilbeis</a>. Many synagogues are appropriated into mosques.</dd>
</dl>
<dl>
<dt>1305</dt>
<dd><a title="Philip IV of France" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Philip_IV_of_France">Philip IV of France</a>&nbsp;seizes all Jewish property (except the clothes they wear) and expels them from France (approx. 100,000). His successor&nbsp;<a title="Louis X of France" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Louis_X_of_France">Louis X of France</a>&nbsp;allows French Jews to return in 1315.</dd>
</dl>
<dl>
<dt>1306</dt>
<dd>Jews of Sens are expelled.</dd>
</dl>
<dl>
<dt>1306</dt>
<dd>Jews expelled from&nbsp;<a title="Castelsarrasin" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Castelsarrasin">Castelsarrasin</a>,&nbsp;<a title="France" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/France">France</a>.</dd>
</dl>
<dl>
<dt>1310</dt>
<dd><a class="mw-redirect" title="Frederick II of Aragon" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Frederick_II_of_Aragon">Frederick II of Aragon</a>&nbsp;adopts anti-Jewish laws, which require them to mark their clothes and shops with the&nbsp;<a title="Yellow badge" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Yellow_badge">yellow badge</a>. Jews were also forbidden from having any relationship with Catholics.</dd>
</dl>
<dl>
<dt>1318</dt>
<dd><a title="Rashid-al-Din Hamadani" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Rashid-al-Din_Hamadani">Rashid-al-Din Hamadani</a>, a&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Persian Jewish" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persian_Jewish">Persian Jewish</a>&nbsp;convert to&nbsp;<a title="Islam" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Islam">Islam</a>&nbsp;was executed on fake charges of poisoning&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="&Ouml;ljeit&uuml;" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/%C3%96ljeit%C3%BC">&Ouml;ljeit&uuml;</a>&nbsp;and for several days crowds carried his head around his native city of Tabriz, chanting "This is the head of the Jew who abused the name of God; may God's curse be upon him!"</dd>
</dl>
<dl>
<dt>1319</dt>
<dd>Jews are expelled from&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Breslau" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Breslau">Breslau</a>.</dd>
</dl>
<dl>
<dt>1320</dt>
<dd>Jews are expelled from&nbsp;<a title="Milan" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Milan">Milan</a>&nbsp;during a persecution of so-called heretics.</dd>
</dl>
<dl>
<dt>1320</dt>
<dd>152 Jews massacred in&nbsp;<a title="Castelsarrasin" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Castelsarrasin">Castelsarrasin</a>,&nbsp;<a title="France" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/France">France</a>.</dd>
</dl>
<dl>
<dt>1320</dt>
<dd><a title="Shepherds' Crusade (1320)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Shepherds%27_Crusade_(1320)">Shepherds' Crusade</a>&nbsp;attacks the Jews of 120 localities in southwest France.</dd>
</dl>
<dl>
<dt>1321</dt>
<dd>King&nbsp;<a title="Henry II of Castile" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Henry_II_of_Castile">Henry II of Castile</a>&nbsp;forces Jews to wear&nbsp;<a title="Yellow badge" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Yellow_badge">Yellow badge</a>.</dd>
</dl>
<dl>
<dt>1321</dt>
<dd>Jews in central France accused of&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="1321 leper scare" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1321_leper_scare">ordering lepers to poison wells</a>. After massacre of est. 5,000 Jews,&nbsp;<a title="Philip V of France" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Philip_V_of_France">King Philip V</a>&nbsp;admits they were innocent.</dd>
</dl>
<dl>
<dt>1321</dt>
<dd>A Muslim mob destroys a synagogue in&nbsp;<a title="Damascus" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Damascus">Damascus</a>.</dd>
</dl>
<dl>
<dt>1322</dt>
<dd>King&nbsp;<a title="Charles IV of France" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Charles_IV_of_France">Charles IV</a>&nbsp;expels Jews from France.</dd>
</dl>
<dl>
<dt>1328</dt>
<dd>5,000 Jews are massacred and their houses are burned down following&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Anti-Jewish" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Anti-Jewish">anti-Jewish</a>&nbsp;preaching by a Franciscan&nbsp;<a title="Friar" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Friar">friar</a>.</dd>
</dl>
<dl>
<dt>1328</dt>
<dd>Jewish martyr&nbsp;<a title="Aaron ben Zerah" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Aaron_ben_Zerah">Aaron ben Zerah</a>, along with his wife and four of his sons are executed.</dd>
</dl>
<dl>
<dt>1333</dt>
<dd>Forced mass conversions in&nbsp;<a title="Baghdad" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Baghdad">Baghdad</a></dd>
</dl>
<dl>
<dt>1336</dt>
<dd>Persecutions against Jews in&nbsp;<a title="Franconia" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Franconia">Franconia</a>&nbsp;and&nbsp;<a title="Alsace" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Alsace">Alsace</a>&nbsp;led by lawless German bands, the Armleder under the highwayman&nbsp;<a title="Arnold von Uissigheim" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arnold_von_Uissigheim">Arnold von Uissigheim</a>. Roughly 1500 Jews are killed.</dd>
</dl>
<dl>
<dt>1336</dt>
<dd>The&nbsp;<a title="Aleinu" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Aleinu">Aleinu</a>&nbsp;prayer is banned in Castile.</dd>
</dl>
<dl>
<dt>1337</dt>
<dd>Host desecration accusations. Violence spreads to over 51 Jewish communities.</dd>
</dl>
<dl>
<dt>1338</dt>
<dd>Pogroms over&nbsp;<a title="Host desecration" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Host_desecration">host desecration</a>&nbsp;in Wolfsberg. The Jews are accused of stealing the bread of the&nbsp;<a title="Eucharist" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Eucharist">Eucharist</a>&nbsp;and trying to burn it. Over 70 Jews are burned at the stake and the entire Jewish community is destroyed.</dd>
</dl>
<dl>
<dt>1343</dt>
<dd>Pre-Easter massacres spread from Germany across Western Europe. Jews fleeing persecution are welcomed in Poland by&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Casimir the Great" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Casimir_the_Great">Casimir the Great</a>.</dd>
</dl>
<dl>
<dt>1344</dt>
<dd>The citizens ask the King's permission to confiscate the houses of the Jews for the cities benefit &ndash; he grants their request.</dd>
</dl>
<dl>
<dt>1348</dt>
<dd>European Jews are blamed for the plague in the&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Black Death persecutions" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Black_Death_persecutions">Black Death persecutions</a>. Charge laid to the Jews that they poisoned the wells. Massacres spread throughout Spain, France, Germany and Austria. More than 200 Jewish communities destroyed by violence. Many communities have been expelled and settle down in Poland.</dd>
</dl>
<dl>
<dt>1349</dt>
<dd><a title="Basel massacre" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Basel_massacre">Basel</a>: 600 Jews burned at the stake, 140 children forcibly baptized, the remaining city's Jews expelled. The city synagogue is turned into a church and the Jewish cemetery is destroyed.</dd>
</dl>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner">
<div class="thumbcaption">1349</div>
<div class="thumbcaption">&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; burning of Jews (from a European chronicle written on the&nbsp;<a title="Black Death" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Black_Death">Black Death</a>&nbsp;between 1349 and 1352)</div>
</div>
</div>
<dl>
<dt>1349</dt>
<dd>The&nbsp;<a title="Erfurt massacre (1349)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Erfurt_massacre_(1349)">Erfurt massacre</a>&nbsp;was a massacre of around 3,000 Jews as a result of&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Black Death Jewish persecutions" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Black_Death_Jewish_persecutions">Black Death Jewish persecutions</a></dd>
</dl>
<dl>
<dt>1349</dt>
<dd>The entire Jewish population of Speyer is destroyed. All Jews are either killed, converted, or fled. All their property and assets was confiscated. Part of the&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Black Death Jewish persecutions" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Black_Death_Jewish_persecutions">Black Death Jewish persecutions</a>.</dd>
</dl>
<dl>
<dt>1349</dt>
<dd>600 Jews are burned at the stake and the entire Jewish community of&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Zurich" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Zurich">Zurich</a>&nbsp;is annihilated as a part of the&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Black Death Jewish persecutions" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Black_Death_Jewish_persecutions">Black Death Jewish persecutions</a>.</dd>
</dl>
<dl>
<dt>1349</dt>
<dd>The Jewish community of&nbsp;<a title="Worms, Germany" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Worms,_Germany">Worms</a>&nbsp;is completely destroyed as a result of the&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Black Death Jewish persecutions" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Black_Death_Jewish_persecutions">Black Death Jewish persecutions</a>. Hundreds of Jews set fire to their homes to avoid the oncoming torture. Their property was seized by the locals.</dd>
</dl>
<dl>
<dt>1349</dt>
<dd>Jews of&nbsp;<a title="Berlin" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Berlin">Berlin</a>&nbsp;are expelled and many are killed as a part of the&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Black Death Jewish persecutions" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Black_Death_Jewish_persecutions">Black Death Jewish persecutions</a>.</dd>
</dl>
<dl>
<dt>1349</dt>
<dd>Jews of&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Breslau" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Breslau">Breslau</a>&nbsp;are expelled as part of the&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Black Death Jewish persecutions" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Black_Death_Jewish_persecutions">Black Death Jewish persecutions</a>.</dd>
</dl>
<dl>
<dt>1349</dt>
<dd>60 Jews are murdered in Breslau. The city claims all property and synagogues, while the Emperor was given the cemetery and all Jewish debts.</dd>
</dl>
<dl>
<dt>1349</dt>
<dd>The Jewish quarter of Cologne is destroyed by an angry mob, and the most of the community is killed. All of their property was split up between the ransackers. It was part of the&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Black Death Jewish persecutions" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Black_Death_Jewish_persecutions">Black Death Jewish persecutions</a>.</dd>
</dl>
<dl>
<dt>1349</dt>
<dd>The&nbsp;<a title="Strasbourg massacre" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Strasbourg_massacre">Strasbourg massacre</a>&nbsp;was a part of the&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Black Death persecutions" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Black_Death_persecutions">Black Death persecutions</a>, where several hundred Jews were publicly burned to death, and the rest of them were expelled. It was one of the first and worst pogroms in pre-modern history.</dd>
</dl>
<dl>
<dt>24 August 1349</dt>
<dd>6,000 Jews are burned to death in&nbsp;<a title="Mainz" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mainz">Mainz</a>&nbsp;as a part of the&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Black Death Jewish persecutions" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Black_Death_Jewish_persecutions">Black Death Jewish persecutions</a>. When the angry mob charged, the Jews initially fought back, killing around 200 of their attackers.<sup id="cite_ref-93" class="reference"></sup></dd>
</dl>
<dl>
<dt>1350</dt>
<dd><a title="Brussels" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Brussels">Brussels</a>&nbsp;Jewish community is decimated after&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Black Death Jewish persecutions" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Black_Death_Jewish_persecutions">they are blamed for the Plague</a>.</dd>
</dl>
<dl>
<dt>1352</dt>
<dd>Church officials order the expulsion of&nbsp;<a title="History of the Jews in Bulgaria" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/History_of_the_Jews_in_Bulgaria">Jews from Bulgaria</a>&nbsp;for "heretical activity."</dd>
</dl>
<dl>
<dt>1354</dt>
<dd>12,000 Jews are massacred throughout&nbsp;<a title="Spain" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Spain">Spain</a>&nbsp;following a bloody civil war.</dd>
</dl>
<dl>
<dt>1359</dt>
<dd><a title="Charles V of France" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Charles_V_of_France">Charles V of France</a>&nbsp;allows Jews to return for a period of 20 years in order to pay ransom for his father&nbsp;<a title="John II of France" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/John_II_of_France">John II of France</a>, imprisoned in England. The period is later extended beyond the 20 years.</dd>
</dl>
<dl>
<dt>1360</dt>
<dd>Jews are expelled from&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Breslau" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Breslau">Breslau</a>.</dd>
</dl>
<dl>
<dt>1360</dt>
<dd>Furious with a pogrom against Castilian Jews in&nbsp;<a title="Miranda de Ebro" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Miranda_de_Ebro">Miranda de Ebro</a>,&nbsp;<a title="Peter of Castile" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Peter_of_Castile">Peter of Castile</a>&nbsp;publicly boils one of the perpetrators, roasts another, and executes others with an axe.</dd>
</dl>
<dl>
<dt>1360</dt>
<dd><a class="mw-redirect" title="Sephardic Jew" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sephardic_Jew">Sephardic Jew</a>&nbsp;Samuel ben Meir Abulafia is arrested and tortured to death in prison for no apparent reason. His lands are confiscated by the king.</dd>
</dl>
<dl>
<dt>1365</dt>
<dd>Jews of&nbsp;<a title="Lorraine" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lorraine">Lorraine</a>&nbsp;are expelled after their presence is cited as the cause of lightning strikes which destroyed twenty-two houses.</dd>
</dl>
<dl>
<dt>1367</dt>
<dd><a title="Host desecration" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Host_desecration">Host desecration</a>&nbsp;trials are held against the Jews of&nbsp;<a title="Barcelona" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Barcelona">Barcelona</a>. They were initiated by the crown prince Don Juan of Aragon.</dd>
</dl>
<dl>
<dt>1368</dt>
<dd>Some 6,000 Jews are killed during a siege in&nbsp;<a title="Toledo, Spain" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Toledo,_Spain">Toledo</a>.</dd>
</dl>
<dl>
<dt>1370</dt>
<dd>The entire Jewish population of&nbsp;<a title="Brussels massacre" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Brussels_massacre">Brussels is massacred</a>&nbsp;over allegations of&nbsp;<a title="Host desecration" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Host_desecration">host desecration</a>. It was an end of the Hebrew community in Brussels. The event was commemorated by local Christians as the Sacrament of Miracle.</dd>
</dl>
<dl>
<dt>1376</dt>
<dd>Jews from expelled from&nbsp;<a title="Hungary" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hungary">Hungary</a>. Most of them flee south into&nbsp;<a title="Greece" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Greece">Greece</a>&nbsp;and neighboring areas.</dd>
</dl>
<dl>
<dt>1377</dt>
<dd>Another&nbsp;<a title="Host desecration" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Host_desecration">Host desecration</a>&nbsp;trial is held against Jews in&nbsp;<a title="Teruel" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Teruel">Teruel</a>&nbsp;and&nbsp;<a title="Huesca" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Huesca">Huesca</a>. The person behind it, as with the previous trial, is the crown prince Don Juan of Aragon. Many Jews are tortured and burned alive publicly.</dd>
</dl>
<dl>
<dt>1382</dt>
<dd>16 Jews are murdered in the Mailotin Riots.</dd>
</dl>
<dl>
<dt>1384</dt>
<dd>200 Jews are killed in&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Noerdlingen" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Noerdlingen">Noerdlingen</a>&nbsp;and the community ceases to exist.</dd>
</dl>
<dl>
<dt>1386</dt>
<dd><a class="mw-redirect" title="Wenceslaus, Holy Roman Emperor" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wenceslaus,_Holy_Roman_Emperor">Wenceslaus, Holy Roman Emperor</a>, expels the Jews from the&nbsp;<a title="Swabian League" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Swabian_League">Swabian League</a>&nbsp;and&nbsp;<a title="Strasbourg" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Strasbourg">Strasbourg</a>&nbsp;and confiscates their property.</dd>
</dl>
<dl>
<dt>1385</dt>
<dd>John of Castile reinforces previous anti-Jewish legislation.</dd>
</dl>
<dl>
<dt>1385</dt>
<dd>All Jews in the Swabian League are arrested, and their books are confiscated.</dd>
</dl>
<dl>
<dt>1389</dt>
<dd>18 March, a Jewish boy is accused of plotting against a priest. The mob slaughters approx. 3,000 of&nbsp;<a title="Prague" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Prague">Prague</a>'s Jews, destroys the city's synagogue and Jewish cemetery. Wenceslaus insists that the responsibility lay with the Jews for going outside during&nbsp;<a title="Holy Week" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Holy_Week">Holy Week</a>.</dd>
</dl>
<dl>
<dt>1391</dt>
<dd>Anti-Jewish riots led by&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Ferrand Martinez" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ferrand_Martinez">Ferrand Martinez</a>&nbsp;erupt in Seville.</dd>
</dl>
<dl>
<dt>1391</dt>
<dd>Led by&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Ferrand Martinez" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ferrand_Martinez">Ferrand Martinez</a>, countless massacres devastate the Sephardic Jewish community, especially in&nbsp;<a title="Castile (historical region)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Castile_(historical_region)">Castile</a>,&nbsp;<a title="Valencia" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Valencia">Valencia</a>,&nbsp;<a title="Catalonia" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Catalonia">Catalonia</a>&nbsp;and&nbsp;<a title="Aragon" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Aragon">Aragon</a>. The Jewish quarter in Barcelona is completely destroyed. By the end of the pogroms, at least 10,000 Jews are murdered and thousands more are forcibly converted.</dd>
</dl>
<dl>
<dt>1391</dt>
<dd><a title="Pogrom" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pogrom">Pogrom</a>&nbsp;against the Jews of&nbsp;<a title="Toledo, Spain" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Toledo,_Spain">Toledo</a>&nbsp;on the&nbsp;<a title="Seventeenth of Tammuz" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Seventeenth_of_Tammuz">Seventeenth of Tammuz</a>. Jewish martyrs&nbsp;<a title="Israel Alnaqua" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel_Alnaqua">Israel Alnaqua</a>&nbsp;and Judah ben Asher died at the stake together.</dd>
</dl>
<dl>
<dt>1391</dt>
<dd>Over 250 Jews are massacred by a mob in&nbsp;<a title="Valencia" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Valencia">Valencia</a>.</dd>
</dl>
<dl>
<dt>1391</dt>
<dd>All Jewish inhabitants of&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Palma, Majorca" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Palma,_Majorca">Palma, Majorca</a>&nbsp;are either converted or killed.</dd>
</dl>
<dl>
<dt>1391</dt>
<dd>More than 400 Jews are massacred in&nbsp;<a title="Barcelona" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Barcelona">Barcelona</a>.</dd>
</dl>
<dl>
<dt>1392</dt>
<dd>The Jews of&nbsp;<a title="Damascus" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Damascus">Damascus</a>&nbsp;are accused by Muslims of setting fire to the central mosque. Although there was no evidence presented, one Jew was burned alive, the leaders of the community were tortured, and the local synagogue was appropriated into a mosque.</dd>
</dl>
<dl>
<dt>1392</dt>
<dd><a class="mw-redirect" title="Sicilian Jews" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sicilian_Jews">Sicilian Jews</a>&nbsp;are forced to live in Ghettos and severe persecution breaks out in&nbsp;<a title="Erice" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Erice">Erice</a>,&nbsp;<a title="Catania" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Catania">Catania</a>&nbsp;and&nbsp;<a title="Syracuse, Sicily" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Syracuse,_Sicily">Syracuse</a>.</dd>
</dl>
<dl>
<dt>1394</dt>
<dd>3 November,&nbsp;<a title="Charles VI of France" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Charles_VI_of_France">Charles VI of France</a>&nbsp;expels all Jews from France.</dd>
</dl>
<dl>
<dt>1397</dt>
<dd><a class="mw-redirect" title="Jewish ghettos" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jewish_ghettos">Jewish ghettos</a>&nbsp;across&nbsp;<a title="History of the Jews in Slovenia" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/History_of_the_Jews_in_Slovenia">Slovenia</a>&nbsp;are set on fire by an anonymous mob.</dd>
</dl>
<dl>
<dt>1399</dt>
<dd>A Christian woman is accused of stealing hosts and giving them to Jews&nbsp;<a title="Host desecration" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Host_desecration">for the purpose of desecration</a>. Thirteen members of the Jewish community of&nbsp;<a title="Poznań" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pozna%C5%84">Posen</a>, along with the woman are all tortured and burned alive slowly. The community is then forced to pay a special tax every year until the 18th century.</dd>
</dl>
<dl>
<dt>1399</dt>
<dd>80 Jews are murdered in&nbsp;<a title="Prague" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Prague">Prague</a>&nbsp;after a converted Jew named Peter accuses them of denigrating Christianity. A number of Jews are also jailed, including&nbsp;<a title="Yom-Tov Lipmann-Muhlhausen" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Yom-Tov_Lipmann-Muhlhausen">Yom-Tov Lipmann-Muhlhausen</a>.</dd>
</dl>
<h2><span id="Fifteenth_century" class="mw-headline">Fifteenth century</span></h2>
<dl>
<dt>1401</dt>
<dd>Two Jews are burned to death for an alleged&nbsp;<a title="Host desecration" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Host_desecration">host desecration</a>&nbsp;in Glogau.</dd>
</dl>
<dl>
<dt>1404</dt>
<dd>Many members of the Jewish community of&nbsp;<a title="Salzburg" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Salzburg">Salzburg</a>&nbsp;and&nbsp;<a title="Hallein" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hallein">Hallein</a>&nbsp;is burned alive on charged of&nbsp;<a title="Host desecration" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Host_desecration">host desecration</a>.</dd>
</dl>
<dl>
<dt>1407</dt>
<dd>Blood libel accusations against the Jews of&nbsp;<a title="Krak&oacute;w" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Krak%C3%B3w">Krak&oacute;w</a>&nbsp;led by a fanatic priest result in anti-Jewish riots.</dd>
</dl>
<dl>
<dt>1411</dt>
<dd>Oppressive legislation against Jews in Spain as an outcome of the preaching of the&nbsp;<a title="Dominican Order" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dominican_Order">Dominican</a>&nbsp;friar&nbsp;<a title="Vincent Ferrer" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vincent_Ferrer">Vicente Ferrer</a>.</dd>
</dl>
<dl>
<dt>1413</dt>
<dd><a title="Disputation" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Disputation">Disputation</a>&nbsp;of&nbsp;<a title="Tortosa" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tortosa">Tortosa</a>, Spain, staged by&nbsp;<a title="Antipope Benedict XIII" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Antipope_Benedict_XIII">the Avignon Pope Benedict XIII</a>, is followed by forced mass conversions.</dd>
</dl>
<dl>
<dt>1418</dt>
<dd>All Jews living in Trier are expelled.</dd>
</dl>
<dl>
<dt>1420</dt>
<dd>All Jews are expelled from&nbsp;<a title="Lyon" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lyon">Lyons</a>.</dd>
</dl>
<dl>
<dt>1421</dt>
<dd>Persecutions of Jews in&nbsp;<a title="Vienna" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vienna">Vienna</a>, known as&nbsp;<em><a class="mw-redirect" title="Wiener Gesera" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wiener_Gesera">Wiener Gesera</a></em>&nbsp;(Vienna Edict), confiscation of their possessions, and forced conversion of Jewish children. 270 Jews burned at stake.</dd>
</dl>
<dl>
<dt>1421</dt>
<dd>All&nbsp;<a title="History of the Jews in Vienna" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/History_of_the_Jews_in_Vienna">Viennese Jews</a>&nbsp;are expelled following persecution.</dd>
</dl>
<dl>
<dt>1422</dt>
<dd><a title="Pope Martin V" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pope_Martin_V">Pope Martin V</a>&nbsp;issues a Bull reminding Christians that&nbsp;<a title="Christianity" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Christianity">Christianity</a>&nbsp;was derived from&nbsp;<a title="Judaism" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Judaism">Judaism</a>&nbsp;and warns the friars not to incite against the Jews. The Bull was withdrawn the following year on allegations that the Jews of Rome attained it by&nbsp;<a title="Fraud" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fraud">fraud</a>.</dd>
</dl>
<dl>
<dt>1424</dt>
<dd>The Jewish population of&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Zurich" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Zurich">Zurich</a>&nbsp;is exiled.</dd>
</dl>
<dl>
<dt>1424</dt>
<dd>Jews are expelled and banned from Cologne.</dd>
</dl>
<dl>
<dt>1426</dt>
<dd>Jews are expelled from&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Iglau" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Iglau">Iglau</a>&nbsp;after they are accused of being in league with the&nbsp;<a title="Hussites" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hussites">Hussites</a>.</dd>
</dl>
<dl>
<dt>1427</dt>
<dd>All Jews living in&nbsp;<a title="Bern" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bern">Bern</a>&nbsp;are expelled and their property is seized.</dd>
</dl>
<dl>
<dt>1428</dt>
<dd>Jews are expelled from&nbsp;<a title="Fribourg" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fribourg">Fribourg</a>.</dd>
</dl>
<dl>
<dt>1430</dt>
<dd>Pogrom in&nbsp;<a title="Aix-en-Provence" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Aix-en-Provence">Aix-en-Provence</a>&nbsp;breaks out in which 9 Jews are killed, many more are injured and 74 are forcibly converted.</dd>
</dl>
<dl>
<dt>1434</dt>
<dd>Council of Basel, Sessio XIX: Jews are forbidden to obtain academic degrees and to act as agents in the conclusion of contracts between Christians.</dd>
</dl>
<dl>
<dt>1435</dt>
<dd>Massacre and forced conversion of&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Majorca" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Majorca">Majorcan</a>&nbsp;Jews.</dd>
</dl>
<dl>
<dt>1435</dt>
<dd>Jews are expelled from Speyer "forever."</dd>
</dl>
<dl>
<dt>1436</dt>
<dd>Jews of Zurich are expelled.<sup id="cite_ref-Zurich_100-1" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_antisemitism#cite_note-Zurich-100">[100]</a></sup></dd>
</dl>
<dl>
<dt>1438</dt>
<dd>Jewish inhabitants of&nbsp;<a title="Augsburg" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Augsburg">Augsburg</a>&nbsp;and&nbsp;<a title="D&uuml;sseldorf" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/D%C3%BCsseldorf">D&uuml;sseldorf</a>&nbsp;are expelled.</dd>
</dl>
<dl>
<dt>1438</dt>
<dd>Establishment of&nbsp;<em><a title="Mellah" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mellah">mellahs</a></em>&nbsp;(ghettos) in&nbsp;<a title="Morocco" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Morocco">Morocco</a>.</dd>
</dl>
<dl>
<dt>1442</dt>
<dd>Synagogues and other Jewish buildings are destroyed by a riot of&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Glogau" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glogau">Glogau</a>.</dd>
</dl>
<dl>
<dt>1442</dt>
<dd>Jews are expelled from Upper Bavaria.</dd>
</dl>
<dl>
<dt>1444</dt>
<dd>Jewish population of&nbsp;<a title="Utrecht" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Utrecht">Utrecht</a>&nbsp;are expelled.</dd>
</dl>
<dl>
<dt>1447</dt>
<dd><a title="Casimir IV Jagiellon" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Casimir_IV_Jagiellon">Casimir IV</a>&nbsp;renews all the rights of Jews of&nbsp;<a title="Poland" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Poland">Poland</a>&nbsp;and makes his charter one of the most liberal in Europe. He revokes it in 1454 at the insistence of Bishop Zbigniew.</dd>
</dl>
<dl>
<dt>1449</dt>
<dd>The Statute of Toledo introduces the rule of&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Racial purity" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Racial_purity">purity of blood</a>&nbsp;discriminating&nbsp;<a title="Converso" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Converso">Conversos</a>.&nbsp;<a title="Pope Nicholas V" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pope_Nicholas_V">Pope Nicholas V</a>&nbsp;condemns it.</dd>
</dl>
<dl>
<dt>1450</dt>
<dd><a title="Louis IX, Duke of Bavaria" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Louis_IX,_Duke_of_Bavaria">Louis IX, Duke of Bavaria</a>&nbsp;expels all Jews who reject baptism.</dd>
</dl>
<dl>
<dt>1453</dt>
<dd>Around 40 Jews in Breslau are burned at the stake on charges of&nbsp;<a title="Host desecration" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Host_desecration">host desecration</a>, while the head Rabbi hung himself to avoid the torture. Jewish children under 7 were stolen and forcibly baptized. The few Jews remaining were banished from Breslau.</dd>
</dl>
<dl>
<dt>1456</dt>
<dd>Pope Caliextus III issues a papal bull which prohibits Jews from testifying against Christians, but permits Christians to testify against a Jew.</dd>
</dl>
<dl>
<dt>1458</dt>
<dd>The city council of&nbsp;<a title="Erfurt" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Erfurt">Erfurt</a>, Germany votes to expel the Jews.</dd>
</dl>
<dl>
<dt>1463</dt>
<dd>Pope Nicholas V authorizes the establishment of the&nbsp;<a title="Inquisition" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Inquisition">Inquisition</a>&nbsp;to investigate heresy among the&nbsp;<a title="Marrano" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marrano">Marranos</a>. See also&nbsp;<a title="Crypto-Judaism" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Crypto-Judaism">Crypto-Judaism</a>.</dd>
</dl>
<dl>
<dt>1465</dt>
<dd>The&nbsp;<a title="1465 Moroccan revolt" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1465_Moroccan_revolt">Moroccan revolt</a>&nbsp;against the&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Marinid" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marinid">Marinid</a>&nbsp;dynasty, accusations against one Jewish&nbsp;<a title="Vizier" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vizier">Vizier</a>&nbsp;lead to a massacre of the entire Jewish population of&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Fes" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fes">Fes</a>.</dd>
</dl>
<dl>
<dt>1465</dt>
<dd>Over 30 Jews in Cracow are killed by an angry mob.</dd>
</dl>
<dl>
<dt>1468</dt>
<dd>Many Jewish homes and plundered and a number are killed during anti-Jewish in Posen.</dd>
</dl>
<dl>
<dt>1468</dt>
<dd>Sultan&nbsp;<a title="Qaitbay" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Qaitbay">Qaitbay</a>&nbsp;forces Jews of Cairo to pay 75,000 gold pieces or be expelled. This severely impoverished the local Jewish community.</dd>
</dl>
<dl>
<dt>1470</dt>
<dd>The Jewish community of&nbsp;<a title="Bavaria" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bavaria">Bavaria</a>&nbsp;are expelled, many migrate into&nbsp;<a title="Bulgaria" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bulgaria">Bulgaria</a>.</dd>
</dl>
<dl>
<dt>1473</dt>
<dd>Massacres of&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Marranos" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marranos">Marranos</a>&nbsp;of&nbsp;<a title="Valladolid" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Valladolid">Valladolid</a>,&nbsp;<a title="C&oacute;rdoba, Spain" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/C%C3%B3rdoba,_Spain">Cordova</a>,&nbsp;<a title="Segovia" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Segovia">Segovia</a>,&nbsp;<a title="Ciudad Real" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ciudad_Real">Ciudad Real</a>, Spain</dd>
</dl>
<dl>
<dt>1474</dt>
<dd>On&nbsp;<a class="new" title="Assumption day (page does not exist)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Assumption_day&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1">Assumption day</a>&nbsp;15 August 1474, Christians wreaked brutal havoc on the Jewish dwellers of the Cartellone area of&nbsp;<a title="Modica" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Modica">Modica</a>. It was the first and most horrible massacre of&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Sicilian Jews" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sicilian_Jews">Sicilian Jews</a>. During the evening a number of Christians slaughtered about 360 Jews causing a total and fierce devastation in&nbsp;<a title="La Giudecca" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/La_Giudecca">La Giudecca</a>. They ran through the streets chanting: "Hurrah for Mary! Death to the Jews!" (Viva Maria! Morte ai Giudei!).</dd>
</dl>
<div class="thumb tright">&nbsp;</div>
<dl>
<dt>1475</dt>
<dd>A student of the preacher&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Giovanni da Capistrano" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Giovanni_da_Capistrano">Giovanni da Capistrano</a>,&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Franciscan" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Franciscan">Franciscan</a>&nbsp;<a title="Bernardine of Feltre" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bernardine_of_Feltre">Bernardine of Feltre</a>, accuses the Jews in murdering an infant,&nbsp;<a title="Simon of Trent" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Simon_of_Trent">Simon</a>. The entire community is arrested, 15 leaders are burned at the stake, the rest are expelled. In 1588,&nbsp;<a title="Pope Sixtus V" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pope_Sixtus_V">Pope Sixtus V</a>&nbsp;confirmed Simon's cultus. Saint Simon was considered a martyr and patron of kidnap and torture victims for almost 500 years. In 1965,&nbsp;<a title="Pope Paul VI" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pope_Paul_VI">Pope Paul VI</a>&nbsp;declared the episode a fraud, and decanonized Simon's sainthood.</dd>
</dl>
<dl>
<dt>1478</dt>
<dd>Jews of&nbsp;<a title="Passau" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Passau">Passau</a>&nbsp;are expelled.</dd>
</dl>
<dl>
<dt>1481</dt>
<dd>The&nbsp;<a title="Spanish Inquisition" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Spanish_Inquisition">Spanish Inquisition</a>&nbsp;is instituted.</dd>
</dl>
<dl>
<dt>1484</dt>
<dd>Pogrom against the&nbsp;<a title="History of the Jews in Arles" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/History_of_the_Jews_in_Arles">Jewish section of Arles</a>. A number of Jews are killed and 50 men are forced to convert.</dd>
</dl>
<dl>
<dt>1487&ndash;1504</dt>
<dd>Bishop Gennady exposes the&nbsp;<a title="Heresy" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Heresy">heresy</a>&nbsp;of&nbsp;<em>Zhidovstvuyushchiye</em>&nbsp;(<a class="mw-redirect" title="Judaizer" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Judaizer">Judaizers</a>) in&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Eastern Orthodoxy" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Eastern_Orthodoxy">Eastern Orthodoxy</a>&nbsp;of&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Muscovy" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Muscovy">Muscovy</a>.</dd>
</dl>
<dl>
<dt>1490</dt>
<dd><a title="Tom&aacute;s de Torquemada" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tom%C3%A1s_de_Torquemada">Tom&aacute;s de Torquemada</a>&nbsp;burns 6,000 volumes of Jewish manuscripts in&nbsp;<a title="Salamanca" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Salamanca">Salamanca</a>.</dd>
</dl>
<dl>
<dt>1490</dt>
<dd>Jews are expelled from&nbsp;<a title="Geneva" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Geneva">Geneva</a>&nbsp;and not allowed to return for over 300 years.</dd>
</dl>
<dl>
<dt>1491</dt>
<dd>The&nbsp;<a title="Blood libel" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Blood_libel">blood libel</a>&nbsp;in La Guardia, Spain, where the alleged victim&nbsp;<a title="Holy Child of La Guardia" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Holy_Child_of_La_Guardia">Holy Child of La Guardia</a>&nbsp;became revered as a saint.</dd>
</dl>
<dl>
<dt>1491</dt>
<dd><a title="Muhammad al-Maghili" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Muhammad_al-Maghili">Muhammad al-Maghili</a>&nbsp;orders the expulsion and murder of the Jewish community in&nbsp;<a title="Tlemcen" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tlemcen">Tlemcen</a>.</dd>
</dl>
<dl>
<dt>1492</dt>
<dd>The Jewish population of&nbsp;<a title="Tuat" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tuat">Tuat</a>&nbsp;is massacred in a pogrom inspired by the preacher al-Maghili.</dd>
</dl>
<dl>
<dt>1492</dt>
<dd><a title="Ferdinand II of Aragon" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ferdinand_II_of_Aragon">Ferdinand II</a>&nbsp;and&nbsp;<a title="Isabella I of Castile" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Isabella_I_of_Castile">Isabella</a>&nbsp;issue&nbsp;<em><a class="mw-redirect" title="Alhambra decree" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Alhambra_decree">General Edict on the Expulsion of the Jews</a></em>&nbsp;from Spain: approx. 200,000. Some return to the&nbsp;<a title="Land of Israel" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Land_of_Israel">Land of Israel</a>. As many localities and entire countries expel their Jewish citizens (after robbing them), and others deny them entrance, the legend of the&nbsp;<em>Wandering Jew</em>, a condemned harbinger of calamity, gains popularity.</dd>
</dl>
<dl>
<dt>1492</dt>
<dd>Jews of&nbsp;<a title="Mecklenburg" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mecklenburg">Mecklenburg</a>, Germany are accused of stabbing a consecrated wafer. 27 Jews are burned, including two women. The spot is still called the&nbsp;<em>Judenberg</em>. All the Jews are expelled from the Duchy.</dd>
</dl>
<dl>
<dt>1492</dt>
<dd><a title="Askia Mohammad I" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Askia_Mohammad_I">Askia Mohammad I</a>&nbsp;decrees that all Jews must convert to Islam, leave or be killed. Judaism becomes illegal in Mali. This was based on the advice of&nbsp;<a title="Muhammad al-Maghili" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Muhammad_al-Maghili">Muhammad al-Maghili</a>. The region of&nbsp;<a title="Timbuktu" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timbuktu">Timbuktu</a>&nbsp;had previously been tolerant of other religions before Askia got into power.</dd>
</dl>
<dl>
<dt>1493</dt>
<dd><a title="John II of Portugal" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/John_II_of_Portugal">John II of Portugal</a>&nbsp;deports several hundred Jewish children to the colony of&nbsp;<a title="S&atilde;o Tom&eacute;" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/S%C3%A3o_Tom%C3%A9">S&atilde;o Tom&eacute;</a>, where most of them die.</dd>
</dl>
<dl>
<dt>1493</dt>
<dd>Expulsion from&nbsp;<a title="Sicily" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sicily">Sicily</a>: approx. 37,000.</dd>
</dl>
<dl>
<dt>1494</dt>
<dd>16 Jews are burned at the stake after a blood libel in&nbsp;<a title="Trnava" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Trnava">Trnava</a>.</dd>
</dl>
<dl>
<dt>1494</dt>
<dd>After a fire destroys the Jewish quarter of Cracow, the Polish king&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Jan I Olbracht" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jan_I_Olbracht">Jan I Olbracht</a>&nbsp;transfers the Jews to&nbsp;<a title="Kazimierz" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kazimierz">Kazimierz</a>, which would become the first Polish ghetto. Jews were confined to the ghetto until 1868.</dd>
</dl>
<dl>
<dt>1495</dt>
<dd>Jews in&nbsp;<a title="Lithuania" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lithuania">Lithuania</a>&nbsp;are expelled and their property is seized. They were allowed to return 8 years later.</dd>
</dl>
<dl>
<dt>1495</dt>
<dd>The Jews of&nbsp;<a title="Lecce" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lecce">Lecce</a>&nbsp;are massacred and the Jewish quarter is burned to the ground.</dd>
</dl>
<dl>
<dt>1495</dt>
<dd>The French conquer&nbsp;<a title="History of the Jews in Naples" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/History_of_the_Jews_in_Naples">Naples</a>&nbsp;and persecute the local Jews.</dd>
</dl>
<dl>
<dt>1496</dt>
<dd>Jews living in&nbsp;<a title="Styria" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Styria">Styria</a>&nbsp;are expelled and all their property is confiscated.</dd>
</dl>
<dl>
<dt>1496</dt>
<dd><a title="Forced conversion" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Forced_conversion">Forced conversion</a>&nbsp;and expulsion of Jews from&nbsp;<a title="Portugal" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Portugal">Portugal</a>. This included many who fled Spain four years earlier.</dd>
</dl>
<dl>
<dt>1497</dt>
<dd>Entire Jewish community of&nbsp;<a title="Graz" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Graz">Graz</a>&nbsp;is expelled.</dd>
</dl>
<dl>
<dt>1497</dt>
<dd><a title="Manuel I of Portugal" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Manuel_I_of_Portugal">Manuel I of Portugal</a>&nbsp;decrees that all Jews must convert or leave Portugal without their children.</dd>
</dl>
<dl>
<dt>1498</dt>
<dd>Prince&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Alexander of Poland" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Alexander_of_Poland">Alexander</a>&nbsp;of&nbsp;<a title="Lithuania" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lithuania">Lithuania</a>&nbsp;forces most of the Jews to forfeit their property or convert. The main motivation is to cancel the debts the nobles owe to the Jews. Within a short time trade grinds to a halt and the Prince invites the Jews back in.</dd>
</dl>
<dl>
<dt>1498</dt>
<dd><a class="mw-redirect" title="French Jews" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/French_Jews">French Jews</a>&nbsp;are expelled from most of France.</dd>
</dl>
<dl>
<dt>1499</dt>
<dd>Jews of&nbsp;<a title="Nuremberg" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nuremberg">Nuremberg</a>&nbsp;are expelled.</dd>
</dl>
<dl>
<dt>1499</dt>
<dd>Jews are banished from&nbsp;<a title="Verona" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Verona">Verona</a>. The Jews who were money lenders were replaced with Christian usurers who oppressed the poor so bad that the Jews were very shortly called to return.</dd>
</dl>
<dl>
<dt>1499</dt>
<dd>All&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="New Christians" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/New_Christians">New Christians</a>&nbsp;are prohibited from leaving Portugal, even those who were forcibly baptized.</dd>
</dl>
<h2><span id="Sixteenth_century" class="mw-headline">Sixteenth century</span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">&nbsp;</div>
<dl>
<dt>1501</dt>
<dd><a class="mw-redirect" title="French Jews" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/French_Jews">French Jews</a>&nbsp;living in Provence are expelled.</dd>
</dl>
<dl>
<dt>1504</dt>
<dd>Jews living in&nbsp;<a title="Plzeň" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Plze%C5%88">Pilsen</a>&nbsp;are expelled on charges of&nbsp;<a title="Host desecration" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Host_desecration">host desecration</a>.</dd>
</dl>
<dl>
<dt>1504</dt>
<dd>Several Jewish scholars are burned at the stake for proselytizing in&nbsp;<a title="Moscow" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Moscow">Moscow</a>.</dd>
</dl>
<dl>
<dt>1505</dt>
<dd>Ten&nbsp;<a title="Česk&eacute; Budějovice" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/%C4%8Cesk%C3%A9_Bud%C4%9Bjovice">Česk&eacute; Budějovice</a>&nbsp;Jews are tortured and executed after being accused of killing a Christian girl; later, on his deathbed, a shepherd confesses to fabricating the accusation.</dd>
</dl>
<dl>
<dt>1506</dt>
<dd>A&nbsp;<a title="Marrano" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marrano">marrano</a>&nbsp;expresses his doubts about miracle visions at St. Dominics Church in&nbsp;<a title="Lisbon" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lisbon">Lisbon</a>,&nbsp;<a title="Portugal" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Portugal">Portugal</a>. The crowd, led by Dominican friars, kills him, then ransacks Jewish houses and slaughters any Jew they could find. The countrymen hear about the massacre and join in. Over 2,000 marranos killed in three days.</dd>
</dl>
<dl>
<dt>1509</dt>
<dd>A converted Jew&nbsp;<a title="Johannes Pfefferkorn" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Johannes_Pfefferkorn">Johannes Pfefferkorn</a>&nbsp;receives authority of&nbsp;<a title="Maximilian I, Holy Roman Emperor" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Maximilian_I,_Holy_Roman_Emperor">Maximilian I, Holy Roman Emperor</a>&nbsp;to destroy the Talmud and other Jewish religious books, except the&nbsp;<a title="Hebrew Bible" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hebrew_Bible">Hebrew Bible</a>, in&nbsp;<a title="Frankfurt" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Frankfurt">Frankfurt</a>.</dd>
</dl>
<dl>
<dt>1510</dt>
<dd>Forty Jews are executed in&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Brandenburg, Germany" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Brandenburg,_Germany">Brandenburg, Germany</a>&nbsp;for allegedly&nbsp;<a title="Host desecration" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Host_desecration">desecrating the host</a>; remainder expelled. 23 November. Less-wealthy Jews expelled from Naples; remainder heavily taxed. 38 Jews burned at the stake in&nbsp;<a title="Berlin" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Berlin">Berlin</a>.</dd>
</dl>
<dl>
<dt>1510</dt>
<dd>Spanish gain control of&nbsp;<a title="Calabria" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Calabria">Calabria</a>&nbsp;and expel all&nbsp;<a title="Jews" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jews">Jews</a>&nbsp;and&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="New Christians" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/New_Christians">New Christians</a>.</dd>
</dl>
<dl>
<dt>1510</dt>
<dd>Spain gains control of&nbsp;<a title="Naples" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Naples">Naples</a>&nbsp;and expels the Jewish population.</dd>
</dl>
<dl>
<dt>1511</dt>
<dd>The officials of&nbsp;<a title="Conegliano" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Conegliano">Conegliano</a>&nbsp;try to expel the Jewish population but are unsuccessful.</dd>
</dl>
<dl>
<dt>1511</dt>
<dd>Eight Roman Catholic converts from Judaism burned at the stake for allegedly reverting.</dd>
</dl>
<dl>
<dt>1511</dt>
<dd>Most&nbsp;<a title="History of the Jews in Apulia" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/History_of_the_Jews_in_Apulia">Apulian Jews</a>&nbsp;are either expelled or are tortured to death. Jewish property is seized and Synagogues are replaced with Catholic Churches.</dd>
</dl>
<dl>
<dt>1514</dt>
<dd>The Jewish population of&nbsp;<a title="Mittelberg" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mittelberg">Mittelberg</a>&nbsp;is accused of&nbsp;<a title="Host desecration" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Host_desecration">host desecration</a>.</dd>
</dl>
<dl>
<dt>1515</dt>
<dd>Jews are expelled from Laibach.</dd>
</dl>
<dl>
<dt>1515</dt>
<dd>Jews are expelled from the city of&nbsp;<a title="Genoa" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Genoa">Genoa</a>, but are allowed back in a year later.</dd>
</dl>
<dl>
<dt>1515</dt>
<dd>Emperor Maximillian expels Jews from&nbsp;<a title="Ljubljana" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ljubljana">Ljubljana</a>.</dd>
</dl>
<dl>
<dt>1516</dt>
<dd>The first&nbsp;<a title="Ghetto" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ghetto">ghetto</a>&nbsp;is established, on one of the islands in&nbsp;<a title="Venice" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Venice">Venice</a>.</dd>
</dl>
<dl>
<dt>1517</dt>
<dd><a title="1517 Hebron attacks" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1517_Hebron_attacks">1517 Hebron attacks</a>: Jews are beaten, raped and killed in&nbsp;<a title="Hebron" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hebron">Hebron</a>, as their homes and businesses are looted and pillaged.</dd>
</dl>
<dl>
<dt>1517</dt>
<dd><a title="1517 Safed attacks" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1517_Safed_attacks">1517 Safed attacks</a>: The Jews of Safed is attacked by Mamluk forces and local Arabs. Many Jews are killed and their homes are plundered.</dd>
</dl>
<dl>
<dt>1519</dt>
<dd>The Jewish community of Ratisbon is expelled. The synagogue is destroyed and replaced with a chapel. Thousands of Jewish gravestones are taken and used for buildings.</dd>
</dl>
<dl>
<dt>1519</dt>
<dd><a title="Martin Luther" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Martin_Luther">Martin Luther</a>&nbsp;leads&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Protestant Reformation" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protestant_Reformation">Protestant Reformation</a>&nbsp;and challenges the doctrine of&nbsp;<em><a title="Corpus Juris Civilis" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Corpus_Juris_Civilis#Servitus_Judaeorum">Servitus Judaeorum</a></em>&nbsp;"... to deal kindly with the Jews and to instruct them to come over to us". 21 February. All Jews expelled from&nbsp;<a title="Regensburg" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Regensburg">Ratisbon/Regensburg</a>.</dd>
</dl>
<dl>
<dt>1520</dt>
<dd><a title="Pope Leo X" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pope_Leo_X">Pope Leo X</a>&nbsp;allows the Jews to print the Talmud in&nbsp;<a title="Venice" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Venice">Venice</a>.</dd>
</dl>
<dl>
<dt>1523</dt>
<dd>The conquest of Cranganore by the Portuguese leads to the complete destruction of the local Jewish community. Most refugees fled to Cochin.</dd>
</dl>
<dl>
<dt>1523</dt>
<dd>Mexico bans immigration from those who can't prove four generations of Catholic ancestry.</dd>
</dl>
<dl>
<dt>1526</dt>
<dd>Jews are expelled from&nbsp;<a title="Jewish history of Sopron" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jewish_history_of_Sopron">Hungary</a>,&nbsp;<a title="Croatia" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Croatia">Croatia</a>, and&nbsp;<a title="History of the Jews in Slovakia" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/History_of_the_Jews_in_Slovakia">Slovakia</a>&nbsp;following the&nbsp;<a title="Battle of Moh&aacute;cs" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Battle_of_Moh%C3%A1cs">Battle of Moh&aacute;cs</a>.</dd>
</dl>
<dl>
<dt>1527</dt>
<dd>Jews are ordered to leave&nbsp;<a title="Florence" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Florence">Florence</a>, but the edict is soon rescinded.</dd>
</dl>
<dl>
<dt>1528</dt>
<dd>Three&nbsp;<em><a class="mw-redirect" title="Judaizer" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Judaizer">judaizers</a></em>&nbsp;are burned at the stake in&nbsp;<a title="Mexico City" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mexico_City">Mexico City</a>'s first&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Auto da fe" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Auto_da_fe">auto da fe</a>.</dd>
</dl>
<dl>
<dt>1529</dt>
<dd>30 Jewish men, women, and children are burned at the stake in&nbsp;<a title="Pezinok" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pezinok">Pezinok</a>.</dd>
</dl>
<dl>
<dt>1532</dt>
<dd><a title="Solomon Molcho" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solomon_Molcho">Solomon Molcho</a>&nbsp;is burned at the stake for refusing to return to Catholicism after reverting to Judaism.</dd>
</dl>
<dl>
<dt>1535</dt>
<dd>After Spanish troops capture&nbsp;<a title="Tunis" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tunis">Tunis</a>&nbsp;all the local Jews are sold into slavery.</dd>
</dl>
<dl>
<dt>1539</dt>
<dd>Jews are expelled from&nbsp;<a title="Nauheim" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nauheim">Nauheim</a>.</dd>
</dl>
<dl>
<dt>1539</dt>
<dd><a title="Katarzyna Weiglowa" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Katarzyna_Weiglowa">Katarzyna Weiglowa</a>, a&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Roman Catholic" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Roman_Catholic">Roman Catholic</a>&nbsp;woman from the&nbsp;<a title="Kingdom of Poland" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kingdom_of_Poland">Kingdom of Poland</a>&nbsp;who converted to Judaism is burned at the stake in Krak&oacute;w under the charge of apostasy for refusing to call&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Jesus Christ" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jesus_Christ">Jesus Christ</a>&nbsp;the&nbsp;<a title="Son of God" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Son_of_God">Son of God</a>. She is regarded by Jews (among others) as a&nbsp;<a title="Martyr" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Martyr">martyr</a>.</dd>
</dl>
<dl>
<dt>1540</dt>
<dd>All Jews are&nbsp;<a title="Exile" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Exile">banished</a>&nbsp;from&nbsp;<a title="Prague" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Prague">Prague</a>.</dd>
</dl>
<dl>
<dt>1542</dt>
<dd>Moses Fishel of Cracow is accused of proselytizing and dies a martyr.</dd>
</dl>
<dl>
<dt>1543</dt>
<dd>Jews are exiled from&nbsp;<a title="Basel" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Basel">Basel</a>.</dd>
</dl>
<dl>
<dt>1543</dt>
<dd>Jeronimo Diaz, a New Christian physician, is burned at the stake for holding heretical opinions in Goa, India.</dd>
</dl>
<div class="thumb tright">&nbsp;</div>
<dl>
<dt>1543</dt>
<dd>In his pamphlet&nbsp;<em><a title="On the Jews and Their Lies" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/On_the_Jews_and_Their_Lies">On the Jews and Their Lies</a></em>&nbsp;Martin Luther advocates an eight-point plan to get rid of the Jews as a distinct group either by&nbsp;<a title="Religious conversion" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Religious_conversion">religious conversion</a>&nbsp;or by expulsion:</dd>
<dd>"...set fire to their synagogues or schools..."</dd>
<dd>"...their houses also be razed and destroyed..."</dd>
<dd>"...their prayer books and Talmudic writings... be taken from them..."</dd>
<dd>"...their rabbis be forbidden to teach henceforth on pain of loss of life and limb..."</dd>
<dd>"...safe-conduct on the highways be abolished completely for the Jews..."</dd>
<dd>"...usury be prohibited to them, and that all cash and treasure of silver and gold be taken from them..." and "Such money should now be used in ... the following [way]... Whenever a Jew is sincerely converted, he should be handed [certain amount]..."</dd>
<dd>"...young, strong Jews and Jewesses [should]... earn their bread in the sweat of their brow..."</dd>
<dd>"If we wish to wash our hands of the Jews' blasphemy and not share in their guilt, we have to part company with them. They must be driven from our country" and "we must drive them out like mad dogs."</dd>
</dl>
<dl>
<dd>Luther "got the Jews expelled from Saxony in 1537, and in the 1540s he drove them from many German towns; he tried unsuccessfully to get the&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="John Frederick, Elector of Saxony" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/John_Frederick,_Elector_of_Saxony">elector</a>&nbsp;to expel them from Brandenburg in 1543. His followers continued to agitate against the Jews there: they sacked the Berlin synagogue in 1572 and the following year finally got their way, the Jews being banned from the entire country."</dd>
</dl>
<dl>
<dt>1546</dt>
<dd>Martin Luther's sermon&nbsp;<em>Admonition against the Jews</em>&nbsp;contains accusations of ritual murder, black magic, and poisoning of wells. Luther recognizes no obligation to protect the Jews.</dd>
</dl>
<dl>
<dt>1547</dt>
<dd><a title="Ivan the Terrible" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ivan_the_Terrible">Ivan the Terrible</a>&nbsp;becomes ruler of Russia and refuses to allow Jews to live in or even enter his kingdom because they "bring about great evil" (quoting his response to request by Polish king&nbsp;<a title="Sigismund II Augustus" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sigismund_II_Augustus">Sigismund II</a>).</dd>
</dl>
<dl>
<dt>1547</dt>
<dd>10 out of the 30 Jews living in&nbsp;<a title="Asolo" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Asolo">Asolo</a>&nbsp;are killed and their houses are robbed.</dd>
</dl>
<dl>
<dt>1550</dt>
<dd>Dr. Joseph Hacohen is chased out of&nbsp;<a title="Genoa" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Genoa">Genoa</a>&nbsp;for practicing medicine; soon all Jews are expelled.</dd>
</dl>
<dl>
<dt>1553</dt>
<dd><a title="Pope Julius III" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pope_Julius_III">Pope Julius III</a>&nbsp;forbids Talmud printing and orders burning of any copy found. Rome's Inquisitor-General, Cardinal Carafa (later&nbsp;<a title="Pope Paul IV" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pope_Paul_IV">Pope Paul IV</a>) has Talmud publicly burnt in Rome on Rosh Hashanah, starting a wave of Talmud burning throughout Italy. About 12,000 copies were destroyed.</dd>
</dl>
<dl>
<dt>1554</dt>
<dd><a class="new" title="Cornelio da Montalcino (page does not exist)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Cornelio_da_Montalcino&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1">Cornelio da Montalcino</a>, a&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Franciscan" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Franciscan">Franciscan</a>&nbsp;Friar who converted to Judaism, is burned alive in Rome.</dd>
</dl>
<dl>
<dt>1555</dt>
<dd>In&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Papal Bull" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Papal_Bull">Papal Bull</a>&nbsp;<em><a title="Cum nimis absurdum" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cum_nimis_absurdum">Cum nimis absurdum</a></em>, Pope Paul IV writes: "It appears utterly absurd and impermissible that the Jews, whom God has condemned to eternal slavery for their guilt, should enjoy our Christian love." He renews anti-Jewish legislation and installs a locked nightly ghetto in Rome. The Bull also forces Jewish males to wear a&nbsp;<a title="Yellow badge" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Yellow_badge">yellow hat</a>, females &ndash;&nbsp;<a title="Yellow badge" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Yellow_badge">yellow kerchief</a>. Owning real estate or practicing medicine on Christians is forbidden. It also limits Jewish communities to only one synagogue.</dd>
</dl>
<dl>
<dt>1555</dt>
<dd>The&nbsp;<a title="History of the Jews in Ancona" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/History_of_the_Jews_in_Ancona#Martyrs_of_1555">Martyrs of 1555</a>. 25 Jews in Ancona are hung or burned at the stake for refusing to convert to Christianity as a result of Pope Paul IV's Bull of 1555.</dd>
</dl>
<dl>
<dt>1556</dt>
<dd>A rumor is sent around that a poor woman in Sokhachev named Dorothy sold Jews the holy wafer received by her during communion, and that it was stabbed until it bled. The Bishop of Khelm accuses the local Jews, and eventually three Jews along with Dorothy Lazhentzka are arrested, put on the rack, and sentenced to death on charges of&nbsp;<a title="Host desecration" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Host_desecration">host desecration</a>.&nbsp;They were burned at the stake. Before their death, the martyred Jews made a declaration:
<blockquote class="templatequote">
<p>"We have never stabbed the host, because we do not believe that the host is the Divine body, knowing that God has no body nor blood. We believe, as did our forefathers, that the Messiah is not God, but His messenger. We also know from experience that there can be no blood in flour."</p>
</blockquote>
</dd>
</dl>
<dl>
<dt>1557</dt>
<dd>Jews are temporarily banished from Prague.</dd>
</dl>
<dl>
<dt>1558</dt>
<dd><a title="Recanati" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Recanati">Recanati</a>, Italy: a baptized Jew Joseph Paul More enters synagogue on&nbsp;<a title="Yom Kippur" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Yom_Kippur">Yom Kippur</a>&nbsp;under the protection of&nbsp;<a title="Pope Paul IV" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pope_Paul_IV">Pope Paul IV</a>&nbsp;and tries to preach a conversion sermon. The congregation evicts him. Soon after, the Jews are expelled from Recanati.</dd>
</dl>
<dl>
<dt>1559</dt>
<dd>Pope Pius IV allows Talmud on conditions that it is printed by a Christian and the text is censored.</dd>
</dl>
<dl>
<dt>1560</dt>
<dd>The&nbsp;<a title="Goa Inquisition" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Goa_Inquisition">Goa Inquisition</a>&nbsp;begins.</dd>
</dl>
<dl>
<dt>1561</dt>
<dd><a title="Ferdinand I, Holy Roman Emperor" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ferdinand_I,_Holy_Roman_Emperor">Ferdinand I</a>&nbsp;takes an oath to expel the Jews. Mordechai Zemach runs to Rome and convinces Pope Pius IV to cancel the decree.</dd>
</dl>
<dl>
<dt>1563</dt>
<dd>Russian troops take&nbsp;<a title="Polotsk" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Polotsk">Polotsk</a>&nbsp;from&nbsp;<a title="Lithuania" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lithuania">Lithuania</a>, Jews are given ultimatum: embrace&nbsp;<a title="Russian Orthodox Church" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Russian_Orthodox_Church">Russian Orthodox Church</a>&nbsp;or die. Around 300 Jewish men, women and children were thrown into ice holes of&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Western Dvina" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Western_Dvina">Dvina</a>&nbsp;river.</dd>
</dl>
<dl>
<dt>1564</dt>
<dd><a title="Brest, Belarus" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Brest,_Belarus">Brest-Litovsk</a>: the son of a wealthy Jewish tax collector is accused of killing the family's Christian servant for ritual purposes. He is tortured and executed in line with the law. King&nbsp;<a title="Sigismund II Augustus" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sigismund_II_Augustus">Sigismund II</a>&nbsp;of Poland forbids future charges of ritual murder, calling them groundless.</dd>
</dl>
<dl>
<dt>1565</dt>
<dd>Jews are temporarily banished from Prague.</dd>
</dl>
<dl>
<dt>1566</dt>
<dd>Antonio Ghislieri elected and, as&nbsp;<a title="Pope Pius V" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pope_Pius_V">Pope Pius V</a>, reinstates the harsh anti-Jewish laws of Pope Paul IV. In 1569 he expels Jews dwelling outside of the ghettos of Rome, Ancona, and Avignon from the&nbsp;<a title="Papal States" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Papal_States">Papal States</a>, thus ensuring that they remain city-dwellers.</dd>
</dl>
<dl>
<dt>1567</dt>
<dd>Jews are allowed to live in France.</dd>
</dl>
<dl>
<dt>1569</dt>
<dd><a title="Pope Pius V" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pope_Pius_V">Pope Pius V</a>&nbsp;expels all the Jews of&nbsp;<a title="Bologna" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bologna">Bologna</a>. He then gave their cemetery away and commended all Jewish gravestones to be destroyed.</dd>
</dl>
<dl>
<dt>1569</dt>
<dd><a title="Pope Pius V" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pope_Pius_V">Pope Pius V</a>&nbsp;issues the Bull&nbsp;<em>Hebraeorum gens sola</em>&nbsp;which orders the expulsion of all Jews who refuse to convert.</dd>
</dl>
<dl>
<dt>1571</dt>
<dd>Jews in&nbsp;<a title="Berlin" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Berlin">Berlin</a>&nbsp;are forced to leave and their property is confiscated.</dd>
</dl>
<dl>
<dt>1571</dt>
<dd>The&nbsp;<a title="Mexican Inquisition" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mexican_Inquisition">Mexican Inquisition</a>&nbsp;begins.</dd>
</dl>
<dl>
<dt>1574</dt>
<dd>First&nbsp;<a title="Auto-da-f&eacute;" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Auto-da-f%C3%A9">auto-da-f&eacute;</a>&nbsp;in Mexico.</dd>
</dl>
<dl>
<dt>1581</dt>
<dd><a title="Pope Gregory XIII" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pope_Gregory_XIII">Pope Gregory XIII</a>&nbsp;issues a Bull which prohibits the use of Jewish doctors.</dd>
</dl>
<dl>
<dt>1583</dt>
<dd>Three Portuguese&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Conversos" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Conversos">conversos</a>&nbsp;are burned at the stake in&nbsp;<a title="Rome" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Rome">Rome</a>.</dd>
</dl>
<dl>
<dt>1586</dt>
<dd><a title="Pope Sixtus V" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pope_Sixtus_V">Pope Sixtus V</a>&nbsp;forbids printing of the Talmud.</dd>
</dl>
<dl>
<dt>1590</dt>
<dd>Jewish quarter of&nbsp;<a title="Mikulov" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mikulov">Mikulov</a>&nbsp;(Nikolsburg) burns to ground and 15 people die while Christians watch or pillage.&nbsp;<a title="Philip II of Spain" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Philip_II_of_Spain">King Philip II of Spain</a>&nbsp;orders expulsion of Jews from&nbsp;<a title="Lombardy" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lombardy">Lombardy</a>. His order is ignored by local authorities until 1597, when 72 Jewish families are forced into exile.</dd>
</dl>
<dl>
<dt>1591</dt>
<dd>Philip II, King of Spain, banished all Jews from the&nbsp;<a title="Duchy of Milan" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Duchy_of_Milan">duchy of Milan</a>.</dd>
</dl>
<dl>
<dt>1592</dt>
<dd>Esther Chiera is executed with one of her sons by the Sultan Murad III's calvary.</dd>
</dl>
<dl>
