<dt>1593</dt>
<dd><a title="Pope Clement VIII" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pope_Clement_VIII">Pope Clement VIII</a>&nbsp;confirms the Papal bull of Paul III that expels Jews from Papal states except ghettos in Rome and Ancona and issues&nbsp;<em>Caeca et obdurata</em>&nbsp;("Blind Obstinacy"): "All the world suffers from the usury of the Jews, their monopolies and deceit. ... Then as now Jews have to be reminded intermittently anew that they were enjoying rights in any country since they left Palestine and the Arabian desert, and subsequently their ethical and moral doctrines as well as their deeds rightly deserve to be exposed to criticism in whatever country they happen to live."</dd>
</dl>
<dl>
<dt>1593</dt>
<dd>At least 900 are expelled from&nbsp;<a title="Bologna" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bologna">Bologna</a>.</dd>
</dl>
<dl>
<dt>1595</dt>
<dd>10 people are accused of practicing Judaism in&nbsp;<a title="Lima" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lima">Lima</a>,&nbsp;<a title="Peru" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Peru">Peru</a>. Four of them are released and one named Francisco Rodr&iacute;guez, is burned alive.</dd>
</dl>
<dl>
<dt>1596</dt>
<dd><a title="Francisca Nu&ntilde;ez de Carabajal" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Francisca_Nu%C3%B1ez_de_Carabajal">Francisca Nu&ntilde;ez de Carabajal</a>&nbsp;was a&nbsp;<a title="Marrano" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marrano">Marrana</a>&nbsp;(Jewish convert to Christianity) in&nbsp;<a title="New Spain" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/New_Spain">New Spain</a>&nbsp;executed by the&nbsp;<a title="Mexican Inquisition" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mexican_Inquisition">Inquisition</a>&nbsp;for "<a title="Judaizers" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Judaizers">judaizing</a>" in 1596. One of her children, Isabel, in her twenties at the time, was tortured until she implicated the whole of the Carabajal family. The whole family was forced to confess and abjure at a public&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Auto de fe" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Auto_de_fe">auto-da-f&eacute;</a>, celebrated on Saturday, 24 February 1590. Luis de Carabajal the younger (one of Francisca's sons), along with Francisca and four of her daughters, was condemned to perpetual imprisonment, and another one of Francisca's sons, Baltasar, who had fled upon the first warning of danger, was, along with his deceased father Francisco Rodriguez de Matos, burnt in effigy. In January 1595, Francisca and her children were accused of a relapse into Judaism and convicted. During their imprisonment they were tempted to communicate with one another on Spanish pear seeds, on which they wrote touching messages of encouragement to remain true to their faith. At the resulting auto-da-f&eacute;, Francisca and her children Isabel, Catalina, Leonor, and Luis, died at the stake, together with Manuel Diaz, Beatriz Enriquez, Diego Enriquez, and Manuel de Lucena. Of her other children, Mariana, who lost her reason for a time, was tried and put to death at an auto-da-f&eacute; held in Mexico City on 25 March 1601; Anica, the youngest child, being "reconciled" at the same time.</dd>
</dl>
<dl>
<dt>1598</dt>
<dd>3 Jews in Lublin are brutally tortured and executed by quartering, after a Christian boy is found in a nearby swamp.</dd>
</dl>
<h2><span id="Seventeenth_century" class="mw-headline">Seventeenth century</span></h2>
<dl>
<dt>1600</dt>
<dd>14 Judaizers are punished in&nbsp;<a title="Lima" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lima">Lima</a>,&nbsp;<a title="Peru" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Peru">Peru</a>.</dd>
</dl>
<dl>
<dt>1603</dt>
<dd><a class="new" title="Frei Diogo da Assumpc&atilde;o (page does not exist)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Frei_Diogo_da_Assumpc%C3%A3o&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1">Frei Diogo da Assumpc&atilde;o</a>, a partly Jewish friar who embraced Judaism, burned alive in&nbsp;<a title="Lisbon" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lisbon">Lisbon</a>.</dd>
</dl>
<dl>
<dt>1605</dt>
<dd>16 Judaizers are arrested in&nbsp;<a title="Lima" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lima">Lima</a>,&nbsp;<a title="Peru" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Peru">Peru</a>.</dd>
</dl>
<dl>
<dt>1608</dt>
<dd>The&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Jesuit order" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jesuit_order">Jesuit order</a>&nbsp;forbids admission to anyone descended from Jews to the fifth generation, a restriction lifted in the 20th century. Three years later&nbsp;<a title="Pope Paul V" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pope_Paul_V">Pope Paul V</a>&nbsp;applies the rule throughout the Church, but his successor revokes it.</dd>
</dl>
<dl>
<dt>1612</dt>
<dd>The&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Senate of Hamburg" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Senate_of_Hamburg">Hamburg Senate</a>&nbsp;decides to officially allow Jews to live in&nbsp;<a title="Hamburg" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hamburg">Hamburg</a>&nbsp;on the condition there is no public worship.</dd>
</dl>
<div class="thumb tright">&nbsp;</div>
<dl>
<dt>1614</dt>
<dd>Vincent Fettmilch, who called himself the "new&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Haman (Judaism)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Haman_(Judaism)">Haman</a>&nbsp;of the Jews", leads a raid on&nbsp;<a title="Frankfurt" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Frankfurt">Frankfurt</a>&nbsp;synagogue that turned into an attack which destroyed the whole community.</dd>
</dl>
<dl>
<dt>1615</dt>
<dd>King&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Louis XIII of France" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Louis_XIII_of_France">Louis XIII of France</a>&nbsp;decrees that all Jews must leave the country within one month on pain of death.</dd>
</dl>
<dl>
<dt>1615</dt>
<dd>The Guild led by Dr. Chemnitz, "non-violently" forced the Jews from&nbsp;<a title="Worms, Germany" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Worms,_Germany">Worms</a>.</dd>
</dl>
<dl>
<dt>1616</dt>
<dd>Jesuits arrive in&nbsp;<a title="Grodno" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Grodno">Grodno</a>&nbsp;and accuse the Jews of host desecration and blood libel.</dd>
</dl>
<dl>
<dt>1618</dt>
<dd>Anti-semitic pamphlet&nbsp;<a title="Mirror of the Polish Crown" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mirror_of_the_Polish_Crown">Mirror of the Polish Crown</a>&nbsp;is published by professor&nbsp;<a title="Sebastian Miczyński" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sebastian_Miczy%C5%84ski">Sebastian Miczyński</a>. It accuses the Jews of murder, sacrileges, witchcraft, and urges their expulsion. It would go on to inspire anti-Jewish riots across Poland.</dd>
</dl>
<dl>
<dt>1619</dt>
<dd>Shah Abbasi of the Persian Sufi Dynasty increases persecution against the Jews, forcing many to outwardly practice Islam. Many keep practicing Judaism in secret.</dd>
</dl>
<dl>
<dt>1622</dt>
<dd><a class="mw-redirect" title="King Christian IV" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/King_Christian_IV">King Christian IV</a>&nbsp;invites Jews to come and live in Denmark.</dd>
</dl>
<dl>
<dt>1624</dt>
<dd><a title="Ghetto" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ghetto">Ghetto</a>&nbsp;established in&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Ferrara, Italy" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ferrara,_Italy">Ferrara, Italy</a>.</dd>
</dl>
<dl>
<dt>1624</dt>
<dd>Christian theologian Antonio Homem is burned at the stake for pursuing Judaism.</dd>
</dl>
<dl>
<dt>1625</dt>
<dd><a title="History of the Jews in Vienna" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/History_of_the_Jews_in_Vienna">Jews of Vienna</a>&nbsp;forced to live in a ghetto in&nbsp;<a title="Leopoldstadt" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Leopoldstadt">Leopoldstadt</a>.</dd>
</dl>
<dl>
<dt>1628</dt>
<dd><a class="mw-redirect" title="Roman Jews" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Roman_Jews">Roman Jewish</a>&nbsp;mistress of the son of the duke of Parma is burned alive.</dd>
</dl>
<dl>
<dt>1630</dt>
<dd>Jewish merchant Moses the Braider is burned alive after being accused of&nbsp;<a title="Host desecration" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Host_desecration">host desecration</a>.</dd>
</dl>
<dl>
<dt>1631</dt>
<dd>Due to awful conditions in the Jewish Ghetto of&nbsp;<a title="Padua" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Padua">Padua</a>, 421 out of the 721 Jews living in the ghetto perish.</dd>
</dl>
<dl>
<dt>1632</dt>
<dd>King&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Ladislaus IV of Poland" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ladislaus_IV_of_Poland">Ladislaus IV of Poland</a>&nbsp;forbids&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Antisemitic" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Antisemitic">antisemitic</a>&nbsp;books and printings.</dd>
</dl>
<dl>
<dt>1632</dt>
<dd>Shortly after Miguel Rodriguez is discovered holding onto Jewish rites, an&nbsp;<a title="Auto-da-f&eacute;" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Auto-da-f%C3%A9">Auto-da-f&eacute;</a>&nbsp;is held in the presence of the King and Queen. Miguel and his wife Isabel Alvarez, and 5 others are burned alive publicly.</dd>
</dl>
<dl>
<dt>1632, 20 April</dt>
<dd>Jewish-convert and martyr&nbsp;<a title="Nicolas Antoine" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nicolas_Antoine">Nicolas Antoine</a>&nbsp;is burned at the stake for heresy.</dd>
</dl>
<dl>
<dt>1633</dt>
<dd>Jews are banned from&nbsp;<a title="Radom" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Radom">Radom</a>.</dd>
</dl>
<dl>
<dt>1635</dt>
<dd><a title="Pogrom" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pogrom">Anti-Jewish riots</a>&nbsp;take place in&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Vilna" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vilna">Vilna</a>.</dd>
</dl>
<dl>
<dt>1637</dt>
<dd>Four Jews are publicly tortured and executed in&nbsp;<a title="Krak&oacute;w" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Krak%C3%B3w">Krak&oacute;w</a>.</dd>
</dl>
<dl>
<dt>1639</dt>
<dd>Over 60 Judaizers are burned at the stake at an&nbsp;<a title="Auto-da-f&eacute;" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Auto-da-f%C3%A9">Auto-da-f&eacute;</a>&nbsp;in&nbsp;<a title="Lima" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lima">Lima</a>,&nbsp;<a title="Peru" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Peru">Peru</a>. Among those martyred was physician&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Francisco Maldonado de Silva" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Francisco_Maldonado_de_Silva">Francisco Maldonado de Silva</a>.</dd>
</dl>
<dl>
<dt>1639</dt>
<dd>Two&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Roman Jews" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Roman_Jews">Roman Jewish</a>&nbsp;children are forcibly baptized by&nbsp;<a title="Pope Urban VIII" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pope_Urban_VIII">Pope Urban VIII</a>.</dd>
</dl>
<dl>
<dt>1639</dt>
<dd>Jews of Lenchitza are accused of ritual murder after a young child is found dead in the woods. The blame falls on the Jews after a local gentile named Foma confesses to the crime then says he had been coerced into doing it by the Jews. Despite the lack of evidence, two Jewish elders named Meyer and Lazar are arrested and tortured, and eventually quartered publicly.</dd>
</dl>
<dl>
<dt>1644</dt>
<dd>Jewish martyr Judah the Believer is burned at the stake as he recites prayers in Hebrew.</dd>
</dl>
<dl>
<dt>1647</dt>
<dd>Jewish martyr&nbsp;<a title="Isaac de Castro Tartas" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Isaac_de_Castro_Tartas">Isaac de Castro Tartas</a>&nbsp;is burned at the stake while he recites the&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Shema" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Shema">Shema</a>&nbsp;along with 6 other Jews.</dd>
</dl>
<dl>
<dt>1648&ndash;1655</dt>
<dd>The&nbsp;<a title="Ukraine" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ukraine">Ukrainian</a>&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Cossack" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cossack">Cossacks</a>&nbsp;led by&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Bohdan Chmielnicki" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bohdan_Chmielnicki">Bohdan Chmielnicki</a>&nbsp;massacre about 100,000 Jews and similar number of&nbsp;<a title="Poland" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Poland">Polish</a>&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Nobles" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nobles">nobles</a>, 300 Jewish communities destroyed.</dd>
</dl>
<dl>
<dt>1649</dt>
<dd>Largest&nbsp;<a title="Auto-da-f&eacute;" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Auto-da-f%C3%A9">Auto-da-f&eacute;</a>&nbsp;in the New World. 109 victims, 13 were burned alive and 57 in effigy.</dd>
</dl>
<dl>
<dt>1655</dt>
<dd><a title="Oliver Cromwell" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Oliver_Cromwell">Oliver Cromwell</a>&nbsp;readmits Jews to England.</dd>
</dl>
<dl>
<dt>1656</dt>
<dd>All Jews are expelled from&nbsp;<a title="Isfahan" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Isfahan">Isfahan</a>&nbsp;because of the common belief of their impurity. The ones who don't are&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Forced to convert to Islam" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Forced_to_convert_to_Islam">forced to convert to Islam</a>.</dd>
</dl>
<dl>
<dt>1657&ndash;1662</dt>
<dd>Jews throughout Iran (including 7,000 in Kashan alone) are forced to convert to Islam as a result of persecutions by&nbsp;<a title="Abbas II of Persia" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Abbas_II_of_Persia">Abbas II of Persia</a>.</dd>
</dl>
<dl>
<dt>1661</dt>
<dd>Sephardic poet&nbsp;<a title="Antonio Enr&iacute;quez G&oacute;mez" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Antonio_Enr%C3%ADquez_G%C3%B3mez">Antonio Enr&iacute;quez G&oacute;mez</a>&nbsp;is publicly burned in effigy in&nbsp;<a title="Seville" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Seville">Seville</a>.</dd>
</dl>
<dl>
<dt>1663</dt>
<dd>Two&nbsp;<a title="Christians" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Christians">Christian</a>&nbsp;<a title="Janissaries" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Janissaries">Janissaries</a>&nbsp;accuse the&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Turkish Jews" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Turkish_Jews">Jews of Istanbul</a>&nbsp;of killing a child who had actually been killed by his own father. After killing his own son, he threw his body onto the Jewish quarter in order to implicate the Jews in the crime. Once the Grand Vizier learned the facts of the case from his spies stationed in the Greek quarter, he informed the Sultan and the Janissaries were put to death. 20 Jews were killed in total by the Greek mobs.</dd>
</dl>
<dl>
<dt>1664 May</dt>
<dd>Jews of&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Lemberg" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lemberg">Lemberg</a>&nbsp;(now&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Lvov" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lvov">Lvov</a>) ghetto organize self-defense against impending assault by students of Jesuit seminary and Cathedral school. The militia sent by the officials to restore order, instead joined the attackers. About 100 Jews killed.</dd>
</dl>
<dl>
<dt>1669</dt>
<dd>The majority of Jews in&nbsp;<a title="Oran" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Oran">Oran</a>&nbsp;are expelled.</dd>
</dl>
<dl>
<dt>1670</dt>
<dd>Jews expelled from&nbsp;<a title="Vienna" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vienna">Vienna</a>.</dd>
</dl>
<dl>
<dt>1670</dt>
<dd><a title="Raphael Levy" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Raphael_Levy">Raphael Levy</a>&nbsp;is burned at the stake over&nbsp;<a title="Blood libel" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Blood_libel">blood libel</a>. After being offered a chance to convert and live, he declared that he had lived a Jew and would die a Jew.</dd>
</dl>
<dl>
<dt>1679</dt>
<dd>The&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Exile of Mawza" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Exile_of_Mawza">Exile of Mawza</a>. It is considered the single most traumatic event experienced collectively by the&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Jews of Yemen" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jews_of_Yemen">Jews of Yemen</a>. All Jews living in nearly all cities and towns throughout Yemen were banished by decree of the king, Imām al-Mahdi Ahmad, and sent to a dry and barren region of the country named Mawza to withstand their fate or to die. Only a few communities who lived in the far eastern quarters of Yemen were spared this fate by virtue of their Arab patrons who refused to obey the King's orders. Many would die along the route and while confined to the hot and arid conditions of this forbidding terrain.</dd>
</dl>
<dl>
<dt>1680</dt>
<dd><a title="Auto-da-f&eacute;" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Auto-da-f%C3%A9">Auto-da-f&eacute;</a>&nbsp;in Madrid.</dd>
</dl>
<dl>
<dt>1681</dt>
<dd>Mob attacks against Jews in&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Vilna" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vilna">Vilna</a>. It was condemned by King John Sobieski, who ordered the punishment of the guilty.</dd>
</dl>
<dl>
<dt>1682</dt>
<dd>Largest trial against alleged Judaizers in&nbsp;<a title="Lisbon" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lisbon">Lisbon</a>,&nbsp;<a title="Portugal" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Portugal">Portugal</a>. 117 were tried in 3 days.</dd>
</dl>
<dl>
<dt>1683</dt>
<dd>Hungarian rebels known as&nbsp;<a title="Kuruc" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kuruc">Kuruc</a>&nbsp;rushes into the town of&nbsp;<a title="Uhersk&yacute; Brod" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Uhersk%C3%BD_Brod">Uhersk&yacute; Brod</a>, massacring the majority of its Jewish inhabitants. Most of the victims were recent refugees who were expelled from Vienna in 1670. One of the Hebrews killed by the mob was Jewish historian&nbsp;<a title="Nathan ben Moses Hannover" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nathan_ben_Moses_Hannover">Nathan ben Moses Hannover</a>, who was a survivor of the&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Chmielnicki massacres" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Chmielnicki_massacres">Chmielnicki massacres</a>. Most of the survivors fled to Upper Hungary.</dd>
</dl>
<dl>
<dt>1684</dt>
<dd>Attack on the Jewish ghetto of&nbsp;<a title="Buda" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Buda">Buda</a>.</dd>
</dl>
<dl>
<dt>1686</dt>
<dd>Only 500 Jews survive after Austrian sieged the city of&nbsp;<a title="Buda" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Buda">Buda</a>. Half of them are sold into slavery.<sup id="cite_ref-152" class="reference"></sup></dd>
</dl>
<dl>
<dt>1689</dt>
<dd><a title="Worms, Germany" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Worms,_Germany">Worms</a>&nbsp;is invaded by the French and the Jewish quarter is reduced to ashes.</dd>
</dl>
<dl>
<dt>1689</dt>
<dd>The Jewish Ghetto of&nbsp;<a title="Prague" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Prague">Prague</a>&nbsp;is destroyed by French troops. After it was over 318 houses, 11 synagogues, and 150 Jews were dead.</dd>
</dl>
<dl>
<dt>1691</dt>
<dd>219 people are convicted of being Jewish in&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Palma, Majorca" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Palma,_Majorca">Palma, Majorca</a>. 37 of them are burned to death. Among those martyred is Raphael and his sister Catalina Benito, who although declaring she wanted to live, jumped right into the flames rather than to be baptized.<sup id="cite_ref-155" class="reference"></sup></dd>
</dl>
<dl>
<dt>1696</dt>
<dd>A number of&nbsp;<a title="Converso" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Converso">Converso</a>&nbsp;Jews are burned alive in&nbsp;<a title="&Eacute;vora" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/%C3%89vora">&Eacute;vora</a>,&nbsp;<a title="Portugal" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Portugal">Portugal</a>.</dd>
</dl>
<dl>
<dt>1698</dt>
<dd>A female child is found dead at a church in Sandomierz. The mother of the child first said she placed her body in the church because she could not afford a burial, but after torture accused the Jewish leader Aaron Berek of the local community of murdering her daughter. The mother and Berek were sentenced the death.</dd>
</dl>
<dl>
<dt>1699</dt>
<dd>A mob attacks the Jewish Quarter of&nbsp;<a title="Bamberg" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bamberg">Bamberg</a>&nbsp;but runs away after one Jew stops them by pouring baskets of ripe plums on the attackers. The event is still commemorated on the 29th of Nisan as the&nbsp;<em>Zwetschgen-Ta&rsquo;anit</em>&nbsp;(Prune-Fest).</dd>
</dl>
<h2><span id="Eighteenth_century" class="mw-headline">Eighteenth century</span></h2>
<dl>
<dt>1703</dt>
<dd>The Aleinu prayer is prohibited in most of Germany.</dd>
</dl>
<dl>
<dt>1706</dt>
<dd>After a plague hits&nbsp;<a title="Algeria" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Algeria">Algeria</a>&nbsp;which pushes the Jewish community into poverty, the local ruler decides the plague was caused by the Jews and orders their expulsion. Property is confiscated, synagogues are destroyed, until a sum is paid which further impoverishes the Jews of Algiers.</dd>
</dl>
<dl>
<dt>1711</dt>
<dd><a title="Johann Andreas Eisenmenger" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Johann_Andreas_Eisenmenger">Johann Andreas Eisenmenger</a>&nbsp;writes his&nbsp;<em>Entdecktes Judenthum</em>&nbsp;("Judaism Unmasked"), a work denouncing&nbsp;<a title="Judaism" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Judaism">Judaism</a>&nbsp;and which had a formative influence on modern antisemitic polemics.</dd>
</dl>
<dl>
<dt>1712</dt>
<dd><a title="Blood libel" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Blood_libel">Blood libel</a>&nbsp;in&nbsp;<a title="Sandomierz" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sandomierz">Sandomierz</a>&nbsp;and expulsion of the town's Jews.</dd>
</dl>
<dl>
<dt>1715</dt>
<dd>Elector Max Emanuel orders the deportation of all Jews living in Bavaria.</dd>
</dl>
<dl>
<dt>1717</dt>
<dd>All Jews living in&nbsp;<a title="Gibraltar" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gibraltar">Gibraltar</a>&nbsp;are expelled.</dd>
</dl>
<dl>
<dt>1718</dt>
<dd>The last Jews of Carniola, Styria and Carinthia are expelled.</dd>
</dl>
<dl>
<dt>1720</dt>
<dd>Arab creditors set fire to an Ashkenazi synagogue, fed up with debts. Ashkenazic Jews are banned from Jerusalem along with anyone who looks like an Ashkenazi Jew. Some Ashkenazim dressed up like Sephardic Jews in order to fool the authorities.</dd>
</dl>
<dl>
<dt>1721</dt>
<dd><a title="Maria Barbara Carillo" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Maria_Barbara_Carillo">Maria Barbara Carillo</a>&nbsp;was&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Burned at the stake" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Burned_at_the_stake">burned at the stake</a>&nbsp;for heresy during the&nbsp;<a title="Spanish Inquisition" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Spanish_Inquisition">Spanish Inquisition</a>. She was executed at the age of 95 or 96&nbsp;and is the oldest person known to have been executed at the instigation of the Inquisition.<sup id="cite_ref-162" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_antisemitism#cite_note-162">[162]</a></sup>&nbsp;Carillo was sentenced to death for heresy for returning to her faith in Judaism.</dd>
</dl>
<dl>
<dt>1724</dt>
<dd>Jews of&nbsp;<a title="Radom" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Radom">Radom</a>&nbsp;are exiled.</dd>
</dl>
<dl>
<dt>1727</dt>
<dd>Edict of&nbsp;<a title="Catherine I of Russia" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Catherine_I_of_Russia">Catherine I of Russia</a>: "The Jews... who are found in Ukraine and in other Russian provinces are to be expelled at once beyond the frontiers of Russia."</dd>
</dl>
<dl>
<dt>1734</dt>
<dd>1736: The&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Haidamaks" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Haidamaks">Haidamaks</a>, paramilitary bands in Polish Ukraine, attack Jews.</dd>
</dl>
<dl>
<dt>1736</dt>
<dd><a title="Ana de Castro" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ana_de_Castro">Mar&iacute;a Francisca Ana de Castro</a>, called&nbsp;<em>La bella toledana</em>, a Spanish immigrant to Peru, was arrested in 1726, accused of "judaizing" (being a practicing Jew). She was burned at the stake after an&nbsp;<em><a class="mw-redirect" title="Auto de fe" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Auto_de_fe">auto de fe</a></em>&nbsp;in 1736. This event was a major spectacle in Lima, but it raised questions about possible irregular procedures and corruption within the&nbsp;<a title="Inquisition" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Inquisition">Inquisition</a>.</dd>
</dl>
<dl>
<dt>1737</dt>
<dd>Blood libel in&nbsp;<a title="Jarosław" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jaros%C5%82aw">Jarosław</a>&nbsp;leads to Jews being tortured and others being put to death.</dd>
</dl>
<dl>
<dt>1742</dt>
<dd><a title="Elizabeth of Russia" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Elizabeth_of_Russia">Elizabeth of Russia</a>&nbsp;issues a decree of expulsion of all the Jews out of&nbsp;<a title="Russian Empire" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Russian_Empire">Russian Empire</a>. Her resolution to the Senate's appeal regarding harm to the trade: "I don't desire any profits from the enemies of Christ". One of the deportees is Antonio Ribera Sanchez, her own personal physician and the head of army's medical dept.</dd>
</dl>
<dl>
<dt>1743</dt>
<dd>The Russians gain control of&nbsp;<a title="Riga" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Riga">Riga</a>&nbsp;and all local Jews are expelled.</dd>
</dl>
<dl>
<dt>1744</dt>
<dd><a class="mw-redirect" title="Frederick II of Prussia" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Frederick_II_of_Prussia">Frederick II</a>&nbsp;The Great (a "heroic genius", according to Hitler) limits&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Breslau" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Breslau">Breslau</a>&nbsp;to ten "protected" Jewish families, on the grounds that otherwise they will "transform it into complete Jerusalem". He encourages this practice in other Prussian cities. In 1750 he issues&nbsp;<em>Revidiertes General Privilegium und Reglement vor die Judenschaft</em>: "protected" Jews had an alternative to "either abstain from marriage or leave Berlin" (Simon Dubnow).</dd>
</dl>
<dl>
<dt>1744</dt>
<dd>Archduchess of Austria&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Maria Theresa of Austria" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Maria_Theresa_of_Austria">Maria Theresa</a>&nbsp;orders: "... no Jew is to be tolerated in our inherited duchy of Bohemia" by the end of Feb. 1745. In December 1748 she reverses her position, on condition that Jews pay for readmission every ten years. This extortion was known as&nbsp;<em>malke-geld</em>&nbsp;(queen's money). In 1752 she introduces the law limiting each Jewish family to one son.</dd>
</dl>
<dl>
<dt>1746</dt>
<dd>The city of&nbsp;<a title="Radom" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Radom">Radom</a>&nbsp;bans Jews from entering.</dd>
</dl>
<dl>
<dt>1753</dt>
<dd>The Jewish community of&nbsp;<a title="Kaunas" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kaunas">Kaunas</a>&nbsp;is expelled.</dd>
</dl>
<dl>
<dt>1755</dt>
<dd>Jeronimo Jose Ramos, a merchant from&nbsp;<a title="Bragan&ccedil;a, Portugal" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bragan%C3%A7a,_Portugal">Bragan&ccedil;a, Portugal</a>, is burned at the stake for being secretly Jewish.</dd>
</dl>
<dl>
<dt>1761</dt>
<dd>Several Jews from&nbsp;<a title="Alsace" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Alsace">Alsace</a>&nbsp;are executed after being accused of&nbsp;<a title="Host desecration" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Host_desecration">host desecration</a>.</dd>
</dl>
<dl>
<dt>1761</dt>
<dd>The Jews of&nbsp;<a title="Kaunas" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kaunas">Kaunas</a>&nbsp;are expelled after anti-Jewish riots.</dd>
</dl>
<dl>
<dt>1762</dt>
<dd><a title="Rhode Island" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Rhode_Island">Rhode Island</a>&nbsp;refuses to grant Jews citizenship stating "no person who is not of the Christian religion can be admitted free to this colony."</dd>
</dl>
<dl>
<dt>1766</dt>
<dd>All but 6 Jews are expelled from&nbsp;<a title="Toruń" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Toru%C5%84">Toruń</a>.</dd>
</dl>
<dl>
<dt>1768</dt>
<dd><a class="mw-redirect" title="Haidamaks" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Haidamaks">Haidamaks</a>&nbsp;massacre the Jews of&nbsp;<a title="Uman" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Uman">Uman</a>,&nbsp;<a title="Ukraine" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ukraine">Ukraine</a>.</dd>
</dl>
<dl>
<dt>1775</dt>
<dd><a title="Pope Pius VI" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pope_Pius_VI">Pope Pius VI</a>&nbsp;issues a severe&nbsp;<em>Editto sopra gli ebrei</em>&nbsp;(Edict concerning the Jews). Previously lifted restrictions are reimposed, Judaism is suppressed.</dd>
</dl>
<dl>
<dt>1776</dt>
<dd>The&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Babylonian Jews" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Babylonian_Jews">Jewish community of Basra</a>&nbsp;is massacred.</dd>
</dl>
<dl>
<dt>1782</dt>
<dd><a title="Holy Roman Emperor" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Holy_Roman_Emperor">Holy Roman Emperor</a>&nbsp;<a title="Joseph II, Holy Roman Emperor" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Joseph_II,_Holy_Roman_Emperor">Joseph II</a>&nbsp;abolishes most of persecution practices in&nbsp;<em><a class="mw-redirect" title="Toleranzpatent" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Toleranzpatent">Toleranzpatent</a></em>&nbsp;on condition that&nbsp;<a title="Yiddish" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Yiddish">Yiddish</a>&nbsp;and&nbsp;<a title="Hebrew language" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hebrew_language">Hebrew</a>&nbsp;are eliminated from public records and judicial autonomy is annulled. Judaism is branded "quintessence of foolishness and nonsense".&nbsp;<a title="Moses Mendelssohn" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Moses_Mendelssohn">Moses Mendelssohn</a>&nbsp;writes: "Such a tolerance... is even more dangerous play in tolerance than open persecution".</dd>
</dl>
<dl>
<dt>1783</dt>
<dd>The&nbsp;<a title="Sultan" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sultan">Sultan</a>&nbsp;expels the&nbsp;<a title="Moroccan Jews" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Moroccan_Jews">Moroccan Jews</a>&nbsp;for failing to pay an exorbitant ransom.</dd>
</dl>
<dl>
<dt>1785</dt>
<dd>Ali Burzi Pasha murders hundreds of&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Libyan Jews" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Libyan_Jews">Libyan Jews</a>.</dd>
</dl>
<dl>
<dt>1786</dt>
<dd>Jews are expelled from&nbsp;<a title="Jeddah" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jeddah">Jeddah</a>, most of them flee to Yemen.</dd>
</dl>
<dl>
<dt>1790</dt>
<dd><a title="Yazid of Morocco" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Yazid_of_Morocco">Yazid</a>&nbsp;becomes the&nbsp;<a title="Sultan" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sultan">Sultan</a>&nbsp;of&nbsp;<a title="Morocco" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Morocco">Morocco</a>&nbsp;and immediately orders troops to massacre and plunder the Jewish quarter of&nbsp;<a title="T&eacute;touan" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/T%C3%A9touan">T&eacute;touan</a>.</dd>
</dl>
<dl>
<dt>1790</dt>
<dd>The&nbsp;<a title="Touro Synagogue" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Touro_Synagogue">Touro Synagogue</a>'s warden, Moses Seixas, wrote to&nbsp;<a title="George Washington" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/George_Washington">George Washington</a>, expressing his support for Washington's administration and good wishes for him. Washington sent a letter in response, which read in part:</dd>
</dl>
<blockquote class="templatequote">
<p>"... the Government of the United States ... gives to bigotry no sanction, to persecution no assistance. ... May the children of the Stock of Abraham, who dwell in this land, continue to merit and enjoy the good will of the other Inhabitants; while every one shall sit in safety under his own vine and figtree, and there shall be none to make him afraid. May the father of all mercies scatter light and not darkness in our paths, and make us all in our several vocations useful here, and in his own due time and way everlastingly happy."</p>
<div class="templatequotecite">&mdash;&thinsp;<cite>Letter of George Washington to the Hebrew Congregation in Newport, Rhode Island</cite></div>
</blockquote>
<p>There is an annual event reading Washington's letter, and speakers at the annual event have included Supreme Court Justices&nbsp;<a title="Ruth Bader Ginsburg" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ruth_Bader_Ginsburg">Ruth Bader Ginsburg</a>&nbsp;and&nbsp;<a title="Elena Kagan" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Elena_Kagan">Elena Kagan</a>;&nbsp;and&nbsp;<a title="Brown University" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Brown_University">Brown University</a>&nbsp;Presidents&nbsp;<a title="Ruth Simmons" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ruth_Simmons">Ruth Simmons</a>&nbsp;and&nbsp;<a title="Christina Paxson" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Christina_Paxson">Christina Paxson</a>.</p>
<dl>
<dt>1790, 20 May</dt>
<dd>Eleazer Solomon is quartered for the alleged murder of a Christian girl in&nbsp;<a title="Grodno" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Grodno">Grodno</a>.</dd>
</dl>
<dl>
<dt>1790&ndash;1792</dt>
<dd>Destruction of most of the Jewish communities of&nbsp;<a title="Morocco" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Morocco">Morocco</a>.</dd>
</dl>
<dl>
<dt>1791</dt>
<dd><a class="mw-redirect" title="Catherine II of Russia" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Catherine_II_of_Russia">Catherine II of Russia</a>&nbsp;confines Jews to the&nbsp;<a title="Pale of Settlement" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pale_of_Settlement">Pale of Settlement</a>&nbsp;and imposes them with double taxes.</dd>
</dl>
<dl>
<dt>1797</dt>
<dd><a title="Napoleon" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Napoleon">Napoleon</a>&nbsp;calls for the end of Jewish segregation, ghettoization and the denial of equal rights.</dd>
</dl>
<h2><span id="Nineteenth_century" class="mw-headline">Nineteenth century</span></h2>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
<h2><span id="1800s" class="mw-headline">1800s</span></h2>
<dl>
<dt>1805, June 29</dt>
<dd>200-500&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Algerian Jews" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Algerian_Jews">Algerian Jews</a>&nbsp;are massacred.</dd>
</dl>
<h2><span id="1810s" class="mw-headline">1810s</span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">&nbsp;</div>
<dl>
<dt>1811</dt>
<dd>Head of the Jewish community of&nbsp;<a title="Algiers" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Algiers">Algiers</a>&nbsp;<a title="David ben Joseph Coen Bakri" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/David_ben_Joseph_Coen_Bakri">David ben Joseph Coen Bakri</a>&nbsp;is decapitated by the&nbsp;<a title="Dey" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dey">Dey</a>&nbsp;Hadj Ali.</dd>
<dt>1815</dt>
<dd>Eight Jews are burned at the stake in&nbsp;<a title="Algiers" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Algiers">Algiers</a>.</dd>
<dt>1815</dt>
<dd><a title="Pope Pius VII" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pope_Pius_VII">Pope Pius VII</a>&nbsp;reestablishes the ghetto in Rome after the defeat of&nbsp;<a title="Napoleon" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Napoleon">Napoleon</a>.</dd>
<dt>1818</dt>
<dd>Turks from&nbsp;<a title="Algiers" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Algiers">Algiers</a>&nbsp;attack&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Constantine" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Constantine">Constantine</a>, massacre and pillage Jewish homes, and abduct 17 young Jewish girls whom they bring to their commander.</dd>
<dt>1819</dt>
<dd>A series of anti-Jewish riots in Germany that spread to several neighboring countries: Denmark,&nbsp;<a title="Latvia" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Latvia">Latvia</a>&nbsp;and&nbsp;<a title="Bohemia" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bohemia">Bohemia</a>&nbsp;known as&nbsp;<em><a title="Hep-Hep riots" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hep-Hep_riots">Hep-Hep riots</a></em>, from the derogatory rallying cry against the Jews in Germany.</dd>
</dl>
<h2><span id="1820s" class="mw-headline">1820s</span></h2>
<dl>
<dt>1827</dt>
<dd>Compulsory military service for the Jews of Russia: Jewish boys under 18 years of age, known as the&nbsp;<em><a title="Cantonist" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cantonist">Cantonists</a></em>, were placed in preparatory military training establishments for 25 years. Cantonists were encouraged and sometimes forced to baptize.</dd>
<dt>1829</dt>
<dd>The law in Canada requiring the oath "on my faith as a Christian" was amended in 1829 to provide for Jews to not take the oath.</dd>
</dl>
<h2><span id="1830s" class="mw-headline">1830s</span></h2>
<dl>
<dt>1830</dt>
<dd>The&nbsp;<a title="Persian Jews" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persian_Jews">Persian Jewish population</a>&nbsp;of&nbsp;<a title="Tabriz" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tabriz">Tabriz</a>,&nbsp;<a title="Iran" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Iran">Iran</a>&nbsp;is attacked by a mob, resulting in most of the Jewish community either being killed or fleeing.</dd>
<dt>1830</dt>
<dd>The&nbsp;<a title="Persian Jews" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persian_Jews">Jews of Shiraz</a>&nbsp;are forced to convert to Islam.</dd>
<dt>1831</dt>
<dd>The prominent French-Canadian politician&nbsp;<a title="Louis-Joseph Papineau" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Louis-Joseph_Papineau">Louis-Joseph Papineau</a>&nbsp;sponsored a law which granted full equivalent political rights to Jews in&nbsp;<a title="Lower Canada" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lower_Canada">Lower Canada</a>, twenty-seven years before anywhere else in the British Empire.</dd>
<dt>1832</dt>
<dd>Partly because of the work of&nbsp;<a title="Ezekiel Hart" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ezekiel_Hart">Ezekiel Hart</a>, a law was passed that guaranteed Jews the same political rights and freedoms as Christians in Canada.</dd>
<dt>1833</dt>
<dd><a title="Clemens Brentano" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Clemens_Brentano">Clemens Brentano</a>&nbsp;published&nbsp;<em>The Dolorous Passion of Our Lord Jesus Christ According to the Meditations of&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Anne Emmerich" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Anne_Emmerich">Anne Catherine Emmerich</a></em>. The "Dolorous Passion" is claimed to reveal a "clear antisemitic strain throughout",&nbsp;with Brentano writing that Emmerich believed that "Jews ... strangled Christian children and&nbsp;<a title="Blood libel" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Blood_libel">used their blood</a>&nbsp;for all sorts of suspicious and diabolical practices."</dd>
<dt>1834</dt>
<dd>The&nbsp;<a title="1834 looting of Safed" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1834_looting_of_Safed">1834 looting of Safed</a>&nbsp;was a month-long attack on the Jewish population of&nbsp;<a title="Safed" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Safed">Safed</a>&nbsp;by local Arab and Druze villagers. It was full of large scale looting, as well as the killing and raping of Jews and the destruction of many homes and synagogues. Before the attacks Jews made up over 50% of the population, but a lot of them fled to nearby cities which reduced their presence drastically.</dd>
<dt>1834</dt>
<dd><a title="La belle juive" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/La_belle_juive">Jewish heroine</a>&nbsp;and&nbsp;<a title="Martyr" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Martyr">martyr</a>&nbsp;<a title="Sol Hachuel" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sol_Hachuel">Sol Hachuel</a>&nbsp;is publicly decapitated at 17 years old in&nbsp;<a title="Fez" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fez">Fez</a>,&nbsp;<a title="Morocco" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Morocco">Morocco</a>. She is executed for refusing to convert to Islam.</dd>
<dt>1835</dt>
<dd>Oppressive constitution for the Jews issued by Czar&nbsp;<a title="Nicholas I of Russia" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nicholas_I_of_Russia">Nicholas I of Russia</a>.</dd>
<dt>1838</dt>
<dd>The&nbsp;<a title="1838 Druze attack on Safed" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1838_Druze_attack_on_Safed">1838 Druze attack on Safed</a>&nbsp;was a plunder of the Jewish community of&nbsp;<a title="Safed" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Safed">Safed</a>&nbsp;by the local Druze during the&nbsp;<a title="1838 Druze revolt" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1838_Druze_revolt">Druze revolt</a></dd>
<dt>1839</dt>
<dd>40+&nbsp;<a title="Persian Jews" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persian_Jews">Persian Jews</a>&nbsp;are killed and the entire Jewish community of&nbsp;<a title="Mashhad" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mashhad">Mashhad</a>&nbsp;is forced to convert to Islam in the&nbsp;<a title="Allahdad" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Allahdad">Allahdad</a>. A lot of them&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Crypto-Jews" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Crypto-Jews">practiced Judaism in secret</a>, which led to the&nbsp;<a title="Mashhadi Jews" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mashhadi_Jews">Mashhadi Jews</a>, whom today number in the thousands.</dd>
</dl>
<h2><span id="1840s" class="mw-headline">1840s</span></h2>
<dl>
<dt>1840</dt>
<dd>The&nbsp;<a title="Damascus affair" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Damascus_affair">Damascus affair</a>: false accusations cause arrests and atrocities, culminating in the seizure of sixty-three Jewish children and attacks on Jewish communities throughout the&nbsp;<a title="Middle East" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Middle_East">Middle East</a>.</dd>
<dt>1844</dt>
<dd><a title="Karl Marx" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Karl_Marx">Karl Marx</a>&nbsp;praises&nbsp;<a title="Bruno Bauer" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bruno_Bauer">Bruno Bauer</a>'s essays containing demands that the Jews abandon Judaism, and publishes his work&nbsp;<em><a title="On the Jewish Question" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/On_the_Jewish_Question">On the Jewish Question</a></em>: "What is the worldly cult of the Jew? Huckstering. What is his worldly god? Money... Money is the jealous God of Israel, besides which no other god may exist... The god of the Jews has been secularized and has become the god of this world", "In the final analysis, the emancipation of the Jews is the emancipation of mankind from Judaism." This probably led to the antisemitic feeling within communism.</dd>
</dl>
<h2><span id="1850s" class="mw-headline">1850s</span></h2>
<dl>
<dt>1850</dt>
<dd><em><a title="Das Judenthum in der Musik" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Das_Judenthum_in_der_Musik">Das Judenthum in der Musik</a></em>&nbsp;(<a title="German language" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/German_language">German</a>&nbsp;for "Jewishness in Music", but normally translated&nbsp;<em>Judaism in Music</em>; spelled after its first publications, according to modern German spelling practice, as &lsquo;Judentum&rsquo;), is an essay by&nbsp;<a title="Richard Wagner" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Richard_Wagner">Richard Wagner</a>&nbsp;which attacks Jews in general and the composers&nbsp;<a title="Giacomo Meyerbeer" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Giacomo_Meyerbeer">Giacomo Meyerbeer</a>&nbsp;and&nbsp;<a title="Felix Mendelssohn" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Felix_Mendelssohn">Felix Mendelssohn</a>&nbsp;in particular. It was published under a&nbsp;<a title="Pseudonym" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pseudonym">pseudonym</a>&nbsp;in the&nbsp;<em><a title="Neue Zeitschrift f&uuml;r Musik" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Neue_Zeitschrift_f%C3%BCr_Musik">Neue Zeitschrift f&uuml;r Musik</a></em>&nbsp;(<em>NZM</em>) of&nbsp;<a title="Leipzig" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Leipzig">Leipzig</a>&nbsp;in September 1850 and was reissued in a greatly expanded version under Wagner's name in 1869. It is regarded by some as an important landmark in the history of&nbsp;<a title="Germany" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Germany">German</a>&nbsp;antisemitism.</dd>
<dt>1853</dt>
<dd><a title="Blood libel" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Blood_libel">Blood libels</a>&nbsp;in&nbsp;<a title="Saratov" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Saratov">Saratov</a>&nbsp;and throughout Russia.</dd>
<dt>1858</dt>
<dd><a class="mw-redirect" title="Edgardo Mortara" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Edgardo_Mortara">Edgardo Mortara</a>, a six-year-old Jewish boy whom a maid had baptised during an illness, is taken from his parents in&nbsp;<a title="Bologna" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bologna">Bologna</a>, an episode which aroused universal indignation in liberal circles.</dd>
</dl>
<h2><span id="1860s" class="mw-headline">1860s</span></h2>
<dl>
<dt>1860</dt>
<dd>The Jews of&nbsp;<a title="Hamadan" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hamadan">Hamadan</a>&nbsp;are accused of mocking the Ta'zieh ceremonies for Imam Husain, several of them are fined and some have their ears and noses cut off as punishment.<sup id="cite_ref-6" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_antisemitism_in_the_19th_century#cite_note-6">[6]</a></sup></dd>
<dt>1862</dt>
<dd>During the&nbsp;<a title="American Civil War" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/American_Civil_War">American Civil War</a>&nbsp;<a title="Ulysses S. Grant" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ulysses_S._Grant">General Grant</a>&nbsp;issues&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="General Order № 11 (1862)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/General_Order_%E2%84%96_11_(1862)">General Order № 11 (1862)</a>, ordering all Jews out of his military district, suspecting them of pro-Confederate sympathy. President Lincoln directs him to rescind the order. Polish Jews are given equal rights. Old&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Privilege (legal ethics)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Privilege_(legal_ethics)">privileges</a>&nbsp;forbidding Jews to settle in some Polish cities are abolished.</dd>
<dt>1863</dt>
<dd>A Jew in&nbsp;<a title="Hamadan" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hamadan">Hamadan</a>&nbsp;is lynched by a Muslim mob, and many others are severely injured after being accused of insulting the Prophet Mohammad.</dd>
<dt>1864</dt>
<dd>At least 500&nbsp;<a title="Moroccan Jews" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Moroccan_Jews">Moroccan Jews</a>&nbsp;are massacred in&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Marrakech" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marrakech">Marrakech</a>&nbsp;and&nbsp;<a title="Fez" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fez">Fez</a>.</dd>
<dt>1866</dt>
<dd>The&nbsp;<a title="History of the Jews in Iran" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/History_of_the_Jews_in_Iran">Jews of Barforush</a>&nbsp;are forcibly converted to Islam. When they are allowed to revert to Judaism thanks to French and British ambassadors, a Muslim mob kills 18 Jews, burning two of them alive.<sup id="cite_ref-9" class="reference"></sup></dd>
<dt>1868</dt>
<dd><a class="mw-redirect" title="Samuel Bierfield" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Samuel_Bierfield">Samuel Bierfield</a>&nbsp;[?-15 August 1868] is believed to be the first Jew&nbsp;<a title="Lynching" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lynching">lynched</a>&nbsp;in the&nbsp;<a title="United States" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States">United States</a>. Bierfield and his&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="African-American" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/African-American">African-American</a>&nbsp;clerk, Lawrence Bowman, were apprehended in Bierfield's store in&nbsp;<a title="Franklin, Tennessee" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Franklin,_Tennessee">Franklin, Tennessee</a>&nbsp;and fatally shot by a group of masked men believed to belong to the&nbsp;<a title="Ku Klux Klan" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ku_Klux_Klan">Ku Klux Klan</a>, on 15 August 1868. No one was ever convicted of the crime, however.<sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"></sup></dd>
<dt>1869</dt>
<dd>18&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Tunisian Jews" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tunisian_Jews">Tunisian Jews</a>&nbsp;are killed in a pogrom and an Arab mob loots Jewish homes and stores, burns synagogues, on&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Jerba Island" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jerba_Island">Jerba Island</a>.</dd>
</dl>
<h2><span id="1870s" class="mw-headline">1870s</span></h2>
<dl>
<dt>1870</dt>
<dd>The 35,000&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Algerian Jews" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Algerian_Jews">Jews living in Algeria</a>&nbsp;are granted French citizenship as a result of the&nbsp;<a title="Cr&eacute;mieux Decree" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cr%C3%A9mieux_Decree">Cr&eacute;mieux Decree</a>. This leads to a rise of anti-Semitism in Algeria and across the Middle East.</dd>
<dt>1871</dt>
<dd>Speech of&nbsp;<a title="Pope Pius IX" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pope_Pius_IX">Pope Pius IX</a>&nbsp;in regard to Jews: "of these dogs, there are too many of them at present in Rome, and we hear them howling in the streets, and they are disturbing us in all places."</dd>
<dt>1873</dt>
<dd>The&nbsp;<a title="Southern Baptist Convention" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Southern_Baptist_Convention">Southern Baptist Convention</a>&nbsp;passed a "Resolution On Anti-Semitism" stating, "RESOLVED, That we do gratefully remember this day our unspeakable indebtedness to the seed of Abraham, and devoutly recognize their peculiar claims upon the sympathies and prayers of all Gentile Christians, and we hereby record our earnest desire to partake in the glorious work of hastening the day when the superscription of the Cross shall be the confession of all Israel 'Jesus of Nazareth, the King of the Jews'."</dd>
<dt>1875</dt>
<dd>20 Jews are killed by a Muslim mob in&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Demnat" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Demnat">Demnat</a>,&nbsp;<a title="Morocco" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Morocco">Morocco</a>.</dd>
<dt>1878</dt>
<dd><a title="Adolf Stoecker" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Adolf_Stoecker">Adolf Stoecker</a>, German antisemitic preacher and politician, founds the&nbsp;<em><a title="Christian Social Party (Germany)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Christian_Social_Party_(Germany)">Christian Social Party</a></em>, which marks the beginning of the political antisemitic movement in Germany.</dd>
<dt>1879</dt>
<dd>9 Jews in&nbsp;<a title="Kutaisi" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kutaisi">Kutaisi</a>&nbsp;are accused of ritual murder, and eventually are tried and found not guilty.</dd>
<dt>1879</dt>
<dd><a title="Heinrich von Treitschke" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Heinrich_von_Treitschke">Heinrich von Treitschke</a>, German historian and politician, justifies the antisemitic campaigns in Germany, bringing antisemitism into learned circles.</dd>
<dt>1879</dt>
<dd><a title="Wilhelm Marr" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wilhelm_Marr">Wilhelm Marr</a>&nbsp;coins the term&nbsp;<em><a class="mw-redirect" title="Anti-Semitism" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Anti-Semitism">Anti-Semitism</a></em>&nbsp;to distinguish himself from religious&nbsp;<em><a title="Anti-Judaism" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Anti-Judaism">Anti-Judaism</a></em>.</dd>
</dl>
<h2><span id="1880s" class="mw-headline">1880s</span></h2>
<dl>
<dt>1881</dt>
<dd><a title="Pogrom" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pogrom">Pogrom</a>&nbsp;against the Jews in&nbsp;<a title="Tlemcen" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tlemcen">Tlemcen</a>,&nbsp;<a title="Algeria" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Algeria">Algeria</a>.</dd>
<dt>1881</dt>
<dd>The German&nbsp;<a title="Reichstag (German Empire)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Reichstag_(German_Empire)">Reichstag</a>&nbsp;receives and rejects a petition with more than 250,000 signatures, and supported by the Kaiser's personal chaplain,&nbsp;<a title="Adolf Stoecker" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Adolf_Stoecker">Adolf Stoecker</a>, calling for the removal of Jews from public life.</dd>
<dt>1881</dt>
<dd><a title="Georg Ritter von Sch&ouml;nerer" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Georg_Ritter_von_Sch%C3%B6nerer">Georg Ritter von Sch&ouml;nerer</a>, a&nbsp;<a title="Pan-Germanism" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pan-Germanism">pan-German</a>&nbsp;Austrian leader and anti-Semite styles himself as "F&uuml;hrer" and he and his followers use the greeting "Heil!"&nbsp;</dd>
<dt>1881&ndash;1884</dt>
<dd><a title="Pogrom" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pogrom">Pogroms</a>&nbsp;sweep southern Russia, propelling mass Jewish emigration from the&nbsp;<a title="Pale of Settlement" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pale_of_Settlement">Pale of Settlement</a>: about 2&nbsp;million Russian Jews emigrated in period 1880&ndash;1924, many of them to the United States (until the&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="National Origins Quota of 1924" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/National_Origins_Quota_of_1924">National Origins Quota of 1924</a>&nbsp;and&nbsp;<a title="Immigration Act of 1924" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Immigration_Act_of_1924">Immigration Act of 1924</a>&nbsp;largely halted immigration to the U.S. from Eastern Europe and Russia). The Russian word "pogrom" becomes international.</dd>
<dt>1882</dt>
<dd>Jewish population of&nbsp;<a title="Algiers" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Algiers">Algiers</a>&nbsp;is attacked by a Muslim mob.</dd>
<dt>1882</dt>
<dd>The&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Tiszaeszl&aacute;r Affair" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tiszaeszl%C3%A1r_Affair">Tiszaeszl&aacute;r blood libel</a>&nbsp;in Hungary arouses public opinion throughout Europe.</dd>
<dt>1882</dt>
<dd>The&nbsp;<a class="new" title="International Anti-Jewish Congress (page does not exist)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=International_Anti-Jewish_Congress&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1">International Anti-Jewish Congress</a>, led by&nbsp;<a class="new" title="Adolph Stoeker (page does not exist)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Adolph_Stoeker&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1">Adolph Stoeker</a>, convenes at&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Dresden, Germany" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dresden,_Germany">Dresden, Germany</a>; it appeals to "the Government and Peoples of Christian Nations Threatened by Judaism" to expel "the Semitic race of Jews" from Europe.</dd>
<dt>1882</dt>
<dd>A series of "temporary laws" by Tsar&nbsp;<a title="Alexander III of Russia" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Alexander_III_of_Russia">Alexander III of Russia</a>&nbsp;(the&nbsp;<em><a title="May Laws" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/May_Laws">May Laws</a></em>), which adopted a systematic policy of discrimination, with the object of removing the Jews from their economic and public positions, in order to "cause one-third of the Jews to emigrate, one-third to accept baptism and one-third to starve" (according to a remark attributed to&nbsp;<a title="Konstantin Pobedonostsev" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Konstantin_Pobedonostsev">Konstantin Pobedonostsev</a>)</dd>
<dt>1887</dt>
<dd>Russia introduces measures to limit Jews access to education, known as the&nbsp;<em>quota</em>.</dd>
<dt>1891</dt>
<dd><a title="Blood libel" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Blood_libel">Blood libel</a>&nbsp;in Xanten, Germany.</dd>
</dl>
<h2><span id="1890s" class="mw-headline">1890s</span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">&nbsp;</div>
<dl>
<dt>1891</dt>
<dd>Expulsion of 20,000 Jews from&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Moscow, Russia" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Moscow,_Russia">Moscow, Russia</a>. The&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Congress of the United States" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Congress_of_the_United_States">Congress of the United States</a>&nbsp;eases immigration restrictions for Jews from the&nbsp;<a title="Russian Empire" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Russian_Empire">Russian Empire</a>. (Webster-Campster report)</dd>
<dt>1891</dt>
<dd>Leading Muslims in Jerusalem asked the Ottoman authorities in Constantinople to prohibit the entry of Jews arriving from Russia.</dd>
<dt>1892</dt>
<dd>Mulla Abdullah issues a&nbsp;<a title="Fatwa" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fatwa">fatwa</a>&nbsp;to kill all the Jews of&nbsp;<a title="Hamadan" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hamadan">Hamadan</a>&nbsp;if they refuse to abide by Jewish restrictions. The local&nbsp;<a title="Persian Jews" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persian_Jews">Persian Jews</a>&nbsp;were later ordered to become Muslims or face death.</dd>
<dt>1892</dt>
<dd>Two&nbsp;<a title="Persian Jews" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persian_Jews">Persian Jews</a>&nbsp;go out to sell merchandise and end up killed with all of their property stolen. Their relatives went out to search for the bodies and when they found them, they were killed by the same villagers. Even after many attempts to plea for their, the governor of&nbsp;<a title="Savojbolagh County" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Savojbolagh_County">Savojbolagh County</a>&nbsp;paid them no mind.</dd>
<dt>1892</dt>
<dd><a title="Justinas Pranaitis" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Justinas_Pranaitis">Justinas Bonaventure Pranaitis</a>&nbsp;writes&nbsp;<a title="The Talmud Unmasked" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/The_Talmud_Unmasked">The Talmud Unmasked</a>&nbsp;an antisemitic and misleading inaccurate anti-Talmudic work.</dd>
<dt>1893</dt>
<dd><a title="Karl Lueger" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Karl_Lueger">Karl Lueger</a>&nbsp;establishes antisemitic&nbsp;<em>Christian Social Party</em>&nbsp;and becomes the Mayor of&nbsp;<a title="Vienna" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vienna">Vienna</a>&nbsp;in 1897.</dd>
<dt>1894</dt>
<dd>The&nbsp;<a title="Dreyfus affair" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dreyfus_affair">Dreyfus Affair</a>&nbsp;in France. In 1898&nbsp;<a title="&Eacute;mile Zola" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/%C3%89mile_Zola">&Eacute;mile Zola</a>&nbsp;publishes open letter&nbsp;<em>J'accuse!</em></dd>
<dt>1895</dt>
<dd><a title="A. C. Cuza" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/A._C._Cuza">A. C. Cuza</a>&nbsp;organizes the&nbsp;<em>Alliance Anti-semitique Universelle</em>&nbsp;in&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Bucharest, Romania" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bucharest,_Romania">Bucharest, Romania</a>.</dd>
<dt>1895</dt>
<dd>Captain Alfred Dreyfus being dishonorably discharged in France.</dd>
<dt>1897</dt>
<dd>Synagogues and Jewish homes are pillaged in&nbsp;<a title="Oran" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Oran">Oran</a>.</dd>
<dt>1897</dt>
<dd>Synagogues are ransacked and Jews are murdered in&nbsp;<a title="Tripolitania" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tripolitania">Tripolitania</a>.</dd>
<dt>1898</dt>
<dd>Violent anti-Jewish riots erupt in&nbsp;<a title="Algiers" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Algiers">Algiers</a>.</dd>
<dt>1899</dt>
<dd><a title="Houston Stewart Chamberlain" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Houston_Stewart_Chamberlain">Houston Stewart Chamberlain</a>, racist and antisemitic author, publishes his&nbsp;<em>Die Grundlagen des 19 Jahrhunderts</em>&nbsp;which later became a basis of&nbsp;<a title="Nazism" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nazism">National-Socialist</a>&nbsp;ideology.;1899:&nbsp;<a title="Blood libel" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Blood_libel">Blood libel</a>&nbsp;in&nbsp;<a title="Bohemia" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bohemia">Bohemia</a>&nbsp;(the&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Hilsner case" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hilsner_case">Hilsner case</a>).</dd>
</dl>
</div>
<h2><span id="Twentieth_century" class="mw-headline">Twentieth century</span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">&nbsp;</div>
<h2><span id="1900s" class="mw-headline">1900s</span></h2>
<dl>
<dt>1903</dt>
<dd>The&nbsp;<a title="Kishinev pogrom" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kishinev_pogrom">Kishinev pogrom</a>: 49 Jews murdered.</dd>
<dt>1903</dt>
<dd>The first publication of&nbsp;<em><a title="The Protocols of the Elders of Zion" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/The_Protocols_of_the_Elders_of_Zion">The Protocols of the Elders of Zion</a></em>&nbsp;<a title="Hoax" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hoax">hoax</a>&nbsp;in St. Petersburg, Russia (by&nbsp;<a title="Pavel Krushevan" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pavel_Krushevan">Pavel Krushevan</a>).</dd>
<dt>1904</dt>
<dd>The&nbsp;<a title="Limerick boycott" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Limerick_boycott">Limerick boycott</a>&nbsp;was an economic boycott waged against the small Jewish community in Limerick, Ireland. It was accompanied by a number of assaults, stone throwing and intimidation, which caused many Jews to leave the city.</dd>
<dt>1905</dt>
<dd>Pogrom in&nbsp;<a title="Dnipro" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dnipro">Yekaterinoslav</a>. 66 Jews were killed and 125 wounded and Jewish homes and shops were looted.</dd>
<dt>1905</dt>
<dd>The&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="1905 Kiev pogrom" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1905_Kiev_pogrom">1905 Kiev pogrom</a>&nbsp;was a massacre of 100 Jews.</dd>
<dt>1906</dt>
<dd><a title="Alfred Dreyfus" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Alfred_Dreyfus">Alfred Dreyfus</a>&nbsp;was exonerated and reinstated as a major in the French Army.</dd>
<dt>1907</dt>
<dd>Over 60 Jews in the&nbsp;<a title="Mellah" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mellah">Mellah</a>&nbsp;of&nbsp;<a title="Casablanca" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Casablanca">Casablanca</a>&nbsp;are killed in a pogrom by&nbsp;<a title="Kabyle people" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kabyle_people">Kabyle</a>&nbsp;<a title="Muslims" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Muslims">Muslims</a>. Many more were wounded, and a large number of women and children were carried off.</dd>
<dt>1909</dt>
<dd><a title="Salomon Reinach" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Salomon_Reinach">Salomon Reinach</a>&nbsp;and Florence Simmonds refer to "this&nbsp;<em>new antisemitism</em>, masquerading as patriotism, which was first propagated at&nbsp;<a title="Berlin" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Berlin">Berlin</a>&nbsp;by the court chaplain&nbsp;<a title="Adolf Stoecker" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Adolf_Stoecker">St&ouml;cker</a>, with the connivance of Bismarck."&nbsp;Similarly, Peter N. Stearns comments that "the ideology behind the new anti-Semitism [in Germany] was more racist than religious."</dd>
</dl>
<h2><span id="1910s" class="mw-headline">1910s</span></h2>
<dl>
<dt>1910</dt>
<dd>The&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="1910 Shiraz blood libel" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1910_Shiraz_blood_libel">1910 Shiraz blood libel</a>&nbsp;was a pogrom of the Jewish quarter in&nbsp;<a title="Shiraz" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Shiraz">Shiraz</a>,&nbsp;<a title="Iran" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Iran">Iran</a>. It was sparked by accusations that the Jews had&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Blood Libel" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Blood_Libel">ritually murdered a Muslim girl</a>. By the end of the pogrom, 12 Jews were killed, 50 or so were wounded, and 6,000 were robbed of all their possessions.</dd>
<dt>1912</dt>
<dd><a class="mw-redirect" title="The Tritl" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/The_Tritl">The Tritl</a>, or the&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="1912 Fez massacre" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1912_Fez_massacre">1912 Fez massacre</a>&nbsp;left 42&nbsp;<a title="Moroccan Jews" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Moroccan_Jews">Moroccan Jews</a>&nbsp;dead.</dd>
<dt>1913</dt>
<dd>The&nbsp;<a title="Blood libel" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Blood_libel">Blood libel</a>&nbsp;trial of&nbsp;<a title="Menahem Mendel Beilis" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Menahem_Mendel_Beilis">Menahem Mendel Beilis</a>&nbsp;in Kiev.</dd>
<dt>1915</dt>
<dd>In one 48-hour interval in May 1915, all 40,000 Jews living in&nbsp;<a title="Kaunas" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kaunas">Kaunas</a>,&nbsp;<a title="Lithuania" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lithuania">Lithuania</a>&nbsp;are forcibly removed from the city.</dd>
<dt>1915</dt>
<dd>The&nbsp;<a title="Leo Frank" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Leo_Frank">Leo Frank</a>&nbsp;trial and&nbsp;<a title="Lynching" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lynching">lynching</a>&nbsp;in&nbsp;<a title="Atlanta" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Atlanta">Atlanta</a>,&nbsp;<a title="Georgia (U.S. state)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Georgia_(U.S._state)">Georgia</a>&nbsp;turns the spotlight on&nbsp;<a title="Antisemitism in the United States" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Antisemitism_in_the_United_States">antisemitism in the United States</a>&nbsp;and leads to the founding of the&nbsp;<a title="Anti-Defamation League" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Anti-Defamation_League">Anti-Defamation League</a>.</dd>
<dt>1917&ndash;1921</dt>
<dd>Attacked for being revolutionaries or counter-revolutionaries, unpatriotic pacifists or warmongers, religious zealots or godless atheists, capitalist exploiters or bourgeois profiteers, masses of Jewish civilians (by various estimates 70,000 to 250,000, the number of orphans exceeded 300,000) were murdered in&nbsp;<a title="Pogrom" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pogrom">pogroms</a>&nbsp;in the course of&nbsp;<a title="Russian Civil War" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Russian_Civil_War">Russian Civil War</a>.</dd>
<dt>1918</dt>
<dd>3,000&ndash;10,000&nbsp;<a title="Mountain Jews" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mountain_Jews">Mountain Jews</a>&nbsp;are killed during&nbsp;<a title="March Days" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/March_Days">March Days</a>.</dd>
<dt>1918</dt>
<dd>The&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Lw&oacute;w pogrom of 1918" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lw%C3%B3w_pogrom_of_1918">Lw&oacute;w pogrom of 1918</a>&nbsp;was an attack on the Jewish population of&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Lw&oacute;w" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lw%C3%B3w">Lw&oacute;w</a>&nbsp;that took place on 21&ndash;23 November 1918 during the&nbsp;<a title="Polish&ndash;Ukrainian War" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Polish%E2%80%93Ukrainian_War">Polish&ndash;Ukrainian War</a>. After the pogrom was over, an estimated 52&ndash;150 Jewish residents were killed and hundreds were injured.</dd>
<dt>1919</dt>
<dd>The&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Kiev pogroms of 1919" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kiev_pogroms_of_1919">Kiev pogroms of 1919</a>&nbsp;were a series of pogroms in various places around&nbsp;<a title="Kiev" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kiev">Kiev</a>&nbsp;carried out by&nbsp;<a class="new" title="White Volunteer Army (page does not exist)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=White_Volunteer_Army&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1">White Volunteer Army</a>&nbsp;troops. There were a total of 1,326 pogroms across Ukraine around that time, in which between 30,000 and 70,000 Jews were massacred. According to some estimates, the pogroms left half a million Jews homeless. The series of events occurred in the following districts:</dd>
<dt>1919</dt>
<dd>The&nbsp;<a title="Pinsk massacre" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pinsk_massacre">Pinsk massacre</a>&nbsp;was the mass execution of thirty-five Jewish residents of&nbsp;<a title="Pinsk" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pinsk">Pinsk</a>&nbsp;on 5 April 1919 by the Polish Army.</dd>
<dt>1919</dt>
<dd>In February 1919 a brigade of&nbsp;<a title="Ukrainian People's Republic" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ukrainian_People%27s_Republic">UNR</a>&nbsp;troops killed 1500 Jews in&nbsp;<a title="Proskurov pogrom" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Proskurov_pogrom">Proskurov</a>.</dd>
<dt>1919</dt>
<dd>In&nbsp;<a class="new" title="Tetiev pogrom (page does not exist)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Tetiev_pogrom&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1">Tetiev</a>&nbsp;on 25 March 1919, Cossack troops under the command of Colonels Cherkovsky, Kurovsky and Shliatoshenko murdered 4,000 Jews.</dd>
<dt>1919&ndash;1920</dt>
<dd>During the&nbsp;<a title="Russian Civil War" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Russian_Civil_War">Russian Civil War</a>&nbsp;the Jews of&nbsp;<a title="Uman" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Uman">Uman</a>&nbsp;in eastern&nbsp;<a title="Podolia" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Podolia">Podolia</a>&nbsp;were subjected to two&nbsp;<a title="Pogrom" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pogrom">pogroms</a>&nbsp;in 1919, as the town changed hands several times. The first pogrom, in spring, claimed 170 victims; the second one, in summer, more than 90. This time the Christian inhabitants helped to hide the Jews. The Council for Public Peace, with a Christian majority and a Jewish minority, saved the city from danger several times. In 1920, for example, it stopped the pogrom initiated by the troops of General&nbsp;<a title="Anton Denikin" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Anton_Denikin">Denikin</a>.</dd>
<dt>1919&ndash;1922</dt>
<dd>Soviet&nbsp;<a title="Yevsektsiya" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Yevsektsiya">Yevsektsiya</a>&nbsp;(the Jewish section of the Communist Party) attacks&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="General Jewish Labor Union" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/General_Jewish_Labor_Union">Bund</a>&nbsp;and Zionist parties for "Jewish cultural particularism". In April 1920, the All-Russian Zionist Congress is broken up by&nbsp;<a title="Cheka" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cheka">Cheka</a>&nbsp;led by&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Bolshevik" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bolshevik">Bolsheviks</a>, whose leadership and ranks included many anti-Jewish Jews. Thousands are arrested and sent to&nbsp;<a title="Gulag" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gulag">Gulag</a>&nbsp;for "counter-revolutionary... collusion in the interests of Anglo-French bourgeoisie... to restore the Palestine state."&nbsp;<a title="Hebrew language" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hebrew_language">Hebrew language</a>&nbsp;is banned, Judaism is suppressed, along with other religions.</dd>
</dl>
<h2><span id="1920s" class="mw-headline">1920s</span></h2>
<dl>
<dt>1920</dt>
<dd>The&nbsp;<a title="1920 Nebi Musa riots" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1920_Nebi_Musa_riots">Jerusalem pogrom of April 1920</a>&nbsp;of old&nbsp;<a title="Yishuv" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Yishuv">Yishuv</a>.</dd>
<dt>1920</dt>
<dd>The idea that the&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Bolshevik revolution" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bolshevik_revolution">Bolshevik revolution</a>&nbsp;was a Jewish&nbsp;<a title="Conspiracy theory" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Conspiracy_theory">conspiracy</a>&nbsp;for the&nbsp;<a title="Hegemony" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hegemony">world domination</a>&nbsp;sparks worldwide interest in&nbsp;<em>The Protocols of the Elders of Zion</em>. In a single year, five editions are sold out in England alone. In the US&nbsp;<a title="Henry Ford" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Henry_Ford">Henry Ford</a>&nbsp;prints 500,000 copies.</dd>
<dt>1920</dt>
<dd>In the Spring of 1920,&nbsp;<a title="Henry Ford" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Henry_Ford">Henry Ford</a>&nbsp;made his personal newspaper,&nbsp;<em><a title="The Dearborn Independent" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/The_Dearborn_Independent">The Dearborn Independent</a></em>, chronicle what he considered the "Jewish menace". Every week for 91 issues, the paper exposed some sort of Jewish-inspired evil major story in a headline. The most popular and aggressive stories were then chosen to be reprinted into four volumes called&nbsp;<em><a title="The International Jew" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/The_International_Jew">The International Jew</a></em>.</dd>
<dt>1921</dt>
<dd>All&nbsp;<a title="History of the Jews in Central Asia" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/History_of_the_Jews_in_Central_Asia">Jews in Mongolia</a>&nbsp;are expelled by Russian anti-Bolshevik forces retreating after being defeated in Central Asia.</dd>
<dt>1921</dt>
<dd><a class="mw-redirect" title="Jaffa riots" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jaffa_riots">Jaffa riots</a>&nbsp;in Palestine.</dd>
<dt>1921&ndash;1925</dt>
<dd>Outbreak of antisemitism in United States, led by&nbsp;<a title="Ku Klux Klan" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ku_Klux_Klan">Ku Klux Klan</a>.</dd>
<dt>1922</dt>
<dd>Soviet&nbsp;<a title="Yevsektsiya" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Yevsektsiya">Yevsektsiya</a>&nbsp;(the Jewish section of the Communist Party) attacks&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="General Jewish Labor Union" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/General_Jewish_Labor_Union">Bund</a>&nbsp;and Zionist parties for "Jewish cultural particularism". In April 1920, the All-Russian Zionist Congress is broken up by&nbsp;<a title="Cheka" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cheka">Cheka</a>&nbsp;led by&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Bolshevik" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bolshevik">Bolsheviks</a>, whose leadership and ranks included many anti-Jewish Jews. Thousands are arrested and sent to&nbsp;<a title="Gulag" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gulag">Gulag</a>&nbsp;for "counter-revolutionary... collusion in the interests of Anglo-French bourgeoisie... to restore the Palestine state."&nbsp;<a title="Hebrew language" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hebrew_language">Hebrew language</a>&nbsp;is banned, Judaism is suppressed, along with other religions.</dd>
<dt>1923</dt>
<dd><em><a title="Der St&uuml;rmer" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Der_St%C3%BCrmer">Der St&uuml;rmer</a></em>&nbsp;(<small>pronounced&nbsp;</small><span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)"><a title="Help:IPA/Standard German" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Help:IPA/Standard_German">[deːɐ̯ ˈʃtʏʁmɐ]</a></span>, lit. "the Attacker") was a weekly&nbsp;<a title="Tabloid (newspaper format)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tabloid_(newspaper_format)">tabloid-format</a>&nbsp;<a title="Nazism" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nazism">Nazi</a>&nbsp;<a title="Newspaper" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Newspaper">newspaper</a>&nbsp;published by&nbsp;<a title="Julius Streicher" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Julius_Streicher">Julius Streicher</a>&nbsp;(a prominent official in the&nbsp;<a title="Nazi Party" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nazi_Party">Nazi Party</a>) from 1923 to the end of&nbsp;<a title="World War II" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/World_War_II">World War II</a>, with brief suspensions in publication due to legal difficulties. It was a significant part of&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Nazi propaganda" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nazi_propaganda">Nazi propaganda</a>&nbsp;and was vehemently anti-Semitic.</dd>
<dt>1924</dt>
<dd>The&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="National Origins Quota of 1924" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/National_Origins_Quota_of_1924">National Origins Quota of 1924</a>&nbsp;and&nbsp;<a title="Immigration Act of 1924" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Immigration_Act_of_1924">Immigration Act of 1924</a>&nbsp;largely halted immigration to the U.S. from Eastern Europe and Russia; this was meant to restrict Eastern European Jews among others, as a great many of these immigrants coming from Russia and Eastern Europe were Jews (the "outbreak of antisemitism" mentioned in the above entry may have also played a part in the passage of these acts).</dd>
<dt>1925</dt>
<dd><em><a title="The Ku Klux Klan in Prophecy" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/The_Ku_Klux_Klan_in_Prophecy">The Ku Klux Klan in Prophecy</a></em>&nbsp;is a 144-page book written by Bishop&nbsp;<a title="Alma Bridwell White" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Alma_Bridwell_White">Alma Bridwell White</a>&nbsp;in 1925 and illustrated by Reverend&nbsp;<a title="Branford Clarke" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Branford_Clarke">Branford Clarke</a>.&nbsp;This book primarily espouses White's deep fear and hatred of the&nbsp;<a title="Catholic Church" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Catholic_Church">Roman Catholic Church</a>&nbsp;while also promoting antisemitism,&nbsp;<a title="Racism" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Racism">racism</a>&nbsp;against&nbsp;<a title="African Americans" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/African_Americans">African Americans</a>,&nbsp;<a title="White supremacy" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/White_supremacy">white supremacy</a>, and&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Women's equality" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Women%27s_equality">women's equality</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"></sup></dd>
<dt>1925</dt>
<dd><a title="Adolf Hitler" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Adolf_Hitler">Adolf Hitler</a>&nbsp;publishes&nbsp;<em><a title="Mein Kampf" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mein_Kampf">Mein Kampf</a></em>.</dd>
<dt>1927</dt>
<dd>The&nbsp;<em><a title="Schwartzbard trial" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Schwartzbard_trial">Schwartzbard trial</a></em>&nbsp;was a sensational 1927&nbsp;<a title="France" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/France">French</a>&nbsp;murder trial that resulted in a&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Mistrial (law)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mistrial_(law)">mistrial</a>&nbsp;of international proportions. At the trial&nbsp;<a title="Sholom Schwartzbard" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sholom_Schwartzbard">Sholom Schwartzbard</a>&nbsp;was accused of murdering the&nbsp;<a title="Ukrainians" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ukrainians">Ukrainian</a>&nbsp;immigrant and head of the Ukrainian government-in-exile&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Symon Petlura" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Symon_Petlura">Symon Petlura</a>&nbsp;in Paris. While the defendant fully admitted to the crime the trial at the end turned in accusation of Petlura's responsibility for the massive 1919&ndash;1920&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Pogroms in Ukraine" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pogroms_in_Ukraine">pogroms in Ukraine</a>&nbsp;in which Schwartzbard had lost all 15 members of his family. Instead of Schwartzbard's murder case the trial was turned into a political case against the Ukrainian government. Schwartzbard was acquitted.</dd>
<dt>1928</dt>
<dd>The&nbsp;<a title="Massena blood libel" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Massena_blood_libel">Massena blood libel</a>&nbsp;was an instance of&nbsp;<a title="Blood libel" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Blood_libel">blood libel</a>&nbsp;against Jews in which the&nbsp;<a title="Jews" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jews">Jews</a>&nbsp;of&nbsp;<a title="Massena (village), New York" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Massena_(village),_New_York">Massena</a>,&nbsp;<a title="New York (state)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/New_York_(state)">New York</a>, were falsely accused of the&nbsp;<a title="Kidnapping" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kidnapping">kidnapping</a>&nbsp;and&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Ritual murder" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ritual_murder">ritual murder</a>&nbsp;of a&nbsp;<a title="Christians" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Christians">Christian</a>&nbsp;girl in September 1928.</dd>
<dt>1929</dt>
<dd>The ancient Jewish community of&nbsp;<a title="Hebron" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hebron">Hebron</a>&nbsp;is&nbsp;<a title="1929 Hebron massacre" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1929_Hebron_massacre">massacred by local Muslims</a>&nbsp;over rumors that the Jews were planning to seize control of the&nbsp;<a title="Temple Mount" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Temple_Mount">Temple Mount</a>.</dd>
<dt>1929</dt>
<dd>18&ndash;20 Jewish residents of&nbsp;<a title="Safed" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Safed">Safed</a>&nbsp;were brutally killed in the&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="1929 Safed massacre" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1929_Safed_massacre">1929 Safed massacre</a>.</dd>
</dl>
<h2><span id="1930s" class="mw-headline">1930s</span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">&nbsp;</div>
<dl>
<dt>1930</dt>
<dd><a title="Pogrom" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pogrom">Pogrom</a>&nbsp;against the Jews of&nbsp;<a title="Bălți" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/B%C4%83l%C8%9Bi">Bălți</a>.</dd>
<dt>1933, 16 August</dt>
