<dd><a title="Christie Pits riot" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Christie_Pits_riot">Christie Pits riot</a>&nbsp;takes place in&nbsp;<a title="Toronto" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Toronto">Toronto</a>,&nbsp;<a title="Ontario" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ontario">Ontario</a>.</dd>
<dt>1933</dt>
<dd>In a series of lectures delivered at the&nbsp;<a title="University of Virginia" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/University_of_Virginia">University of Virginia</a>&nbsp;in 1933, published under the title&nbsp;<em>After Strange Gods: A Primer of Modern Heresy</em>&nbsp;(1934),&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="T.S. Eliot" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/T.S._Eliot">T.S. Eliot</a>&nbsp;wrote of societal tradition and coherence, "What is still more important [than cultural homogeneity] is unity of religious background, and reasons of race and religion combine to make any large number of free-thinking Jews undesirable."&nbsp;Eliot never re-published this book/lecture.</dd>
<dt>1933&ndash;1941</dt>
<dd>Persecution of Jews in Germany rises until they are stripped of their rights not only as citizens, but also as human beings. During this time antisemitism reached its all-time high.
<ul>
<li>Law against Overcrowding of German Schools and Universities</li>
<li>Law for the Reestablishment of the Professional Civil Service (ban on professions)</li>
<li>The&nbsp;<a title="Reich Flight Tax" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Reich_Flight_Tax">Reich Flight Tax</a>&nbsp;is used to expropriate funds from Jewish &eacute;migr&eacute;s.</li>
</ul>
</dd>
</dl>
<dl>
<dt>1934</dt>
<dd>2,000&nbsp;<a title="Afghanistan" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Afghanistan">Afghani</a>&nbsp;Jews are expelled from their towns and forced to live in the wilderness.</dd>
<dt>1934</dt>
<dd>The&nbsp;<a title="1934 Thrace pogroms" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1934_Thrace_pogroms">1934 Thrace pogroms</a>&nbsp;were a series of violent attacks that occurred in&nbsp;<a title="Tekirdağ" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tekirda%C4%9F">Tekirdağ</a>,&nbsp;<a title="Edirne" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Edirne">Edirne</a>,&nbsp;<a title="Kırklareli" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/K%C4%B1rklareli">Kırklareli</a>, and&nbsp;<a title="&Ccedil;anakkale" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/%C3%87anakkale">&Ccedil;anakkale</a>. Over 15,000 Jews had to flee from the region.</dd>
<dt>1934</dt>
<dd>34&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Algerian Jews" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Algerian_Jews">Algerian Jews</a>&nbsp;were killed and hundreds were injured by Muslim mobs during the&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="1934 Constantine pogrom" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1934_Constantine_pogrom">1934 Constantine pogrom</a>. 200 Jewish stores were raided, the total property damage was estimated at over 150&nbsp;million Poincare francs. It also sent a quarter of Constantine's Jewish population into poverty.</dd>
<dt>1934</dt>
<dd>The first appearance of&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="The Franklin Prophecy" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/The_Franklin_Prophecy">The Franklin Prophecy</a>&nbsp;on the pages of&nbsp;<a title="William Dudley Pelley" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/William_Dudley_Pelley">William Dudley Pelley</a>'s pro-Nazi weekly magazine&nbsp;<em>Liberation</em>. According to the&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="US Congress" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/US_Congress">US Congress</a>&nbsp;report:</dd>
</dl>
<blockquote>
<p>"The Franklin "Prophecy" is a classic&nbsp;<a title="Antisemitic canard" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Antisemitic_canard">antisemitic canard</a>&nbsp;that falsely claims that American statesman&nbsp;<a title="Benjamin Franklin" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Benjamin_Franklin">Benjamin Franklin</a>&nbsp;made anti-Jewish statements during the&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Philadelphia Convention" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Philadelphia_Convention">Constitutional Convention</a>&nbsp;of 1787. It has found widening acceptance in Muslim and Arab media, where it has been used to criticize Israel and Jews..."</p>
</blockquote>
<dl>
<dt>1934</dt>
<dd>In his 1934 pageant play&nbsp;<em>The Rock</em>,&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="T.S. Eliot" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/T.S._Eliot">T.S. Eliot</a>&nbsp;distances himself from Fascist movements of the thirties by caricaturing&nbsp;<a title="Oswald Mosley" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Oswald_Mosley">Oswald Mosley</a>'s Blackshirts, who 'firmly refuse/ To descend to palaver with anthropoid Jews'. The "new evangels"&nbsp;of totalitarianism are presented as antithetical to the spirit of Christianity.</dd>
<dt>1935</dt>
<dd><a title="Nuremberg Laws" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nuremberg_Laws">Nuremberg Laws</a>&nbsp;introduced. Jewish rights rescinded. The Reich Citizenship Law strips them of citizenship. The Law for the Protection of German Blood and German Honor:
<ul>
<li>Marriages between Jews and citizens of German or kindred blood are forbidden.</li>
<li>Sexual relations outside marriage between Jews and nationals of German or kindred blood are forbidden.</li>
<li>Jews will not be permitted to employ female citizens of German or kindred blood as domestic servants.</li>
<li>Jews are forbidden to display the Reich and national flag or the national colors. On the other hand, they are permitted to display the Jewish colors.</li>
</ul>
</dd>
</dl>
<dl>
<dt>1936</dt>
<dd><a class="mw-redirect" title="The Bloody Day in Jaffa" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/The_Bloody_Day_in_Jaffa">The Bloody Day in Jaffa</a>&nbsp;refers to various violent attacks on Jews in&nbsp;<a title="Jaffa" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jaffa">Jaffa</a>&nbsp;by mobs of Muslims.</dd>
<dt>1936</dt>
<dd>The&nbsp;<a title="Przytyk pogrom" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Przytyk_pogrom">Przytyk pogrom</a>&nbsp;was an altercation between Jewish and Polish peasants, ending with two Jews and one Pole dead.</dd>
<dt>1936</dt>
<dd>Cardinal&nbsp;<a title="August Hlond" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/August_Hlond">August Hlond</a>, as Primate of Poland issued a pastoral letter on Catholic moral principles.&nbsp;The long (5600-word) letter covered Catholic ethics policy, ethics principles and a section on "sins" (<em>Z Naszych Grzech&oacute;w</em>) that addressed Christian shortcomings to&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Second greatest commandment" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Second_greatest_commandment">love one's neighbours</a>&nbsp;in accordance with God's law. The latter section included a brief discussion of the "Jewish problem" (<em>Problem żydowski</em>): "So long as Jews remain Jews, a Jewish problem exists and will continue to exist (...) It is a fact that Jews are waging war against the Catholic church, that they are steeped in free-thinking, and constitute the vanguard of atheism, the Bolshevik movement, and revolutionary activity. It is a fact that Jews have a corruptive influence on morals and that their publishing houses are spreading pornography. It is true that Jews are perpetrating fraud, practicing usury, and dealing in prostitution. It is true that, from a religious and ethical point of view, Jewish youth are having a negative influence on the Catholic youth in our schools."&nbsp;Hlond tempered these remarks with an admission that "not all Jews are this way" and forbade assaults on Jews or attacks on their property. Yet, despite a warning to Catholics not to take an anti-Jewish moral stance, interspersed in the letter's words of friendship was an explicit condemnation of Jewish culture and also Judaism for its rejection of&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Christ" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Christ">Jesus Christ</a>: "It is good to prefer your own kind when shopping, to avoid Jewish stores and Jewish stalls in the marketplace (...) One should stay away from the harmful moral influence of Jews, keep away from their anti-Christian culture, and especially boycott the Jewish press and demoralizing Jewish publications. (...) We do not honor the indescribable tragedy of that nation, which was the guardian of the idea of the&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Christ" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Christ">Messiah</a>&nbsp;and from which was born the Savior. When divine mercy enlightens a Jew to sincerely accept his and our Messiah, let us greet him into our Christian ranks with joy."&nbsp;Hlond's letter was criticized by Polish Jewish groups who saw it as offering support and a rationalization for antisemitism.&nbsp;What also caught the attention of historians was the remark about not hating anyone, "not even Jews", implying "not even enemies". Were Jews to be loved as neighbors or enemies?&nbsp;However, while Hlond promoted the expulsion of German civilians after World War II, he had always consistently condemned the Nazi persecution of the Jews.</dd>
<dt>1937</dt>
<dd>"<a title="The Eternal Jew (art exhibition)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/The_Eternal_Jew_(art_exhibition)">The Eternal Jew</a>" was the title of an exhibition of&nbsp;<a title="Degenerate art" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Degenerate_art">degenerate art</a>&nbsp;(<em>entartete Kunst</em>) displayed at the Library of the&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="German Museum" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/German_Museum">German Museum</a>&nbsp;in&nbsp;<a title="Munich" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Munich">Munich</a>&nbsp;from 8 November 1937 to 31 January 1938. The exhibition attracted 412,300 visitors, over 5,000 per day.</dd>
<dt>1938</dt>
<dd><a title="Ecuador" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ecuador">Ecuador</a>&nbsp;issues an order that states all&nbsp;<a title="History of the Jews in Ecuador" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/History_of_the_Jews_in_Ecuador">Ecuadorian Jewish</a>&nbsp;residents not working in agriculture need to leave the country.</dd>
<dt>1938</dt>
<dd><a title="Anschluss" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Anschluss">Anschluss</a>,&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Pogroms" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pogroms">pogroms</a>&nbsp;in&nbsp;<a title="Vienna" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vienna">Vienna</a>, anti-Jewish legislation, deportations to&nbsp;<a title="Nazi concentration camps" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nazi_concentration_camps">Nazi concentration camps</a>.
<ul>
<li>Decree authorizing local authorities to bar Jews from the streets on certain days</li>
<li>Decree empowering the justice Ministry to void wills offending the "sound judgment of the people"</li>
<li>Decree providing for the compulsory sale of Jewish real estate</li>
<li>Decree providing for the liquidation of Jewish real estate agencies, brokerage agencies, and marriage agencies catering to non-Jews</li>
<li>Directive providing for the concentration of Jews in houses</li>
</ul>
</dd>
</dl>
<dl>
<dt>1938 July 6&ndash;15</dt>
<dd><a class="mw-redirect" title="Evian Conference" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Evian_Conference">Evian Conference</a>: 31 countries refuse to accept Jews trying to escape Nazi Germany (with the exception of&nbsp;<a title="Dominican Republic" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dominican_Republic">Dominican Republic</a>). Most find temporary refuge in Poland. See also&nbsp;<a title="Bermuda Conference" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bermuda_Conference">Bermuda Conference</a>.</dd>
<dt>1938</dt>
<dd>Arab rioters rush into the Jewish Kiryat Shmuel neighborhood, killing 19 Jews, 11 of whom were children in the&nbsp;<a title="1938 Tiberias massacre" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1938_Tiberias_massacre">1938 Tiberias massacre</a>.</dd>
<dt>1938</dt>
<dd>Father&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Charles E. Coughlin" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Charles_E._Coughlin">Charles E. Coughlin</a>, a Roman Catholic priest, starts antisemitic weekly radio broadcasts in the United States.</dd>
<dt>1938</dt>
<dd><a title="Kristallnacht" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kristallnacht">Kristallnacht</a>&nbsp;(Night of The Broken Glass). In one night most German synagogues and hundreds of Jewish-owned German businesses are destroyed. Almost 100 Jews are killed, and 10,000 are sent to concentration camps.</dd>
<dt>1938</dt>
<dd>Racial legislation introduced in&nbsp;<a title="Italy" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Italy">Italy</a>. Anti Jewish economic legislation introduced in&nbsp;<a title="Hungary" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hungary">Hungary</a>.</dd>
<dt>1938</dt>
<dd><em><a title="Der Giftpilz" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Der_Giftpilz">Der Giftpilz</a></em>&nbsp;is a children's book published by&nbsp;<a title="Julius Streicher" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Julius_Streicher">Julius Streicher</a>&nbsp;in 1938.&nbsp;The title is German for "the&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Toadstool" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Toadstool">toadstool</a>" or "the poisonous mushroom".&nbsp;The book was intended as anti-Semitic&nbsp;<a title="Propaganda" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Propaganda">propaganda</a>. The text is by&nbsp;<a title="Ernst Hiemer" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ernst_Hiemer">Ernst Hiemer</a>, with illustrations by&nbsp;<a title="Philipp Rupprecht" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Philipp_Rupprecht">Philipp Rupprecht</a>&nbsp;(also known as&nbsp;<em>Fips</em>).</dd>
<dt>1939</dt>
<dd>The "Voyage of the damned":&nbsp;<a title="MS St. Louis" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/MS_St._Louis">S.S. St. Louis</a>, carrying 907 Jewish refugees from Germany, is turned back by&nbsp;<a title="Canada" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Canada">Canada</a>,&nbsp;<a title="Cuba" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cuba">Cuba</a>&nbsp;and the&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="United States of America" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States_of_America">US</a>.&nbsp;After they were denied entry to those places, the refugees were finally accepted in various European countries, including Belgium, the Netherlands, the UK, and France. Historians have estimated that approximately a quarter of them died in death camps during World War II.</dd>
<dt>1939</dt>
<dd>In this year&nbsp;<a title="Ezra Pound" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ezra_Pound">Ezra Pound</a>&nbsp;returned to Italy from the States and began writing&nbsp;<a title="Antisemitism" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Antisemitism">antisemitic</a>&nbsp;material for Italian newspapers. He wrote to&nbsp;<a title="James Laughlin" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/James_Laughlin">James Laughlin</a>&nbsp;that&nbsp;<a title="Franklin D. Roosevelt" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Franklin_D._Roosevelt">Roosevelt</a>&nbsp;represented Jewry, and signed the letter with "<a class="mw-redirect" title="Heil Hitler" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Heil_Hitler">Heil Hitler</a>".</dd>
<dt>1939</dt>
<dd><em><a title="Linen from Ireland" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Linen_from_Ireland">Linen from Ireland</a></em>&nbsp;is a 1939 German&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Drama film" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Drama_film">drama film</a>&nbsp;that was part of an ongoing campaign of antisemitism in German cinema of the era, and it also attacked&nbsp;<a title="United Kingdom" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_Kingdom">Britain</a>&nbsp;with whom Germany was at war by the time of the film's release.</dd>
<dt>1939</dt>
<dd><em><a title="Robert and Bertram (1939 film)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Robert_and_Bertram_(1939_film)">Robert and Bertram</a></em>&nbsp;is a 1939 German&nbsp;<a title="Musical film" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Musical_film">musical</a>&nbsp;<a title="Comedy film" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Comedy_film">comedy film</a>; it was the only anti-semitic&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Musical comedy" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Musical_comedy">musical comedy</a>&nbsp;released during the&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Nazi" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nazi">Nazi</a>&nbsp;era.</dd>
<dt>1939 February</dt>
<dd>The&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Congress of the United States" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Congress_of_the_United_States">Congress of the United States</a>&nbsp;rejects the&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Wagner-Rogers Bill" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wagner-Rogers_Bill">Wagner-Rogers Bill</a>, an effort to admit 20,000 Jewish refugee children under the age of 14 from Nazi Germany.</dd>
<dt>1939&ndash;1945</dt>
<dd><strong><a title="The Holocaust" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/The_Holocaust">The Holocaust</a></strong>. About 6&nbsp;million Jews, including about 1&nbsp;million children, systematically killed by&nbsp;<a title="Nazi Germany" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nazi_Germany">Nazi Germany</a>&nbsp;and other&nbsp;<a title="Axis powers" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Axis_powers">Axis powers</a>. See also&nbsp;<a title="Holocaust denial" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Holocaust_denial">Holocaust denial</a>.</dd>
<dt>1939&ndash;1958</dt>
<dd>Some post-war critics have accused&nbsp;<a title="Pope Pius XII" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pope_Pius_XII">Pope Pius XII</a>, who had his papacy in 1939&ndash;1958, of either being overly cautious, or of "not doing enough," or even of "silence" in the face of&nbsp;<a title="The Holocaust" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/The_Holocaust">the Holocaust</a>. Yet, by the writings of Jewish men and women and mainly the Israeli State archives, it is well established that Pope Pius XII supervised a secret rescue network which saved approximately 800,000 Jewish lives.</dd>
</dl>
<h2><span id="1940s" class="mw-headline">1940s</span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">&nbsp;</div>
<dl>
<dt>1940</dt>
<dd>On 16 May 1940 the&nbsp;<em><a class="mw-redirect" title="Administrasjonsr&aring;det" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Administrasjonsr%C3%A5det">Administrasjonsr&aring;det</a></em>&nbsp;asked&nbsp;<a class="new" title="Rikskommisariatet (page does not exist)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Rikskommisariatet&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1">Rikskommisariatet</a>&nbsp;why radio receivers had been confiscated from Jews in Norway.&nbsp;That&nbsp;<em>Administrasjonsr&aring;det</em>&nbsp;thereafter "quietly" accepted&nbsp;racial segregation between Norwegian citizens, has been claimed by&nbsp;<a title="Tor Bomann-Larsen" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tor_Bomann-Larsen">Tor Bomann-Larsen</a>. Furthermore, he claimed that this segregation "created a&nbsp;<a title="Precedent" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Precedent">precedent</a>." Two years later (with&nbsp;<em>NS-styret</em>&nbsp;in the ministries of Norway) Norwegian police&nbsp;<a title="Jewish deportees from Norway during World War II" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jewish_deportees_from_Norway_during_World_War_II">arrested citizens at the addresses</a>&nbsp;where radios had previously been confiscated from Jews.</dd>
<dt>1940</dt>
<dd>In the&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Vichy regime" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vichy_regime">Vichy regime</a>: 10 July 1940 &ndash;&nbsp;<a title="Pierre Laval" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pierre_Laval">Pierre Laval</a>&nbsp;induces Parliament to vote complete powers (constituent, legislative, executive and judicial) to Marshal&nbsp;<a title="Philippe P&eacute;tain" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Philippe_P%C3%A9tain">Philippe P&eacute;tain</a>&nbsp;who becomes Head of state of the French State (&Eacute;tat fran&ccedil;ais). 21 July 1940 &ndash; Minister of Justice&nbsp;<a title="Rapha&euml;l Alibert" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Rapha%C3%ABl_Alibert">Rapha&euml;l Alibert</a>&nbsp;creates a board to review 500,000 naturalizations accorded since 1927. Withdrawal of nationality for 15,000 people, 40% of whom were Jews. July 1940 &ndash; The Germans expel more than 20,000 Alsace-Lorraine Jews to the southern zone. 27 September 1940 &ndash; Ordinance on the status of Jews in the Occupied Zone. A census of Jews ("the Tulard file") and obligatory sign indicating "Jew" on shops owned by Jews. 27 September 1940 &ndash; A Vichy law allows any foreigner "redundant to the French economy" to be interned among "groups of foreign workers". 3 October 1940 &ndash; first law on the status of Jews. French Jewish citizens are excluded from civil service, army, education, the press, radio and film. "Surplus" Jews are excluded from the professions. Article 9: This law is applicable to Algeria, to the colonies, protectorates and mandated territories. 4 October 1940 &ndash; prefects can detain foreigners of Jewish extraction in special camps or to assign residence. 7 October 1940 &ndash; repeal of the 1871 Cr&eacute;mieux Decree; French nationality is removed from Jews from&nbsp;<a title="Algeria" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Algeria">Algeria</a>. 7 October 1940 &ndash; Aryanization of businesses in the Occupied Zone.</dd>
<dt>1940</dt>
<dd><em><a class="mw-redirect" title="Jud S&uuml;&szlig; (1940 film)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jud_S%C3%BC%C3%9F_(1940_film)">Jud S&uuml;&szlig;</a></em>&nbsp;is a 1940&nbsp;<a title="Nazi Germany" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nazi_Germany">Nazi</a>&nbsp;<a title="Propaganda film" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Propaganda_film">propaganda film</a>&nbsp;produced by Terra Filmkunst at the behest of&nbsp;<a title="Joseph Goebbels" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Joseph_Goebbels">Joseph Goebbels</a>, and considered one of the most antisemitic films of all time.&nbsp;The film has been characterized as "one of the most notorious and successful pieces of antisemitic film propaganda produced in Nazi Germany."&nbsp;It was a great success in Germany, with some 20&nbsp;million viewers. Although the film's budget of 2&nbsp;million&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Reichsmarks" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Reichsmarks">Reichsmarks</a>&nbsp;was considered high for films of that era, the box office receipts of 6.5&nbsp;million Reichsmarks made it a financial success.&nbsp;<a title="Heinrich Himmler" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Heinrich_Himmler">Heinrich Himmler</a>&nbsp;urged members of the&nbsp;<a title="Schutzstaffel" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Schutzstaffel">SS</a>&nbsp;and police to watch the movie.</dd>
<dt>1940</dt>
<dd><em><a title="The Rothschilds (film)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/The_Rothschilds_(film)">The Rothschilds</a></em>&nbsp;is a 1940 German film directed by Erich Waschneck. It portrays the role of the&nbsp;<a title="Rothschild family" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Rothschild_family">Rothschild family</a>&nbsp;in the&nbsp;<a title="Napoleonic Wars" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Napoleonic_Wars">Napoleonic Wars</a>. The Jewish Rothschilds are depicted in a negative manner, consistent with the anti-Semitic policy of Nazi Germany.</dd>
<dt>1940</dt>
<dd><em><a title="Vom B&auml;umlein, das andere Bl&auml;tter hat gewollt" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vom_B%C3%A4umlein,_das_andere_Bl%C3%A4tter_hat_gewollt">Vom B&auml;umlein, das andere Bl&auml;tter hat gewollt</a></em>&nbsp;is a short anti-Semitic propaganda cartoon produced in 1940 in the Nazi movie studio Zeichenfilm GmbH.</dd>
<dt>1940</dt>
<dd><em><a title="The Eternal Jew (1940 film)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/The_Eternal_Jew_(1940_film)">The Eternal Jew</a></em>&nbsp;(1940) is an antisemitic&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="German Nazi" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/German_Nazi">German Nazi</a>&nbsp;<a title="Propaganda film" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Propaganda_film">propaganda film</a>,&nbsp;presented as a documentary.</dd>
<dt>1941</dt>
<dd>The&nbsp;<a title="Farhud" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Farhud">Farhud</a>&nbsp;pogrom in&nbsp;<a title="Baghdad" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Baghdad">Baghdad</a>&nbsp;results in 780 Jews dead, over 1,000 wounded.</dd>
<dt>1941</dt>
<dd><a title="Gab&egrave;s pogrom" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gab%C3%A8s_pogrom">Gab&egrave;s pogrom</a>&nbsp;in&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="French Tunisia" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/French_Tunisia">French Tunisia</a>&nbsp;leaves 8 Jews dead and at least 20 wounded.</dd>
<dt>1941</dt>
<dd><a title="Iași pogrom" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ia%C8%99i_pogrom">Iași pogrom</a>&nbsp;in&nbsp;<a title="Iași" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ia%C8%99i">Iași</a>&nbsp;city was the incident where more than 13,266 Jews were killed by angry mobs of locals, and together with military personnel they exterminated about 1/3 of Jewish population in Romania.</dd>
<dt>1941</dt>
<dd>Encouraged by the Nazis, Ukrainian militias and local mobs perpetrated the&nbsp;<a title="Lviv pogroms (1941)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lviv_pogroms_(1941)">Lviv pogroms</a>, killing around 6,000 Polish Jews.</dd>
<dt>1941</dt>
<dd>Some villagers in Jedwabne, Poland burned at least 340 local Jews alive.</dd>
<dt>1941</dt>
<dd>Nazis and their collaborators shot to death 33,771 Jews at&nbsp;<a title="Babi Yar" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Babi_Yar">Babi Yar</a>&nbsp;over the course of two days.</dd>
<dt>1941</dt>
<dd>German forces and Latvian collaborators killed around 5,000 Jews in the&nbsp;<a title="Liepāja massacres" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Liep%C4%81ja_massacres">Liepāja massacres</a>.</dd>
<dt>1941</dt>
<dd>In a speech at an America First rally at the&nbsp;<a title="Des Moines Coliseum" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Des_Moines_Coliseum">Des Moines Coliseum</a>&nbsp;on 11 September 1941, "Who Are the War Agitators?",&nbsp;<a title="Charles Lindbergh" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Charles_Lindbergh">Charles Lindbergh</a>&nbsp;warned of the Jewish people's "large ownership and influence in our motion pictures, our press, our radio, and our government"&nbsp;and claimed the three groups "pressing this country toward war [are] the British, the Jewish, and the Roosevelt Administration",&nbsp;and said of Jewish groups,</dd>
<dt>1941</dt>
<dd>Collaboration of the&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Vichy regime" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vichy_regime">Vichy regime</a>&nbsp;with the&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Holocaust" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Holocaust">Holocaust</a>: 29 March 1941: creation of the&nbsp;<a title="Commissariat-General for Jewish Affairs" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Commissariat-General_for_Jewish_Affairs">Commissariat-General for Jewish Affairs</a>&nbsp;(CGQJ), with Xavier Vallat as the first commissioner. 11 May 1941 &ndash; Creation of the French Institute for Jewish Affairs, an anti-Semitic propaganda agency, financed by the nazis (Theodor Dannecker) and directed by French antisemitic agitators Paul S&eacute;zille (fr), Ren&eacute; G&eacute;rard (fr) and others. 14 May 1941 &ndash; the Billet Vert roundup (fr) organized by the Prefecture of Police with the agreement of the general delegation of the French government in the occupied zone and upon demand by the occupying authorities: 3,747 Jewish foreigners, (out of 6,494 summoned by the prefecture) were crammed into the Pithiviers and Beaune-la-Rolande internment camps under French administration. 2 June 1941 &ndash; second law concerning Jews. Compared to the first one, an increasingly stringent definition of who is a Jew, additional professional work restrictions, quotas in University (3%) and the liberal professions (2%). Jews were obligated to take part in a census in the Zone libre. Article 11 of the Statute: "This law is applicable to Algeria, the colonies, protectorates and territories under mandate. This law authorizes prefects to perform administrative detention of Jews of French nationality." 21 July 1941 &ndash; Aryanization of Jewish companies in the Zone libre. August 1941: Occupied zone: internment of 3,200 foreign and 1,000 French Jews in various camps including Drancy. December 1941 &ndash; Occupied zone: 740 French Jews, members of the liberal and intellectual professions, interned in Compi&egrave;gne.</dd>
<dt>January 1942</dt>
<dd>The&nbsp;<a title="Wannsee Conference" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wannsee_Conference">Wannsee Conference</a>&nbsp;in Berlin: Nazi officials define the practical arrangements for the "Final Solution", that is to say, the complete extermination of European Jewry, including children.</dd>
<dt>1942</dt>
<dd>The&nbsp;<a title="Antisemitic Exhibition in Zagreb" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Antisemitic_Exhibition_in_Zagreb">Antisemitic Exhibition in Zagreb</a>&nbsp;took place in the&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Art Pavilion in Zagreb" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Art_Pavilion_in_Zagreb">Art Pavilion</a>&nbsp;in&nbsp;<a title="Zagreb" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Zagreb">Zagreb</a>, the capital city of the&nbsp;<a title="Independent State of Croatia" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Independent_State_of_Croatia">Independent State of Croatia</a>&nbsp;(NDH), in May 1942. According to its organizers, the exhibition sought to expose the "destructive and exploitative work of&nbsp;<a title="Croatia" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Croatia">Croatia</a>'s Jews prior to 1941."</dd>
<dt>1942</dt>
<dd>Collaboration of the&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Vichy regime" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vichy_regime">Vichy regime</a>&nbsp;with the&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Holocaust" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Holocaust">Holocaust</a>: 27 March 1942 &ndash; The first convoy of Jewish deportees leaves Compi&egrave;gne (Frontstalag 122) towards an extermination camp. 20 May 1942 &ndash; Occupied zone: Compulsory wearing of yellow Jewish star badge. (effective 7 June). 2 July 1942 &ndash; Oberg-Bousquet agreement for collaboration between French and German police, in the presence of&nbsp;<a title="Reinhard Heydrich" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Reinhard_Heydrich">Reinhard Heydrich</a>,&nbsp;<a title="Heinrich Himmler" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Heinrich_Himmler">Heinrich Himmler</a>'s deputy. 16&ndash;17 July 1942 &ndash;&nbsp;<a title="Vel' d'Hiv Roundup" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vel%27_d%27Hiv_Roundup">Roundup of the Vel d'Hiv</a>: arrest of 13,152 "stateless" Jews (3,031 men, 5,802 women and 4,051 children). 19 July 1942 &ndash; failed Roundup of Nancy (fr), after Jews were warned overnight to flee by Nancy Police Commissioner for Foreign Affairs &Eacute;douard Vigneron. 26&ndash;28 August 1942 Zone libre &ndash; series of roundups resulting in the deportation of 7,000 people.</dd>
<dt>1943</dt>
<dd><em><a title="Vienna 1910" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vienna_1910">Vienna 1910</a></em>&nbsp;is a 1943 German biographical film directed by Emerich Walter Emo and starring Rudolf Forster, Heinrich George and Lil Dagover. It is based on the life of Mayor of Vienna Karl Lueger. Its antisemitic content led to it being banned by the Allied Occupation forces following World War II.</dd>
<dt>1943</dt>
<dd><em><a title="Forces occultes" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Forces_occultes">Forces occultes</a></em>&nbsp;is a French film of 1943 that virulently denounces Jews,&nbsp;<a title="Freemasonry" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Freemasonry">Freemasonry</a>, and parliamentarianism as part of the&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Vichy regime" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vichy_regime">Vichy regime</a>'s drive against them and seeks to prove a Jewish-Masonic plot.</dd>
<dt>1943</dt>
<dd>Collaboration of the&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Vichy regime" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vichy_regime">Vichy regime</a>&nbsp;with the&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Holocaust" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Holocaust">Holocaust</a>: January 1943 &ndash;&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Roundup of Marseille" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Roundup_of_Marseille">Roundup of Marseille</a>: destruction of the Old Port and roundups by French authorities. Nearly 2,000 Marseilles Jews arrested and deported. Le Petit Marseillais of 30 January 1943 wrote: "Note that the evacuation operations in the Northern district of the Old Port were carried out exclusively by French police and that no incidents were reported. The Opera district, where many Sephardic families lived, is emptied of its inhabitants. February 1943 &ndash; Lyon raid on the premises of the Union g&eacute;n&eacute;rale des isra&eacute;lites de France (fr) (UGIF). September 8, 1943 &ndash; surrender of Italy leading to the Allied occupation of Italian-occupied France hitherto spared the roundups. April 1943 &ndash; N&icirc;mes and Avignon roundups. September 1943 &ndash; roundups of Nice and surrounding area."</dd>
<dt>1943</dt>
<dd>The&nbsp;<a title="Bermuda Conference" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bermuda_Conference">Bermuda Conference</a>&nbsp;was an international conference between the&nbsp;<a title="United Kingdom" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_Kingdom">United Kingdom</a>&nbsp;and the&nbsp;<a title="United States" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States">United States</a>&nbsp;held from 19 April 1943, through 30 April 1943, at&nbsp;<a title="Hamilton, Bermuda" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hamilton,_Bermuda">Hamilton, Bermuda</a>. The topic of discussion was the question of&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Jew" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jew">Jewish</a>&nbsp;<a title="Refugee" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Refugee">refugees</a>&nbsp;who had been liberated by&nbsp;<a title="Allies of World War II" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Allies_of_World_War_II">Allied forces</a>&nbsp;and those who still remained in&nbsp;<a title="Nazi Germany" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nazi_Germany">Nazi</a>-occupied Europe. The only agreement made was that the war must be won against the Nazis. US immigration quotas were not raised nor was the British prohibition on Jewish refugees seeking refuge in the&nbsp;<a title="Mandatory Palestine" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mandatory_Palestine">British Mandate of Palestine</a>&nbsp;lifted.</dd>
<dt>1944</dt>
<dd>Collaboration of the&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Vichy regime" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vichy_regime">Vichy regime</a>&nbsp;with the&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Holocaust" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Holocaust">Holocaust</a>: February 1944 &ndash; roundups of Grenoble and Is&egrave;re. 15 August 1944 &ndash; last deportation convoy from Clermont-Ferrand.</dd>
<dt>1945</dt>
<dd>The&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="1945 Tripoli pogrom" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1945_Tripoli_pogrom">1945 Tripoli pogrom</a>&nbsp;was a violent massacre of the&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Libyan Jews" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Libyan_Jews">Jewish population of Tripoli</a>&nbsp;by Muslim rioters. After days of violence 140+ Jews were dead and hundreds were injured. In the aftermath 4,000 Jews were left homeless and thousands were reduced to poverty. 9 Synagogues were destroyed, along with thousands of Jewish homes and businesses.</dd>
<dt>1945</dt>
<dd>The&nbsp;<a title="1945 Anti-Jewish riots in Egypt" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1945_Anti-Jewish_riots_in_Egypt">1945 Anti-Jewish riots in Egypt</a>&nbsp;started as an&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Anti-Zionist" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Anti-Zionist">anti-Zionist</a>&nbsp;demonstration, but it ended with the killing of 5&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Egyptian Jews" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Egyptian_Jews">Egyptian Zionists</a>&nbsp;by a Muslim mob and over 300 other Jews were injured.</dd>
<dt>1945</dt>
<dd><a title="Bess Myerson" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bess_Myerson">Bess Myerson</a>&nbsp;was the first Jewish-American and the first&nbsp;<a title="Miss New York" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Miss_New_York">Miss New York</a>&nbsp;(competing as Miss New York City, a competition organized by a local radio station) to win the Miss America Pageant as Miss America 1945.&nbsp;As the only Jewish contestant, Myerson was encouraged by the pageant directors to change her name to "Bess Meredith"&nbsp;or "Beth Merrick"&nbsp;but she refused.&nbsp;After winning the title (and as a Jewish Miss America), Myerson received few endorsements&nbsp;and later recalled that "I couldn't even stay in certain hotels [...] there would be signs that read no coloreds, no Jews, no dogs. I felt so rejected. Here I was chosen to represent American womanhood and then America treated me like this."&nbsp;She thus cut short her Miss America tour and instead traveled with the&nbsp;<a title="Anti-Defamation League" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Anti-Defamation_League">Anti-Defamation League</a>. In this capacity, she spoke against discrimination in a talk entitled, "You Can't Be Beautiful and Hate."<sup id="cite_ref-wsjobitbm_57-2" class="reference"></sup></dd>
<dt>1945</dt>
<dd>The&nbsp;<a title="Krak&oacute;w pogrom" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Krak%C3%B3w_pogrom">Krak&oacute;w pogrom</a>&nbsp;was a post-WW2 pogrom, resulting in the death of&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Auschwitz" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Auschwitz">Auschwitz</a>&nbsp;survivor&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="R&oacute;ża Berger" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/R%C3%B3%C5%BCa_Berger">R&oacute;ża Berger</a>.</dd>
<dt>1946</dt>
<dd>The&nbsp;<a title="Kielce pogrom" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kielce_pogrom">Kielce pogrom</a>. 40 Jews were massacred and 80 other Jews were wounded out of about 200 who had returned home after&nbsp;<a title="World War II" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/World_War_II">World War II</a>&nbsp;had ended. 2 non-Jewish Poles were also killed. Controversy was caused by&nbsp;<a title="August Hlond" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/August_Hlond">August Hlond</a>'s reaction to the&nbsp;<a title="Kielce pogrom" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kielce_pogrom">Kielce pogrom</a>. While condemning murders, Hlond denied the racist nature of this crime.&nbsp;He saw the pogrom as a reaction against Jewish bureaucrats serving the Communist regime.&nbsp;This position was echoed by&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Cardinal Sapieha" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cardinal_Sapieha">Cardinal Sapieha</a>, who was reported to have said that the Jews brought it on themselves.</dd>
<dt>1946</dt>
<dd><a title="Nikita Khrushchev" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nikita_Khrushchev">Nikita Khrushchev</a>, then the first secretary of the&nbsp;<a title="Communist party" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Communist_party">Communist party</a>&nbsp;of&nbsp;<a title="Ukraine" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ukraine">Ukraine</a>, closes many synagogues (the number declines from 450 to 60) and prevents Jewish refugees from returning to their homes.</dd>
<dt>1946</dt>
<dd>The post-WW2&nbsp;<a title="Kunmadaras pogrom" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kunmadaras_pogrom">Kunmadaras pogrom</a>&nbsp;was the killing of 6 Jewish&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Holocaust" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Holocaust">Holocaust</a>&nbsp;survivors in&nbsp;<a title="Kunmadaras" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kunmadaras">Kunmadaras</a>,&nbsp;<a title="Hungary" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hungary">Hungary</a>.</dd>
<dt>1946</dt>
<dd>The&nbsp;<a title="Miskolc pogrom" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Miskolc_pogrom">Miskolc pogrom</a></dd>
<dt>1947</dt>
<dd><a title="1947 anti-Jewish riots in Aleppo" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1947_anti-Jewish_riots_in_Aleppo">Anti-Jewish riots erupt in Aleppo</a>, resulting in some 75 Jews murdered and several hundred wounded.</dd>
<dt>1947</dt>
<dd>A mob of Muslim sailors looted Jewish homes and shops in the&nbsp;<a title="1947 Manama riots" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1947_Manama_riots">Manama riots</a>. In the end one Jewish woman was dead and a Synagogue was destroyed.</dd>
<dt>1947</dt>
<dd><a title="1947 Aden riots" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1947_Aden_riots">A three-day riot</a>&nbsp;broke out between the&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Jews of Aden" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jews_of_Aden">Jews of Aden</a>&nbsp;and the local Muslim population. When it was over, 82 Jews were killed and 76 Jews were injured.</dd>
<dt>1947</dt>
<dd>In Austria, the&nbsp;<a title="Verbotsgesetz 1947" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Verbotsgesetz_1947">Verbotsgesetz 1947</a>&nbsp;provided the legal framework for the process of&nbsp;<a title="Denazification" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Denazification">denazification</a>&nbsp;in Austria and the suppression of any potential&nbsp;<a title="Neo-Nazism" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Neo-Nazism">revival of Nazism</a>. In 1992, it was amended to prohibit the denial or gross minimisation of the Holocaust.</dd>
</dl>
<blockquote class="templatequote">
<p><strong>National Socialism Prohibition Law (1947, amendments of 1992)</strong></p>
<p>&sect; 3g. He who operates in a manner characterized other than that in &sect; &sect; 3a &ndash; 3f will be punished (revitalising of the NSDAP or identification with), with imprisonment from one to up to ten years, and in cases of particularly dangerous suspects or activity, be punished with up to twenty years' imprisonment.</p>
<p>&sect; 3h. As an amendment to &sect; 3 g., whoever denies, grossly plays down, approves or tries to excuse the National Socialist genocide or other National Socialist crimes against humanity in a print publication, in broadcast or other media.</p>
</blockquote>
<dl>
<dt>1947, 5 December</dt>
<dd><a title="1947 Manama riots" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1947_Manama_riots">1947 Manama riots</a>.</dd>
<dt>1948&ndash;2001</dt>
<dd>Antisemitism played a major role in the&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Jewish exodus from Arab lands" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jewish_exodus_from_Arab_lands">Jewish exodus from Arab lands</a>. The Jewish population in the Arab&nbsp;<a title="Middle East" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Middle_East">Middle East</a>&nbsp;and&nbsp;<a title="North Africa" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/North_Africa">North Africa</a>&nbsp;has decreased from 900,000 in 1948 to less than 8,000 in 2001.</dd>
<dt>1948</dt>
<dd>The&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="1948 Anti-Jewish Riots in Oujda and Jerada" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1948_Anti-Jewish_Riots_in_Oujda_and_Jerada">Djereda</a>&nbsp;was a pogrom against the tiny Jewish population of&nbsp;<a title="Jerada" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jerada">Jerada</a>&nbsp;at the hands of the local Muslims. It ended with 43 Jews dead and around 150 Jews injured.</dd>
<dt>1948</dt>
<dd>The&nbsp;<a title="1948 Anti-Jewish riots in Tripolitania" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1948_Anti-Jewish_riots_in_Tripolitania">1948 Anti-Jewish riots in Tripolitania</a>&nbsp;was a riot between the Jewish and Arab populations of Tripoli. Unlike the&nbsp;<a title="1945 Anti-Jewish riots in Tripolitania" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1945_Anti-Jewish_riots_in_Tripolitania">previous Tripoli pogrom</a>, the Jewish community of Tripoli fought back against the Muslim rioters. When it was over, 14 Jews and 4 Muslims were dead and many on both sides were injured.</dd>
<dt>1948</dt>
<dd>The&nbsp;<a title="1948 Cairo bombings" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1948_Cairo_bombings">1948 Cairo bombings</a>&nbsp;were several bombings which targeted the&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Egyptian Jews" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Egyptian_Jews">Jewish population of Cairo</a>. The bombings claimed the lives of 70 Jews and 200 other Jews were wounded.</dd>
<dt>1948</dt>
<dd>The&nbsp;<a title="Southern Baptist Convention" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Southern_Baptist_Convention">Southern Baptist Convention</a>&nbsp;passed a resolution stating in part, "RESOLVED, That&nbsp;<a title="Communism" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Communism">communism</a>,&nbsp;<a title="Fascism" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fascism">fascism</a>, political ecclesiasticism, and anti-Semitism are utterly contrary to the genius of our Baptist concept of freedom and spiritual values."</dd>
<dt>1948</dt>
<dd><a title="Solomon Mikhoels" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solomon_Mikhoels">Solomon Mikhoels</a>, actor-director of the&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Moscow State Jewish Theater" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Moscow_State_Jewish_Theater">Moscow State Jewish Theater</a>&nbsp;and chairman of the&nbsp;<a title="Jewish Anti-Fascist Committee" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jewish_Anti-Fascist_Committee">Jewish Anti-Fascist Committee</a>&nbsp;is killed in a suspicious car accident (see&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="MGB (USSR)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/MGB_(USSR)">MGB</a>). Mass arrests of prominent Jewish intellectuals and suppression of Jewish culture follow under the banners of campaign on&nbsp;<em><a title="Rootless cosmopolitan" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Rootless_cosmopolitan">rootless cosmopolitanism</a></em>&nbsp;and&nbsp;<em><a title="Anti-Zionism" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Anti-Zionism">anti-Zionism</a></em>.</dd>
<dt>1948</dt>
<dd>During the&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Battle for Jerusalem (1948)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Battle_for_Jerusalem_(1948)">Siege of Jerusalem</a>&nbsp;of the&nbsp;<a title="1948 Arab&ndash;Israeli War" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1948_Arab%E2%80%93Israeli_War">1948 Arab&ndash;Israeli War</a>, Arab armies were able to conquer the part of the West Bank and Jerusalem; they expelled all Jews (about 2,000) from the&nbsp;<a title="Old City (Jerusalem)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Old_City_(Jerusalem)">Old City</a>&nbsp;(the&nbsp;<a title="Jewish Quarter (Jerusalem)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jewish_Quarter_(Jerusalem)">Jewish Quarter</a>) and destroyed the ancient synagogues that were in the Old City as well.</dd>
<dt>1949</dt>
<dd>The&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Menarsha synagogue attack" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Menarsha_synagogue_attack">Menarsha synagogue attack</a>&nbsp;was a grenade attack in the Jewish quarter of&nbsp;<a title="Damascus" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Damascus">Damascus</a>&nbsp;that took 12 lives.</dd>
</dl>
<h2><span id="1950s" class="mw-headline">1950s</span></h2>
<dl>
<dt>1952</dt>
<dd>The&nbsp;<a title="Night of the Murdered Poets" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Night_of_the_Murdered_Poets">Night of the Murdered Poets</a>. The thirteen most prominent Soviet Yiddish writers, poets, actors and other intellectuals were executed, among them&nbsp;<a title="Peretz Markish" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Peretz_Markish">Peretz Markish</a>,&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Leib Kwitko" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Leib_Kwitko">Leib Kwitko</a>,&nbsp;<a title="David Hofstein" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/David_Hofstein">David Hofstein</a>,&nbsp;<a title="Itzik Feffer" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Itzik_Feffer">Itzik Feffer</a>,&nbsp;<a title="David Bergelson" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/David_Bergelson">David Bergelson</a>.&nbsp;In 1955 UN General Assembly's session a high Soviet official still denied the "rumors" about their disappearance.</dd>
<dt>1952</dt>
<dd>The&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Prague Trials" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Prague_Trials">Prague Trials</a>&nbsp;in&nbsp;<a title="Czechoslovakia" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Czechoslovakia">Czechoslovakia</a>.</dd>
<dt>1953</dt>
<dd>The&nbsp;<a title="Doctors' plot" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Doctors%27_plot">Doctors' plot</a>&nbsp;false accusation in the&nbsp;<a title="Soviet Union" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Soviet_Union">USSR</a>. Scores of Soviet Jews dismissed from their jobs, arrested, some executed. The USSR was accused of pursuing a "new antisemitism."&nbsp;Stalinist opposition to "<a title="Rootless cosmopolitan" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Rootless_cosmopolitan">rootless cosmopolitans</a>" &ndash; a euphemism for Jews &ndash; was rooted in the belief, as expressed by&nbsp;<a title="Klement Gottwald" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Klement_Gottwald">Klement Gottwald</a>, that "treason and espionage infiltrate the ranks of the Communist Party. This channel is&nbsp;<a title="Zionism" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Zionism">Zionism</a>."&nbsp;This newer antisemitism was, in effect, a species of anti-Zionism.</dd>
<dt>1953</dt>
<dd>Holocaust Remembrance Day in Israel is inaugurated.</dd>
<dt>1956</dt>
<dd>The&nbsp;<a title="Alaska Mental Health Enabling Act" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Alaska_Mental_Health_Enabling_Act">Alaska Mental Health Enabling Act</a>&nbsp;of 1956 (<a class="mw-redirect" title="Act of Congress" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Act_of_Congress">Public Law</a>&nbsp;84-830) was an&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Act of Congress" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Act_of_Congress">Act of Congress</a>&nbsp;passed to improve&nbsp;<a title="Mental health" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mental_health">mental health</a>&nbsp;care in the United States&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Alaska Territory" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Alaska_Territory">territory</a>&nbsp;of&nbsp;<a title="Alaska" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Alaska">Alaska</a>. It became the focus of a major political controversy&nbsp;after opponents nicknamed it the "<a title="Siberia" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Siberia">Siberia</a>&nbsp;Bill" and denounced it as being part of a&nbsp;<a title="Communism" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Communism">communist</a>&nbsp;plot to hospitalize and&nbsp;<a title="Brainwashing" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Brainwashing">brainwash</a>&nbsp;Americans. Campaigners asserted that it was part of an international Jewish,&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Roman Catholic Church" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Roman_Catholic_Church">Roman Catholic</a>&nbsp;or&nbsp;<a title="Psychiatry" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Psychiatry">psychiatric</a>&nbsp;conspiracy intended to establish&nbsp;<a title="United Nations" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_Nations">United Nations</a>-run&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Concentration camp" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Concentration_camp">concentration camps</a>&nbsp;in the United States.</dd>
<dt>1956</dt>
<dd>Antisemitism swept across Poland as part of a purge of Stalinists.</dd>
<dt>1958</dt>
<dd>On 28 April 1958, Birmingham, Alabama, 54 sticks of&nbsp;<a title="Dynamite" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dynamite">dynamite</a>&nbsp;were placed outside&nbsp;<a title="Temple Beth-El (Birmingham, Alabama)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Temple_Beth-El_(Birmingham,_Alabama)">Temple Beth-El</a>&nbsp;in a bombing attempt. According to police reports, the burning fuses were doused by heavy rainfall, preventing the dynamite from exploding. Although the crime was never solved, police considered&nbsp;<a title="Bobby Frank Cherry" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bobby_Frank_Cherry">Bobby Frank Cherry</a>, later convicted of bombing the&nbsp;<a title="16th Street Baptist Church bombing" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/16th_Street_Baptist_Church_bombing">Sixteenth Street Baptist Church</a>, to be a suspect.</dd>
<dt>1958</dt>
<dd>The&nbsp;<a title="Hebrew Benevolent Congregation Temple bombing" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hebrew_Benevolent_Congregation_Temple_bombing">Hebrew Benevolent Congregation Temple bombing</a>&nbsp;occurred on 12 October 1958. The&nbsp;<a title="The Temple (Atlanta)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/The_Temple_(Atlanta)">Temple</a>, on&nbsp;<a title="Peachtree Street" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Peachtree_Street">Peachtree Street</a>&nbsp;in&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Atlanta, Georgia" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Atlanta,_Georgia">Atlanta, Georgia</a>, housed a&nbsp;<a title="Reform Judaism" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Reform_Judaism">Reform Jewish</a>&nbsp;congregation. The building was damaged extensively by the dynamite-fueled explosion, although no one was injured. Five suspects were arrested almost immediately after the bombing. One of them, George Bright, was tried twice. His first trial ended with a hung jury and his second with an acquittal. As a result of Bright's acquittal the other suspects were not tried, and no one was ever convicted of the bombing.</dd>
<dt>1959</dt>
<dd><em><a class="mw-redirect" title="Impeachment of Man" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Impeachment_of_Man">Impeachment of Man</a></em>&nbsp;is a book by&nbsp;<a title="Savitri Devi" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Savitri_Devi">Savitri Devi</a>, first published in 1959, in which she recounts a history of the general indifference toward the suffering of non-human life. She puts forth a pro-<a class="mw-redirect" title="Vegetarian" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vegetarian">vegetarian</a>, anti-<a title="Vivisection" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vivisection">vivisectionist</a>,&nbsp;<a title="Biocentrism (ethics)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Biocentrism_(ethics)">biocentric</a>, and&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Misanthropic" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Misanthropic">misanthropic</a>&nbsp;<a title="Conservation movement" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Conservation_movement">conservationist</a>&nbsp;point of view. However, she does so within the context of her pro-<a class="mw-redirect" title="Hitler" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hitler">Hitler</a>&nbsp;and pro-<a title="Nazism" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nazism">Nazi</a>&nbsp;political views, and devotes space to antisemitism and denouncing Jewish dietary practices.</dd>
<dt>1959</dt>
<dd>On 21 March 1959,&nbsp;<a title="Pope John XXIII" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pope_John_XXIII">Pope John XXIII</a>&nbsp;ordered that the word "faithless" (<a class="mw-redirect" title="Latin language" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Latin_language">Latin</a>:&nbsp;<em lang="la">perfidis</em>) be removed from the prayer for the conversion of the Jews,&nbsp;actually interrupting the Service and asking the prayer to be repeated without that word.&nbsp;This word had caused much trouble in recent times because of misconceptions that the&nbsp;<a title="Latin" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Latin">Latin</a>&nbsp;<em>perfidis</em>&nbsp;was equivalent to "<a class="extiw" title="wiktionary:perfidious" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/perfidious">perfidious</a>", giving birth to the view that the prayer accused the Jews of treachery (perfidy), though the word is more correctly translated as "faithless" or "unbelieving". Accordingly, the prayer was revised to read:</dd>
<dd>Let us pray also for the Jews: that almighty God may remove the veil from their hearts; so that they too may acknowledge Jesus Christ our Lord. Let us pray. Let us kneel. Arise. Almighty and eternal God, who dost also not exclude from thy mercy the Jews: hear our prayers, which we offer for the blindness of that people; that acknowledging the light of thy Truth, which is Christ, they may be delivered from their darkness. Through the same our Lord Jesus Christ, who liveth and reigneth with thee in the unity of the Holy Spirit, God, for ever and ever. Amen.&nbsp;On Good Friday of 1963,&nbsp;by mistake the old text of the prayer was given to the deacon, who read "perfidis".&nbsp;<a title="Pope John XXIII" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pope_John_XXIII">Pope John XXIII</a>&nbsp;interrupted the liturgy again, and ordered that the prayer be repeated with the word omitted.</dd>
</dl>
<h2><span id="1960s" class="mw-headline">1960s</span></h2>
<dl>
<dt>1960s</dt>
<dd>Chess player&nbsp;<a title="Bobby Fischer" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bobby_Fischer">Bobby Fischer</a>&nbsp;made numerous anti-Jewish statements and professed a general hatred for Jews since at least the early 1960s.&nbsp;Although Fischer described his mother as Jewish in a 1962 interview,&nbsp;he later denied his Jewish ancestry.</dd>
<dt>1960</dt>
<dd>The Badges Act 1960 (Abzeichengesetz 1960) prohibits the public display of Nazi symbols in Austria, and violations are punishable by up to &euro;4000.- fine and up to 1 month imprisonment.</dd>
<dt>1960</dt>
<dd>On 25 March, 1960, the synagogue&nbsp;<a title="Congregation Beth Israel (Gadsden, Alabama)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Congregation_Beth_Israel_(Gadsden,_Alabama)">Congregation Beth Israel</a>&nbsp;and its members were subject to an&nbsp;<a title="Antisemitism" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Antisemitism">antisemitic</a>&nbsp;attack. About 180 members were attending a Friday evening service to dedicate the new Zemurray Social Hall, and led by then-rabbi Saul Rubin and Rev. John Speaks and Dr. Franklin Denson of First Methodist Church, when windows were smashed and the synagogue&nbsp;<a title="Firebombing" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Firebombing">fire-bombed</a>. Two members&mdash;Alvin Lowi and Alan Cohn&mdash;who rushed out to see what was happening were met by Jerry Hunt, a 16-year-old&nbsp;<a title="Neo-Nazism" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Neo-Nazism">Nazi sympathizer</a>, who wounded them both with a&nbsp;<a title="Shotgun" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Shotgun">shotgun</a>, then fled. Lowi was just shot in the hand, but one of Cohn's aortas was nicked, and he almost died, requiring 22 US pints (10&nbsp;l) of blood.&nbsp;Earlier that week Hunt had attended a rally for antisemitic and&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="White supremacism" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/White_supremacism">white supremacist</a>&nbsp;politician&nbsp;<a title="John G. Crommelin" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/John_G._Crommelin">John G. Crommelin</a>, and had had a fight with a Jewish boy over a chess game at the Gadsden Community Centre.</dd>
<dt>1961</dt>
<dd>In 1961, a prot&eacute;g&eacute; of&nbsp;<a title="Harry Elmer Barnes" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Harry_Elmer_Barnes">Harry Elmer Barnes</a>,&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="David Hoggan" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/David_Hoggan">David Hoggan</a>&nbsp;published&nbsp;<em>Der Erzwungene Krieg</em>&nbsp;(<em>The Forced War</em>) in West Germany, which claimed that Germany had been the victim of an Anglo-Polish conspiracy in 1939. Though&nbsp;<em>Der Erzwungene Krieg</em>&nbsp;was primarily concerned with the origins of World War II, it also down-played or justified the effects of Nazi&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Antisemitic" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Antisemitic">antisemitic</a>&nbsp;measures in the pre-1939 period.&nbsp;For example, Hoggan justified the huge one billion&nbsp;<em>Reich</em>-mark fine imposed on the entire Jewish community in Germany after the 1938&nbsp;<em><a title="Kristallnacht" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kristallnacht">Kristallnacht</a></em>&nbsp;as a reasonable measure to prevent what he called "Jewish profiteering" at the expense of German insurance companies and alleged that no Jews were killed in the&nbsp;<em>Kristallnacht</em>&nbsp;(in fact, 91 German Jews were killed in the&nbsp;<em>Kristallnacht</em>).</dd>
<dt>1962</dt>
<dd>In his 1962 pamphlet,&nbsp;<em>Revisionism and Brainwashing</em>,&nbsp;<a title="Harry Elmer Barnes" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Harry_Elmer_Barnes">Harry Elmer Barnes</a>&nbsp;claimed that there was a "lack of any serious opposition or concerted challenge to the atrocity stories and other modes of defamation of German national character and conduct".&nbsp;Barnes argued that there was "a failure to point out the atrocities of the Allies were more brutal, painful, mortal and numerous than the most extreme allegations made against the Germans".&nbsp;He claimed that in order to justify the "horrors and evils of the Second World War", the Allies made the Nazis the "scapegoat" for their own misdeeds.</dd>
<dt>1963</dt>
<dd>"Judaism Without Embellishments" published by the Academy of Sciences of the Ukrainian SSR in 1963.</dd>
<dt>1964</dt>
<dd>In a 1964 article, "Zionist Fraud", published in the&nbsp;<em><a class="mw-redirect" title="American Mercury" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/American_Mercury">American Mercury</a></em>,&nbsp;<a title="Harry Elmer Barnes" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Harry_Elmer_Barnes">Harry Elmer Barnes</a>&nbsp;wrote: "The courageous author [Rassinier] lays the chief blame for misrepresentation on those whom we must call the swindlers of the crematoria, the Israeli politicians who derive billions of marks from nonexistent, mythical and imaginary cadavers, whose numbers have been reckoned in an unusually distorted and dishonest manner."&nbsp;Using Rassinier as his source, Barnes claimed that Germany was the victim of aggression in both 1914 and 1939, and that reports of the Holocaust were propaganda to justify a war of aggression against Germany.</dd>
<dt>1964</dt>
<dd><a title="Gamal Abdel Nasser" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gamal_Abdel_Nasser">Nasser</a>&nbsp;told a German newspaper in 1964 that "no person, not even the most simple one, takes seriously the lie of the six million Jews that were murdered [in the Holocaust]."<sup id="cite_ref-92" class="reference"></sup></dd>
<dt>1964</dt>
<dd>The&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Roman Catholic Church" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Roman_Catholic_Church">Roman Catholic Church</a>&nbsp;under&nbsp;<a title="Pope Paul VI" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pope_Paul_VI">Pope Paul VI</a>&nbsp;issues the document&nbsp;<em><a title="Nostra aetate" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nostra_aetate">Nostra aetate</a></em>&nbsp;as part of&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Vatican II" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vatican_II">Vatican II</a>, repudiating the doctrine of&nbsp;<a class="new" title="Jewish guilt (page does not exist)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Jewish_guilt&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1">Jewish guilt</a>&nbsp;for the&nbsp;<a title="Crucifixion" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Crucifixion">Crucifixion</a>.</dd>
<dt>1964</dt>
<dd>In 1964, French historian&nbsp;<a title="Paul Rassinier" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Paul_Rassinier">Paul Rassinier</a>&nbsp;published&nbsp;<em>The Drama of the European Jews</em>. Rassinier was himself a concentration camp survivor (he was held in&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Buchenwald" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Buchenwald">Buchenwald</a>&nbsp;for having helped French Jews escape the Nazis), and modern-day holocaust deniers continue to cite his works as scholarly research that questions the accepted facts of the Holocaust. Critics argued that Rassinier did not cite evidence for his claims and ignored information that contradicted his assertions; he nevertheless remains influential in Holocaust denial circles for being one of the first deniers to propose that a vast Zionist/Allied/Soviet conspiracy faked the Holocaust, a theme that would be picked up in later years by other authors.</dd>
<dt>1964</dt>
<dd>The&nbsp;<a title="Civil Rights Act of 1964" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Civil_Rights_Act_of_1964">Civil Rights Act of 1964</a>&nbsp;(<a class="mw-redirect" title="Act of Congress" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Act_of_Congress">Pub.L.</a>&nbsp;<a class="external text" href="http://legislink.org/us/pl-88-352" rel="nofollow">88&ndash;352</a>, 78&nbsp;<a title="United States Statutes at Large" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States_Statutes_at_Large">Stat.</a>&nbsp;<a class="external text" href="http://legislink.org/us/stat-78-241" rel="nofollow">241</a>, enacted July&nbsp;2, 1964) is a landmark piece of&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Civil rights" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Civil_rights">civil rights</a>&nbsp;legislation in the&nbsp;<a title="United States" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States">United States</a>&nbsp;that outlawed discrimination based on religion, race, color, sex, or national origin.</dd>
<dt>1965</dt>
<dd>The&nbsp;<a title="Frankfurt Auschwitz trials" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Frankfurt_Auschwitz_trials">Frankfurt Auschwitz trials</a>, known in&nbsp;<a title="German language" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/German_language">German</a>&nbsp;as&nbsp;<em>der Auschwitz-Prozess</em>, or&nbsp;<em>der zweite Auschwitz-Prozess,</em>&nbsp;(the "second Auschwitz trial") was a series of trials running from 20 December 1963 to 19 August 1965, charging 22 defendants under German&nbsp;<a title="Criminal law" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Criminal_law">criminal law</a>&nbsp;for their roles in the&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Holocaust" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Holocaust">Holocaust</a>&nbsp;as mid- to lower-level officials in the&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Auschwitz-Birkenau" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Auschwitz-Birkenau">Auschwitz-Birkenau</a>&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Death camp" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Death_camp">death</a>&nbsp;and&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Concentration camp" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Concentration_camp">concentration camp</a>&nbsp;complex.&nbsp;<a title="Hans Hofmeyer" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hans_Hofmeyer">Hans Hofmeyer</a>&nbsp;led as Chief Judge the "criminal case against&nbsp;<a title="Robert Mulka" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Robert_Mulka">Mulka</a>&nbsp;and others" (reference number 4 Ks 2/63).</dd>
<dd>Overall, only 789 individuals of the approximately 6,500 surviving&nbsp;<em>SS</em>&nbsp;personnel who served at Auschwitz and its sub-camps were ever tried, of which 750 received sentences.&nbsp;Unlike the first trial in Poland held almost two decades earlier, the trials in Frankfurt were not based on the legal definition of&nbsp;<a title="Crimes against humanity" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Crimes_against_humanity">crimes against humanity</a>&nbsp;as recognized by international law, but according to the state laws of the Federal Republic.</dd>
<dt>1967</dt>
<dd><a title="Allen Ginsberg" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Allen_Ginsberg">Allen Ginsberg</a>&nbsp;stated that, in a private conversation in 1967,&nbsp;<a title="Ezra Pound" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ezra_Pound">Ezra Pound</a>&nbsp;told the young poet, "my poems don't make sense." He went on to supposedly call himself a "moron", to characterize his writing as "stupid and ignorant", "a mess". Ginsberg reassured Pound that he "had shown us the way", but Pound refused to be mollified:</dd>
</dl>
<blockquote>
<p>'Any good I've done has been spoiled by bad intentions &ndash; the preoccupation with irrelevant and stupid things,' [he] replied. Then very slowly, with emphasis, surely conscious of Ginsberg's being Jewish: 'But the worst mistake I made was that stupid, suburban prejudice of anti-semitism.'</p>
</blockquote>
<dl>
<dt>1967</dt>
<dd>In 1967,&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Congregation Beth Israel (Jackson, Mississippi)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Congregation_Beth_Israel_(Jackson,_Mississippi)">Congregation Beth Israel</a>&nbsp;moved to its current location, a building on Old Canton Road&nbsp;described by&nbsp;<a title="Jack Nelson (journalist)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jack_Nelson_(journalist)">Jack Nelson</a>&nbsp;as "an octagonal structure dominated by a massive roof".&nbsp;On 18 September 1967 the new building was wrecked by a dynamite bomb placed by Klan members in a recessed doorway.&nbsp;According to Nelson, the explosion had "ripped through administrative offices and a conference room, torn a hole in the ceiling, blown out windows, ruptured a water pipe and buckled a wall."&nbsp;The perpetrators were not discovered.&nbsp;In November of that year the same group planted a bomb that blew out the front of the house of Dr. Perry Nussbaum (Beth Israel's rabbi from 1954 to 1973), while he and his wife were sleeping there.<sup id="cite_ref-Chalmers2003p82_103-1" class="reference"></sup></dd>
<dt>1967</dt>
<dd>All Jewish men in Egypt were placed in camps in 1967 during the&nbsp;<a title="Six-Day War" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Six-Day_War">Six-Day War</a>, and they were kept there for more than two years;&nbsp;<a title="Karaite Judaism" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Karaite_Judaism">Karaite Jews</a>&nbsp;were the last to leave.</dd>
<dt>1968&ndash;1971</dt>
<dd>State-supported anti-Semitism swept across Poland in 1968, not subsiding until 1971, by which time half of Poland's Jews had fled Poland.</dd>
<dt>1968</dt>
<dd>During the&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="American Civil Rights Movement" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/American_Civil_Rights_Movement">American Civil Rights Movement</a>&nbsp;in the 1960s, the leadership of&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Congregation Beth Israel (Jackson, Mississippi)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Congregation_Beth_Israel_(Jackson,_Mississippi)">Beth Israel</a>&nbsp;spoke out against the&nbsp;<a title="Ku Klux Klan" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ku_Klux_Klan">Ku Klux Klan</a>'s attacks on black churches. In response, Thomas Tarrants of&nbsp;<a title="Mobile, Alabama" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mobile,_Alabama">Mobile, Alabama</a>, who had helped bomb the synagogue building of a different synagogue,&nbsp;<a title="Beth Israel Congregation (Jackson, Mississippi)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Beth_Israel_Congregation_(Jackson,_Mississippi)">Beth Israel Congregation</a>, and its rabbi's house there (see previous entry in this timeline) bombed Beth Israel's education building on 28 May 1968.&nbsp;The force of the blast knocked down several walls of the education building and caved in part of the roof while also destroying a door at the opposite end of the synagogue building.&nbsp;A hole approximately 24 inches (61&nbsp;cm) in diameter was left in the concrete floor, and damages were estimated to be around $50,000 (equivalent to $368,000 today).&nbsp;According to Sammy Feltenstein, past president of Congregation Beth Israel, pieces of stained glass that survived the bombing were salvaged and adorn the front window of the synagogue today.&nbsp;Later that year, on 30 June, Tarrants&nbsp;returned to Meridian to bomb the home of Meyer Davidson, an outspoken leader of the Jewish community, on 29th Avenue.<span style="font-size: xx-small;">&nbsp;</span>&nbsp;But the&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="FBI" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/FBI">FBI</a>&nbsp;and police chief Roy Gunn convinced Raymond and Alton Wayne Roberts, local Klan members, to gather information about the Klan's operations, and leaders of the Jewish communities in Jackson and in Meridian had raised money to pay the two informants, who tipped off the FBI about the attack before it happened.</dd>
<dt>1969</dt>
<dd><a class="mw-redirect" title="David Hoggan" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/David_Hoggan">David Hoggan</a>&nbsp;explicitly denied the Holocaust in 1969 in a book entitled&nbsp;<em>The Myth of the Six Million</em>, which was published by the&nbsp;<a title="Noontide Press" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Noontide_Press">Noontide Press</a>, a small Los Angeles publisher specializing in antisemitic literature.</dd>
<dt>1960s&ndash;1991</dt>
<dd>The rise of&nbsp;<em><a class="mw-redirect" title="Zionology" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Zionology">Zionology</a></em>&nbsp;in the&nbsp;<a title="Soviet Union" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Soviet_Union">Soviet Union</a>. In 1983, the Department of Propaganda and the&nbsp;<a title="KGB" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/KGB">KGB</a>'s&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Anti-Zionist committee of the Soviet public" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Anti-Zionist_committee_of_the_Soviet_public">Anti-Zionist committee of the Soviet public</a>&nbsp;orchestrates formally "anti-Zionist" campaign.</dd>
<dt>1968</dt>
<dd><a title="1968 Polish political crisis" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1968_Polish_political_crisis">Polish 1968 political crisis</a>. The state-organized antisemitic campaign in the&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="People's Republic of Poland" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/People%27s_Republic_of_Poland">People's Republic of Poland</a>&nbsp;under guise of "anti-Zionism" drives out most of remaining Jewish population.</dd>
<dt>1968</dt>
<dd>The ancient Jewish community of&nbsp;<a title="Hebron" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hebron">Hebron</a>, which had been destroyed in the&nbsp;<a title="1929 Hebron massacre" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1929_Hebron_massacre">1929 Hebron massacre</a>, is revived at&nbsp;<a title="Kiryat Arba" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kiryat_Arba">Kiryat Arba</a>. The community, in 1979 and afterwards, moves into Hebron proper and rebuilds the demolished&nbsp;<a title="Avraham Avinu Synagogue" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Avraham_Avinu_Synagogue">Abraham Avinu Synagogue</a>, the site of which had been used by&nbsp;<a title="Jordan" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jordan">Jordan</a>&nbsp;as a cattle-pen.</dd>
<dt>1968</dt>
<dd>The&nbsp;<a title="Alhambra Decree" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Alhambra_Decree">Alhambra Decree</a>&nbsp;was formally revoked on 16 December 1968.</dd>
<dt>1968</dt>
<dd>The&nbsp;<em><a class="mw-redirect" title="Fair Housing Act" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fair_Housing_Act">Fair Housing Act</a></em>&nbsp;(Title VIII of the&nbsp;<em>Civil Rights Act of 1968</em>) in the United States introduced meaningful federal enforcement mechanisms. It outlawed:</dd>
</dl>
<ul>
<li>Refusal to sell or rent a dwelling to any person because of&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Race (human classification)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Race_(human_classification)">race</a>,&nbsp;<a title="Human skin color" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human_skin_color">color</a>,&nbsp;<a title="Religion" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Religion">religion</a>,&nbsp;<a title="Sex" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sex">sex</a>, or&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="National origin" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/National_origin">national origin</a>.</li>
<li>Discrimination based on race, color, religion or national origin in the terms, conditions or privilege of the sale or rental of a dwelling.</li>
<li>Advertising the sale or rental of a dwelling indicating preference of discrimination based on race, color, religion or national origin.</li>
<li>Coercing, threatening, intimidating, or interfering with a person's enjoyment or exercise of housing rights based on discriminatory reasons or retaliating against a person or organization that aids or encourages the exercise or enjoyment of fair housing rights.</li>
</ul>
<dl>
<dt>1969 November 9</dt>
<dd><a title="Tupamaros West-Berlin" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tupamaros_West-Berlin">Tupamaros West-Berlin</a>&nbsp;attempted to bomb of&nbsp;<a title="West Berlin" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/West_Berlin">West Berlin</a>'s&nbsp;<a title="Fasanenstrasse Synagogue" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fasanenstrasse_Synagogue#Jewish_Community_Center">Jewish Community Centre</a>. The bomb, supplied by the undercover government agent&nbsp;<a title="Peter Urbach" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Peter_Urbach">Peter Urbach</a>, failed to explode.<sup id="cite_ref-116" class="reference"></sup></dd>
</dl>
<h2><span id="1970s" class="mw-headline">1970s</span></h2>
<dl>
<dt>1970s</dt>
<dd><a title="Lyndon LaRouche" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lyndon_LaRouche">Lyndon LaRouche</a>&nbsp;and his ideas have been called antisemitic since at least the mid-1970s by dozens of individuals and organizations in countries across Europe and North America. LaRouche and his followers have responded to these allegations by claiming that LaRouche has Jewish supporters and by denying the accusations.</dd>
<dt>1970</dt>
<dd>Canada has no legislation specifically restricting the ownership, display, purchase, import or export of Nazi flags. However, sections 318&ndash;320 of the Criminal Code,&nbsp;adopted by&nbsp;<a title="Parliament of Canada" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Parliament_of_Canada">Canada's parliament</a>&nbsp;in 1970 and based in large part on the 1965 Cohen Committee recommendations,&nbsp;provide law enforcement agencies with broad scope to intervene if such flags are used to communicate hatred in a public place (particularly sections 319(1), 319(2), and 319(7).</dd>
<dt>1970</dt>
<dd>After the&nbsp;<a title="Second Vatican Council" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Second_Vatican_Council">Second Vatican Council</a>, the&nbsp;<a title="Good Friday prayer for the Jews" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Good_Friday_prayer_for_the_Jews">Good Friday prayer for the Jews</a>&nbsp;was completely revised for the 1970 edition of the Roman Missal. Because of the possibility of a misinterpretation similar to that of the word "perfidis" (see above in 1959), the reference to the veil on the hearts of the Jews, which was based on&nbsp;<a class="external text" href="https://bible.oremus.org/?passage=2+Corinthians+3:14%E2%80%933:14&amp;version=nrsv" rel="nofollow">2 Corinthians 3:14</a>, was removed. The 1973&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="ICEL" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/ICEL">ICEL</a>&nbsp;English translation of the revised prayer is as follows:</dd>
<dd>Let us pray for the Jewish people, the first to hear the word of God, that they may continue to grow in the love of his name and in faithfulness to his covenant. (<em>Prayer in silence. Then the&nbsp;<a title="Priest" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Priest">priest</a>&nbsp;says:</em>) Almighty and eternal God, long ago you gave your promise to Abraham and his posterity. Listen to your Church as we pray that the people you first made your own may arrive at the fullness of redemption. We ask this through Christ our Lord. Amen.</dd>
<dt>1971</dt>
<dd>The ban on Jewish immigration to Israel from the Soviet Union was lifted in 1971 leading to the&nbsp;<a title="1970s Soviet Union aliyah" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1970s_Soviet_Union_aliyah">1970s Soviet Union aliyah</a>.</dd>
<dt>1971</dt>
<dd>The&nbsp;<a title="Southern Baptist Convention" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Southern_Baptist_Convention">Southern Baptist Convention</a>&nbsp;passed a resolution stating in part, "we point out particularly one area of concern known as anti-Semitism, which some think erroneously is inherent in Christianity, and which we disavow."</dd>
<dt>1971</dt>
<dd>To further the goal of reconciliation, the Catholic Church established an internal&nbsp;<a title="International Catholic-Jewish Liaison Committee" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/International_Catholic-Jewish_Liaison_Committee">International Catholic-Jewish Liaison Committee</a>&nbsp;and the&nbsp;<a title="Mordecai Waxman" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mordecai_Waxman">International Jewish Committee for Interreligious Consultations</a>. (This Committee is not a part of the Church's&nbsp;<a title="Magisterium" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Magisterium">Magisterium</a>.)</dd>
<dt>1972</dt>
<dd>The&nbsp;<a title="Southern Baptist Convention" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Southern_Baptist_Convention">Southern Baptist Convention</a>&nbsp;passed a "Resolution on Anti-Semitism" stating in part:</dd>
