<dd>"Therefore, be it RESOLVED, That this Convention go on record as opposed to any and all forms of anti-Semitism; that it declare anti-Semitism unchristian; that we messengers to this Convention pledge ourselves to combat anti-Semitism in every honorable, Christian way."</dd>
<dd>"Be it further RESOLVED, That Southern Baptists covenant to work positively to replace all anti-Semitic bias with the Christian attitude and practice of love for Jews, who along with all other men, are equally beloved of God."</dd>
<dt>1972</dt>
<dd>11 Israeli Olympic athletes are taken hostage and eventually tortured and killed in the&nbsp;<a title="Munich massacre" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Munich_massacre">Munich massacre</a>.</dd>
<dt>1974</dt>
<dd>Four Jewish girls were raped, murdered and mutilated after attempting to flee to Israel. Their bodies were discovered by border police in a cave in the&nbsp;<a title="Al-Zabadani" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Al-Zabadani">Zabdani Mountains</a>&nbsp;northwest of Damascus along with the remains of two Jewish boys, Natan Shaya 18 and Kassem Abadi 20, victims of an earlier massacre.&nbsp;Syrian authorities deposited the bodies of all six in sacks before the homes of their parents in the Jewish ghetto in Damascus.</dd>
<dt>1974</dt>
<dd><em><a title="Did Six Million Really Die?" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Did_Six_Million_Really_Die%3F">Did Six Million Really Die? The Truth at Last</a></em>&nbsp;is a Holocaust denial pamphlet allegedly written by&nbsp;<a title="Great Britain" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Great_Britain">British</a>&nbsp;<a title="National Front (UK)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/National_Front_(UK)">National Front</a>&nbsp;member&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Richard Verrall (political writer)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Richard_Verrall_(political_writer)">Richard Verrall</a>&nbsp;under the pseudonym&nbsp;<em>Richard E. Harwood</em>&nbsp;and published by&nbsp;<a title="Ernst Z&uuml;ndel" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ernst_Z%C3%BCndel">Ernst Z&uuml;ndel</a>&nbsp;in 1974.</dd>
<dt>1975</dt>
<dd>The United Nations passed a resolution determining that "Zionism is a form of racism and racial discrimination." (It was revoked in 1991, as mentioned below.)</dd>
<dt>1976</dt>
<dd><a title="Arthur Butz" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arthur_Butz">Arthur Butz</a>'s&nbsp;<em><a title="The Hoax of the Twentieth Century" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/The_Hoax_of_the_Twentieth_Century">The Hoax of the Twentieth Century</a>: The case against the presumed extermination of European Jewry</em>&nbsp;was published.</dd>
<dt>1977</dt>
<dd><a title="David Irving" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/David_Irving">David Irving</a>'s Holocaust denying book&nbsp;<em><a title="Hitler's War" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hitler%27s_War">Hitler's War</a></em>&nbsp;was published.</dd>
<dt>1977 March 9&ndash;11</dt>
<dd><a title="1977 Washington, D.C. attack and hostage taking" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1977_Washington,_D.C._attack_and_hostage_taking">1977 Washington, D.C. attack and hostage taking</a>.</dd>
<dt>1977 October 3</dt>
<dd>In suburban&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="St. Louis, Missouri" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/St._Louis,_Missouri">St. Louis, Missouri</a>,&nbsp;<a title="Joseph Paul Franklin" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Joseph_Paul_Franklin">Joseph Paul Franklin</a>&nbsp;hid in the bushes near a&nbsp;<a title="Shaare Zedek Synagogue (University City, Missouri)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Shaare_Zedek_Synagogue_(University_City,_Missouri)">Shaare Zedek Synagogue (University City, Missouri)</a>&nbsp;and fired on a group attending services. In this incident, Franklin killed forty-two-year-old Gerald Gordon and wounded Steven Goldman and William Ash.</dd>
<dt>1977</dt>
<dd>In a 1977&nbsp;<em>Globe-Democrat</em>&nbsp;column discussing&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="John Toland (author)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/John_Toland_(author)">John Toland</a>'s biography of&nbsp;<a title="Adolf Hitler" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Adolf_Hitler">Adolf Hitler</a>,&nbsp;<a title="Pat Buchanan" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pat_Buchanan">Pat Buchanan</a>&nbsp;wrote:
<blockquote class="templatequote">
<p>Though Hitler was indeed racist and anti-Semitic to the core, a man who without compunction could commit murder and genocide, he was also an individual of great courage, a soldier's soldier in the Great War, a political organizer of the first rank, a leader steeped in the history of Europe, who possessed oratorical powers that could awe even those who despised him... Hitler's success was not based on his extraordinary gifts alone. His genius was an intuitive sense of the mushiness, the character flaws, the weakness masquerading as morality that was in the hearts of the statesmen who stood in his path.</p>
</blockquote>
</dd>
<dd>Buchanan supporters say the paragraph is taken out of context. They point out that in the same review Buchanan praised&nbsp;<a title="Winston Churchill" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Winston_Churchill">Winston Churchill</a>&nbsp;for seeing that "Hitler was marching along the road toward a New Order where Western civilization would not survive" and concluded that modern-day statesmen were not following that example.</dd>
<dt>1977</dt>
<dd><em><a title="National Socialist Party of America v. Village of Skokie" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/National_Socialist_Party_of_America_v._Village_of_Skokie">National Socialist Party of America v. Village of Skokie</a></em>,&nbsp;<a title="Case citation" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Case_citation">432 U.S. 43</a>&nbsp;(1977) (also known as&nbsp;<em><a class="mw-redirect" title="Smith v. Collin" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Smith_v._Collin">Smith v. Collin</a></em>; sometimes referred to as the&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Skokie Affair" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Skokie_Affair">Skokie Affair</a>), was a&nbsp;<a title="Supreme Court of the United States" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Supreme_Court_of_the_United_States">United States Supreme Court</a>&nbsp;case dealing with&nbsp;<a title="Freedom of assembly" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Freedom_of_assembly">freedom of assembly</a>. The outcome was that the Illinois Supreme Court ruled that the use of the&nbsp;<a title="Swastika" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Swastika">swastika</a>&nbsp;is a symbolic form of free speech entitled to&nbsp;<a title="First Amendment to the United States Constitution" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/First_Amendment_to_the_United_States_Constitution">First Amendment</a>&nbsp;protections and determined that the swastika itself did not constitute "<a title="Fighting words" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fighting_words">fighting words</a>." Its ruling allowed the National Socialist Party of America to march.<sup id="cite_ref-caselaw.lp.findlaw.com_128-0" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_antisemitism_in_the_20th_century#cite_note-caselaw.lp.findlaw.com-128">[128]</a></sup></dd>
<dt>1978</dt>
<dd>In 1978&nbsp;<a title="Willis Carto" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Willis_Carto">Willis Carto</a>&nbsp;founded the&nbsp;<a title="Institute for Historical Review" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Institute_for_Historical_Review">Institute for Historical Review</a>&nbsp;(IHR), an organization dedicated to publicly challenging the commonly accepted history of the Holocaust.</dd>
<dt>1978/1979</dt>
<dd>In December 1978 and January 1979,&nbsp;<a title="Robert Faurisson" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Robert_Faurisson">Robert Faurisson</a>, a French professor of literature at the&nbsp;<a title="University of Lyon" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/University_of_Lyon">University of Lyon</a>, wrote two letters to&nbsp;<em><a title="Le Monde" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Le_Monde">Le Monde</a></em>&nbsp;claiming that the&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Gas chambers" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gas_chambers">gas chambers</a>&nbsp;used by the Nazis to exterminate the Jews did not exist.</dd>
<dt>1979</dt>
<dd>A House Joint resolution 1014 designated 28 and 29 April 1979 as "<a class="mw-redirect" title="The Days of Remembrance of the Victims of the Holocaust (DRVH)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/The_Days_of_Remembrance_of_the_Victims_of_the_Holocaust_(DRVH)">The Days of Remembrance of the Victims of the Holocaust (DRVH)</a>." After that the Days of Remembrance of the Victims of the Holocaust (DRVH) has been an annual 8-day period designated by the United States Congress for civic commemorations and special educational programs that help citizens remember and draw lessons from the Holocaust.</dd>
<dt>1979</dt>
<dd>When the&nbsp;<a title="Anti-Defamation League" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Anti-Defamation_League">Anti-Defamation League</a>&nbsp;accused&nbsp;<a title="Lyndon LaRouche" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lyndon_LaRouche">Lyndon LaRouche</a>&nbsp;of antisemitism in 1979, he filed a $26-million libel suit; however, the case failed when Justice Michael Dontzin of the New York Supreme Court ruled that it was&nbsp;<a title="Fair comment" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fair_comment">fair comment</a>, and that the facts "reasonably give rise" to that description.<sup id="cite_ref-131" class="reference"></sup></dd>
<dt>1979</dt>
<dd>"Jewish Princess" is a song by&nbsp;<a title="Frank Zappa" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Frank_Zappa">Frank Zappa</a>&nbsp;released on his album&nbsp;<em><a title="Sheik Yerbouti" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sheik_Yerbouti">Sheik Yerbouti</a></em>&nbsp;in 1979. The song is a humorous look at the&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Jewish-American princess stereotype" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jewish-American_princess_stereotype">Jewish-American princess stereotype</a>&nbsp;which attracted attention from the&nbsp;<a title="Anti-Defamation League" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Anti-Defamation_League">Anti-Defamation League</a>, to which Zappa denied an apology, arguing: "Unlike the unicorn, such creatures do exist &ndash; and deserve to be 'commemorated' with their own special opus". In an interview with&nbsp;<a title="Spin (magazine)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Spin_(magazine)">Spin</a>&nbsp;magazine he was almost offended saying, "...as if to say there is no such thing as a Jewish Princess. Like I invented this?"&nbsp;Biographer Barry Miles claimed in his book,&nbsp;<em>Frank Zappa</em>&nbsp;(Atlantic Books of London, 2005), that the ADL asked the Federal Communications Commission (FCC) to ban the record from being played on the air &ndash; a symbolic effort given that the song was not being played anyway.</dd>
</dl>
<h2><span id="1980s" class="mw-headline">1980s</span></h2>
<dl>
<dt>1980, 27 July</dt>
<dd><a title="1980 Antwerp attack" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1980_Antwerp_attack">1980 Antwerp attack</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-WaPoAttack_134-0" class="reference"></sup></dd>
<dt>1980, 3 October</dt>
<dd><a title="1980 Paris synagogue bombing" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1980_Paris_synagogue_bombing">1980 Paris synagogue bombing</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-138" class="reference"></sup></dd>
<dt>1980</dt>
<dd>In 1980, the&nbsp;<a title="Institute for Historical Review" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Institute_for_Historical_Review">Institute for Historical Review</a>&nbsp;promised a $50,000 reward to anyone who could prove that Jews were gassed at Auschwitz.&nbsp;<a title="Mel Mermelstein" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mel_Mermelstein">Mel Mermelstein</a>&nbsp;wrote a&nbsp;<a title="Letter to the editor" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Letter_to_the_editor">letter to the editors</a>&nbsp;of the&nbsp;<em><a class="mw-redirect" title="LA Times" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/LA_Times">LA Times</a></em>&nbsp;and others including&nbsp;<em><a title="The Jerusalem Post" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/The_Jerusalem_Post">The Jerusalem Post</a></em>. The IHR wrote back, offering him $50,000 for proof that Jews were, in fact, gassed in the gas chambers at Auschwitz. Mermelstein, in turn, submitted a notarized account of his internment at Auschwitz and how he witnessed Nazi guards ushering his mother and two sisters and others towards (as he learned later) gas chamber number five. Despite this, the IHR refused to pay the reward. Represented by public interest attorney&nbsp;<a title="William John Cox" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/William_John_Cox">William John Cox</a>, Mermelstein subsequently sued the IHR in the&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Superior Court of Los Angeles County" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Superior_Court_of_Los_Angeles_County">Superior Court of Los Angeles County</a>ℳ for&nbsp;<a title="Breach of contract" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Breach_of_contract">breach of contract</a>,&nbsp;<a title="Anticipatory repudiation" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Anticipatory_repudiation">anticipatory repudiation</a>,&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Libel" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Libel">libel</a>,&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Injurious denial of established fact" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Injurious_denial_of_established_fact">injurious denial of established fact</a>,&nbsp;<a title="Intentional infliction of emotional distress" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Intentional_infliction_of_emotional_distress">intentional infliction of emotional distress</a>, and&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Declaratory relief" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Declaratory_relief">declaratory relief</a>. On 9 October 1981, both parties in the Mermelstein case filed motions for&nbsp;<a title="Summary judgment" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Summary_judgment">summary judgment</a>&nbsp;in consideration of which Judge Thomas T. Johnson of the&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Superior Court of Los Angeles County" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Superior_Court_of_Los_Angeles_County">Superior Court of Los Angeles County</a>&nbsp;took "<a title="Judicial notice" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Judicial_notice">judicial notice</a>&nbsp;of the fact that Jews were gassed to death at the Auschwitz Concentration Camp in Poland during the summer of 1944,"&nbsp;judicial notice meaning that the court treated the gas chambers as common knowledge, and therefore did not require evidence that the gas chambers existed. On 5 August 1985, Judge Robert A. Wenke entered a judgment based upon the&nbsp;<a title="Stipulation" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Stipulation">Stipulation</a>&nbsp;for Entry of Judgment agreed upon by the parties on 22 July 1985. The judgment required IHR and other defendants to pay $90,000 to Mermelstein and to issue a letter of apology to "Mr. Mel Mermelstein, a survivor of Auschwitz-Birkenau and Buchenwald, and all other survivors of Auschwitz" for "pain, anguish and suffering" caused to them.</dd>
<dt>Early 1980s</dt>
<dd><a title="Jesse Jackson" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jesse_Jackson">Jesse Jackson</a>&nbsp;was criticized in the early 1980s for remarks made to a reporter where he referred to New York City as "Hymietown".&nbsp;(<a class="mw-redirect" title="List of ethnic slurs of Jews" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_ethnic_slurs_of_Jews">Hymie</a>&nbsp;is a&nbsp;<a title="Pejorative" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pejorative">pejorative</a>&nbsp;term for Jews.) Jackson ultimately acknowledged he had used the term, and said he had been wrong; however, he also said that he had considered the conversation with the reporter to be off-the-record at the time he made the remarks.&nbsp;Jackson apologized during a speech before national Jewish leaders in a&nbsp;<a title="Manchester, New Hampshire" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Manchester,_New_Hampshire">Manchester, New Hampshire</a>&nbsp;<a title="Synagogue" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Synagogue">synagogue</a>, but an enduring split between Jackson and many in the Jewish community continued at least through the 1990s.</dd>
<dt>1981 August 29</dt>
<dd><a title="1981 Vienna synagogue attack" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1981_Vienna_synagogue_attack">1981 Vienna synagogue attack</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-query.nytimes.com_145-0" class="reference"></sup></dd>
<dt>1981 October 20</dt>
<dd><a title="1981 Antwerp synagogue bombing" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1981_Antwerp_synagogue_bombing">1981 Antwerp synagogue bombing</a>.</dd>
<dt>1981</dt>
<dd>The&nbsp;<a title="Southern Baptist Convention" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Southern_Baptist_Convention">Southern Baptist Convention</a>&nbsp;passed a "Resolution On Anti-Semitism" stating in part, "Be it therefore RESOLVED, That the messengers at the 1981 Southern Baptist Convention meeting in Los Angeles, June 9&ndash;11, 1981, commend our Southern Baptist Convention leaders as they seek sincere friendship and meaningful dialogue with our Jewish neighbors."</dd>
<dt>1981</dt>
<dd>Elana Steinberg was killed by her husband Steven Steinberg, who claimed that she was a "spoiled, over-indulged brat &ndash; the stereotypical&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Jewish American Princess" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jewish_American_Princess">Jewish American Princess</a>," and that she made him insane by spending and insisting that he become more successful; he was found not guilty.</dd>
<dt>1981-3</dt>
<dd>From 1981 to 1982, Holocaust denier&nbsp;<a title="Ernst Z&uuml;ndel" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ernst_Z%C3%BCndel">Ernst Z&uuml;ndel</a>&nbsp;had his mailing privileges suspended by the Canadian government on the grounds that he had been using the mail to send&nbsp;<a title="Hate speech" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hate_speech">hate propaganda</a>, a criminal offence in Canada. Z&uuml;ndel then began shipping from a post office box in&nbsp;<a title="Niagara Falls, New York" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Niagara_Falls,_New_York">Niagara Falls, New York</a>, until the ban on his mailing in Canada was lifted in January 1983.</dd>
<dt>1982</dt>
<dd>A bomb placed by neo-Nazis exploded outside the Jewish hunter of Nazis&nbsp;<a title="Simon Wiesenthal" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Simon_Wiesenthal">Simon Wiesenthal</a>'s house in Vienna on 11 June 1982, after which police guards were stationed outside his home 24 hours a day.<sup id="cite_ref-150" class="reference"></sup></dd>
<dt>1982 October 9</dt>
<dd><a title="Great Synagogue of Rome attack" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Great_Synagogue_of_Rome_attack">Great Synagogue of Rome attack</a>&nbsp;takes place.</dd>
<dt>1982</dt>
<dd>The thesis of the 1982 doctoral dissertation of&nbsp;<a title="Mahmoud Abbas" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mahmoud_Abbas">Mahmoud Abbas</a>, a co-founder of&nbsp;<a title="Fatah" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fatah">Fatah</a>&nbsp;and president of the&nbsp;<a title="Palestinian National Authority" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Palestinian_National_Authority">Palestinian National Authority</a>, was "The Secret Connection between the Nazis and the Leaders of the Zionist Movement".&nbsp;In his 1983 book&nbsp;<em><a class="mw-redirect" title="The Other Side: the Secret Relationship Between Nazism and Zionism" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/The_Other_Side:_the_Secret_Relationship_Between_Nazism_and_Zionism">The Other Side: the Secret Relationship Between Nazism and Zionism</a></em>&nbsp;based on the dissertation, Abbas denied that six million Jews had died in the Holocaust; dismissing it as a "myth" and a "fantastic lie".&nbsp;At most, he wrote, 890,000 Jews were killed by the Germans. Abbas claimed that the number of deaths has been exaggerated for political purposes. "It seems that the interest of the Zionist movement, however, is to inflate this figure [of Holocaust deaths] so that their gains will be greater. This led them to emphasize this figure [six million] in order to gain the solidarity of international public opinion with Zionism. Many scholars have debated the figure of six million and reached stunning conclusions&mdash;fixing the number of Jewish victims at only a few hundred thousand."&nbsp;In his March 2006 interview with&nbsp;<em><a title="Haaretz" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Haaretz">Haaretz</a></em>, Abbas stated, "I wrote in detail about the Holocaust and said I did not want to discuss numbers. I quoted an argument between historians in which various numbers of casualties were mentioned. One wrote there were 12&nbsp;million victims and another wrote there were 800,000. I have no desire to argue with the figures. The Holocaust was a terrible, unforgivable crime against the Jewish nation, a crime against humanity that cannot be accepted by humankind. The Holocaust was a terrible thing and nobody can claim I denied it."&nbsp;While acknowledging the existence of the Holocaust in 2006 and 2014,&nbsp;Abbas has defended the position that Zionists collaborated with the Nazis to perpetrate it. In 2012, Abbas told&nbsp;<a title="Al Mayadeen" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Al_Mayadeen">Al Mayadeen</a>, a Beirut TV station affiliated with Iran and Hezbollah, that he "challenges anyone who can deny that the Zionist movement had ties with the Nazis before World War II".</dd>
<dt>1982 September 18</dt>
<dd><a title="Great Synagogue of Europe" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Great_Synagogue_of_Europe">Great Synagogue of Europe</a>&nbsp;attacked by a man with a submachine gun, seriously wounding four people.<sup id="cite_ref-162" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_antisemitism_in_the_20th_century#cite_note-162">[162]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-163" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_antisemitism_in_the_20th_century#cite_note-163">[163]</a></sup>&nbsp;The attack has been attributed to the&nbsp;<a title="Abu Nidal Organization" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Abu_Nidal_Organization">Abu Nidal Organization</a>.</dd>
<dt>1983</dt>
<dd>The&nbsp;<a title="Lutheran Church&ndash;Missouri Synod" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lutheran_Church%E2%80%93Missouri_Synod">Lutheran Church&ndash;Missouri Synod</a>&nbsp;officially disassociates itself from "intemperate remarks about Jews" in Luther's works. Since then, many&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Lutheran church" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lutheran_church">Lutheran church</a>&nbsp;bodies and organizations have issued similar statements.&nbsp;</dd>
<dt>1984</dt>
<dd>On the evening of 18 June 1984,&nbsp;<a title="Alan Berg" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Alan_Berg">Alan Berg</a>&nbsp;was fatally shot in the driveway of his Denver home by members of the&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="White Nationalism" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/White_Nationalism">white nationalist</a>&nbsp;group&nbsp;<a title="The Order (white supremacist group)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/The_Order_(white_supremacist_group)">The Order</a>. His provocative talk show sought to flush out "the anti-Semitism latent in the area's conservative population". He succeeded in provoking members of The Order to engage him in conversations on this talk show and his "often-abrasive on-air persona" ignited the anger of The Order.&nbsp;Subsequently, members of The Order involved in the killing were identified as being part of a group planning to kill prominent Jews.&nbsp;Ultimately, two members of The Order,&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="David Lane (white nationalist)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/David_Lane_(white_nationalist)">David Lane</a>&nbsp;and Bruce Pierce, were convicted for their involvement in the case, though neither of&nbsp;<a title="Homicide" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Homicide">homicide</a>.</dd>
<dt>1984</dt>
<dd>In 1984,&nbsp;<a title="James Keegstra" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/James_Keegstra">James Keegstra</a>, a Canadian high-school teacher, was charged under the Canadian&nbsp;<a title="Criminal Code (Canada)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Criminal_Code_(Canada)"><em>Criminal Code</em></a>&nbsp;for "promoting hatred against an identifiable group by communicating anti-Semitic statements to his students". During class, he would describe Jews as a people of profound evil who had "created the Holocaust to gain sympathy." He also tested his students in exams on his theories and opinion of Jews.</dd>
<dd>Keegstra was charged under s 281.2(2) of the&nbsp;<em>Criminal Code</em>&nbsp;(now s 319(2), which provides that "Every one who, by communicating statements, other than in private conversation, wilfully promotes hatred against any identifiable group" commits a criminal offence.&nbsp;He was convicted at trial before the&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Alberta Court of Queen's Bench" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Alberta_Court_of_Queen%27s_Bench">Alberta Court of Queen's Bench</a>. The court rejected the argument, advanced by Keegstra and his lawyer,&nbsp;<a title="Doug Christie (lawyer)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Doug_Christie_(lawyer)">Doug Christie</a>, that promoting hatred is a constitutionally protected freedom of expression as per&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Section Two of the Canadian Charter of Rights and Freedoms" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Section_Two_of_the_Canadian_Charter_of_Rights_and_Freedoms">s 2(b) of the Canadian Charter of Rights and Freedoms</a>. Keegstra appealed to the&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Alberta Court of Appeal" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Alberta_Court_of_Appeal">Alberta Court of Appeal</a>. That court agreed with Keegstra, and he was acquitted. The Crown then appealed the case to the&nbsp;<a title="Supreme Court of Canada" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Supreme_Court_of_Canada">Supreme Court of Canada</a>, which rule by a 4&ndash;3 majority that promoting hatred could be&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="R. v. Keegstra" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/R._v._Keegstra#Reasons_of_the_court">justifiably</a>&nbsp;restricted under&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Section 1 of the canadian charter of rights and freedoms" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Section_1_of_the_canadian_charter_of_rights_and_freedoms">s 1 of the Charter</a>. The Supreme Court restored Keegstra's conviction.&nbsp;He was fired from his teaching position shortly afterwards.</dd>
<dt>1985, 22 July</dt>
<dd><a title="1985 Copenhagen bombings" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1985_Copenhagen_bombings">1985 Copenhagen bombings</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-TerroristExplosions_173-0" class="reference"></sup></dd>
<dt>1985</dt>
<dd>At a meeting of the Nation of Islam at&nbsp;<a title="Madison Square Garden" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Madison_Square_Garden">Madison Square Garden</a>&nbsp;in 1985,&nbsp;<a title="Louis Farrakhan" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Louis_Farrakhan">Louis Farrakhan</a>&nbsp;said of the Jews: "And don't you forget, when it's God who puts you in the ovens, it's forever!"</dd>
<dt>1985</dt>
<dd>On 24 December 1985,&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="David Lewis Rice" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/David_Lewis_Rice">David Lewis Rice</a>, a follower of the right-wing extremist group the&nbsp;<a title="Duck Club" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Duck_Club">Duck Club</a>, gained entry to the&nbsp;<a title="Seattle" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Seattle">Seattle</a>&nbsp;home of&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Civil litigation" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Civil_litigation">civil litigation</a>&nbsp;attorney Charles Goldmark using a toy gun and pretending to be a deliveryman.&nbsp;He tied the family up,&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Chloroformed" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Chloroformed">chloroformed</a>&nbsp;them into unconsciousness, beat them with a steam iron, and stabbed them.&nbsp;Rice mistakenly believed the family to be Jewish and&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Communist" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Communist">Communist</a>. In 1998, he&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Guilty plea" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Guilty_plea">pleaded guilty</a>&nbsp;to the crimes&nbsp;in exchange for avoiding the death penalty. The Goldmark Murders remain one of the most notorious antisemitic hate crimes as well as&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Right-wing violence" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Right-wing_violence">politically motivated killings</a>&nbsp;in recent memory in the United States, even though the victims were not actually Jewish and Communist as the killer mistakenly believed.</dd>
<dt>1985</dt>
<dd><a title="Ronald Reagan" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ronald_Reagan">Ronald Reagan</a>&nbsp;visited a German military cemetery in&nbsp;<a title="Bitburg" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bitburg">Bitburg</a>&nbsp;to lay a wreath with West German Chancellor&nbsp;<a title="Helmut Kohl" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Helmut_Kohl">Helmut Kohl</a>. It was determined that the cemetery held the graves of forty-nine members of the&nbsp;<a title="Waffen-SS" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Waffen-SS">Waffen-SS</a>. Reagan issued a statement that called the Nazi soldiers buried in that cemetery as themselves "victims," a designation which ignited a stir over whether Reagan had equated the SS men to victims of&nbsp;<a title="The Holocaust" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/The_Holocaust">the Holocaust</a>;&nbsp;<a title="Pat Buchanan" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pat_Buchanan">Pat Buchanan</a>, Reagan's Director of Communications, argued that the president did not equate the SS members with the actual Holocaust.&nbsp;Now strongly urged to cancel the visit, the president responded that it would be wrong to back down on a promise he had made to Chancellor Kohl. He ultimately attended the ceremony where two military generals laid a wreath.</dd>
<dt>1986</dt>
<dd><a title="Leo Frank" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Leo_Frank">Leo Frank</a>&nbsp;was posthumously pardoned by the Georgia State Board of Pardons and Paroles.</dd>
<dt>1986</dt>
<dd>In Israel, a law to criminalize Holocaust denial was passed by the&nbsp;<a title="Knesset" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Knesset">Knesset</a>&nbsp;on 8 July 1986.</dd>
<dt>1986 September 6</dt>
<dd>Gunmen opened fire during a Shabbat service in&nbsp;<a title="Neve Shalom Synagogue" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Neve_Shalom_Synagogue">Neve Shalom Synagogue</a>&nbsp;in&nbsp;<a title="Istanbul" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Istanbul">Istanbul</a>,&nbsp;<a title="Turkey" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Turkey">Turkey</a>&nbsp;which resulted in the death of 22 people. This attack is attributed to the&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Palestinian people" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Palestinian_people">Palestinian</a>&nbsp;militant&nbsp;<a title="Abu Nidal" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Abu_Nidal">Abu Nidal</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-foxnews_185-0" class="reference"></sup></dd>
<dt>1987</dt>
<dd>On 13 September 1987&nbsp;<a title="Jean-Marie Le Pen" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jean-Marie_Le_Pen">Jean-Marie Le Pen</a>&nbsp;said, "I ask myself several questions. I'm not saying the gas chambers didn't exist. I haven't seen them myself. I haven't particularly studied the question. But I believe it's just a detail in the history of World War II." He was condemned under the&nbsp;<a title="Gayssot Act" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gayssot_Act">Gayssot Act</a>&nbsp;and ordered to pay 1.2&nbsp;million&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="French Franc" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/French_Franc">francs</a>&nbsp;(183,200 euros).</dd>
<dt>1987</dt>
<dd><a title="Pat Buchanan" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pat_Buchanan">Pat Buchanan</a>&nbsp;called for ending prosecution of Nazi camp guards, saying it was "running down 70-year-old camp guards."</dd>
<dt>1987</dt>
<dd>In 1987, Bradley R. Smith, a former media director of the Institute for Historical Review,&nbsp;founded the Committee for Open Debate on the Holocaust (CODOH).</dd>
<dt>1987</dt>
<dd>John Koehler was the communications director for five working days under President Ronald Reagan; Koehler, who was an immigrant from Germany, had been in Hitler Youth.</dd>
<dd></dd>
<dt>Since 1987</dt>
<dd>Activities of&nbsp;<a title="Pamyat" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pamyat">Pamyat</a>&nbsp;and other "nonformal"&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Ultra-nationalist" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ultra-nationalist">ultra-nationalist</a>&nbsp;organizations in the&nbsp;<a title="Soviet Union" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Soviet_Union">Soviet Union</a>.</dd>
<dt>1988</dt>
<dd>In 1988, the American historian&nbsp;<a title="Arno J. Mayer" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arno_J._Mayer">Arno J. Mayer</a>&nbsp;published a book entitled&nbsp;<em>Why Did the Heavens Not Darken?</em>, which did not explicitly deny the Holocaust, but lent support to Holocaust denial by stating that most people who died at&nbsp;<a title="Auschwitz concentration camp" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Auschwitz_concentration_camp">Auschwitz</a>&nbsp;were the victims of "natural causes" such as disease, not gassing.&nbsp;Mayer also cited the works of Holocaust deniers&nbsp;<a title="Arthur Butz" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arthur_Butz">Arthur Butz</a>&nbsp;and&nbsp;<a title="Paul Rassinier" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Paul_Rassinier">Paul Rassinier</a>&nbsp;in his book's bibliography. Critics such as&nbsp;<a title="Lucy Dawidowicz" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lucy_Dawidowicz">Lucy Dawidowicz</a>&nbsp;criticized Mayer's citation of deniers, and argued that his statements about Auschwitz were factually incorrect.&nbsp;Holocaust expert&nbsp;<a title="Robert Jan van Pelt" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Robert_Jan_van_Pelt">Robert Jan van Pelt</a>&nbsp;has noted that Mayer's book is as close as a mainstream historian has ever come to supporting Holocaust denial.&nbsp;Holocaust deniers such as&nbsp;<a title="David Irving" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/David_Irving">David Irving</a>&nbsp;have often cited Mayer's book as one reason for embracing Holocaust denial.&nbsp;Though Mayer has been often condemned for his statement about the reasons for the Auschwitz death toll, his book does not deny the use of gas chambers at Auschwitz, as Holocaust deniers often claim.</dd>
<dd>Some mainstream Holocaust historians have labeled Mayer a denier. The Israeli historian&nbsp;<a title="Yehuda Bauer" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Yehuda_Bauer">Yehuda Bauer</a>&nbsp;wrote that Mayer "popularizes the nonsense that the Nazis saw in Marxism and Bolshevism their main enemy, and the Jews unfortunately got caught up in this; when he links the destruction of the Jews to the ups and downs of German warfare in the Soviet Union, in a book that is so cocksure of itself that it does not need a proper scientific apparatus, he is really engaging in a much more subtle form of Holocaust denial".</dd>
<dd>Defenders of Mayer argue that his statement that "Sources for the study of the gas chambers at once rare and unreliable" has been taken out of context, particularly by Holocaust deniers.&nbsp;<a title="Michael Shermer" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Michael_Shermer">Michael Shermer</a>&nbsp;and&nbsp;<a title="Alex Grobman" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Alex_Grobman">Alex Grobman</a>&nbsp;observe that the paragraph from which the statement is taken asserts that the SS destroyed the majority of the documentation relating to the operation of the gas chambers in the death camps, which is why Mayer feels that sources for the operation of the gas chambers are "rare" and "unreliable".</dd>
<dt>1988</dt>
<dd>In February 1988, an improperly drawn&nbsp;<a title="Swastika" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Swastika">swastika</a>&nbsp;and anti-Semitic slogans and "Jesus Lives; You Can't Kill Him" and "Accept Hitler, Respect Christ" were plastered across the synagogue&nbsp;<a title="Bet Shira Congregation" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bet_Shira_Congregation">Bet Shira Congregation</a>, and 30 windows were smashed.&nbsp;In response, a neighboring church put a&nbsp;<a title="Star of David" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Star_of_David">Star of David</a>&nbsp;on its lawn, and its parish donated $1,000 towards repairing the windows.&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Miami Sunset High School" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Miami_Sunset_High_School">Miami Sunset High School</a>&nbsp;students painted over the anti-Semitic slurs spray-painted by the vandals.&nbsp;Four teenagers, three of whom were football players at&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Miami Palmetto High School" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Miami_Palmetto_High_School">Miami Palmetto High School</a>, were sentenced for having vandalized the synagogue to 200 hours of&nbsp;<a title="Community service" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Community_service">community service</a>&nbsp;and ordered to pay the $14,800 ($32,000 today) in damages.<sup id="cite_ref-205" class="reference"></sup></dd>
<dt>1989</dt>
<dd><a title="Finland" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Finland">Finland</a>&nbsp;has no specific legislation aimed at controlling ownership, display, purchase, import or export of&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Nazi flag" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nazi_flag">Nazi flags</a>, however the&nbsp;<a title="Criminal Code of Finland" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Criminal_Code_of_Finland">Criminal Code</a>&nbsp;(39/1889)&nbsp;(especially Chapter 11 'War crimes and offences against humanity' Section 8)<span style="font-size: xx-small;">&nbsp;</span>&nbsp;may be applied where an offence has been directed at a person belonging to a national, racial, ethnic or other population group due to his/her membership in such a group.</dd>
</dl>
<p>&nbsp;</p>
<h2><span id="1990s" class="mw-headline">1990s</span></h2>
<dl>
<dt>1990s</dt>
<dd><a title="Ruth Bader Ginsburg" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ruth_Bader_Ginsburg">Ruth Bader Ginsburg</a>&nbsp;objected to the United States Supreme Court bar inscribing its certificates "in the year of our Lord", at the request of some Orthodox Jews who opposed it, and due to her objection, Supreme Court bar members have since been given other choices of how to inscribe the year on their certificates.</dd>
<dt>1990</dt>
<dd><a title="Lake Forest, Illinois" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lake_Forest,_Illinois">Lake Forest, Illinois</a>&nbsp;kept anti-Jewish and anti-<a class="mw-redirect" title="African-American" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/African-American">African-American</a>&nbsp;housing covenants until 1990.</dd>
<dt>1990</dt>
<dd>On five occasions in six weeks vandals shot at windows at the synagogue&nbsp;<a title="Bet Shira Congregation" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bet_Shira_Congregation">Bet Shira Congregation</a>.&nbsp;Three teenagers, two of them students at Palmetto High School, were arrested for shooting out the windows.</dd>
<dt>1990</dt>
<dd>For his portrayal of Jewish nightclub owners Moe and Josh Flatbush in the 1990 film&nbsp;<em><a title="Mo' Better Blues" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mo%27_Better_Blues">Mo' Better Blues</a></em>,&nbsp;<a title="Spike Lee" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Spike_Lee">Spike Lee</a>&nbsp;drew the ire of the&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Anti Defamation League" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Anti_Defamation_League">Anti Defamation League</a>,&nbsp;<a title="B'nai B'rith" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/B%27nai_B%27rith">B'nai B'rith</a>, and other such Jewish organizations. The Anti-Defamation League claimed that the characterizations of the nightclub owners "dredge up an age-old and highly dangerous form of&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Anti-Semitic" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Anti-Semitic">anti-Semitic</a>&nbsp;stereotyping", and stated it was "...disappointed that Spike Lee &ndash; whose success is largely due to his efforts to break down racial stereotypes and prejudice &ndash; has employed the same kind of tactics that he supposedly deplores."&nbsp;Lee eventually responded in an editorial in&nbsp;<em><a title="The New York Times" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/The_New_York_Times">The New York Times</a></em>,&nbsp;alleging "a double standard at work in the accusations of anti-Semitism" given the long history of negative portrayals of African-Americans in film: "Not every black person is a pimp, murderer, prostitute, convict, rapist or drug addict, but that hasn't stopped&nbsp;<a title="Hollywood" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hollywood">Hollywood</a>&nbsp;from writing these roles for African-Americans". Lee argues that even if the Flatbush brothers are stereotyped figures, their "10 minutes of screen time" is insignificant when compared to "100 years of Hollywood cinema... [and] a slew of really racist, anti-Semitic filmmakers". According to Lee, his status as a successful African-American artist has led to hostility and unfair treatment: "Don't hold me to a higher moral standard than the rest of my filmmaking colleagues... Now that young black filmmakers have arisen in the film industry, all of a sudden stereotypes are a big issue... I think it's reaching the point where&nbsp;<em>I'm</em>&nbsp;getting reviewed, not my films." Ultimately, however, Lee refused to apologize for his portrayal of the Flatbush brothers: "I stand behind all my work, including my characters, Moe and Josh Flatbush... if critics are telling me that to avoid charges of anti-Semitism, all Jewish characters I write have to be model citizens, and not one can be a villain, cheat or a crook, and that no Jewish people have ever exploited black artists in the history of the entertainment industry, that's unrealistic and unfair."</dd>
<dt>1990</dt>
<dd>In France, the&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Loi Gayssot" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Loi_Gayssot">Gayssot Act</a>, voted for on 13 July 1990, makes it illegal to question the existence of crimes that fall in the category of&nbsp;<a title="Crimes against humanity" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Crimes_against_humanity">crimes against humanity</a>&nbsp;as defined in the&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="London Charter of the International Military Tribunal" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/London_Charter_of_the_International_Military_Tribunal">London Charter of 1945</a>, on the basis of which&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="List of Nazi leaders" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_Nazi_leaders">Nazi leaders</a>&nbsp;were convicted by the&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="International Military Tribunal" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/International_Military_Tribunal">International Military Tribunal</a>&nbsp;at&nbsp;<a title="Nuremberg" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nuremberg">Nuremberg</a>&nbsp;in 1945&ndash;46. When the act was challenged by&nbsp;<a title="Robert Faurisson" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Robert_Faurisson">Robert Faurisson</a>, the&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Human Rights Committee" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human_Rights_Committee">Human Rights Committee</a>&nbsp;upheld it as a necessary means to counter possible&nbsp;<a title="Antisemitism" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Antisemitism">antisemitism</a>.</dd>
<dt>1990</dt>
<dd>In a 1990 column defending&nbsp;<a title="John Demjanjuk" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/John_Demjanjuk">John Demjanjuk</a>,&nbsp;<a title="Pat Buchanan" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pat_Buchanan">Pat Buchanan</a>&nbsp;said:</dd>
</dl>
<blockquote class="templatequote">
<p>Diesel engines do not emit enough carbon monoxide to kill anybody. In 1988, 97 kids, trapped 400 feet (120&nbsp;m) underground in a Washington, DC, tunnel while two locomotives spewed diesel exhaust into the car, emerged unharmed after 45 minutes. Demjanjuk's weapon of mass murder cannot kill.</p>
</blockquote>
<dl>
<dd>When asked for his source, Buchanan said, "somebody sent it to me." Critic Jamie McCarthy says this claim may have come from the German American Information and Education Association's newsletter, a publication he accused of anti-Semitism and&nbsp;<a title="Holocaust denial" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Holocaust_denial">Holocaust denial</a>. He also argues that:</dd>
</dl>
<blockquote class="templatequote">
<p>Unlike the locomotive engineer in Buchanan's example, who was concerned with saving the lives of trapped people, the Nazis had no qualms about opening the engine's throttle and restricting the air intake.</p>
</blockquote>
<dl>
<dd>The&nbsp;<em><a class="mw-redirect" title="Washington Post" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Washington_Post">Washington Post</a></em>&nbsp;had reported in 1989, before the controversy, that:</dd>
</dl>
<blockquote class="templatequote">
<p>An&nbsp;<a title="Amtrak" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Amtrak">Amtrak</a>&nbsp;train had been stalled in a tunnel for half an hour, and smoke from the diesel engine had filled the first car, where there were 97 fifth-grade pupils and 27 adult chaperones. [EMT Cynthia] Brown boarded the train, guided the passengers &ndash; most of whom suffered from smoke inhalation &ndash; from the car and assisted those who needed immediate attention.</p>
</blockquote>
<dl>
<dt>1990</dt>
<dd>French literature professor&nbsp;<a title="Robert Faurisson" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Robert_Faurisson">Robert Faurisson</a>&nbsp;was convicted and punished for Holocaust denial under the Gayssot Act in 1990.</dd>
<dt>1991</dt>
<dd><em><a title="The Secret Relationship Between Blacks and Jews" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/The_Secret_Relationship_Between_Blacks_and_Jews">The Secret Relationship Between Blacks and Jews</a></em>, published in 1991, is a book that asserts that Jews dominated the&nbsp;<a title="Atlantic slave trade" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Atlantic_slave_trade">Atlantic slave trade</a>.&nbsp;The book has been labeled an&nbsp;<a title="Antisemitic canard" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Antisemitic_canard">Antisemitic canard</a>&nbsp;by historians including&nbsp;<a title="Saul S. Friedman" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Saul_S._Friedman">Saul S. Friedman</a>, who writes that Jews had a minimal role in New World slave trade.&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Henry Louis Gates, Jr." href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Henry_Louis_Gates,_Jr.">Henry Louis Gates, Jr.</a>, head of the department of Afro-American studies at Harvard University, called the book "the Bible of new anti-Semitism" and added that "the book massively misinterprets the historical record, largely through a process of cunningly selective quotations of often reputable sources".</dd>
<dd>The book was criticized for being antisemitic, and for failing to provide an objective analysis of the role of Jews in the slave trade. Common criticisms were that the book used selective quotes, made "crude use of statistics,"&nbsp;and was purposefully trying to exaggerate the role of Jews.</dd>
<dd>Historian Ralph A. Austen criticized the book, saying that the "distortions are produced almost entirely by selective citation rather than explicit falsehood.... more frequently there are innuendos imbedded in the accounts of Jewish involvement in the slave trade,"&nbsp;and "[w]hile we should not ignore the anti-Semitism of The Secret Relationship..., we must recognize the legitimacy of the stated aim of examining fully and directly even the most uncomfortable elements in our [Black and Jewish] common past."&nbsp;Austen acknowledges that the book was the first book on the subject aimed at a non-scholarly audience.</dd>
<dd>In 1995, the&nbsp;<a title="American Historical Association" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/American_Historical_Association">American Historical Association</a>&nbsp;(AHA) issued a statement condemning "any statement alleging that Jews played a disproportionate role in the Atlantic slave trade."</dd>
<dd></dd>
<dd>The publication of&nbsp;<em>The Secret Relationship</em>&nbsp;spurred retorts published specifically to refute the thesis of&nbsp;<em>The Secret Relationship</em>:</dd>
</dl>
<ul>
<li>1992 &ndash; Harold Brackman,&nbsp;<em>Jew on the Brain: A Public Refutation of the Nation of Islam's The Secret Relationship Between Blacks and Jews</em>.</li>
<li>1992 &ndash;&nbsp;<a title="David Brion Davis" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/David_Brion_Davis">David Brion Davis</a>, "Jews in the Slave Trade," in&nbsp;<em>Culturefront</em>&nbsp;(Fall 1992) pp 42&ndash;45.</li>
<li>1993 &ndash;&nbsp;<a title="Seymour Drescher" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Seymour_Drescher">Seymour Drescher</a>, "The Role of Jews in the Atlantic Slave Trade,"&nbsp;<em>Immigrants and Minorities</em>, 12 (1993), pp 113&ndash;125.</li>
<li>1993 &ndash; Marc Caplan,&nbsp;<em>Jew-Hatred As History: An Analysis of the Nation of Islam's "The Secret Relationship"</em>&nbsp;(Published by the&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Anti Defamation League" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Anti_Defamation_League">Anti Defamation League</a>).</li>
<li>1998 &ndash; Eli Faber,&nbsp;<em>Jews, Slaves, and the Slave Trade: Setting the Record Straight</em>, New York University Press.</li>
<li>1999 &ndash;&nbsp;<a title="Saul S. Friedman" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Saul_S._Friedman">Saul S. Friedman</a>,&nbsp;<em>Jews and the American Slave Trade</em>, Transaction.</li>
</ul>
<dl>
<dd>A post-1991 scholar who analyzed the role of Jews in the overall Atlantic slave trade concluded that it was "minimal," and only identified certain regions (such as Brazil and the Caribbean) where the participation was "significant."</dd>
<dd>Wim Klooster wrote: "In no period did Jews play a leading role as financiers, shipowners, or factors in the Transatlantic or Caribbean slave trades. They possessed far fewer slaves than non-Jews in every British territory in North America and the Caribbean. Even when Jews in a handful of places owned slaves in proportions slightly above their representation among a town's families, such cases do not come close to corroborating the assertions of The Secret Relationship."</dd>
<dd>The&nbsp;<a title="Anti-Defamation League" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Anti-Defamation_League">Anti-Defamation League</a>&nbsp;states that Volume Two of&nbsp;<em>The Secret Relationship</em>&nbsp;blames Jews for "promoting a myth of black racial inferiority and makes a range of conspiratorial accusations about Jewish involvement in the slave trade and in the cotton, textiles, and banking industries".</dd>
<dt>1991</dt>
<dd>The United Nations's resolution determining that "Zionism is a form of racism and racial discrimination" was revoked.</dd>
<dt>1991</dt>
<dd>The&nbsp;<a title="Crown Heights riot" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Crown_Heights_riot">Crown Heights riot</a>&nbsp;was a three-day racial riot that occurred from 19&ndash;21 August 1991 in the&nbsp;<a title="Crown Heights, Brooklyn" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Crown_Heights,_Brooklyn">Crown Heights</a>&nbsp;section of&nbsp;<a title="Brooklyn" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Brooklyn">Brooklyn</a>,&nbsp;<a title="New York City" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/New_York_City">New York City</a>. It turned black residents and&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Orthodox Jewish" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Orthodox_Jewish">Orthodox Jewish</a>&nbsp;residents against each other, causing deteriorated racial relations. The riots began on 19 August 1991, after two children of&nbsp;<a title="Guyana" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Guyana">Guyanese</a>&nbsp;immigrants were unintentionally struck by an automobile in the motorcade of&nbsp;<a title="Menachem Mendel Schneerson" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Menachem_Mendel_Schneerson">Menachem Mendel Schneerson</a>, the&nbsp;<a title="Rebbe" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Rebbe">leader of a Jewish religious sect</a>. One child died and the second was severely injured. This event was said to cause tensions between Jewish and black residents to erupt.</dd>
<dd>In its wake, several Jews were seriously injured; one Orthodox Jewish man was killed; and a non-Jewish man, apparently mistaken by rioters for a Jew, was killed by a group of black men. The riots were a major issue in the 1993 mayoral race, contributing to the defeat of Mayor&nbsp;<a title="David Dinkins" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/David_Dinkins">David Dinkins</a>, an African American, who was blamed for an ineffective police response. Ultimately, black and Jewish leaders developed an outreach program between their communities to help calm and possibly improve racial relations in Crown Heights over the next decade.</dd>
<dt>1991</dt>
<dd>In December 1991 the&nbsp;<a title="American Historical Association" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/American_Historical_Association">American Historical Association</a>&nbsp;issued the following statement:&nbsp;<em>The American Historical Association Council strongly deplores the publicly reported attempts to deny the fact of the Holocaust. No serious historian questions that the Holocaust took place.</em>&nbsp;This followed a strong reaction by many of its members and commentary in the press against a near-unanimous decision that the AHA had made in May 1991 that studying the&nbsp;<em>significance of the Holocaust</em>&nbsp;should be encouraged. The association's May 1991 statement was in response to an incident where certain of its members had questioned the reality of the Holocaust. The December 1991 declaration is a reversal of the AHA's earlier stance that the association should not set a precedent by certifying historical facts.</dd>
<dt>1992 March 1</dt>
<dd>A bomb attack was carried out by two men&nbsp;<a title="Neve Shalom Synagogue" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Neve_Shalom_Synagogue">Neve Shalom Synagogue</a>&nbsp;in&nbsp;<a title="Istanbul" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Istanbul">Istanbul</a>,&nbsp;<a title="Turkey" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Turkey">Turkey</a>&nbsp;causing no damage or casualties.</dd>
<dt>1994 February 25</dt>
<dd>Second&nbsp;<a title="Cave of the Patriarchs massacre" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cave_of_the_Patriarchs_massacre">Hebron massacre</a>.&nbsp;<a title="Baruch Goldstein" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Baruch_Goldstein">Baruch Goldstein</a>, a Jew, kills several Muslim worshippers; this leads to riots that kill both Muslims and Jews.</dd>
<dt>1994</dt>
<dd>On 1 March 1994, on the&nbsp;<a title="Brooklyn Bridge" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Brooklyn_Bridge">Brooklyn Bridge</a>&nbsp;in&nbsp;<a title="New York City" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/New_York_City">New York City</a>, Lebanese-born immigrant Rashid Baz shot at a van of 15&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Chabad-Lubavitch" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Chabad-Lubavitch">Chabad-Lubavitch</a>&nbsp;<a title="Orthodox Judaism" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Orthodox_Judaism">Orthodox Jewish</a>&nbsp;students that was traveling on the Brooklyn Bridge, killing one and injuring three others.&nbsp;</dd>
<dt>1994, 20 March</dt>
<dd>Chris Lord, an individual associated with the&nbsp;<a title="Volksfront" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Volksfront">Volksfront</a>&nbsp;and&nbsp;<a title="American Front" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/American_Front">American Front</a>, fired ten rounds with an assault rifle into&nbsp;<a title="Temple Beth Israel (Eugene, Oregon)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Temple_Beth_Israel_(Eugene,_Oregon)">Temple Beth Israel (Eugene, Oregon)</a>, damaging the interior.</dd>
<dt>1994</dt>
<dd><a title="AMIA bombing" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/AMIA_bombing">AMIA bombing</a>&nbsp;against the Jewish community of Buenos Aires.</dd>
<dt>1995</dt>
<dd>In February 1995 a Japanese magazine named&nbsp;<em>Marco Polo</em>, a 250,000-circulation monthly published by&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Bungei Shunju" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bungei_Shunju">Bungei Shunju</a>, ran a Holocaust denial article by physician Masanori Nishioka which stated:</dd>
</dl>
<blockquote class="templatequote">
<p>The '<a class="mw-redirect" title="Holocaust" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Holocaust">Holocaust</a>' is a fabrication. There were no execution&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Gas chambers" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gas_chambers">gas chambers</a>&nbsp;in&nbsp;<a title="Auschwitz concentration camp" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Auschwitz_concentration_camp">Auschwitz</a>&nbsp;or in any other&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Concentration camp" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Concentration_camp">concentration camp</a>. Today, what are displayed as 'gas chambers' at the remains of the Auschwitz camp in Poland are a post-war fabrication by the Polish communist regime or by the&nbsp;<a title="Soviet Union" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Soviet_Union">Soviet Union</a>, which controlled the country. Not once, neither at Auschwitz nor in any territory controlled by the Germans during the Second World War, was there 'mass murder of Jews' in 'gas chambers.'</p>
</blockquote>
<dl>
<dd>The Los Angeles-based&nbsp;<a title="Simon Wiesenthal Center" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Simon_Wiesenthal_Center">Simon Wiesenthal Center</a>&nbsp;instigated a&nbsp;<a title="Boycott" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Boycott">boycott</a>&nbsp;of Bungei Shunju advertisers, including&nbsp;<a title="Volkswagen" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Volkswagen">Volkswagen</a>,&nbsp;<a title="Mitsubishi" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mitsubishi">Mitsubishi</a>, and&nbsp;<a title="Cartier (jeweler)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cartier_(jeweler)">Cartier</a>. Within days, Bungei Shunju shut down&nbsp;<em>Marco Polo</em>&nbsp;and its editor, Kazuyoshi Hanada, quit, as did the president of Bungei Shunju, Kengo Tanaka.</dd>
<dt>1995</dt>
<dd>In Belgium, Holocaust denial was made illegal in 1995.</dd>
<dt>1996</dt>
<dd>In Turkey, in 1996, the Islamic preacher&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Harun Yahya" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Harun_Yahya">Harun Yahya</a>&nbsp;distributed thousands of copies of a book which was originally published the previous year, entitled&nbsp;<em>Soykırım Yalanı</em>&nbsp;("The Holocaust Lie") and mailed unsolicited texts to American and European schools and colleges.&nbsp;The publication of&nbsp;<em>Soykırım Yalanı</em>&nbsp;sparked much public debate.&nbsp;This book claims, "what is presented as Holocaust is the death of some Jews due to the typhus plague during the war and the famine towards the end of the war caused by the defeat of the Germans."&nbsp;In March 1996, a Turkish painter and intellectual,&nbsp;<a title="Bedri Baykam" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bedri_Baykam">Bedri Baykam</a>, published a strongly worded critique of the book in the Ankara daily newspaper&nbsp;<em>Siyah-Beyaz</em>&nbsp;("Black and White"). A legal suit for slander was brought against him. During the trial in September, Baykam exposed the real author of the book as&nbsp;<a title="Adnan Oktar" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Adnan_Oktar">Adnan Oktar</a>.&nbsp;The suit was withdrawn in March 1997.<sup id="cite_ref-241" class="reference"></sup></dd>
<dt>1996</dt>
<dd>The depiction of&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Jew" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jew">Jews</a>&nbsp;in some of&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="T.S. Eliot" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/T.S._Eliot">T.S. Eliot</a>'s poems has led several critics to accuse him of anti-Semitism. This case has been presented most forcefully in a study by&nbsp;<a title="Anthony Julius" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Anthony_Julius">Anthony Julius</a>:&nbsp;<em>T. S. Eliot, Anti-Semitism, and Literary Form</em>&nbsp;(1996).&nbsp;In "<a title="Gerontion" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gerontion">Gerontion</a>", Eliot writes, in the voice of the poem's elderly narrator, "And the jew squats on the window sill, the owner [of my building] / Spawned in some estaminet of Antwerp."&nbsp;Another well-known example appears in the poem, "Burbank with a Baedeker: Bleistein with a Cigar". In this poem, Eliot wrote, "The rats are underneath the piles. / The jew is underneath the lot. / Money in furs."&nbsp;Interpreting the line as an indirect comparison of Jews to rats, Julius writes, "The anti-Semitism is unmistakable. It reaches out like a clear signal to the reader." Julius's viewpoint has been supported by literary critics such as&nbsp;<a title="Harold Bloom" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Harold_Bloom">Harold Bloom</a>,&nbsp;<a title="Christopher Ricks" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Christopher_Ricks">Christopher Ricks</a>,&nbsp;<a title="George Steiner" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/George_Steiner">George Steiner</a>,&nbsp;<a title="Tom Paulin" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tom_Paulin">Tom Paulin</a>&nbsp;and&nbsp;<a title="James Fenton" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/James_Fenton">James Fenton</a>.</dd>
<dt>1997</dt>
<dd>This year the&nbsp;<a title="European Parliament" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/European_Parliament">European Parliament</a>, of which&nbsp;<a title="Jean-Marie Le Pen" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jean-Marie_Le_Pen">Jean-Marie Le Pen</a>&nbsp;was then a member, removed his&nbsp;<a title="Parliamentary immunity" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Parliamentary_immunity">parliamentary immunity</a>&nbsp;so that Le Pen could be tried by a German court for comments he made at a December 1996 press conference before the German&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Republicans (Germany)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Republicans_(Germany)">Republikaner</a>&nbsp;party. Echoing his 1987 remarks in France (see above), Le Pen stated: "If you take a 1,000-page book on World War II, the concentration camps take up only two pages and the gas chambers 10 to 15 lines. This is what one calls a detail." In June 1999, a&nbsp;<a title="Munich" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Munich">Munich</a>&nbsp;court found this statement to be "minimizing the Holocaust, which caused the deaths of six million Jews," and convicted and fined Le Pen for his remarks.&nbsp;Le Pen retorted ironically: "I understand now that it's the Second World War which is a detail of the history of the gas chambers."</dd>
<dt>1997</dt>
<dd><a title="Jean-Marie Le Pen" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jean-Marie_Le_Pen">Jean-Marie Le Pen</a>&nbsp;accused&nbsp;<a title="Jacques Chirac" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jacques_Chirac">Jacques Chirac</a>&nbsp;of being "on the payroll of Jewish organizations, and particularly of the&nbsp;<a title="B'nai B'rith" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/B%27nai_B%27rith">B'nai B'rith</a>."<sup id="cite_ref-1997jewr_251-0" class="reference"></sup></dd>
<dt>1997</dt>
<dd>In&nbsp;<a title="Luxembourg" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Luxembourg">Luxembourg</a>, Article 457&ndash;3 of the Criminal Code, Act of 19 July 1997 outlaws Holocaust denial and denial of other genocides.&nbsp;The punishment is imprisonment for between 8 days and 6 months and/or a fine.</dd>
<dt>1998</dt>
<dd>In a May 1998 interview with ABC's John Miller,&nbsp;<a title="Osama bin Laden" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Osama_bin_Laden">Osama bin Laden</a>&nbsp;stated that the Israeli state's ultimate goal was to annex the Arabian Peninsula and the Middle East into its territory and enslave its peoples, as part of what he called a "<a title="Greater Israel" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Greater_Israel">Greater Israel</a>". He stated that Jews and Muslims could never get along and that war was "inevitable" between them, and further accused the U.S. of stirring up anti-Islamic sentiment.&nbsp;He claimed that the U.S. State Department and U.S. Department of Defense were controlled by Jews, for the sole purpose of serving the Israeli state's goals.</dd>
<dt>1998</dt>
<dd>In a December 1998 interview with Pakistani journalist&nbsp;<a title="Rahimullah Yusufzai" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Rahimullah_Yusufzai">Rahimullah Yusufzai</a>,&nbsp;<a title="Osama bin Laden" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Osama_bin_Laden">Osama bin Laden</a>&nbsp;stated that&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Operation Desert Fox" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Operation_Desert_Fox">Operation Desert Fox</a>&nbsp;was proof that Israeli Jews controlled the governments of the United States and United Kingdom, directing them to kill as many Muslims as they could.</dd>
<dt>1999</dt>
<dd>Holocaust Remembrance Day has been commemorated as a national remembrance day in Sweden every year since 1999.</dd>
<dt>1999</dt>
<dd><a class="mw-redirect" title="1999 Arrest and trial of 13 Jews in Iran" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1999_Arrest_and_trial_of_13_Jews_in_Iran">Intelligence Ministry of Iran arrested 13 Iranian Jews</a>, accusing them of spying for&nbsp;<a title="Israel" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel">Israel</a>. Arrestees were five merchants, a rabbi, two university professors, three teachers in private Hebrew schools, a kosher butcher and a 16-year-old boy. Ten of them were sentenced to 4&ndash;13 years in prison. As a result of the pressure campaigns and secret negotiations, the prisoners were gradually freed in small groups. All of them&nbsp;<a title="Aliyah" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Aliyah">emigrated to Israel</a>&nbsp;with their families.</dd>
<dt>1999</dt>
<dd><a title="Abraham Foxman" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Abraham_Foxman">Abraham Foxman</a>&nbsp;of the&nbsp;<a title="Anti-Defamation League" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Anti-Defamation_League">Anti-Defamation League</a>, in an 11 October 1999, letter to&nbsp;<em><a title="The Washington Post" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/The_Washington_Post">The Washington Post</a></em>&nbsp;claimed that&nbsp;<em>A Republic, Not an Empire</em>&nbsp;by&nbsp;<a title="Pat Buchanan" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pat_Buchanan">Pat Buchanan</a>&nbsp;"defends&nbsp;<a title="Charles Lindbergh" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Charles_Lindbergh">Charles Lindbergh</a>&nbsp;against charges of anti-Semitism, not mentioning the infamous 1940 [sic] speech in which he accused the Jews of warmongering."&nbsp;<a title="Pat Buchanan" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pat_Buchanan">Pat Buchanan</a>&nbsp;denies this and points out Foxman's error, saying that he mentioned the 1941 speech to say it "ignited a national firestorm," which lingered after the aviator's death, and shows "the explosiveness of mixing ethnic politics and foreign policy."</dd>
<dt>1999</dt>
<dd><a title="Richard Baumhammers" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Richard_Baumhammers">Richard Baumhammers</a>&nbsp;was arrested in&nbsp;<a title="Paris" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Paris">Paris</a>,&nbsp;<a title="France" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/France">France</a>&nbsp;for striking a 50-year-old female bartender named Vivianne Le Garrac because he "believed she was Jewish". Baumhammers then told both Le Garrac and the arresting officers that he was "mentally ill." The police took Baumhammers to the psychiatric ward of the&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="H&ocirc;tel-Dieu de Paris" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/H%C3%B4tel-Dieu_de_Paris">H&ocirc;tel-Dieu de Paris</a>&nbsp;for evaluation, then detained him at a police station. By week's end, he left on a flight for&nbsp;<a title="Spain" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Spain">Spain</a>.</dd>
<dt>1999</dt>
<dd>There were&nbsp;<a title="Murder of Gary Matson and Winfield Mowder" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Murder_of_Gary_Matson_and_Winfield_Mowder#Synagogue_and_clinic_arsons">arson attacks in Sacramento, California</a>&nbsp;&ndash;&nbsp;<a title="Congregation B'nai Israel (Sacramento, California)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Congregation_B%27nai_Israel_(Sacramento,_California)">Congregation B'nai Israel</a>, Congregation Beth Shalom, and Knesset Israel Torah Center. The fires caused over $1&nbsp;million in damage. On 17 March 2000, brothers Benjamin Matthew Williams and James Tyler Williams were charged with setting the three synagogue fires and a 2 July fire at the Country Club Medical center, which housed an&nbsp;<a title="Abortion" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Abortion">abortion</a>&nbsp;clinic.&nbsp;The charges carried up to 235 years in prison.&nbsp;Matthew Williams later admitted to reporters that he was one of eight or nine men who set fire to the synagogues and the clinic; he also claimed that his brother Tyler had not been involved.</dd>
<dt>1999 August 10</dt>
<dd><a class="mw-redirect" title="Buford O. Furrow, Jr." href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Buford_O._Furrow,_Jr.">Buford O. Furrow, Jr.</a>&nbsp;kills mail carrier&nbsp;<a title="Los Angeles Jewish Community Center shooting" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Jewish_Community_Center_shooting">Joseph Santos Ileto</a>&nbsp;and shoots five people in the&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="August 1999 Los Angeles Jewish Community Center shooting" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/August_1999_Los_Angeles_Jewish_Community_Center_shooting">August 1999 Los Angeles Jewish Community Center shooting</a>.</dd>
</dl>
<h2><span id="Twenty-first_century" class="mw-headline">Twenty-first century</span></h2>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
<dl>
<dt>2000s</dt>
<dd><a title="Craig Raine" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Craig_Raine">Craig Raine</a>, in his books&nbsp;<em>In Defence of&nbsp;<a title="T. S. Eliot" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/T._S._Eliot">T. S. Eliot</a></em>&nbsp;(2001) and&nbsp;<em>T. S. Eliot</em>&nbsp;(2006), sought to defend Eliot from the charge of anti-Semitism. Reviewing the 2006 book, Paul Dean stated that he was not convinced by Raine's argument. Nevertheless, he concluded, "Ultimately, as both Raine and, to do him justice, Julius insist, however much Eliot may have been compromised as a person, as we all are in our several ways, his greatness as a poet remains."&nbsp;In another review of Raine's 2006 book, the literary critic&nbsp;<a title="Terry Eagleton" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Terry_Eagleton">Terry Eagleton</a>&nbsp;also questioned the validity of Raine's defense of Eliot's character flaws as well as the entire basis for Raine's book, writing, "Why do critics feel a need to defend the authors they write on, like doting parents deaf to all criticism of their obnoxious children? Eliot's well-earned reputation [as a poet] is established beyond all doubt, and making him out to be as unflawed as the&nbsp;<a title="Gabriel" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gabriel">Archangel Gabriel</a>&nbsp;does him no favours."</dd>
<dt>2000</dt>
<dd><a title="Richard Baumhammers" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Richard_Baumhammers">Richard Baumhammers</a>&nbsp;walked to the home of his next-door neighbor, a 63-year-old Jewish woman named Anita "Nicki" Gordon and fatally shot her, then set her house on fire.&nbsp;Some time after that, he drove to the Beth El Congregation in&nbsp;<a title="Scott Township, Allegheny County, Pennsylvania" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Scott_Township,_Allegheny_County,_Pennsylvania">Scott Township</a>, where Gordon was a member of the synagogue. There, he fired into the windows of the synagogue, then exited his vehicle and spray-painted two red swastikas on the building.&nbsp;Baumhammers later drove to the Ahavath Achim Congregation in&nbsp;<a title="Carnegie, Pennsylvania" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Carnegie,_Pennsylvania">Carnegie</a>&nbsp;where he shattered the synagogue's glass windows with gunfire.</dd>
<dt>2000</dt>
<dd>In April 2000 the&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="International League against Racism and Anti-Semitism" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/International_League_against_Racism_and_Anti-Semitism">International League against Racism and Anti-Semitism</a>&nbsp;and&nbsp;<a title="Union des &eacute;tudiants juifs de France" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Union_des_%C3%A9tudiants_juifs_de_France">Union des &eacute;tudiants juifs de France</a>&nbsp;(the Union of French Jewish Students) brought a case against&nbsp;<a title="Yahoo!" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Yahoo!">Yahoo!</a>&nbsp;in which it objected to the auctioning of Nazi memorabilia, in France, via Yahoo!'s website on the basis that it contravened Article R645-1.&nbsp;Though a French judge initially ordered Yahoo! to take measures to make it impossible for users in France to purchase any Nazi memorabilia through the Yahoo! site, in December 2001, the US District Court for the Northern District of California ruled that Yahoo! would be shielded from the judgement of the French court.</dd>
<dt>2000</dt>
<dd>The&nbsp;<a title="Temple Beth El (Syracuse, New York)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Temple_Beth_El_(Syracuse,_New_York)">Temple Beth El</a>&nbsp;building, but not the sanctuary, was heavily damaged&nbsp;in an&nbsp;<a title="Arson" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arson">arson</a>&nbsp;attack on 13 October 2000.&nbsp;Palestinian-American Ramsi Uthman was convicted in the attack.&nbsp;Ahed Shehadeh was convicted of aiding and abetting the arson.&nbsp;According to Shehadeh's testimony, after Uthman set fire to the Temple, he yelled "I did this for you, God!"&nbsp;In exchange for his testimony Shehadeh received a five-year prison sentence, and was released in 2008. Uthman received the maximum possible sentence of 25 years, to be served in New York's&nbsp;<a title="Attica Correctional Facility" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Attica_Correctional_Facility">Attica Correctional Facility</a>, although he will be eligible for parole in 2021.&nbsp;The building reopened in 2001&nbsp;after repairing some $700,000 of damage from the attack.</dd>
<dt>2000</dt>
<dd>Firebombing of a New York synagogue (<a title="Conservative Synagogue Adath Israel of Riverdale" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Conservative_Synagogue_Adath_Israel_of_Riverdale">Conservative Synagogue Adath Israel of Riverdale</a>),&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="2000 New York terror attack" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2000_New_York_terror_attack">2000 New York terror attack</a>.</dd>
<dt>2000</dt>
<dd>The Canadian provinces of Alberta,&nbsp;Manitoba and Nova Scotia&nbsp;enacted legislation to recognize Holocaust Memorial Day in 2000.</dd>
<dt>2000 October 31</dt>
<dd><a title="Beth Israel Synagogue (Edmonton)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Beth_Israel_Synagogue_(Edmonton)">Beth Israel Synagogue (Edmonton)</a>&nbsp;is firebombed.</dd>
<dt>2000</dt>
<dd>On 22 November 2000, Judge&nbsp;<a title="Edward R. Korman" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Edward_R._Korman">Edward R. Korman</a>&nbsp;announced a settlement of the&nbsp;<a title="World Jewish Congress lawsuit against Swiss banks" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/World_Jewish_Congress_lawsuit_against_Swiss_banks">World Jewish Congress lawsuit against Swiss banks</a>&nbsp;with his approval of a&nbsp;<a class="external text" href="http://www.swissbankclaims.com/Documents/Doc_9_Settlement.pdf" rel="nofollow">plan</a>&nbsp;featuring the payment of $1.25 billion into funds controlled by the Israeli Banking Trust. Judah Gribetz was appointed Special Master to administer the plan, which is sometimes called the Gribetz Plan after its chief author.</dd>
<dt>2000</dt>
<dd><em><a class="mw-redirect" title="David Irving v Penguin Books and Deborah Lipstadt" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/David_Irving_v_Penguin_Books_and_Deborah_Lipstadt">David Irving v Penguin Books and Deborah Lipstadt</a></em>&nbsp;is a case in English law, decided in 2000, against American author&nbsp;<a title="Deborah Lipstadt" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Deborah_Lipstadt">Deborah Lipstadt</a>&nbsp;and her publisher Penguin Books, filed in an English court by the British author&nbsp;<a title="David Irving" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/David_Irving">David Irving</a>&nbsp;in 1996, asserting that Lipstadt had libeled him in her book&nbsp;<em><a title="Denying the Holocaust" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Denying_the_Holocaust">Denying the Holocaust</a></em>. The court ruled that the Irving's claim of libel relating to English defamation law and Holocaust denial was not valid because his deliberate distortion of evidence has been shown to be substantially true. English libel law puts the burden of proof on the defence, meaning that it was up to Lipstadt and her publisher to prove that her claims of Irving's deliberate misrepresentation of evidence to conform to his ideological viewpoints were substantially true. Lipstadt hired British-Jewish lawyer Anthony Julius while Penguin hired libel experts Kevin Bays and Mark Bateman of media law firm Davenport Lyons. Richard J. Evans, an established historian, was hired by the defence to serve as an expert witness. Evans spent two years examining Irving's work, and presented evidence of Irving's misrepresentations, including evidence that Irving had knowingly used forged documents as source material. Upon mutual agreement, the case was argued as a bench trial before Mr. Justice Charles Gray, who produced a written judgment 333 pages long in favour of the defendants, in which he detailed Irving's systematic distortion of the historical record of World War II.</dd>
<dt>2000</dt>
<dd>During the&nbsp;<a title="2000 United States presidential election" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2000_United_States_presidential_election">2000 Presidential election</a>, Lee Alcorn, president of the Dallas&nbsp;<a title="NAACP" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/NAACP">NAACP</a>&nbsp;branch, criticized&nbsp;<a title="Al Gore" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Al_Gore">Al Gore</a>'s selection of Senator&nbsp;<a title="Joe Lieberman" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Joe_Lieberman">Joe Lieberman</a>&nbsp;for his Vice-Presidential candidate because Lieberman was Jewish. On a gospel talk radio show on station KHVN, Alcorn stated, "If we get a Jew person, then what I'm wondering is, I mean, what is this movement for, you know? Does it have anything to do with the failed peace talks?" ... "So I think we need to be very suspicious of any kind of partnerships between the Jews at that kind of level because we know that their interest primarily has to do with money and these kind of things."<br />NAACP President&nbsp;<a title="Kweisi Mfume" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kweisi_Mfume">Kweisi Mfume</a>&nbsp;immediately suspended Alcorn and condemned his remarks. Mfume stated, "I strongly condemn those remarks. I find them to be repulsive, anti-Semitic, anti-NAACP and anti-American. Mr. Alcorn does not speak for the NAACP, its board, its staff or its membership. We are proud of our long-standing relationship with the&nbsp;<a title="American Jews" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/American_Jews">Jewish community</a>&nbsp;and I personally will not tolerate statements that run counter to the history and beliefs of the NAACP in that regard."</dd>
<dd>Alcorn, who had been suspended three times in the previous five years for misconduct, subsequently resigned from the NAACP and started his own organization called the Coalition for the Advancement of Civil Rights.
