Alcorn criticized the NAACP, saying, "I can't support the leadership of the NAACP. Large amounts of money are being given to them by large corporations that I have a problem with."&nbsp;Alcorn also said, "I cannot be bought. For this reason I gladly offer my resignation and my membership to the NAACP because I cannot work under these constraints."</dd>
<dd>Alcorn's remarks were also condemned by the Reverend&nbsp;<a title="Jesse Jackson" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jesse_Jackson">Jesse Jackson</a>, Jewish groups and George W. Bush's rival&nbsp;<a title="Republican Party (United States)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Republican_Party_(United_States)">Republican</a>&nbsp;presidential campaign. Jackson said he strongly supported Lieberman's addition to the&nbsp;<a title="Democratic Party (United States)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Democratic_Party_(United_States)">Democratic</a>&nbsp;ticket, saying, "When we live our faith, we live under the law. He [Lieberman] is a firewall of exemplary behavior."</dd>
<dd><a title="Al Sharpton" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Al_Sharpton">Al Sharpton</a>, another prominent African-American leader, said, "The appointment of Mr. Lieberman was to be welcomed as a positive step."&nbsp;The leaders of the&nbsp;<a title="American Jewish Congress" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/American_Jewish_Congress">American Jewish Congress</a>&nbsp;praised the NAACP for its quick response, stating that: "It will take more than one bigot like Alcorn to shake the sense of fellowship of American Jews with the NAACP and black America... Our common concerns are too urgent, our history too long, our connection too sturdy, to let anything like this disturb our relationship."</dd>
<dt>2001</dt>
<dd>During the&nbsp;<a title="World Conference against Racism 2001" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/World_Conference_against_Racism_2001">World Conference against Racism 2001</a>, in&nbsp;<a title="Durban" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Durban">Durban</a>, two delegations, the United States and Israel, withdraw from the conference due to their objections to a draft document equating&nbsp;<a title="Zionism" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Zionism">Zionism</a>&nbsp;with racism.</dd>
<dt>2001</dt>
<dd>Every year since 2001, there has been an annual national memorial to the victims of the Holocaust in the United Kingdom.</dd>
<dt>2001</dt>
<dd>In Belgium in 2001,&nbsp;<a title="Roeland Raes" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Roeland_Raes">Roeland Raes</a>, the ideologue and vice-president of one of the country's largest political parties, the&nbsp;<a title="Vlaams Belang" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vlaams_Belang">Vlaams Belang</a>&nbsp;(formerly named&nbsp;<a title="Vlaams Blok" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vlaams_Blok">Vlaams Blok</a>, Flemish Bloc), gave an interview on Dutch TV where he cast doubt over the number of Jews murdered by the Nazis during the Holocaust. In the same interview he questioned the scale of the Nazis' use of gas chambers and the authenticity of&nbsp;<a title="Anne Frank" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Anne_Frank">Anne Frank</a>'s diary. In response to the media assault following the interview, Raes was forced to resign his position but vowed to remain active within the party.&nbsp;Three years later, the Vlaams Blok was convicted of racism and chose to disband. Immediately afterwards, it legally reformed under the new name Vlaams Belang (Flemish Interest) with the same leaders and the same membership.</dd>
<dt>2001</dt>
<dd>Slovakia criminalized denial of fascist crimes in general in late 2001; in May 2005, the term "Holocaust" was explicitly adopted by the penal code and in 2009, it became illegal to deny any act regarded by an international criminal court as genocide.</dd>
<dt>2001</dt>
<dd><em><a title="Untersturmf&uuml;hrer" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Untersturmf%C3%BChrer">Untersturmf&uuml;hrer</a></em>&nbsp;Julius Viel was convicted in 2001 of shooting seven Jewish prisoners from the Theresienstadt concentration camp in 1945.<sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"></sup></dd>
<dt>2001 May 4</dt>
<dd>At the 17th meeting of the International Liaison Committee in&nbsp;<a title="New York City" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/New_York_City">New York</a>, Catholic Church officials state that they will change how Judaism is dealt with in Catholic seminaries and schools. In part, they state:</dd>
</dl>
<dl>
<dd>The curricula of Catholic seminaries and schools of theology should reflect the central importance of the Church's new understanding of its relationship to Jews....Courses on Bible, developments by which both the Church and rabbinic Judaism emerged from early Judaism will establish a substantial foundation for ameliorating "the painful ignorance of the history and traditions of Judaism of which only negative aspects and often caricature seem to form part of the stock ideas of many Christians".&nbsp;</dd>
</dl>
<dl>
<dd>...Courses dealing with the biblical, historical and theological aspects of relations between Jews and Christians should be an integral part of the seminary and theologate curriculum, and not merely electives. All who graduate from Catholic seminaries and theology schools should have studied the revolution in Catholic teaching on Jews and Judaism from&nbsp;<em><a title="Nostra aetate" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nostra_aetate">Nostra aetate</a></em>&nbsp;to the prayer of Pope John Paul II in Jerusalem at the Western Wall on 26 March 2000....For historic reasons, many Jews find it difficult to overcome generational memories of anti-Semitic oppression. Therefore: Lay and Religious Jewish leaders need to advocate and promote a program of education in our Jewish schools and seminaries &ndash; about the history of Catholic-Jewish relations and knowledge of Christianity and its relationship to Judaism....Encouragement of dialogue between the two faiths does involve recognition, understanding and respect for each other's beliefs, without having to accept them. It is particularly important that Jewish schools teach about the&nbsp;<a title="Second Vatican Council" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Second_Vatican_Council">Second Vatican Council</a>, and subsequent documents and attitudinal changes that opened new perspectives and possibilities for both faiths.</dd>
<dt>2002</dt>
<dd>In a letter released in late 2002,&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Osama Bin Laden" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Osama_Bin_Laden">Osama Bin Laden</a>&nbsp;stated that Jews controlled the civilian media outlets, politics, and economic institutions of the United States.</dd>
<dt>2002</dt>
<dd>In&nbsp;<a title="Romania" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Romania">Romania</a>, Emergency Ordinance No. 31 13 March 2002 prohibits Holocaust denial. It was ratified on 6 May 2006. The law also prohibits racist, fascist, xenophobic symbols, uniforms and gestures: proliferation of which is punishable with imprisonment from between six months to five years.</dd>
<dt>2002 March 11</dt>
<dd>Arson attack on&nbsp;<a title="Anshei Minsk" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Anshei_Minsk">Anshei Minsk</a>&nbsp;Synagogue in&nbsp;<a title="Toronto" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Toronto">Toronto</a>,&nbsp;<a title="Ontario" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ontario">Ontario</a>, Canada.</dd>
<dt>2002 March 30</dt>
<dd><a class="mw-redirect" title="2002 Lyon car attack" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2002_Lyon_car_attack">2002 Lyon car attack</a>&nbsp;takes place.<sup id="cite_ref-NornViolence_31-0" class="reference"></sup></dd>
<dt>2002</dt>
<dd>During the Watergate affair, there were suggestions that&nbsp;<a title="Billy Graham" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Billy_Graham">Billy Graham</a>&nbsp;had agreed with many of President&nbsp;<a title="Richard Nixon" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Richard_Nixon">Richard Nixon</a>'s antisemitic opinions, but he denied them and stressed his efforts to build bridges to the Jewish community. In 2002, the controversy was renewed when declassified "<a title="Nixon White House tapes" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nixon_White_House_tapes">Richard Nixon tapes</a>" confirmed remarks made by Graham to Nixon three decades earlier.&nbsp;Captured on the tapes, Graham agreed with Nixon that&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Jewish control of media" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jewish_control_of_media">Jews control</a>&nbsp;the&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Media of the United States" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Media_of_the_United_States">American media</a>, calling it a "stranglehold" during a 1972 conversation with Nixon, and suggesting that if Nixon was&nbsp;<a title="1972 United States presidential election" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1972_United_States_presidential_election">re-elected</a>, they might be able to do something about it.&nbsp;When the tapes were made public, Graham apologized&nbsp;and said, "Although I have no memory of the occasion, I deeply regret comments I apparently made in an Oval Office conversation with President Nixon ... some 30 years ago. ... They do not reflect my views and I sincerely apologize for any offense caused by the remarks."&nbsp;According to&nbsp;<em><a title="Newsweek" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Newsweek">Newsweek</a></em>&nbsp;magazine, "[T]he shock of the revelation was magnified because of Graham's longtime support of&nbsp;<a title="Israel" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel">Israel</a>&nbsp;and his refusal to join in calls for&nbsp;<a title="Proselytization and counter-proselytization of Jews" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Proselytization_and_counter-proselytization_of_Jews">conversion of the Jews</a>."</dd>
<dt>2002</dt>
<dd>On 11 April,&nbsp;<a title="Ghriba synagogue bombing" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ghriba_synagogue_bombing">Ghriba synagogue bombing</a>&nbsp;takes place in&nbsp;<a title="Tunisia" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tunisia">Tunisia</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-proces_38-0" class="reference"></sup></dd>
<dt>2002</dt>
<dd>On 4 July 2002, a lone gunman opened fire at the airline ticket counter of&nbsp;<a title="El Al" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/El_Al">El Al</a>,&nbsp;<a title="Israel" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel">Israel</a>'s national airline, at&nbsp;<a title="Los Angeles International Airport" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_International_Airport">Los Angeles International Airport</a>&nbsp;in&nbsp;<a title="Los Angeles" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles">Los Angeles</a>,&nbsp;<a title="California" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/California">California</a>. Two people were killed and four others were injured before the gunman was fatally shot by a security guard after also being wounded by him. This was the&nbsp;<a title="2002 Los Angeles International Airport shooting" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2002_Los_Angeles_International_Airport_shooting">2002 Los Angeles International Airport shooting</a>.</dd>
<dt>2002</dt>
<dd><a title="Pat Buchanan" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pat_Buchanan">Pat Buchanan</a>&nbsp;said
<blockquote class="templatequote">
<p>There was nothing immoral, or unwise, about the isolationists' position of 1940&ndash;41. Because of the courageous efforts of Lindbergh and America First, the United States stayed out of the war until Hitler threw the full force of his war machine against Stalin. Thus, the Soviet Union, not America&rsquo;s young, bore the brunt of defeating Nazi Germany.</p>
</blockquote>
</dd>
<dt>2002</dt>
<dd>In an interview for the magazine&nbsp;<em><a title="Lyon" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lyon">Lyon</a>&nbsp;Capitale</em>&nbsp;in January 2002,&nbsp;<a title="Dieudonn&eacute; M'bala M'bala" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dieudonn%C3%A9_M%27bala_M%27bala">Dieudonn&eacute; M'bala M'bala</a>&nbsp;described "the Jews" as "a sect, a fraud, which is the worst of all, because it was the first" and said he preferred "the charisma of&nbsp;<a title="Osama bin Laden" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Osama_bin_Laden">bin Laden</a>&nbsp;to that of&nbsp;<a title="George W. Bush" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/George_W._Bush">Bush</a>".</dd>
<dt>2002</dt>
<dd>During a&nbsp;<a title="2002 white supremacist terror plot" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2002_white_supremacist_terror_plot">2002 white supremacist terror plot</a>, a pair of&nbsp;<a title="White supremacy" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/White_supremacy">white supremacists</a>&nbsp;planned to bomb a series of institutions and people associated with&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="African American" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/African_American">African American</a>&nbsp;and American Jewish communities.&nbsp;Targets included the&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="United States Holocaust Museum" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States_Holocaust_Museum">United States Holocaust Museum</a>, the&nbsp;<a title="New England Holocaust Memorial" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/New_England_Holocaust_Memorial">New England Holocaust Memorial</a>; well-known Jews, including&nbsp;<a title="Steven Spielberg" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Steven_Spielberg">Steven Spielberg</a>; and black leaders, including Rev.&nbsp;<a title="Jesse Jackson" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jesse_Jackson">Jesse Jackson</a>.</dd>
<dt>2002</dt>
<dd>Massive European wave of attacks on Jews and Jewish institutions between March and May, with largest number of attacks occurring in France.</dd>
<dt>2002</dt>
<dd>In January 2002, the Canadian Human Rights Tribunal delivered a ruling in a complaint involving Holocaust denier&nbsp;<a title="Ernst Z&uuml;ndel" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ernst_Z%C3%BCndel">Ernst Z&uuml;ndel</a>'s website, in which it was found to be contravening the Canadian Human Rights Act. The court ordered Z&uuml;ndel to cease communicating hate messages.</dd>
<dt>2003</dt>
<dd><a title="Bulgaria" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bulgaria">Bulgaria</a>&nbsp;officially designates 10 March as Holocaust Remembrance Day and the "Day of the Salvation of the Bulgarian Jews and of the Victims of the Holocaust and of the Crimes against Humanity".</dd>
<dt>2003 May 16</dt>
<dd><a title="2003 Casablanca bombings" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2003_Casablanca_bombings">2003 Casablanca bombings</a>&nbsp;target multiple locations, including a Jewish comunity center.</dd>
<dt>2003</dt>
<dd>The&nbsp;<a title="Southern Baptist Convention" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Southern_Baptist_Convention">Southern Baptist Convention</a>&nbsp;passed a resolution "On Anti-Semitism" stating in part:</dd>
<dd>"RESOLVED, That the messengers to the Southern Baptist Convention meeting in Phoenix, Arizona, June 17&ndash;18, 2003, denounce all forms of anti-Semitism as contrary to the teachings of our Messiah and an assault on the revelation of Holy Scripture; and be it further</dd>
<dd>"RESOLVED, That we affirm to Jewish people around the world that we stand with them against any harassment that violates our historic commitments to religious liberty and human dignity; and be it finally</dd>
<dd>"RESOLVED, That we call on governmental and religious leaders across the world to stand against all forms of bigotry, hatred, or persecution."</dd>
<dt>2003</dt>
<dd><a title="People for the Ethical Treatment of Animals" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/People_for_the_Ethical_Treatment_of_Animals">People for the Ethical Treatment of Animals</a>'s "Holocaust on your Plate" exhibition consisted of eight 60-square-foot (5.6&nbsp;m<sup>2</sup>) panels, each juxtaposing images of the Holocaust with images of&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Factory farming" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Factory_farming">factory-farmed animals</a>. Photographs of concentration camp inmates were displayed next to photographs of battery chickens, and piled bodies of Holocaust victims next to a pile of pig carcasses. Captions alleged that "like the Jews murdered in&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Concentration camp" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Concentration_camp">concentration camps</a>, animals are terrorized when they are housed in huge filthy warehouses and rounded up for shipment to slaughter. The leather sofa and handbag are the moral equivalent of the&nbsp;<a title="Lampshades made from human skin" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lampshades_made_from_human_skin">lampshades made from the skins of people</a>&nbsp;killed in the&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Extermination camps in the Holocaust" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Extermination_camps_in_the_Holocaust">death camps</a>."</dd>
<dd>The exhibition was funded by an anonymous Jewish philanthropist,&nbsp;and created by Matt Prescott, who lost several relatives in the Holocaust. Prescott said: "The very same mindset that made the Holocaust possible &ndash; that we can do anything we want to those we decide are 'different or inferior' &ndash; is what allows us to commit atrocities against animals every single day. ... The fact is, all animals feel pain, fear and loneliness. We're asking people to recognize that what Jews and others went through in the Holocaust is what animals go through every day in&nbsp;<a title="Intensive animal farming" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Intensive_animal_farming">factory farms</a>."</dd>
<dd>However,&nbsp;<a title="Abraham Foxman" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Abraham_Foxman">Abraham Foxman</a>, chairman of the&nbsp;<a title="Anti-Defamation League" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Anti-Defamation_League">Anti-Defamation League</a>, said the exhibition was "outrageous, offensive and takes&nbsp;<a title="Chutzpah" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Chutzpah">chutzpah</a>&nbsp;to new heights ... The effort by PETA to compare the deliberate systematic murder of millions of Jews to the issue of animal rights is abhorrent."&nbsp;Stuart Bender, legal counsel for the United States Holocaust Memorial Museum, wrote to PETA asking them to "cease and desist this reprehensible misuse of Holocaust materials."</dd>
<dd>On 20 February 2009, the German Federal Constitutional Court dismissed a legal move challenging an appeal court's ruling that PETA's campaign was not protected by free speech laws. While not entering formal proceedings to decide in the matter, the court expressed severe doubts as to whether the campaign constituted an offense against human rights in its opinion to dismiss the appeal, as had been found by the orderly courts, but acceded to the other grounds of the former rulings that the campaign constituted a trivialization of the Holocaust and hence a severe violation of living Jews' personality rights.&nbsp;The subtleties of the ruling are sometimes not reflected adequately in press reports.</dd>
<dt>2003</dt>
<dd>On&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Yom Ha'atzmaut" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Yom_Ha%27atzmaut">Yom Ha'atzmaut</a>&nbsp;2003, a&nbsp;<a title="Molotov cocktail" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Molotov_cocktail">Molotov cocktail</a>&nbsp;was thrown through one of the synagogue&nbsp;<a title="Valley Beth Shalom" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Valley_Beth_Shalom">Valley Beth Shalom</a>'s stained-glass windows.</dd>
<dt>2003 October 16</dt>
<dd>The&nbsp;<a title="Malaysia" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Malaysia">Malaysian</a>&nbsp;Prime Minister Dr.&nbsp;<a title="Mahathir Mohamad" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mahathir_Mohamad">Mahathir Mohammed</a>&nbsp;draws a standing ovation at the 57-member&nbsp;<a title="Organisation of Islamic Cooperation" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Organisation_of_Islamic_Cooperation">Organisation of the Islamic Conference</a>&nbsp;for his speech. An excerpt: "[Muslims] are actually very strong. 1.3&nbsp;billion people cannot be simply wiped out. The Nazis killed 6&nbsp;million Jews out of 12&nbsp;million. But today the Jews rule this world by proxy. They get others to fight and die for them. They invented socialism, communism, human rights and democracy so that persecuting them would appear to be wrong so they may enjoy equal rights with others. With these they have now gained control of the most powerful countries. And they, this tiny community, have become a world power."</dd>
<dt>2003 November 16</dt>
<dd><a title="Neve Shalom Synagogue" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Neve_Shalom_Synagogue">Neve Shalom Synagogue</a>&nbsp;was hit by one of four&nbsp;<a title="Car bomb" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Car_bomb">car bomb</a>&nbsp;attacks carried out in Istanbul that week&nbsp;<sup id="cite_ref-:0_51-0" class="reference"></sup></dd>
<dt>2004</dt>
<dd>Romania officially denied the Holocaust occurred on its territory up until the&nbsp;<a title="Wiesel Commission" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wiesel_Commission">Wiesel Commission</a>&nbsp;in 2004.<sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"></sup></dd>
<dt>2004</dt>
<dd>National Holocaust Memorial Day has been recognized in Greece since 2004.<a title="Greek language" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Greek_language">Greek</a>:&nbsp;<span lang="el">&Epsilon;&theta;&nu;&iota;&kappa;ή &Eta;&mu;έ&rho;&alpha; &Mu;&nu;ή&mu;&eta;&sigmaf; &Omicron;&lambda;&omicron;&kappa;&alpha;&upsilon;&tau;ώ&mu;&alpha;&tau;&omicron;&sigmaf;</span>&nbsp;(<em>Ethniki Imera Mnimis Olokaftomatos</em>), since 2004.</dd>
<dt>2004</dt>
<dd>The film&nbsp;<em><a class="mw-redirect" title="The Passion of The Christ" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/The_Passion_of_The_Christ">The Passion of The Christ</a></em>&nbsp;was released in 2004. Before the film was even released, there were prominent criticisms of perceived antisemitic content in the film.&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="20th Century Fox" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/20th_Century_Fox">20th Century Fox</a>&nbsp;told New York Assemblyman&nbsp;<a title="Dov Hikind" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dov_Hikind">Dov Hikind</a>&nbsp;they had passed on distributing the film in response to a protest outside the&nbsp;<a title="News Corporation (1980&ndash;2013)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/News_Corporation_(1980%E2%80%932013)">News Corporation</a>&nbsp;building. Hikind warned other companies that "they should not distribute this film. This is unhealthy for Jews all over the world."</dd>
<dd>A joint committee of the Secretariat for Ecumenical and Inter-religious Affairs of the&nbsp;<a title="United States Conference of Catholic Bishops" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States_Conference_of_Catholic_Bishops">United States Conference of Catholic Bishops</a>&nbsp;and the Department of Inter-religious Affairs of the&nbsp;<a title="Anti-Defamation League" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Anti-Defamation_League">Anti-Defamation League</a>&nbsp;obtained a version of the script before it was released in theaters. They released a statement, calling it
<blockquote>
<p>one of the most troublesome texts, relative to anti-Semitic potential, that any of us had seen in twenty-five years. It must be emphasized that the main storyline presented Jesus as having been relentlessly pursued by an evil cabal of Jews, headed by the high priest&nbsp;<a title="Caiaphas" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Caiaphas">Caiaphas</a>, who finally&nbsp;<a title="Blackmail" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Blackmail">blackmailed</a>&nbsp;a weak-kneed&nbsp;<a title="Pontius Pilate" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pontius_Pilate">Pilate</a>&nbsp;into putting Jesus to death. This is precisely the storyline that fueled centuries of anti-Semitism within Christian societies. This is also a storyline rejected by the Roman Catholic Church at&nbsp;<a title="Second Vatican Council" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Second_Vatican_Council">Vatican II</a>&nbsp;in its document&nbsp;<em><a title="Nostra aetate" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nostra_aetate">Nostra aetate</a></em>, and by nearly all mainline Protestant churches in parallel documents. ... Unless this basic storyline has been altered by Mr. Gibson, a fringe Catholic who is building his own church in the Los Angeles area and who apparently accepts neither the teachings of Vatican II nor modern biblical scholarship,&nbsp;<em>The Passion of the Christ</em>&nbsp;retains a real potential for undermining the repudiation of classical Christian anti-Semitism by the churches in the last forty years.</p>
</blockquote>
</dd>
<dd>The ADL itself also released a statement about the yet-to-be-released film:</dd>
</dl>
<blockquote>
<p>For filmmakers to do justice to the biblical accounts of the passion, they must complement their artistic vision with sound scholarship, which includes knowledge of how the passion accounts have been used historically to disparage and attack Jews and Judaism. Absent such scholarly and theological understanding, productions such as&nbsp;<em>The Passion</em>&nbsp;could likely falsify history and fuel the animus of those who hate Jews.</p>
</blockquote>
<p><a class="mw-redirect" title="Rabbi Daniel Lapin" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Rabbi_Daniel_Lapin">Rabbi Daniel Lapin</a>, the head of the&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Toward Tradition" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Toward_Tradition">Toward Tradition</a>&nbsp;organization, criticized this statement, and said of Foxman, the head of the ADL, "what he is saying is that the only way to escape the wrath of Foxman is to repudiate your faith".</p>
<dl>
<dd>In&nbsp;<em><a title="The Nation" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/The_Nation">The Nation</a></em>, reviewer&nbsp;<a title="Katha Pollitt" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Katha_Pollitt">Katha Pollitt</a>&nbsp;said: "Gibson has violated just about every precept of the United States Conference of Catholic Bishops own 1988 'Criteria' for the portrayal of Jews in dramatizations of the Passion (no bloodthirsty Jews, no rabble, no use of Scripture that reinforces negative stereotypes of Jews, etc.) [...] The priests have big noses and gnarly faces, lumpish bodies, yellow teeth;&nbsp;<a title="Herod Antipas" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Herod_Antipas">Herod Antipas</a>&nbsp;and his court are a bizarre collection of oily-haired,&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Epicene" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Epicene">epicene</a>&nbsp;perverts. The 'good Jews' look like Italian movie stars (Italian sex symbol&nbsp;<a title="Monica Bellucci" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Monica_Bellucci">Monica Bellucci</a>&nbsp;is&nbsp;<a title="Mary Magdalene" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mary_Magdalene">Mary Magdalene</a>); Mary, who would have been around 50 and appeared 70, could pass for a ripe 35."<span style="font-size: xx-small;">&nbsp;</span><a class="mw-redirect" title="Jesuit" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jesuit">Jesuit</a>&nbsp;priest Fr.&nbsp;<a title="William Fulco" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/William_Fulco">William Fulco</a>, S.J., of&nbsp;<a title="Loyola Marymount University" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Loyola_Marymount_University">Loyola Marymount University</a>&mdash;and the film's&nbsp;<a title="Hebrew language" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hebrew_language">Hebrew</a>&nbsp;dialogue translator&mdash;specifically disagreed with that assessment, and disagreed with concerns that the film accused the Jewish community of&nbsp;<a title="Deicide" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Deicide">deicide</a>.</dd>
<dd>One specific scene in the film perceived as an example of anti-Semitism was in the dialogue of Caiaphas, when he states "His blood [is] on us and on our children!", a quote historically interpreted by some as a curse taken upon by the Jewish people. Certain Jewish groups asked this be removed from the film. However, only the subtitles were removed; the original dialogue remains in the Hebrew soundtrack.&nbsp;When asked about this scene, Gibson said: "I wanted it in. My brother said I was wimping out if I didn't include it. But, man, if I included that in there, they'd be coming after me at my house. They'd come to kill me."&nbsp;In another interview when asked about the scene, he said, "It's one little passage, and I believe it, but I don't and never have believed it refers to Jews, and implicates them in any sort of curse. It's directed at all of us, all men who were there, and all that came after. His blood is on us, and that's what Jesus wanted. But I finally had to admit that one of the reasons I felt strongly about keeping it, aside from the fact it's true, is that I didn't want to let someone else dictate what could or couldn't be said."</dd>
<dd>Additionally, the film's suggestion that the Temple's destruction was a direct result of the Jews' actions towards Jesus could also be interpreted as an offensive take on an event which Jewish tradition views as a tragedy, and which is still mourned by many Jews today on the fast day of&nbsp;<a title="Tisha B'Av" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tisha_B%27Av">Tisha B'Av</a>.</dd>
<dd>Asked by&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Bill O'Reilly (commentator)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bill_O%27Reilly_(commentator)">Bill O'Reilly</a>&nbsp;if his movie would "upset Jews", Gibson responded, "It's not meant to. I think it's meant to just tell the truth. I want to be as truthful as possible."&nbsp;In an interview in&nbsp;<em><a title="The Globe and Mail" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/The_Globe_and_Mail">The Globe and Mail</a></em>&nbsp;newspaper, he added: "If anyone has distorted Gospel passages to rationalize cruelty towards Jews or anyone, it's in defiance of repeated Papal condemnation. The&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Papacy" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Papacy">Papacy</a>&nbsp;has condemned racism in any form. ... Jesus died for the sins of all times, and I'll be the first on the line for culpability".</dd>
<dd>Conservative columnist&nbsp;<a title="Cal Thomas" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cal_Thomas">Cal Thomas</a>&nbsp;also disagreed with allegations of antisemitism, saying "To those in the Jewish community who worry that the film [...] might contain anti-Semitic elements, or encourage people to persecute Jews, fear not. The film does not indict Jews for the death of Jesus."&nbsp;Two&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Orthodox Jew" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Orthodox_Jew">Orthodox Jews</a>, Rabbi Daniel Lapin and conservative talk-show host and author&nbsp;<a title="Michael Medved" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Michael_Medved">Michael Medved</a>, also vocally rejected claims that the film is anti-Semitic. They have noted the film's many sympathetic portrayals of Jews:&nbsp;<a title="Simon of Cyrene" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Simon_of_Cyrene">Simon of Cyrene</a>&nbsp;(who helps Jesus carry the cross),&nbsp;<a title="Mary Magdalene" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mary_Magdalene">Mary Magdalene</a>, the&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Mary (mother of Jesus)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mary_(mother_of_Jesus)">Virgin Mary</a>,&nbsp;<a title="Saint Peter" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Saint_Peter">St. Peter</a>,&nbsp;<a title="John the Evangelist" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/John_the_Evangelist">St. John</a>,&nbsp;<a title="Saint Veronica" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Saint_Veronica">Veronica</a>&nbsp;(who wipes Jesus' face and offers him water) and several Jewish priests who protest Jesus' arrest (<a title="Nicodemus" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nicodemus">Nicodemus</a>&nbsp;and&nbsp;<a title="Joseph of Arimathea" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Joseph_of_Arimathea">Joseph of Arimathea</a>) during&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Sanhedrin Trial of Jesus" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sanhedrin_Trial_of_Jesus">Caiaphas' trial of Jesus</a>.</dd>
<dd>Bob Smithouser of Plugged in Online believed that film was trying to convey the evils and sins of humanity rather than specifically targeting Jews, stating: "The anthropomorphic portrayal of Satan as a player in these events brilliantly pulls the proceedings into the supernatural realm&mdash;a fact that should have quelled the much-publicized cries of anti-Semitism since it shows a diabolical force at work beyond any political and religious agendas of the Jews and Romans."</dd>
<dd>Moreover, Senior Vatican officer&nbsp;<a title="Dar&iacute;o Castrill&oacute;n Hoyos" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dar%C3%ADo_Castrill%C3%B3n_Hoyos">Cardinal Dar&iacute;o Castrill&oacute;n Hoyos</a>, who has seen the film, addressed the matter so:</dd>
</dl>
<blockquote>
<p>Anti-Semitism, like all forms of racism, distorts the truth in order to put a whole race of people in a bad light. This film does nothing of the sort. It draws out from the historical objectivity of the Gospel narratives sentiments of forgiveness, mercy, and reconciliation. It captures the subtleties and the horror of sin, as well as the gentle power of love and forgiveness, without making or insinuating blanket condemnations against one group. This film expressed the exact opposite, that learning from the example of Christ, there should never be any more violence against any other human being.</p>
</blockquote>
<dl>
<dt>2004</dt>
<dd>The first National Day of Commemorating the Holocaust in Romania was held in 2004.</dd>
<dt>2004 April 4</dt>
<dd><a class="mw-redirect" title="United Talmud Torah" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_Talmud_Torah">United Talmud Torah</a>&nbsp;school library is firebombed in&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Montreal, Quebec" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Montreal,_Quebec">Montreal, Quebec</a>, Canada.</dd>
<dt>2004 May</dt>
<dd>Jewish organizations and leaders protest&nbsp;<a title="Estonia" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Estonia">Estonia</a>'s erection of a statue commemorating&nbsp;<a title="Alfons Rebane" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Alfons_Rebane">Alfons Rebane</a>, an Estonian&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="SS" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/SS">SS</a>&nbsp;volunteer accused of serving as a "a Nazi executioner"&nbsp;who was "responsible for the slaughter of thousands of Jews and Russians between 1941 and 1945."</dd>
<dt>2004 June</dt>
<dd>A series of attacks on Jewish cemeteries in&nbsp;<a title="Wellington" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wellington">Wellington</a>, New Zealand.</dd>
<dt>2004 September</dt>
<dd>The&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="European Monitoring Centre on Racism and Xenophobia" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/European_Monitoring_Centre_on_Racism_and_Xenophobia">European Commission against Racism and Intolerance</a>, a part of the&nbsp;<a title="Council of Europe" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Council_of_Europe">Council of Europe</a>, called on its member nations to "ensure that criminal law in the field of combating racism covers anti-Semitism" and to penalize intentional acts of public incitement to violence, hatred or discrimination, public insults and defamation, threats against a person or group, and the expression of antisemitic ideologies. It urged member nations to "prosecute people who deny, trivialize or justify the Holocaust". The report was drawn up in wake of a rise in attacks on Jews in Europe. The report said it was Europe's "duty to remember the past by remaining vigilant and actively opposing any manifestations of racism, xenophobia, anti-Semitism and intolerance... Anti-Semitism is not a phenomenon of the past and... the slogan 'never again' is as relevant today as it was 60 years ago."&nbsp;</dd>
<dt>2005</dt>
<dd>The&nbsp;<a title="European Union" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/European_Union">European Union</a>&nbsp;has recognized&nbsp;<a title="International Holocaust Remembrance Day" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/International_Holocaust_Remembrance_Day">International Holocaust Remembrance Day</a>&nbsp;since 2005.</dd>
<dt>2005</dt>
<dd>In 2005 the United States had a "moment of silence" on the 60th anniversary of the surrender of Nazi Germany.</dd>
<dt>2005</dt>
<dd><a title="Dieudonn&eacute; M'bala M'bala" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dieudonn%C3%A9_M%27bala_M%27bala">Dieudonn&eacute; M'bala M'bala</a>&nbsp;declared during a press conference in&nbsp;<a title="Algiers" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Algiers">Algiers</a>&nbsp;that the Central Council of French Jews CRIF (<em>Conseil repr&eacute;sentatif des institutions juives de France</em>) was a "mafia" that had "total control over French policy exercise", called the commemoration of&nbsp;<a title="The Holocaust" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/The_Holocaust">the Holocaust</a>&nbsp;"memorial pornography"&nbsp;("<em>pornographie m&eacute;morielle</em>"), and claimed that the "Zionists of the&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Centre National de la Cin&eacute;matographie" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Centre_National_de_la_Cin%C3%A9matographie">Centre National de la Cin&eacute;matographie</a>," which "control French cinema" prevented him from making a film about the&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Slave trade" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Slave_trade">slave trade</a>.&nbsp;Dieudonn&eacute; was also trying to appear as a spokesman for French blacks, but, after some initial sympathy, notably from the novelist&nbsp;<a title="Calixthe Beyala" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Calixthe_Beyala">Calixthe Beyala</a>, the journalists&nbsp;<a class="new" title="Antoine Garnier (page does not exist)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Antoine_Garnier&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1">Antoine Garnier</a>&nbsp;and&nbsp;<a class="new" title="Claudy Siar (page does not exist)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Claudy_Siar&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1">Claudy Siar</a>, as well as the founding members of the&nbsp;<em>Conseil repr&eacute;sentatif des associations noires</em>&nbsp;(CRAN), he increasingly met with their rejection.</dd>
<dt>2005</dt>
<dd>In 2005 the Egyptian&nbsp;<a title="Muslim Brotherhood" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Muslim_Brotherhood">Muslim Brotherhood</a>&nbsp;leader,&nbsp;<a title="Mohammed Mahdi Akef" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mohammed_Mahdi_Akef">Mohammed Mahdi Akef</a>, denounced what he called "the myth of the Holocaust" in defending Iranian president&nbsp;<a title="Mahmoud Ahmadinejad" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mahmoud_Ahmadinejad">Mahmoud Ahmadinejad</a>'s denial of the Holocaust.</dd>
<dt>2005 September</dt>
<dd>Throughout the&nbsp;<a title="Poland" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Poland">Polish</a>&nbsp;election&nbsp;<a title="Radio Maryja" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Radio_Maryja">Radio Maryja</a>&nbsp;continued to promote antisemitic views, including denial of the facts of the&nbsp;<a title="Jedwabne pogrom" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jedwabne_pogrom">Jedwabne pogrom</a>&nbsp;in 1941. Their support of right-wing conservative&nbsp;<a title="Law and Justice" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Law_and_Justice">Law and Justice party</a>&nbsp;is considered a major factor in their electoral victory.</dd>
<dt>2005</dt>
<dd>A group of 15 members of the State&nbsp;<a title="Duma" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Duma">Duma</a>&nbsp;of Russia demands that Judaism and Jewish organizations be banned from the country. In June, 500 prominent Russians demand that the state prosecutor investigate ancient Jewish texts as "anti-Russian" and ban Judaism. The investigation was launched, but halted among international outcry.</dd>
<dt>2005</dt>
<dd>The&nbsp;<a title="2005 Los Angeles bomb plot" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2005_Los_Angeles_bomb_plot">2005 Los Angeles bomb plot</a>&nbsp;was a 2005 effort by a group of ex-convicts calling themselves&nbsp;<em>Jamiyyat Ul-Islam Is-Saheeh</em>&nbsp;to bomb several military bases, a number of synagogues, and an Israeli consulate in California.</dd>
<dd>On 31 August 2005, Kevin James and three other men were indicted on terrorism charges related to conspiracy to attack military facilities in the Los Angeles area and of attempting to fund their campaign by robbing gas stations in Southern California over the previous three months. Kevin James, a&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Muslim" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Muslim">Muslim</a>&nbsp;convert, was accused of founding a radical Islamic group called J.I.S (Jam&rsquo;iyyat Ul-Islam Is-Saheehجمعية الإسلام الصحيح, Arabic for "Assembly of Authentic&nbsp;<a title="Islam" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Islam">Islam</a>") from his cell in&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Folsom Prison" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Folsom_Prison">Folsom Prison</a>&nbsp;in California, and of recruiting fellow inmates to join his mission to kill infidels.</dd>
<dt>2005</dt>
<dd><a class="mw-redirect" title="Prince Harry" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Prince_Harry">Prince Harry</a>&nbsp;was photographed at&nbsp;<a title="Highgrove House" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Highgrove_House">Highgrove House</a>&nbsp;at a "Colonial and Native" themed&nbsp;<a title="Costume party" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Costume_party">costume party</a>&nbsp;wearing a Nazi German&nbsp;<a title="Afrika Korps" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Afrika_Korps">Afrika Korps</a>&nbsp;uniform with a&nbsp;<a title="Swastika" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Swastika">swastika</a>&nbsp;armband.&nbsp;He later issued a public statement apologising for his behavior.</dd>
<dt>2005</dt>
<dd><a title="International Holocaust Remembrance Day" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/International_Holocaust_Remembrance_Day">International Holocaust Remembrance Day</a>&nbsp;was designated by the United Nations General Assembly Resolution 60/7 on 1 November 2005 during the 42nd plenary session.</dd>
<dt>2005 December</dt>
<dd><a title="Iran" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Iran">Iranian</a>&nbsp;president&nbsp;<a title="Mahmoud Ahmadinejad" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mahmoud_Ahmadinejad">Mahmoud Ahmadinejad</a>&nbsp;widens the hostility between Iran and Israel by&nbsp;<a title="Holocaust denial" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Holocaust_denial">denying the Holocaust</a>&nbsp;during a speech in the Iranian city of&nbsp;<a title="Zahedan" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Zahedan">Zahedan</a>. He made the following comments on live television: "They have invented a myth that Jews were massacred and place this above God, religions and the prophets." Continuing, he suggested that if the Holocaust had occurred, that it was the responsibility of Europeans to offer up territory to Jews: "This is our proposal: give a part of your own land in Europe, the United States, Canada or Alaska to them [the Jews] so that the Jews can establish their country." See&nbsp;<a title="Mahmoud Ahmadinejad and Israel" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mahmoud_Ahmadinejad_and_Israel">Mahmoud Ahmadinejad and Israel</a></dd>
<dt>2006, 11 January</dt>
<dd><a title="Alexandr Koptsev" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Alexandr_Koptsev">Alexandr Koptsev</a>&nbsp;stabbbed nine people at&nbsp;<a title="Bolshaya Bronnaya Synagogue" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bolshaya_Bronnaya_Synagogue">Bolshaya Bronnaya Synagogue</a>.</dd>
<dt>2006</dt>
<dd>On 11 December 2006, the Iranian state-sponsored "<a title="International Conference to Review the Global Vision of the Holocaust" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/International_Conference_to_Review_the_Global_Vision_of_the_Holocaust">International Conference to Review the Global Vision of the Holocaust</a>" opened to widespread condemnation.&nbsp;The conference, called for by and held at the behest of Ahmadinejad,&nbsp;was widely described as a "Holocaust denial conference" or a "meeting of Holocaust deniers",&nbsp;though Iran denied it was a Holocaust denial conference.&nbsp;A few months before it opened, the Iranian Foreign Ministry spokesman Hamid Reza Asefi stated: "The Holocaust is not a sacred issue that one can't touch. I have visited the Nazi camps in Eastern Europe. I think it is exaggerated."</dd>
<dt>2006</dt>
<dd><a title="John Gudenus" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/John_Gudenus">John Gudenus</a>&nbsp;received a one-year suspended sentence for breaking the&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Verbotsgesetz" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Verbotsgesetz">Verbotsgesetz</a>, Austria's laws against denying or diminishing the Holocaust.&nbsp;Gudenus had suggested that it was necessary to verify the existence of gas chambers in Nazi Germany and later remarked that there had been gas chambers in Poland but not in Germany.</dd>
<dt>2006</dt>
<dd>In 2006,&nbsp;<a title="Mel Gibson" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mel_Gibson">Mel Gibson</a>&nbsp;was arrested for&nbsp;<a title="Driving under the influence" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Driving_under_the_influence">driving under the influence</a>&nbsp;(DUI) while speeding in his vehicle with an open container of alcohol, which is illegal in much of the United States. According to the arrest report, Gibson exploded into an angry tirade when the arresting officer would not allow him to drive home. Gibson climaxed with the words, "Fucking Jews... the Jews are responsible for all the wars in the world. Are you a Jew?"</dd>
<dt>2006</dt>
<dd>In 2006, sixty of&nbsp;<a title="Arthur Butz" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arthur_Butz">Arthur Butz</a>'s colleagues from the Department of Electrical Engineering and Computer Science faculty signed a censure describing Butz's Holocaust denial as "an affront to our humanity and our standards as scholars".&nbsp;The letter also called for Butz to "leave our Department and our University and stop trading on our reputation for academic excellence".</dd>
<dt>2006</dt>
<dd>The Netherlands rejected a draft law proposing a maximum sentence of one year on denial of genocidal acts in general, although specifically denying the Holocaust remains a criminal offense there.</dd>
<dt>2006</dt>
<dd><a title="Dieudonn&eacute; M'bala M'bala" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dieudonn%C3%A9_M%27bala_M%27bala">Dieudonn&eacute; M'bala M'bala</a>&nbsp;was sentenced to a penalty of &euro;4,500 for defamation after having called a prominent Jewish television presenter a "secret donor of the child-murdering Israeli army".</dd>
<dt>2006 February</dt>
<dd>A French Jew,&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Ilan Halimi" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ilan_Halimi">Ilan Halimi</a>&nbsp;is kidnapped and&nbsp;<a title="Torture murder" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Torture_murder">tortured to death</a>&nbsp;for 23 days in what Paris police have officially declared an antisemitic act.&nbsp;The event causes international outcry.&nbsp;On 9 May, the Helsinki Commission held a briefing titled "Tools for Combating Anti-Semitism: Police Training and Holocaust Education".</dd>
<dt>2006 February</dt>
<dd>In February 2006&nbsp;<a title="David Irving" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/David_Irving">David Irving</a>&nbsp;was convicted in Austria, where Holocaust denial is illegal, for a speech he had made in 1989 in which he denied the existence of gas chambers at Auschwitz.&nbsp;Irving was aware of the outstanding arrest warrant, but chose to go to Austria anyway "to give a lecture to a far-right student fraternity".&nbsp;Although he pleaded guilty to the charge, Irving said he had been "mistaken", and had changed his opinions on the Holocaust. "I said that then, based on my knowledge at the time, but by 1991 when I came across the Eichmann papers, I wasn't saying that anymore and I wouldn't say that now. The Nazis did murder millions of Jews."&nbsp;Irving served 13 months of a 3-year sentence in an Austrian prison, including the period between his arrest and conviction, and was deported in early 2007.</dd>
<dt>2006 July</dt>
<dd><a title="Naveed Afzal Haq" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Naveed_Afzal_Haq">Naveed Afzal Haq</a>&nbsp;kills Pamela Waechter and injures five others in the&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Seattle Jewish Federation shooting" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Seattle_Jewish_Federation_shooting">July 2006 Seattle Jewish Federation shooting</a>.</dd>
<dt>2006 December</dt>
<dd>The&nbsp;<a title="International Conference to Review the Global Vision of the Holocaust" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/International_Conference_to_Review_the_Global_Vision_of_the_Holocaust">International Conference to Review the Global Vision of the Holocaust</a>&nbsp;was a two-day conference that opened on 11 December 2006 in Tehran, Iran; many saw it as a conference rife with antisemitism,&nbsp;<a title="Anti-Zionism" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Anti-Zionism">anti-Zionism</a>, and&nbsp;<a title="Holocaust denial" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Holocaust_denial">Holocaust denial</a>.</dd>
<dt>2007</dt>
<dd><a title="Elie Wiesel" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Elie_Wiesel">Elie Wiesel</a>&nbsp;was attacked in a&nbsp;<a title="San Francisco" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/San_Francisco">San Francisco</a>&nbsp;hotel by 22-year-old&nbsp;<a title="Holocaust denial" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Holocaust_denial">Holocaust denier</a>&nbsp;Eric Hunt in February 2007, but was not injured. Hunt was arrested the following month and charged with multiple offenses.<sup id="cite_ref-102" class="reference"></sup></dd>
<dt>2007</dt>
<dd>In May 2007 Ekrem Ajanovic, a&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Bosniak" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bosniak">Bosniak</a>&nbsp;MP in the Bosnian Parliament proposed a legislation on criminalizing the denial of Holocaust, genocide and crimes against humanity. This was the first time that somebody in&nbsp;<a title="Bosnia and Herzegovina" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bosnia_and_Herzegovina">Bosnia and Herzegovina</a>'s Parliament proposed such a legislation. Bosnian Serb MPs voted against this legislation and proposed that such an issue should be resolved within the Criminal Code of Bosnia and Herzegovina.&nbsp;Following this, on 6 May 2009 Bosniak MPs Adem Huskic, Ekrem Ajanovic and Remzija Kadric proposed to the BH parliament a change to the Criminal Code of&nbsp;<a title="Bosnia and Herzegovina" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bosnia_and_Herzegovina">Bosnia and Herzegovina</a>&nbsp;where Holocaust, genocide and crimes against humanity denial would be criminalized.&nbsp;Bosnian Serb MPs have repeatedly been against such a legislation claiming that the law "would cause disagreement and even animosity" according to&nbsp;<a title="Alliance of Independent Social Democrats" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Alliance_of_Independent_Social_Democrats">SNSD</a>&nbsp;member Lazar Prodanovic.</dd>
<dt>2007</dt>
<dd>In October 2007, a tribunal declared Spain's Holocaust denial law&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Unconstitutional" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Unconstitutional">unconstitutional</a>.</dd>
<dt>2007</dt>
<dd>On 15 November 2007, an appellate court sentenced&nbsp;<a title="Dieudonn&eacute; M'bala M'bala" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dieudonn%C3%A9_M%27bala_M%27bala">Dieudonn&eacute; M'bala M'bala</a>&nbsp;to a &euro;5,000 fine because he had characterized "the Jews" as "slave traders" after being attacked in le Th&eacute;&acirc;tre de la Main d'Or.</dd>
<dt>2007</dt>
<dd>In 2007 Italy rejected a Holocaust denial law proposing a prison sentence of up to four years.</dd>
<dt>2007</dt>
<dd>A Jewish professor, Elizabeth Midlarsky, had a swastika spraypainted on her office door in 2007.</dd>
<dt>2007</dt>
<dd>On 15 February 2007, Holocaust denier&nbsp;<a title="Ernst Z&uuml;ndel" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ernst_Z%C3%BCndel">Ernst Z&uuml;ndel</a>&nbsp;was convicted on 14 counts of incitement under Germany's&nbsp;<em><a title="Volksverhetzung" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Volksverhetzung">Volksverhetzung</a></em>&nbsp;law, which bans the incitement of hatred against a portion of the population, and given the maximum sentence of five years in prison.</dd>
<dt>2007</dt>
<dd>On 7 July 2007, the&nbsp;<a title="Holy See" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Holy_See">Vatican</a>&nbsp;released&nbsp;<a title="Pope Benedict XVI" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pope_Benedict_XVI">Pope Benedict XVI</a>'s&nbsp;<a title="Motu proprio" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Motu_proprio">motu proprio</a>&nbsp;entitled,&nbsp;<em><a title="Summorum Pontificum" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Summorum_Pontificum">Summorum Pontificum</a></em>&nbsp;which permitted more widespread celebration of&nbsp;<a title="Mass (liturgy)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mass_(liturgy)">Mass</a>&nbsp;according to the "<a title="Missal" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Missal">Missal</a>&nbsp;promulgated by&nbsp;<a title="Pope John XXIII" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pope_John_XXIII">Pope John XXIII</a>&nbsp;in 1962". Jewish reactions to the motu proprio underlined their concern that the traditional formulation of the&nbsp;<a title="Good Friday prayer for the Jews" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Good_Friday_prayer_for_the_Jews">Good Friday prayer for the Jews</a>, which Jews felt offensive, would be more broadly used.<br />In the form in which they appear in the 1962 Missal, the set of prayers in which that of the Jews is included are for: the Holy Church, the Supreme Pontiff; all orders and grades of the faithful (clergy and laity); public officials (added in 1955, replacing an older prayer for the&nbsp;<a title="Holy Roman Emperor" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Holy_Roman_Emperor">Holy Roman Emperor</a>, not used since the abdication of&nbsp;<a title="Francis II, Holy Roman Emperor" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Francis_II,_Holy_Roman_Emperor">Francis II</a>&nbsp;in 1806 but still printed in the Roman Missal); catechumens; the needs of the faithful; heretics and schismatics; the conversion of the Jews (without the word "perfidis"); the conversion of pagans.<br />In later editions of the Missal, the prayers are for: the Church; the Pope, the clergy and laity of the Church; those preparing for baptism; the unity of Christians, the Jewish people; those who do not believe in Christ; those who do not believe in God; all in public office; those in special need.</dd>
<dt>2007 August/September</dt>
<dd>The Jewish state, Israel, is shocked to find a&nbsp;<a title="Neo-Nazism" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Neo-Nazism">neo-Nazi</a>&nbsp;group of immigrants (from Russia) called&nbsp;<a title="Patrol 36" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Patrol_36">Patrol 36</a>&nbsp;committing vandalism and voicing anti-Semitic rhetoric within its borders. Some members had immigrated under the&nbsp;<a title="Law of Return" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Law_of_Return">Law of Return</a>. One of that group's members was a grandchild of a Holocaust survivor, and all were of Jewish descent. The group was violent against gays, Ethiopian Jews,&nbsp;<a title="Haredi Judaism" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Haredi_Judaism">haredi</a>&nbsp;Jews, and drug addicts.</dd>
<dt>2007 and 2008</dt>
<dd><a title="Pope Benedict XVI" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pope_Benedict_XVI">Pope Benedict XVI</a>, via the document&nbsp;<em><a title="Summorum Pontificum" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Summorum_Pontificum">Summorum Pontificum</a></em>, officially revives the&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Tridentine mass" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tridentine_mass">Tridentine mass</a>, which contains a&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Good Friday Prayer for the Jews" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Good_Friday_Prayer_for_the_Jews">Good Friday prayer asking for the conversion of the Jews</a>. This leads to criticism from Jewish leaders, charging that the prayer is anti-Semitic. The Vatican subsequently issues a statement condemning anti-Semitism, but is reluctant to remove the prayer. and Benedict visits the&nbsp;<a title="Park East Synagogue" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Park_East_Synagogue">Park East Synagogue</a>&nbsp;in an April 2008 visit to New York, which is apparently well-received, with the congregants and the Pope exchanging gifts with each other.<sup id="cite_ref-113" class="reference"></sup></dd>
<dd>Jewish communities around the world are rocked by firebombings, assaults, and death threats during a spate of&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Antisemitic incidents during the Gaza War (2008-09)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Antisemitic_incidents_during_the_Gaza_War_(2008-09)">Antisemitic incidents during the Gaza War</a>.</dd>
<dt>2008</dt>
<dd>On 8 September 2009, the&nbsp;<em>Harvard Crimson</em>&nbsp;school paper ran a paid Holocaust denial ad from Bradley R Smith. It was quickly criticized and an apology was issued from the editor, claiming it was a mistake.</dd>
<dt>2008</dt>
<dd>The&nbsp;<a title="Southern Baptist Convention" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Southern_Baptist_Convention">Southern Baptist Convention</a>&nbsp;passed a resolution stating in part, "RESOLVED, That we join in prayer for the peace of Jerusalem (Psalm 122:6-7), calling upon world leaders to renounce the growing tide of anti-Semitism".</dd>
<dt>2008</dt>
<dd>On 26 June 2008,&nbsp;<a title="Dieudonn&eacute; M'bala M'bala" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dieudonn%C3%A9_M%27bala_M%27bala">Dieudonn&eacute; M'bala M'bala</a>&nbsp;was sentenced in the highest judicial instance to a &euro;7,000 fine for his characterization of Holocaust commemorations as "memorial pornography".</dd>
<dt>2008</dt>
<dd>26&ndash;29 November:&nbsp;<a title="2008 Mumbai attacks" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2008_Mumbai_attacks">2008 Mumbai attacks</a>.&nbsp;<a title="Nariman House" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nariman_House">Nariman House</a>&nbsp;also attacked.</dd>
<dt>2008</dt>
<dd>On 26 December 2008, at an event at the&nbsp;<a title="Parc de la Villette" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Parc_de_la_Villette">Parc de la Villette</a>&nbsp;in Paris,&nbsp;<a title="Dieudonn&eacute; M'bala M'bala" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dieudonn%C3%A9_M%27bala_M%27bala">Dieudonn&eacute; M'bala M'bala</a>&nbsp;awarded the Holocaust denier&nbsp;<a title="Robert Faurisson" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Robert_Faurisson">Robert Faurisson</a>&nbsp;an "insolent outcast" prize [<em>prix de l'infr&eacute;quentabilit&eacute; et de l'insolence</em>]. The award was presented by one of Dieudonn&eacute;'s assistants, Jacky, dressed in a&nbsp;<a title="Nazi concentration camps" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nazi_concentration_camps">concentration camp</a>&nbsp;uniform with a&nbsp;<a title="Yellow badge" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Yellow_badge">yellow badge</a>. This caused a scandal and earned him his sixth court conviction to date.</dd>
<dt>2008</dt>
<dd>The universal permission given to priests by&nbsp;<a title="Pope Benedict XVI" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pope_Benedict_XVI">Pope Benedict XVI</a>&nbsp;in 2007 to celebrate (privately and, under certain conditions, even publicly) the&nbsp;<a title="Tridentine Mass" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tridentine_Mass">Tridentine Mass</a>&nbsp;as printed in the 1962&nbsp;<a title="Roman Missal" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Roman_Missal">Roman Missal</a>&nbsp;was followed by complaints from Jewish groups and some Catholic leaders over what they perceived as a return to a&nbsp;<a title="Supersessionism" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Supersessionism">supersessionist</a>&nbsp;theology that they saw expressed in the 1960&nbsp;<a title="Good Friday prayer for the Jews" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Good_Friday_prayer_for_the_Jews">Good Friday prayer for the Jews</a>. In response to the complaints, Pope Benedict amended the Good Friday prayer.&nbsp;On 6 February 2008, the Vatican newspaper,&nbsp;<em><a title="L'Osservatore Romano" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/L%27Osservatore_Romano">L'Osservatore Romano</a></em>, published a note&nbsp;&nbsp;of the&nbsp;<a title="Secretariat of State (Holy See)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Secretariat_of_State_(Holy_See)">Secretariat of State</a>&nbsp;announcing that Pope Benedict XVI had amended the Good Friday prayer for the Jews contained in the 1962 Roman Missal, and decreeing that the amended text "be used, beginning from the current year, in all celebrations of the Liturgy of Good Friday according to the aforementioned&nbsp;<em>Missale Romanum</em>".</dd>
<dd>The new prayer reads as follows:</dd>
<dd><em>Let us also pray for the Jews: That our God and Lord may illuminate their hearts, that they acknowledge Jesus Christ is the Savior of all men.</em>&nbsp;(<em>Let us pray.</em>&nbsp;<em>Kneel.</em>&nbsp;<em>Rise.</em>)&nbsp;<em>Almighty and eternal God, who want that all men be saved and come to the recognition of the truth, propitiously grant that even as the fullness of the peoples enters Thy Church, all Israel be saved. Through Christ Our Lord. Amen.</em></dd>
<dd>Even the new formulation met with reservations from groups such as the Anti-Defamation League. They considered the removal of "blindness" and "immersion in darkness" with respect to the Jews an improvement over the original language in the Tridentine Mass, but saw no reason why the prayer in the rite as revised by Paul VI was not used instead.</dd>
<dt>2008 26&ndash;29 November</dt>
<dd>Mumbai, India: Nariman House, a Chabad Lubavitch Jewish centre in Colaba known as the Mumbai Chabad House, was taken over by two Pakistani terrorists and several residents were held hostage. The house was stormed by NSG commandos and, after a long battle, the two attackers were killed. Rabbi&nbsp;<a title="Gavriel Holtzberg" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gavriel_Holtzberg">Gavriel Holtzberg</a>&nbsp;and his wife Rivka, who was six months pregnant, were murdered with other hostages inside the house by the attackers. Indian forces found the body of six hostages inside the house.</dd>
<dt>2009</dt>
<dd>Swedish television broadcast an interview recorded at the&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Society of St. Pius X" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Society_of_St._Pius_X">Society of St. Pius X</a>'s seminary in&nbsp;<a title="Schierling" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Schierling">Zaitzkofen</a>,&nbsp;<a title="Bavaria" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bavaria">Bavaria</a>. During the interview,&nbsp;<a title="Richard Williamson (bishop)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Richard_Williamson_(bishop)">Richard Williamson</a>&nbsp;expressed a belief that&nbsp;<a title="Nazi Germany" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nazi_Germany">Nazi Germany</a>&nbsp;did not use&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Gas chambers" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gas_chambers">gas chambers</a>&nbsp;during the&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Holocaust" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Holocaust">Holocaust</a>&nbsp;and that a total of between 200,000 and 300,000 Jews were killed. Based upon these statements, the Bishop was immediately charged with and convicted of&nbsp;<a title="Holocaust denial" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Holocaust_denial">Holocaust denial</a>&nbsp;by a German court. The Holy See declared that Pope Benedict had been unaware of Williamson's views when he lifted the excommunication of four bishops including him, and that Williamson would remain suspended from his episcopal functions until he unequivocally and publicly distanced himself from his position on the&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Holocaust" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Holocaust">Holocaust</a>.&nbsp;In 2010 Williamson was convicted of incitement in a German court in relation to those views; the conviction was later vacated on appeal but then reinstated on retrial in early 2013.&nbsp;He appealed again, but his appeal was rejected.</dd>
<dt>2009</dt>
<dd>In August 2009, Hamas&nbsp;<a title="Hamas&ndash;UNRWA Holocaust dispute" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hamas%E2%80%93UNRWA_Holocaust_dispute">refused to allow Palestinian children to learn about the Holocaust</a>, which it called "a lie invented by the Zionists" and referred to Holocaust education as a "war crime".</dd>
<dt>2009</dt>
<dd>On 27 February 2009,&nbsp;<a title="Dieudonn&eacute; M'bala M'bala" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dieudonn%C3%A9_M%27bala_M%27bala">Dieudonn&eacute; M'bala M'bala</a>&nbsp;was ordered to pay 75,000&nbsp;<a title="Canadian dollar" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Canadian_dollar">Canadian dollars</a>&nbsp;in&nbsp;<a title="Montreal" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Montreal">Montreal</a>&nbsp;to singer and actor&nbsp;<a title="Patrick Bruel" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Patrick_Bruel">Patrick Bruel</a>&nbsp;for defamatory statements. He had called Bruel a "liar" and an "Israeli soldier".</dd>
<dt>2009</dt>
<dd>On 26 March 2009,&nbsp;<a title="Dieudonn&eacute; M'bala M'bala" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dieudonn%C3%A9_M%27bala_M%27bala">Dieudonn&eacute; M'bala M'bala</a>&nbsp;was fined &euro;1,000 and ordered to pay &euro;2,000 in damages for having defamed Elisabeth Schemla, a Jewish journalist who ran the now-defunct Proche-Orient.info website. He declared on 31 May 2005 that the website wanted to "eradicate Dieudonn&eacute; from the audiovisual landscape" and had said of him that "he's an anti-Semite, he's the son of Hitler, he will exterminate everyone".</dd>
<dt>2009</dt>
<dd>On 27 October 2009,&nbsp;<a title="Dieudonn&eacute; M'bala M'bala" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dieudonn%C3%A9_M%27bala_M%27bala">Dieudonn&eacute; M'bala M'bala</a>&nbsp;was sentenced to a fine of &euro;10,000 for "public insult of people of Jewish faith or origin" related to his show with&nbsp;<a title="Robert Faurisson" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Robert_Faurisson">Robert Faurisson</a>.&nbsp;Dieudonn&eacute; appealed to the European Court of Human Rights, which rejected his case on 10 November 2015.</dd>
<dt>2009</dt>
<dd>On 29 January 2009,&nbsp;<a title="Dieudonn&eacute; M'bala M'bala" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dieudonn%C3%A9_M%27bala_M%27bala">Dieudonn&eacute; M'bala M'bala</a>&nbsp;celebrated the 80th birthday of Holocaust denier&nbsp;<a title="Robert Faurisson" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Robert_Faurisson">Robert Faurisson</a>&nbsp;in his theater, in the midst of a representative gathering of Holocaust deniers, right-wing radicals, and radical Shiites.</dd>
<dt>2009</dt>
<dd><a title="Kevin Myers" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kevin_Myers">Kevin Myers</a>&nbsp;attracted criticism for a 2009 article for the&nbsp;<em><a title="Irish Independent" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Irish_Independent">Irish Independent</a></em>&nbsp;in which he claims: "There was no holocaust (or Holocaust, as my computer software insists) and six million Jews were not murdered by the Third Reich. These two statements of mine are irrefutable truths".&nbsp;In the article, Myers criticises the 6-million figure &ndash; though he says "millions of Jews were murdered" &ndash; and criticises the term&nbsp;<em>holocaust</em>&nbsp;because "[m]ost Jewish victims of the Third Reich were not burnt in the ovens in Auschwitz. They were shot by the hundreds of thousands in the Lebensraum of the east, or were worked or starved to death in a hundred other camps, across the Reich." Overall, he states: "I'm a holocaust denier; but I also believe that the Nazis planned the extermination of the Jewish people, as far as their evil hands could reach."<sup id="cite_ref-Myers2009_132-1" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_antisemitism_in_the_21st_century#cite_note-Myers2009-132">[</a></sup></dd>
<dt>2009</dt>
<dd>Tapes were released in which&nbsp;<a title="Billy Graham" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Billy_Graham">Billy Graham</a>&nbsp;is heard in a 1973 conversation with&nbsp;<a title="Richard Nixon" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Richard_Nixon">Richard Nixon</a>&nbsp;referring to Jews and "the synagogue of&nbsp;<a title="Satan" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Satan">Satan</a>". A spokesman for Graham said that Graham has never been an antisemite and that the comparison (in accord with the context of the quotation in the&nbsp;<a title="Book of Revelation" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Book_of_Revelation">Book of Revelation</a>) was directed specifically at those claiming to be Jews, but not holding to traditional Jewish values.</dd>
<dt>2009</dt>
<dd>In a 14 April 2009, column,&nbsp;<a title="Pat Buchanan" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pat_Buchanan">Pat Buchanan</a>&nbsp;likened the persecution of&nbsp;<a title="John Demjanjuk" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/John_Demjanjuk">John Demjanjuk</a>&nbsp;to that of&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Jesus Christ" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jesus_Christ">Jesus Christ</a>&nbsp;on&nbsp;<a class="new" title="Calvary Hill (page does not exist)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Calvary_Hill&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1">Calvary Hill</a>, stating:</dd>
</dl>
<blockquote class="templatequote">
<p>It is the same Satanic brew of hate and revenge that drove another innocent Man up Calvary that first&nbsp;<a title="Good Friday" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Good_Friday">Good Friday</a>&nbsp;2,000 years ago.</p>
</blockquote>
<dl>
<dt>2009 April</dt>
<dd>Members of the Lithuanian Jewish community report significant increases in anti-Semitism. Local Jewish leader Simonas Aperavicius notes anti-Semitism in the Lithuanian media.</dd>
<dt>2009 May</dt>
<dd>On 20 May 2009,&nbsp;<a title="Law enforcement in the United States" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Law_enforcement_in_the_United_States">US law enforcement</a>&nbsp;arrested four men in connection with a plot to shoot down military airplanes flying out of an&nbsp;<a title="Air National Guard" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Air_National_Guard">Air National Guard</a>&nbsp;base in&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Newburgh (town), New York" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Newburgh_(town),_New_York">Newburgh, New York</a>, and blow up two&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Synagogues" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Synagogues">synagogues</a>&nbsp;in the&nbsp;<a title="Riverdale, Bronx" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Riverdale,_Bronx">Riverdale</a>&nbsp;community of&nbsp;<a title="The Bronx" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/The_Bronx">the Bronx</a>.&nbsp;The group, led by James Cromitie, was tried and all four were convicted. It was later brought to light that the four men were actually encouraged into participating in the plot by the FBI. The men argue that this was a case of entrapment. See&nbsp;<a title="2009 Bronx terrorism plot" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2009_Bronx_terrorism_plot">2009 Bronx terrorism plot</a>.</dd>
<dt>2009 June</dt>
<dd>A lone 88-year-old gunman and Neo-Nazi,&nbsp;<a title="James von Brunn" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/James_von_Brunn">James von Brunn</a>&nbsp;enters the&nbsp;<a title="United States Holocaust Memorial Museum" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States_Holocaust_Memorial_Museum">United States Holocaust Memorial Museum</a>&nbsp;in&nbsp;<a title="Washington, D.C." href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Washington,_D.C.">Washington, D.C.</a>, shooting and fatally wounding&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Stephen Tyrone Johns" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Stephen_Tyrone_Johns">Stephen Tyrone Johns</a>, a security officer of African-American descent.</dd>
<dt>2010, 5 January</dt>
<dd><a title="Etz Hayyim Synagogue" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Etz_Hayyim_Synagogue">Etz Hayyim Synagogue</a>&nbsp;was targeted for an arson attack.</dd>
<dt>2010, 21 February&nbsp;<a title="Sha'ar Hashamayim Synagogue (Cairo)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sha%27ar_Hashamayim_Synagogue_(Cairo)">Sha'ar Hashamayim Synagogue (Cairo)</a>&nbsp;bombed, no caualties.</dt>
<dt>2010, 23 July</dt>
<dd><a title="Malm&ouml; Synagogue" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Malm%C3%B6_Synagogue">Malm&ouml; Synagogue</a>&nbsp;in&nbsp;<a title="Sweden" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sweden">Sweden</a>&nbsp;is attacked with explosives.&nbsp;The explosion was caused with some kind of fireworks or firecracker containing too little gunpowder to seriously damage the building.</dd>
<dt>2010</dt>
<dd>In 2010 the Parliament of Hungary adopted legislation punishing the denial of the genocides committed by National Socialist or Communist systems, without mentioning the word "Holocaust".</dd>
<dt>2010</dt>
<dd>On 8 June 2010,&nbsp;<a title="Dieudonn&eacute; M'bala M'bala" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dieudonn%C3%A9_M%27bala_M%27bala">Dieudonn&eacute; M'bala M'bala</a>&nbsp;was sentenced to a fine of &euro;10,000 for&nbsp;<a title="Defamation" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Defamation">defamation</a>&nbsp;towards the&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="International League against Racism and Anti-Semitism" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/International_League_against_Racism_and_Anti-Semitism">International League against Racism and Anti-Semitism</a>, which he had called "a&nbsp;<a title="Mafia" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mafia">mafia</a>-like association that organizes censorship".</dd>
<dt>2011, 15 January</dt>
<dd><a title="Congregation Dorshei Emet" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Congregation_Dorshei_Emet">Congregation Dorshei Emet</a>&nbsp;was one of six Jewish institutions in Montreal that were attacked by vandals on the night of 15 January 2011. The other buildings, all in&nbsp;<a title="C&ocirc;te Saint-Luc" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/C%C3%B4te_Saint-Luc">C&ocirc;te Saint-Luc</a>, consisted of four synagogues and a school.</dd>
<dt>2011</dt>
<dd>In 2011, the first man was charged with Holocaust denial in Budapest. The Court sentenced the man to 18 months in prison, suspended for three years, and probation. He also had to visit either Budapest's memorial museum, Auschwitz or Yad Vashem in Jerusalem. He chose his local Holocaust Memorial Center and had to make three visits in total and record his observations.</dd>
<dt>2011</dt>
<dd>In 2011,&nbsp;<a title="J. Z. Knight" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/J._Z._Knight">J. Z. Knight</a>&nbsp;stated, among other things, "Fuck God's chosen people! I think they have earned enough cash to have paid their way out of the goddamned gas chambers by now."</dd>
<dt>2011</dt>
<dd>The&nbsp;<a title="2011 Manhattan terrorism plot" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2011_Manhattan_terrorism_plot">2011 Manhattan terrorism plot</a>&nbsp;was a conspiracy by two&nbsp;<a title="Islam in the United States" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Islam_in_the_United_States">Muslim</a>&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Arab-Americans" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arab-Americans">Arab-Americans</a>&nbsp;to bomb various targets in the&nbsp;<a title="Manhattan" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Manhattan">Manhattan</a>&nbsp;borough of&nbsp;<a title="New York City" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/New_York_City">New York City</a>,&nbsp;<a title="New York (state)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/New_York_(state)">New York</a>, USA. They had planned to attack an unspecified synagogue and one of them expressed interest in blowing up a church and the&nbsp;<a title="Empire State Building" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Empire_State_Building">Empire State Building</a>. New York City law enforcement arrested the two suspects, 26-year-old Ahmed Ferhani and 20-year-old Mohamed Mamdouh, in a&nbsp;<a title="Sting operation" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sting_operation">sting operation</a>&nbsp;on 11 May 2011. Their plot was motivated primarily by "hatred of infidels and anti-semitism" according to the authorities.</dd>
<dt>2011</dt>
<dd>After the town of Wunsiedel became the scene of pilgrimages and&nbsp;<a title="Neo-Nazism" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Neo-Nazism">neo-Nazi</a>&nbsp;demonstrations every August on the date of&nbsp;<a title="Rudolf Hess" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Rudolf_Hess">Rudolf Hess</a>'s death, the parish council decided not to allow an extension on the grave site's lease when it expired in 2011.&nbsp;With the eventual consent of his family, Hess's grave was re-opened on 20 July 2011 and his remains were&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Exhumation" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Exhumation">exhumed</a>, and then cremated. His ashes were scattered at sea by family members; the gravestone, which bore the epitaph&nbsp;<em>"Ich hab's gewagt"</em>&nbsp;("I have dared"), was destroyed.</dd>
<dt>2012 March</dt>
<dd>Mohammed Merah, a 23-year-old Algerian Muslim&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="2012 Midi-Pyr&eacute;n&eacute;es shootings" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Midi-Pyr%C3%A9n%C3%A9es_shootings">kills four Jews</a>&nbsp;(including three children) outside a school in Toulouse, France.</dd>
<dt>2012</dt>
<dd>Jew Pond, a small body of water in&nbsp;<a title="Mont Vernon, New Hampshire" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mont_Vernon,_New_Hampshire">Mont Vernon, New Hampshire</a>, is officially renamed Carleton Pond.</dd>
<dt>2012</dt>
<dd>Section 335 of the Act C of 2012 on the Criminal Code of Hungary regulates the "use of symbols of totalitarianism", including the swastika, the insignia of the SS, the&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Arrow cross" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arrow_cross">arrow cross</a>, the&nbsp;<a title="Hammer and sickle" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hammer_and_sickle">hammer and sickle</a>, and the five-pointed&nbsp;<a title="Red star" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Red_star">red star</a>.</dd>
<dt>2012</dt>
<dd>In February 2012, a member of&nbsp;<a title="The Church of Jesus Christ of Latter-day Saints" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/The_Church_of_Jesus_Christ_of_Latter-day_Saints">The Church of Jesus Christ of Latter-day Saints</a>&nbsp;performed a&nbsp;<a title="Baptism for the dead" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Baptism_for_the_dead">posthumous baptism</a>&nbsp;for&nbsp;<a title="Simon Wiesenthal" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Simon_Wiesenthal">Simon Wiesenthal</a>'s parents without proper authorization.<span style="font-size: xx-small;">&nbsp;</span>&nbsp;After his own name was submitted for proxy baptism,&nbsp;<a title="Elie Wiesel" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Elie_Wiesel">Elie Wiesel</a>&nbsp;spoke out against the unauthorized practice of posthumously baptizing Jews and asked presidential candidate and Latter-day Saint&nbsp;<a title="Mitt Romney" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mitt_Romney">Mitt Romney</a>&nbsp;to denounce it. Romney's campaign declined to comment, directing such questions to church officials.</dd>
<dt>2012, 28 September</dt>
<dd><a title="Malm&ouml; Synagogue" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Malm%C3%B6_Synagogue">Malm&ouml; Synagogue</a>&nbsp;in&nbsp;<a title="Sweden" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sweden">Sweden</a>&nbsp;is attacked with an explosive device on 28 September 2012, shattering a window.</dd>
<dt>2013</dt>
<dd>In an interview with CNN, newly elected Iranian President&nbsp;<a title="Hassan Rouhani" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hassan_Rouhani">Hassan Rouhani</a>&nbsp;was quoted as condemning the Holocaust, stating, "I can tell you that any crime that happens in history against humanity, including the crime the Nazis created towards the Jews as well as non-Jews is reprehensible and condemnable.
