Whatever criminality they committed against the Jews, we condemn."&nbsp;Iranian media later accused CNN of fabricating Rouhani's comments.</dd>
<dt>2013</dt>
<dd><a title="Alice Walker" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Alice_Walker">Alice Walker</a>&nbsp;expressed appreciation for the works of the conspiracy theorist&nbsp;<a title="David Icke" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/David_Icke">David Icke</a>.&nbsp;On&nbsp;<a title="BBC Radio 4" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/BBC_Radio_4">BBC Radio 4</a>'s&nbsp;<em><a title="Desert Island Discs" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Desert_Island_Discs">Desert Island Discs</a></em>, she said that Icke's book&nbsp;<em>Human Race Get Off Your Knees</em>&nbsp;would be her choice if she could have only one book.&nbsp;The book promotes the theory that the Earth is ruled by&nbsp;<a title="Shapeshifting" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Shapeshifting">shapeshifting</a>&nbsp;<a title="Reptilian humanoid" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Reptilian_humanoid">reptilian humanoids</a>&nbsp;and "Rothschild Zionists."&nbsp;<a title="Jonathan Kay" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jonathan_Kay">Jonathan Kay</a>&nbsp;of the&nbsp;<em><a title="National Post" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/National_Post">National Post</a></em>&nbsp;described the book as "hateful, hallucinogenic nonsense." He wrote that Walker's public praise for Icke's book was "stunningly offensive" and that by taking it seriously, she was disqualifying herself "from the mainstream marketplace of ideas."</dd>
<dt>2013</dt>
<dd>In December, while performing onstage,&nbsp;<a title="Dieudonn&eacute; M'bala M'bala" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dieudonn%C3%A9_M%27bala_M%27bala">Dieudonn&eacute; M'bala M'bala</a>&nbsp;was recorded saying about prominent French Jewish radio journalist Patrick Cohen: "Me, you see, when I hear Patrick Cohen speak, I think to myself: &lsquo;Gas chambers... too bad.&rsquo;"</dd>
<dt>2013</dt>
<dd>On 31 December,&nbsp;<a title="Dieudonn&eacute; M'bala M'bala" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dieudonn%C3%A9_M%27bala_M%27bala">Dieudonn&eacute; M'bala M'bala</a>&nbsp;released a 15-minute video proposing that "2014 will be the year of the&nbsp;<a title="Quenelle (gesture)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Quenelle_(gesture)">quenelle</a>!".&nbsp;In it, Dieudonn&eacute; attacks "bankers" and "slavers", so as not to say "Jews"&nbsp;and end up in a lawsuit, and calls upon his followers, "quenelleurs"&mdash;those who listen and follow him&mdash;towards a hatred of Jews.</dd>
<dt>2013</dt>
<dd><a title="Louis Farrakhan" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Louis_Farrakhan">Louis Farrakhan</a>&nbsp;made antisemitic comments during his 16&ndash;17 May 2013 visit to Detroit&nbsp;and in his weekly sermons titled "The Time and What Must Be Done", begun during January 2013.</dd>
<dt>2013</dt>
<dd>In his official 2013&nbsp;<a title="Nowruz" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nowruz">Nowruz</a>&nbsp;address,&nbsp;<a title="Supreme Leader of Iran" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Supreme_Leader_of_Iran">Supreme Leader of Iran</a>&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Grand Ayatollah Ali Khamenei" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Grand_Ayatollah_Ali_Khamenei">Grand Ayatollah Ali Khamenei</a>&nbsp;questioned the veracity of the Holocaust, remarking that "The Holocaust is an event whose reality is uncertain and if it has happened, it's uncertain how it has happened." This was consistent with Khamenei's previous comments regarding the holocaust.</dd>
<dt>2014</dt>
<dd>On 6 January, France's interior minister&nbsp;<a title="Manuel Valls" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Manuel_Valls">Manuel Valls</a>&nbsp;said that performances considered anti-Semitic may be banned by local officials. Within hours, Bordeaux became the first French city to ban&nbsp;<a title="Dieudonn&eacute; M'bala M'bala" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dieudonn%C3%A9_M%27bala_M%27bala">Dieudonn&eacute; M'bala M'bala</a>&nbsp;when mayor&nbsp;<a title="Alain Jupp&eacute;" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Alain_Jupp%C3%A9">Alain Jupp&eacute;</a>&nbsp;canceled a local appearance planned as part of a scheduled national tour,&nbsp;followed closely by Nantes,&nbsp;Tours, Orleans, Toulouse, Limoges, and Biarritz. The show in Switzerland will go on as scheduled, while other cities are still studying the situation.&nbsp;The Paris Prefect of Police on 10 January prohibited Dieudonn&eacute; from staging his next three upcoming shows at his Paris theatre.&nbsp;In February, Dieudonn&eacute; was banned from entry in the United Kingdom.</dd>
<dt>2014 April 13</dt>
<dd>Antisemitic Ku Klux Klan leader&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Frazier Glenn Cross" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Frazier_Glenn_Cross">Frazier Glenn Cross</a>, also known as Frazier Glenn Miller,&nbsp;<a title="Overland Park Jewish Community Center shooting" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Overland_Park_Jewish_Community_Center_shooting">kills three non-Jewish people</a>&nbsp;at a Jewish community center and a Jewish retirement in home in&nbsp;<a title="Overland Park, Kansas" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Overland_Park,_Kansas">Overland Park, Kansas</a>, the day before the start of Passover.<sup id="cite_ref-179" class="reference"></sup></dd>
<dt>2014 May</dt>
<dd>Residents of a village in Spain called&nbsp;<em>Castrillo Matajud&iacute;os</em>&nbsp;("Jew-killer Camp") since 1627 vote to change the name of the village to the older name&nbsp;<em><a title="Castrillo Mota de Jud&iacute;os" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Castrillo_Mota_de_Jud%C3%ADos">Castrillo Mota de Jud&iacute;os</a></em>&nbsp;("Hill of Jews Camp").&nbsp;The name is changed in June 2015.<sup id="cite_ref-graunjun15_182-0" class="reference"></sup></dd>
<dt>2015</dt>
<dd>The Mayors United Against Antisemitism initiative was developed by the&nbsp;<a title="American Jewish Committee" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/American_Jewish_Committee">American Jewish Committee</a>&nbsp;in July 2015 and launched in Europe later in 2015.<sup id="cite_ref-183" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_antisemitism_in_the_21st_century#cite_note-183">[183]</a></sup></dd>
<dt>2015</dt>
<dd>The&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Porte de Vincennes siege" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Porte_de_Vincennes_siege">Porte de Vincennes siege</a>&nbsp;occurred at a&nbsp;<a title="Hypercacher" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hypercacher">Hypercacher</a>&nbsp;<a title="Kosher foods" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kosher_foods">kosher</a>&nbsp;<a title="Superette" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Superette">superette</a>&nbsp;in&nbsp;<a title="Porte de Vincennes" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Porte_de_Vincennes">Porte de Vincennes</a>&nbsp;(<a title="20th arrondissement of Paris" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/20th_arrondissement_of_Paris">20th arrondissement of Paris</a>) in the wake of the&nbsp;<a title="Charlie Hebdo shooting" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Charlie_Hebdo_shooting"><em>Charlie Hebdo</em>&nbsp;shooting</a>&nbsp;two days earlier, and concurrently with the Dammartin-en-Go&euml;le hostage crisis in which the two&nbsp;<em>Charlie Hebdo</em>&nbsp;gunmen were cornered.</dd>
<dd><a title="Amedy Coulibaly" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Amedy_Coulibaly">Amedy Coulibaly</a>&nbsp;had pledged allegiance to the&nbsp;<a title="Islamic State of Iraq and the Levant" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Islamic_State_of_Iraq_and_the_Levant">Islamic State of Iraq and the Levant</a>, and was a close friend of&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Sa&iuml;d Kouachi" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sa%C3%AFd_Kouachi">Sa&iuml;d Kouachi</a>&nbsp;and&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Ch&eacute;rif Kouachi" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ch%C3%A9rif_Kouachi">Ch&eacute;rif Kouachi</a>&nbsp;(whom he had met in jail in 2005), the gunmen in the&nbsp;<em>Charlie Hebdo</em>&nbsp;attack. Armed with a&nbsp;<a title="Submachine gun" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Submachine_gun">submachine gun</a>, an&nbsp;<a title="Assault rifle" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Assault_rifle">assault rifle</a>, and two&nbsp;<a title="TT pistol" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TT_pistol">Tokarev pistols</a>, he entered and attacked the people in the&nbsp;<a title="Kosher foods" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kosher_foods">kosher food</a>&nbsp;superette. He had a female accomplice, speculated to be his wife,&nbsp;<a title="Hayat Boumeddiene" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hayat_Boumeddiene">Hayat Boumeddiene</a>.&nbsp;Coulibaly murdered four Jewish hostages, and held fifteen other hostages during a siege in which he demanded that the Kouachi brothers not be harmed. The police ended the siege by storming the store and killing Coulibaly.</dd>
<dt>2015</dt>
<dd>On 10 January 2015, following the&nbsp;<a title="Charlie Hebdo shooting" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Charlie_Hebdo_shooting"><em>Charlie Hebdo</em>&nbsp;shooting</a>, the&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Porte de Vincennes siege" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Porte_de_Vincennes_siege">Porte de Vincennes siege</a>&nbsp;of a kosher supermarket, and the 1,500,000-strong "<a title="Republican marches" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Republican_marches">march against hatred</a>" in Paris,&nbsp;<a title="Dieudonn&eacute; M'bala M'bala" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dieudonn%C3%A9_M%27bala_M%27bala">Dieudonn&eacute; M'bala M'bala</a>&nbsp;wrote on Facebook "As far as I am concerned, I feel I am Charlie Coulibaly."&nbsp;In this way he mixed the popular slogan "<a title="Je suis Charlie" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Je_suis_Charlie">Je suis Charlie</a>", used to support the journalists killed at the&nbsp;<em><a title="Charlie Hebdo" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Charlie_Hebdo">Charlie Hebdo</a></em>&nbsp;magazine, with a reference to&nbsp;<a title="Amedy Coulibaly" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Amedy_Coulibaly">Amedy Coulibaly</a>&nbsp;who was responsible for the hostage-taking at the kosher supermarket which included the killing of four Jews.&nbsp;On 13 January, Dieudonn&eacute; was arrested in Paris, accused of publicly supporting terrorism,&nbsp;based on his earlier Facebook comments where he appeared to support the kosher supermarket gunman Amedy Coulibaly.&nbsp;Dieudonn&eacute;'s arrest over his "Je suis Charlie Coulibaly" comments sparked discussion over a perceived hypocrisy concerning freedom of speech, contrasting his bans and arrest, with the freedom for&nbsp;<em>Charlie Hebdo</em>&nbsp;to publish controversial cartoons of&nbsp;<a title="Muhammad" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Muhammad">Muhammad</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-190" class="reference"></sup></dd>
<dt>2015 February 3</dt>
<dd><a title="2015 Nice stabbing" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2015_Nice_stabbing">2015 Nice stabbing</a>&nbsp;three&nbsp;<a title="French Army" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/French_Army">soldiers</a>, guarding a&nbsp;<a title="History of the Jews in France" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/History_of_the_Jews_in_France">Jewish</a>&nbsp;community center in&nbsp;<a title="Nice" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nice">Nice</a>, France, were attacked with a knife by Moussa Coulibaly, a&nbsp;<a title="Lone wolf (terrorism)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lone_wolf_(terrorism)">lone-wolf terrorist</a>.</dd>
<dt>2015</dt>
<dd>In 2015, the House of Cartoon and the Sarcheshmeh Cultural Complex in Iran organized the&nbsp;<a title="International Holocaust Cartoon Competition" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/International_Holocaust_Cartoon_Competition">International Holocaust Cartoon Competition</a>, a competition in which artists were encouraged to submit&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Cartoons" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cartoons">cartoons</a>&nbsp;on the theme of Holocaust denial.&nbsp;<em><a title="Hamshahri" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hamshahri">Hamshahri</a></em>, a popular Iranian newspaper, held a&nbsp;<a title="International Holocaust Cartoon Competition" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/International_Holocaust_Cartoon_Competition">similar contest</a>&nbsp;in 2006.</dd>
<dt>2015</dt>
<dd>Within hours of his being announced as&nbsp;<a title="Jon Stewart" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jon_Stewart">Jon Stewart</a>'s successor, attention was drawn on the Internet to several jokes that&nbsp;<a title="Trevor Noah" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Trevor_Noah">Trevor Noah</a>&nbsp;had made through his&nbsp;<a title="Twitter" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Twitter">Twitter</a>&nbsp;account, which were criticized as being offensive to women and&nbsp;<a title="Jews" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jews">Jews</a>,&nbsp;and to be making fun of the Holocaust.&nbsp;Noah responded by tweeting, "To reduce my views to a handful of jokes that didn't land is not a true reflection of my character, nor my evolution as a comedian."&nbsp;<a title="Comedy Central" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Comedy_Central">Comedy Central</a>&nbsp;stood behind Noah, saying in a statement, "Like many comedians, Trevor Noah pushes boundaries; he is provocative and spares no one, himself included... To judge him or his comedy based on a handful of jokes is unfair. Trevor is a talented comedian with a bright future at Comedy Central."&nbsp;Mary Kluk, chairperson of the South African Jewish Board of Deputies (SAJBD), said that the jokes were not signs of anti-Jewish prejudice and that they were part of Noah's style of comedy.</dd>
<dt>2015</dt>
<dd>In March 2015,&nbsp;<a title="Louis Farrakhan" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Louis_Farrakhan">Louis Farrakhan</a>&nbsp;accused Jews of involvement in the&nbsp;<a title="September 11 attacks" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/September_11_attacks">September 11 attacks</a>.</dd>
<dt>2015</dt>
<dd>In June 2015&nbsp;<a title="Laurent Louis" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Laurent_Louis">Laurent Louis</a>&nbsp;got a suspended 6-month sentence for breaking the&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Laws against Holocaust denial" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Laws_against_Holocaust_denial#Belgium">1995 Belgian law against Holocaust denial</a>&nbsp;and lost his right to run for office in the next six years. He filed an appeal.&nbsp;Louis was ordered by the&nbsp;<a title="Court of appeal (Belgium)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Court_of_appeal_(Belgium)">Belgian court of appeal</a>&nbsp;in 2017, in lieu of a sentence and fine, to visit one Nazi concentration camp a year for the next five years.<sup id="cite_ref-wpost_202-0" class="reference"></sup></dd>
<dt>January 2015</dt>
<dd>In January 2015, the Hungarian court ordered far-right on-line newspaper&nbsp;<em>Kuruc.info</em>&nbsp;to delete its article denying the Holocaust published in July 2013, which was the first ruling in Hungary of its kind.&nbsp;The Association for Civil Liberties (TASZ) offered free legal aid to the website as a protest against restrictions on freedom of speech,&nbsp;but the site refused citing the liberal views of the association, and also refused to delete the article.</dd>
<dt>January 2015</dt>
<dd>Spray-painted swastikas were drawn on the outside wall of a Jewish fraternity at U.C. Davis, on the 70th anniversary of the liberation of Auschwitz from the Nazis.</dd>
<dt>January 2015</dt>
<dd><a title="La Mort aux Juifs" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/La_Mort_aux_Juifs">La Mort aux Juifs</a>&nbsp;was a&nbsp;<a title="Hamlet (place)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hamlet_(place)">hamlet</a>&nbsp;under the jurisdiction of the French&nbsp;<a title="Communes of France" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Communes_of_France">commune</a>&nbsp;of&nbsp;<a title="Courtemaux" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Courtemaux">Courtemaux</a>&nbsp;in the&nbsp;<a title="Loiret" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Loiret">Loiret</a>&nbsp;<a title="Departments of France" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Departments_of_France">department</a>&nbsp;in north-central France. Its name has been translated as "Death to Jews"&nbsp;or "The death of the Jews".&nbsp;Under pressure from the national authorities, the municipal council retired the name in January 2015.&nbsp;A similar request about the name had been denied in 1992.&nbsp;The area is now split between the nearby hamlets of&nbsp;<em>Les Croisilles</em>&nbsp;and&nbsp;<em>La Dogetterie</em>.</dd>
<dt>2015 January 10</dt>
<dd>French terrorist&nbsp;<a title="Amedy Coulibaly" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Amedy_Coulibaly">Amedy Coulibaly</a>&nbsp;takes hostages in a kosher supermarket in&nbsp;<a title="Paris" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Paris">Paris</a>&nbsp;in the course of the&nbsp;<a title="Charlie Hebdo shooting" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Charlie_Hebdo_shooting">Charlie Hebdo shooting</a>.&nbsp;He claims in the media that he wanted to kill Jews.</dd>
<dt>2015 February 14&ndash;15</dt>
<dd><a title="2015 Copenhagen shootings" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2015_Copenhagen_shootings">2015 Copenhagen shootings</a></dd>
<dt>2015 February 16</dt>
<dd>Israel's PM&nbsp;<a title="Benjamin Netanyahu" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Benjamin_Netanyahu">Benjamin Netanyahu</a>&nbsp;causes outrage by calling for a massive immigration of Jewish people from Europe to Israel saying "we say to the Jews, to our brothers and sisters, Israel is your home and that of every Jew."&nbsp;French PM&nbsp;<a title="Manuel Valls" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Manuel_Valls">Manuel Valls</a>&nbsp;replied by saying "the place for French Jews is France."</dd>
<dt>2015 March</dt>
<dd>Stanford University student senate candidate Molly Horwitz was asked by a student group how her Jewish faith would affect her decision-making.</dd>
<dt>2015 August</dt>
<dd>Two Jewish synagogues and a Jewish neighborhood on the North Side of San Antonio, Texas, are vandalized with anti-Semitic graffiti.</dd>
<dt>2015 October</dt>
<dd>The Catholic Church in Poland publishes a letter referring to antisemitism as a sin against the commandment to love one's neighbor. The letter also acknowledged the heroism of those Poles who risked their lives to shelter Jews as Nazi Germany carried out the Holocaust in occupied Poland. The bishops who signed the letter cited the Polish Pope&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="John Paul II" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/John_Paul_II">John Paul II</a>&nbsp;who was opposed to antisemitism, and believed in founding Catholic-Jewish relations.</dd>
<dt>2015 October</dt>
<dd>Facebook has been accused of being a public platform used to incite terrorism. In October 2015, 20,000 Israelis claimed that Facebook was ignoring Palestinian incitement on its platform and filed a&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Class-action" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Class-action">class-action</a>&nbsp;suit demanding that Facebook remove all posts "containing incitement to murder Jews".</dd>
<dt>2015 December</dt>
<dd>The&nbsp;<a title="Holy See" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Holy_See">Vatican</a>&nbsp;releases a 10,000-word document that, among other things, states that Jews do not need to be converted to find salvation, and that&nbsp;<a title="Catholic Church" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Catholic_Church">Catholics</a>&nbsp;should work with Jews to fight antisemitism.<sup id="cite_ref-221" class="reference"></sup></dd>
<dt>2015 December</dt>
<dd>The&nbsp;<a title="United Nations" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_Nations">United Nations</a>&nbsp;officially recognizes&nbsp;<a title="Yom Kippur" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Yom_Kippur">Yom Kippur</a>, stating that from then on no official meetings will take place on the day.&nbsp;As well, the United Nations states that, beginning in 2016, they will have nine official holidays and seven floating holidays which each employee will be able to choose one of.&nbsp;It stated that the floating holidays will be Yom Kippur, Day of&nbsp;<a title="Vesak" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vesak">Vesak</a>,&nbsp;<a title="Diwali" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Diwali">Diwali</a>,&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Gurpurab" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gurpurab">Gurpurab</a>,&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Orthodox Christmas" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Orthodox_Christmas">Orthodox Christmas</a>, Orthodox&nbsp;<a title="Good Friday" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Good_Friday">Good Friday</a>, and&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Presidents' Day" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Presidents%27_Day">Presidents' Day</a>.&nbsp;This is the first time the United Nations officially recognizes any Jewish holiday.</dd>
<dt>2016</dt>
<dd>Natasha Waldorf of Alameda, who was Jewish, was subjected to two boys sending her text messages that included the word "kike" and other anti-Semitic insults, and the picture of product mascot Mr. Clean in a Nazi uniform called "Mr. Ethnic Cleansing." Two other students joked about the Holocaust and, when she confronted them, told her that "Hitler should have finished the job."</dd>
<dt>2016</dt>
<dd>Amidst an ongoing controversy in the Labour Party about antisemitism,&nbsp;<a title="Naz Shah" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Naz_Shah">Naz Shah</a>&nbsp;was discovered by&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Blogging" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Blogging">blogger</a>&nbsp;<a title="Paul Staines" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Paul_Staines">Paul Staines</a>&nbsp;in April 2016 to have reposted a&nbsp;<a title="Facebook" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Facebook">Facebook</a>&nbsp;meme in August 2014 supporting the relocation of Israel to the USA.&nbsp;Shah also commented on the post, suggesting the plan might "save them some pocket money".&nbsp;In July 2014, she wrote on Facebook about a newspaper poll concerning alleged Israeli war crimes in the&nbsp;<a title="2014 Israel&ndash;Gaza conflict" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2014_Israel%E2%80%93Gaza_conflict">Gaza conflict</a>&nbsp;that "The Jews are rallying to the poll" and in September appeared to compare Israeli policies to those of&nbsp;<a title="Adolf Hitler" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Adolf_Hitler">Adolf Hitler</a>. Shah asserted that her views on Israel had moderated in the 20 months since the post and on 26 April 2016 she resigned from her unpaid post as John McDonnell's PPS&nbsp;while still holding her seat on the&nbsp;<a title="Home Affairs Select Committee" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Home_Affairs_Select_Committee">Home Affairs Select Committee</a>&nbsp;investigating the rise of antisemitism in the UK. She was suspended by the Labour Party on 27 April 2016,&nbsp;forfeiting all roles.</dd>
<dt>2016</dt>
<dd>In April 2016,&nbsp;<a title="Ken Livingstone" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ken_Livingstone">Ken Livingstone</a>&nbsp;commented publicly on the suspension of Labour MP&nbsp;<a title="Naz Shah" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Naz_Shah">Naz Shah</a>; she had been removed from the party after it was revealed that she had made comments on Facebook suggesting that Israeli Jews should be relocated to the United States.&nbsp;Livingstone stated that Shah's postings, which were made before she became an MP at the&nbsp;<a title="2015 United Kingdom general election" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2015_United_Kingdom_general_election">2015 general election</a>, were "completely over the top" and "rude",&nbsp;although he did not deem them antisemitic.&nbsp;He asserted that there is a "well-orchestrated campaign by the Israel lobby to smear anybody who criticises Israeli policy as antisemitic",&nbsp;and also stated that&nbsp;<a title="Adolf Hitler" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Adolf_Hitler">Adolf Hitler</a>&nbsp;"was supporting Zionism before he went mad and ended up killing six million Jews".</dd>
</dl>
<p>He defended his claims by reference to&nbsp;<a title="Lenni Brenner" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lenni_Brenner">Lenni Brenner</a>'s&nbsp;<em><a title="Zionism in the Age of the Dictators" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Zionism_in_the_Age_of_the_Dictators">Zionism in the Age of the Dictators</a></em>,&nbsp;and many commentators suggested that Livingstone was referring to the&nbsp;<a title="Haavara Agreement" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Haavara_Agreement">Haavara Agreement</a>&nbsp;between&nbsp;<a title="Nazi Germany" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nazi_Germany">Nazi Germany</a>&nbsp;and the&nbsp;<a title="Zionist Federation of Germany" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Zionist_Federation_of_Germany">Zionist Federation of Germany</a>.&nbsp;Livingstone's statements were criticised by historians,&nbsp;among them&nbsp;<a title="Roger Moorhouse" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Roger_Moorhouse">Roger Moorhouse</a>, who said that they were historically inaccurate.&nbsp;He also became involved in a public argument on the subject with the Labour MP&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="John Mann (British politician)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/John_Mann_(British_politician)">John Mann</a>.</p>
<p>Livingstone was subsequently suspended from Labour Party membership "for bringing the party into disrepute".&nbsp;Over 20 Labour MPs called for Livingstone's suspension, while&nbsp;<a title="Jon Lansman" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jon_Lansman">Jon Lansman</a>, founder of the pro-Corbyn&nbsp;<a title="Momentum (organisation)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Momentum_(organisation)">Momentum</a>&nbsp;group, called for Livingstone to leave politics altogether,&nbsp;and Khan called for his expulsion from the party.&nbsp;In a subsequent interview, Livingstone expressed regret both for mentioning Hitler and for offending Jews but added that "I'm not going to apologise for telling the truth."&nbsp;Corbyn announced that the decision to expel Livingstone would be made by a&nbsp;<a title="National Executive Committee of the Labour Party" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/National_Executive_Committee_of_the_Labour_Party">National Executive Committee</a>&nbsp;internal inquiry, whilst Livingstone insisted that he would be exonerated on the basis of Brenner's book, saying "how can the truth be an offence?"&nbsp;Following this controversy, Livingstone has questioned whether or not he has Jewish ancestry on his mother's side stating that&nbsp;<a title="Greville Janner" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Greville_Janner">Greville Janner</a>&nbsp;used to speculate whether or not he was Jewish because "my grandmother's name was Zona."</p>
<p>Livingstone was sacked in Spring 2016 by&nbsp;<a title="LBC" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/LBC">LBC</a>. He was quoted by&nbsp;<em>The Daily Telegraph</em>&nbsp;as saying this was because of his comments about Hitler.</p>
<dl>
<dt>2016</dt>
<dd>The U.C. Board of Regents approved a set of Principles Against Intolerance, which condemns "anti-Semitism" and which, in an opening contextual statement, includes "anti-Semitic forms of anti-Zionism" as something that has "no place at the University of California." The principles, passed unanimously at a 23 March board meeting in San Francisco, apply to students and faculty at all 10 U.C. campuses, though the document includes no enforcement mechanism or consequences for violations.</dd>
<dt>2016</dt>
<dd>An ethics rule of the&nbsp;<a title="American Bar Association" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/American_Bar_Association">American Bar Association</a>&nbsp;now forbids comments or actions that single out someone on the basis of religion, as well as other factors.</dd>
<dt>2016</dt>
<dd><a title="Richard B. Spencer" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Richard_B._Spencer">Richard B. Spencer</a>&nbsp;and his organization drew considerable media attention in the weeks following the 2016 presidential election, where, in response to his cry "Hail&nbsp;<a title="Donald Trump" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Donald_Trump">Trump</a>, hail our people, hail victory!", a number of his supporters gave the&nbsp;<a title="Nazi salute" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nazi_salute">Nazi salute</a>&nbsp;similar to the&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Sieg heil" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sieg_heil">Sieg Heil</a>&nbsp;chant used at the Nazis' mass rallies. Spencer has defended their conduct, stating that the Nazi salute was given in a spirit of "irony and exuberance".</dd>
<dt>2016</dt>
<dd>The campus chapter of Students for Justice in Palestine at the&nbsp;<a title="University of California, Irvine" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/University_of_California,_Irvine">University of California, Irvine</a>&nbsp;was sanctioned because they disrupted a program hosted by a Jewish campus group in May and intimidated Jewish students.</dd>
<dt>2016</dt>
<dd><a title="Ted Nugent" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ted_Nugent">Ted Nugent</a>&nbsp;posted an image on his Facebook page implying that Jews were responsible for gun control.&nbsp;Nugent's antisemitic rant sparked outrage and gun owners called for his NRA resignation.</dd>
<dt>2016</dt>
<dd>The nations that make up the Organization for Security and Cooperation in Europe began a three-year initiative to promote awareness and learning about anti-Semitism and to help the security of Jewish communities.</dd>
<dt>2016</dt>
<dd>On 13 November 2016,&nbsp;<a title="Steve Bannon" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Steve_Bannon">Steve Bannon</a>, formerly the executive chair of&nbsp;<a title="Breitbart News" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Breitbart_News">Breitbart News</a>, was appointed chief strategist and senior counselor to President-elect&nbsp;<a title="Donald Trump" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Donald_Trump">Donald Trump</a>.&nbsp;This appointment drew opposition from the&nbsp;<a title="Anti-Defamation League" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Anti-Defamation_League">Anti-Defamation League</a>, the&nbsp;<a title="Council on American&ndash;Islamic Relations" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Council_on_American%E2%80%93Islamic_Relations">Council on American&ndash;Islamic Relations</a>, the&nbsp;<a title="Southern Poverty Law Center" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Southern_Poverty_Law_Center">Southern Poverty Law Center</a>, Democrat&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Senate Minority Leader" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Senate_Minority_Leader">Senate Minority Leader</a>&nbsp;<a title="Harry Reid" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Harry_Reid">Harry Reid</a>, and some Republican strategists, because of statements in Breitbart News that were alleged to be racist or anti-Semitic.<sup id="cite_ref-auto1_260-0" class="reference"></sup></dd>
</dl>
<p><a title="Ben Shapiro" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ben_Shapiro">Ben Shapiro</a>,&nbsp;<a title="Bernard Marcus" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bernard_Marcus">Bernard Marcus</a>&nbsp;of the Republican Jewish Coalition,&nbsp;<a title="Morton Klein" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Morton_Klein">Morton Klein</a>&nbsp;and the&nbsp;<a title="Zionist Organization of America" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Zionist_Organization_of_America">Zionist Organization of America</a>,&nbsp;<a title="Pamela Geller" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pamela_Geller">Pamela Geller</a>,&nbsp;<a title="Shmuley Boteach" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Shmuley_Boteach">Shmuley Boteach</a>, and&nbsp;<a title="David Horowitz" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/David_Horowitz">David Horowitz</a>&nbsp;defended Bannon against the allegations of antisemitism.&nbsp;<a title="Alan Dershowitz" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Alan_Dershowitz">Alan Dershowitz</a>&nbsp;first defended Bannon and said there was no evidence he was anti-semitic,&nbsp;but in a later piece stated that Bannon and Breitbart had made bigoted statements against Muslims, women, and others. The ADL said "we are not aware of any anti-Semitic statements from Bannon", while adding "under his stewardship, Breitbart has emerged as the leading source for the extreme views of a vocal minority who peddle bigotry and promote hate."&nbsp;Shapiro, who previously worked for Breitbart, said that he has no evidence of Bannon being racist or an anti-Semite, but that he was "happy to pander to those people and make common cause with them in order to transform conservatism into European far-right nationalist populism",&nbsp;an assertion supported by other sources and his alluding to&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="National Front (France)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/National_Front_(France)">Front National</a>&nbsp;politician&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Marion Mar&eacute;chal-Le Pen" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marion_Mar%C3%A9chal-Le_Pen">Marion Mar&eacute;chal-Le Pen</a>&nbsp;as "the new rising star".</p>
<dl>
<dt>2016</dt>
<dd>In December 2016, the neo-Nazi and white supremacist website&nbsp;<em><a title="The Daily Stormer" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/The_Daily_Stormer">The Daily Stormer</a></em>&nbsp;published a list of six local Jews in&nbsp;<a title="Whitefish, Montana" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Whitefish,_Montana">Whitefish, Montana</a>&nbsp;along with their personal information, claiming that they were harming the business of&nbsp;<a title="Richard B. Spencer" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Richard_B._Spencer">Richard Spencer</a>'s mother and asking readers to "take action" against them.&nbsp;Whitefish police increased local patrols, and monitored Internet activity; Montana politicians and community groups responded with various efforts to focus attention on the question of antisemitism. On 28 Dec. 2016, Spencer indicated that he did not want to bring ongoing national attention to Whitefish with his political views, and an offer was made to call off a proposed armed march against Jews, Jewish businesses and people who support either in the town.&nbsp;The march was postponed because the proper permitting materials were not submitted and the required fee was not paid.</dd>
<dt>2017</dt>
<dd>The&nbsp;<a title="Court of appeal (Belgium)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Court_of_appeal_(Belgium)">court of appeal</a>&nbsp;of Li&egrave;ge confirmed a first instance sentence of two months of jail time and a 9.000 euros fine for&nbsp;<a title="Dieudonn&eacute; M'bala M'bala" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dieudonn%C3%A9_M%27bala_M%27bala">Dieudonn&eacute; M'bala M'bala</a>'s anti-Semitic remarks in a performance on&nbsp;<a title="Herstal" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Herstal">Herstal</a>&nbsp;on 14 March 2012.</dd>
<dt>2017</dt>
<dd>In 2017,&nbsp;<a title="Alice Walker" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Alice_Walker">Alice Walker</a>&nbsp;published a poem on her blog entitled "It Is Our (Frightful) Duty to Study the Talmud", recommending that the reader should start with&nbsp;<a title="YouTube" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/YouTube">YouTube</a>&nbsp;to learn about the evils of the&nbsp;<a title="Talmud" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Talmud">Talmud</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-284" class="reference"></sup></dd>
<dt>2017</dt>
<dd>With the beginning of the year,&nbsp;<a title="2017 Jewish Community Center bomb threats" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2017_Jewish_Community_Center_bomb_threats">a wave of threats</a>, including&nbsp;<a title="Bomb threat" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bomb_threat">bomb threats</a>, were made against&nbsp;<a title="Jewish Community Center" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jewish_Community_Center">Jewish Community Centers</a>&nbsp;and other Jewish institutions in the United States.&nbsp;<a title="Juan M. Thompson" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Juan_M._Thompson">Juan M. Thompson</a>, an African American former journalist for&nbsp;<em><a title="The Intercept" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/The_Intercept">The Intercept</a></em>, was arrested and charged with making at least eight of the hoax threats, as well as a threat made against the&nbsp;<a title="Anti-Defamation League" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Anti-Defamation_League">Anti-Defamation League</a>, while allegedly impersonating a former girlfriend.&nbsp;Another suspect, an unidentified 19-year-old&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Israeli-American" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israeli-American">Israeli-American</a>&nbsp;man, was arrested in&nbsp;<a title="Ashkelon" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ashkelon">Ashkelon</a>,&nbsp;<a title="Israel" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel">Israel</a>&nbsp;and charged with responsibility for "dozens" of the threats.</dd>
<dt>2017</dt>
<dd>Brutal&nbsp;<a title="Murder of Sarah Halimi" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Murder_of_Sarah_Halimi">Murder of Sarah Halimi</a>&nbsp;in Paris 4 April 2017. The murderer is a Muslim migrant from Mali, commenced a typical hate crime, crying "Allahu Abkar", mentioning his victim's ethnicity and religion but pretended to be mad and still hidden in psychology hospital instead of prison.</dd>
<dt>2017</dt>
<dd><a title="Sebastian Gorka" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sebastian_Gorka">Sebastian Gorka</a>&nbsp;appeared on&nbsp;<a title="Fox News" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fox_News">Fox News</a>&nbsp;on the evening of the U.S. presidential inauguration wearing a badge, tunic, and ring associated with Order of Vit&eacute;z.&nbsp;According to some sources, Gorka was a member of the&nbsp;<a title="Order of Vit&eacute;z" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Order_of_Vit%C3%A9z">Order of Vit&eacute;z</a>&nbsp;by inheritance, a group the&nbsp;<a title="United States Department of State" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States_Department_of_State">US State Department</a>&nbsp;lists as a&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Nazi" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nazi">Nazi</a>-linked group.&nbsp;This has given rise to claims that Gorka himself carries sympathy for the Nazis.&nbsp;His father, Paul Gorka, was never a member of this Order and received a "Vit&eacute;z" (literally: "Valiant") medal from Hungarian exiles "for his resistance to dictatorship" in 1979.&nbsp;Gorka himself stated that he wears this medal in remembrance of his father, who was awarded the decoration for his efforts to create an anti-Communist, pro-democracy organization at the university he attended in Hungary.&nbsp;Robert Kerepeszki, Hungarian expert of the Order of Vit&eacute;z, has confirmed that there were ruptures in the organization of the Order of Vit&eacute;z on the question of Nazism during the war, many of them died fighting against&nbsp;<a title="Arrow Cross Party" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arrow_Cross_Party">Hungarian Nazis</a>, and Gorka's medal had nothing to do with the war period, but was awarded "for his resistance to dictatorship."<sup id="cite_ref-Horthy_298-0" class="reference"></sup></dd>
<dt>2017</dt>
<dd>Leaders of one of two successor organisations of the&nbsp;<a title="Order of Vit&eacute;z" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Order_of_Vit%C3%A9z">Vit&eacute;zi Rend</a>&nbsp;stated that&nbsp;<a title="Sebastian Gorka" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sebastian_Gorka">Sebastian Gorka</a>&nbsp;was an official member of the Historical Vit&eacute;zi Rend faction, to which he is said to have taken a lifelong oath of loyalty. Gorka denied the allegations.&nbsp;The&nbsp;<a title="Anne Frank Center for Mutual Respect" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Anne_Frank_Center_for_Mutual_Respect">Anne Frank Center for Mutual Respect</a>, the&nbsp;<a title="National Jewish Democratic Council" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/National_Jewish_Democratic_Council">National Jewish Democratic Council</a>, and the&nbsp;<a title="Interfaith Alliance" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Interfaith_Alliance">Interfaith Alliance</a>&nbsp;have called for Gorka's resignation over his ties to Hungarian far-right groups. The&nbsp;<a title="Anti-Defamation League" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Anti-Defamation_League">Anti-Defamation League</a>&nbsp;has asked Gorka to disavow the Hungarian far-right groups that he has been associated with.&nbsp;Democratic Senators Ben Cardin, Dick Durbin and Richard Blumenthal sent a letter to the Department of Justice and the Department of Homeland Security requesting that the DHS look into whether Gorka "illegally procured his citizenship" by omitting membership in Historical Vit&eacute;zi Rend, which could have been grounds for keeping him out of the country.<sup id="cite_ref-304" class="reference"></sup></dd>
<dt>2017</dt>
<dd><a class="mw-redirect" title="Chicago Dyke March" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Chicago_Dyke_March">Chicago Dyke March</a>&nbsp;organizers singled out and approached a group of women carrying Jewish pride flags and began questioning them on their political stance in regards to Zionism and Israel, and then after a discussion asked them to leave the event, insisting that their presence "made people feel unsafe".&nbsp;The organizers attributed the responses of the women and the white star of David, featured at the center of the rainbow flag as a "zionist expression". This prompted widespread accusations of antisemitism.</dd>
<dt>2017</dt>
<dd>In the early morning hours of 28 June 2017, one of the 9 feet (2.7&nbsp;m) glass panels on the&nbsp;<a title="New England Holocaust Memorial" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/New_England_Holocaust_Memorial">New England Holocaust Memorial</a>&nbsp;was smashed with a rock.<sup id="cite_ref-308" class="reference"></sup></dd>
<dt>2017</dt>
<dd>In&nbsp;<a title="Ukraine" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ukraine">Ukraine</a>, some men vandalized the Space of Synagogues [Holocaust] memorial display; they wrote neo-Nazi slogans and the English words "white power", and drew a swastika and ultranationalist Ukrainian symbols.</dd>
<dt>2017</dt>
<dd><a title="Viktor Orb&aacute;n" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Viktor_Orb%C3%A1n">Viktor Orb&aacute;n</a>, Prime Minister of Hungary, made a speech in which he called&nbsp;<a title="Mikl&oacute;s Horthy" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mikl%C3%B3s_Horthy">Mikl&oacute;s Horthy</a>&nbsp;an "exceptional statesman" and gave him the credit for the survival of Hungary. The&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="U.S. Holocaust Museum" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/U.S._Holocaust_Museum">U.S. Holocaust Museum</a>&nbsp;then issued a statement denouncing Orb&aacute;n and the Hungarian government for trying to "rehabilitate the reputation of Hungary's wartime leader, Miklos Horthy, who was a vocal anti-Semite and complicit in the murder of the country's Jewish population during the Holocaust."</dd>
<dt>2017</dt>
<dd>The BBC removed a line from one of its online articles which had offended Jews and Muslims; the line had stated, "The Holocaust is a sensitive topic for many Muslims because Jewish survivors settled in British-mandate Palestine, on land which later became the state of Israel."</dd>
<dt>2017</dt>
<dd>Antisemitic fliers were circulated around Lakewood, New Jersey.</dd>
<dt>2017</dt>
<dd>An antisemitic banner was found in front of a Holocaust memorial at a synagogue in Lakewood, New Jersey.</dd>
<dt>2017</dt>
<dd>Fliers were found around Little Italy saying among other things, "We are killing off the entire white race by making them addicted to cocaine, crack, meth, spiked marijuana, ecstasy, spice, heroine, hash and other poisons, Adolph Hilter's [sic] Nazi's [sic] killed off six million ugly Jews by telling them to go into showers to get cleaned up for their new lives, then they locked the shower doors and poisoned them all to death with a deadly gas, and finally they grabbed all of the dead Jew's properties."</dd>
<dt>2017</dt>
<dd>The chairpersons of Chicago&nbsp;<a title="SlutWalk" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/SlutWalk">SlutWalk</a>&nbsp;wrote, "We still stand behind Dyke March Chicago's decision to remove the Zionist contingent from their event, &amp; we won't allow Zionist displays at ours", referring to a then-upcoming demonstration of theirs. The Chicago SlutWalk's organizers made the following declaration about the&nbsp;<a title="Star of David" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Star_of_David">Star of David</a>, "its connections to the oppression enacted by Israel is too strong for it to be neutral &amp; IN CONTEXT [at the Dyke March Chicago event] it was used as a Zionist symbol."</dd>
<dt>2017</dt>
<dd>A resolution was passed by the San Francisco Board of Supervisors against "verbal and violent anti-Semitic assaults, both nationally and in the Bay Area"; the resolution also contained a promise to "stand in solidarity with Jewish and other communities whenever they are targeted or marginalized."</dd>
<dt>2017</dt>
<dd>A Jewish cemetery in&nbsp;<a title="St. Louis" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/St._Louis">St. Louis</a>,&nbsp;<a title="Missouri" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Missouri">Missouri</a>&nbsp;was vandalized in an apparent anti-Semitic incident in February 2017,&nbsp;after which&nbsp;<a title="Linda Sarsour" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Linda_Sarsour">Linda Sarsour</a>&nbsp;worked with other Muslim activists to launch a&nbsp;<a title="Crowdfunding" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Crowdfunding">crowdfunding</a>&nbsp;campaign to raise money to repair the damage and restore the gravesites. More than $125,000 was raised, and Sarsour pledged to donate any funds not needed at the cemetery to other Jewish community centers or sites targeted by vandalism. She said the fundraising effort would "send a united message from the Jewish and Muslim communities that there is no place for this type of hate, desecration, and violence in America".&nbsp;St. Louis's&nbsp;<a title="United Hebrew Congregation (Chesterfield, Missouri)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_Hebrew_Congregation_(Chesterfield,_Missouri)">United Hebrew Congregation</a>&nbsp;Senior Rabbi, Brigitte S. Rosenberg, whose congregants had family members buried in the vandalized cemetery, called the campaign "a beautiful gesture".&nbsp;However, the project generated some controversy as the funds were not distributed as quickly as some had expected.&nbsp;In 2018, Alzado Harris confessed to the desecration.<sup id="cite_ref-322" class="reference"></sup></dd>
<dt>2017</dt>
<dd>Imam Sheikh Ammar Shahin gave an anti-semitic sermon at the Islamic Center of Davis, but apologized for it a few days later.</dd>
<dt>2017</dt>
<dd>At the end of July 2017,&nbsp;<a title="Kevin Myers" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kevin_Myers">Kevin Myers</a>&nbsp;contributed an article entitled "Sorry, ladies - equal pay has to be earned" to the Irish edition of&nbsp;<em><a title="The Sunday Times" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/The_Sunday_Times">The Sunday Times</a></em>&nbsp;about the lower income of female presenters working for the&nbsp;<a title="BBC" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/BBC">BBC</a>,&nbsp;after it was reported that two thirds of the BBC's top paid stars were men and only one of its top ten best paid presenters is a woman. He speculated: "Is it because men are more charismatic performers? Because they work harder? Because they are more driven? Possibly a bit of each"&nbsp;and that men might be paid more because they "work harder, get sick less frequently and seldom get pregnant".&nbsp;Myers further alleged that&nbsp;<a title="Claudia Winkleman" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Claudia_Winkleman">Claudia Winkleman</a>&nbsp;and&nbsp;<a title="Vanessa Feltz" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vanessa_Feltz">Vanessa Feltz</a>&nbsp;are higher paid than other female presenters because they are Jewish. He wrote: "Jews are not generally noted for their insistence on selling their talent for the lowest possible price, which is the most useful measure there is of inveterate, lost-with-all-hands stupidity". The editor of the Irish edition, Frank Fitzgibbon, issued a statement saying in part "This newspaper abhors anti-Semitism and did not intend to cause offence to Jewish people".&nbsp;<a title="Martin Ivens" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Martin_Ivens">Martin Ivens</a>, editor of&nbsp;<em>The Sunday Times</em>, said the article should not have been published. Ivens and Fitzgibbon apologised for publishing it.&nbsp;After complaints from readers and the&nbsp;<a title="Campaign Against Antisemitism" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Campaign_Against_Antisemitism">Campaign Against Antisemitism</a>, the article was removed from the website.&nbsp;It has been announced by the newspaper that Myers will not write for&nbsp;<em>The Sunday Times</em>&nbsp;again.&nbsp;Myers was defended by the chair of the Jewish Representative Council of Ireland, Maurice Cohen, who said that Myers was not antisemitic, but had rather "inadvertently stumbled into an antisemitic trope. ... Branding Kevin Myers as either an antisemite or a Holocaust denier is an absolute distortion of the facts."&nbsp;Myers apologised for this article on radio, saying that "it is over for me professionally as far as I can see", and that "I think they [Jewish people] are the most gifted people who have ever existed on this planet and civilisation owes an enormous debt to them &ndash; I am very, very sorry that I should have so offended them."</dd>
<dt>2017</dt>
<dd>The&nbsp;<a title="Unite the Right rally" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Unite_the_Right_rally">Unite the Right rally</a>&nbsp;was a gathering of&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Far-right" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Far-right">far-right</a>&nbsp;groups in&nbsp;<a title="Charlottesville, Virginia" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Charlottesville,_Virginia">Charlottesville, Virginia</a>, United States, on 11 and 12 August 2017.<sup id="cite_ref-nyt94_331-0" class="reference"></sup></dd>
</dl>
<p>On the evening of Friday, 11 August, a group of white nationalists&mdash;variously numbered at dozens,&nbsp;around 100,&nbsp;and hundreds &mdash;marched through the University of Virginia's campus while chanting things including "Jews will not replace us",&nbsp;and the&nbsp;<a title="Nazism" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nazism">Nazi</a>&nbsp;slogan "<a class="mw-redirect" title="Blood and Soil" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Blood_and_Soil">Blood and Soil</a>".&nbsp;On 12 August protesters and counterprotesters gathered at&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Emancipation Park (Charlottesville, Virginia)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Emancipation_Park_(Charlottesville,_Virginia)">Emancipation Park</a>&nbsp;(formerly known as Lee Park). White nationalist protesters chanted Nazi-era slogans,&nbsp;including "<a class="mw-redirect" title="Blood and Soil" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Blood_and_Soil">Blood and Soil</a>".&nbsp;They shouted among other things, "Jews will not replace us."<span style="font-size: xx-small;">&nbsp;</span>&nbsp;Some held posters targeting Jews that read "the&nbsp;<a title="Goy" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Goy#Modern_usage">Goyim</a>&nbsp;know", using the Hebrew word for non-Jews, as well as "the&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Jewish control of media" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jewish_control_of_media">Jewish media is going down</a>".&nbsp;Also on 12 August, an attendee drove his car into a crowd of people protesting the rally, killing 32-year-old Heather D. Heyer and injuring 19 others, in what police have called&nbsp;<a title="Vehicle-ramming attack" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vehicle-ramming_attack">a deliberate attack</a>. The driver was identified as James Alex Fields Jr.; following the crash, his former high school history teacher said he was a Nazi sympathizer who held white supremacist views and was infatuated with&nbsp;<a title="Adolf Hitler" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Adolf_Hitler">Adolf Hitler</a>.&nbsp;Two hours before the crash, a&nbsp;<em><a title="New York Daily News" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/New_York_Daily_News">New York Daily News</a></em>&nbsp;photographer snapped James brandishing a wooden shield emblazoned with the logo for&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Neo-Nazi" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Neo-Nazi">neo-Nazi</a>&nbsp;group Vanguard America, standing alongside its members. However, after he was arrested, the group issued a statement denying he was a member and saying "the shields were freely handed out to anyone in attendance."</p>
<dl>
<dt>2017</dt>
<dd>Several internet companies, such as domain registrar&nbsp;<a title="GoDaddy" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/GoDaddy">GoDaddy</a>&nbsp;and video game chat application&nbsp;<a title="Discord (software)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Discord_(software)">Discord</a>, shut down services for&nbsp;<a title="Neo-Nazism" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Neo-Nazism">neo-Nazi</a>,&nbsp;<a title="White supremacy" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/White_supremacy">white supremacist</a>,&nbsp;<a title="Alt-right" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Alt-right">alt-right</a>&nbsp;website&nbsp;<em><a title="The Daily Stormer" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/The_Daily_Stormer">The Daily Stormer</a></em>&nbsp;for violation of&nbsp;<a title="Terms of service" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Terms_of_service">terms of service</a>, and in response to the violence in&nbsp;<a title="Charlottesville, Virginia" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Charlottesville,_Virginia">Charlottesville, Virginia</a>&nbsp;<sup id="cite_ref-343" class="reference"></sup></dd>
<dt>2017</dt>
<dd>On 14 August 2017, the&nbsp;<a title="New England Holocaust Memorial" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/New_England_Holocaust_Memorial">New England Holocaust Memorial</a>&nbsp;was damaged for the second time in as many months, by a 17-year-old who threw a rock at one of the glass panels.</dd>
<dt>2017</dt>
<dd>Two classroom windows at Temple Israel in&nbsp;<a title="Alameda, California" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Alameda,_California">Alameda</a>&nbsp;were smashed.</dd>
<dt>2017</dt>
<dd>Ruth Thomann, the manager of the Paradies Arosa hotel in Switzerland, stated that it was wrong of her to post signs telling "Jewish guests" to shower before entering the pool and to use the refrigerator at set times, which she had done that year.</dd>
<dt>2017</dt>
<dd>Extremists marked the death of&nbsp;<a title="Adolf Hitler" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Adolf_Hitler">Adolf Hitler</a>'s deputy,&nbsp;<a title="Rudolf Hess" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Rudolf_Hess">Rudolf Hess</a>, in Berlin. However, protestors blocked them from going to the former Spandau prison, where Hess hanged himself in 1987.</dd>
<dt>2017</dt>
<dd>Antisemitic graffiti was written on the walls of Oakland's&nbsp;<a title="Temple Sinai (Oakland, California)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Temple_Sinai_(Oakland,_California)">Temple Sinai</a>&nbsp;on Rosh Hashanah.</dd>
<dt>2017</dt>
<dd>ProPublica stated in September that a website was able to target ads at Facebook users who were interested in "how to burn Jew" and "Jew hater". Facebook removed the categories and said it would try to stop them from appearing to potential advertisers.</dd>
<dt>2017</dt>
<dd>An 18 October cartoon in the Daily Californian depicting&nbsp;<a title="Alan Dershowitz" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Alan_Dershowitz">Alan Dershowitz</a>&nbsp;was denounced as anti-semitic by UC Berkeley Chancellor&nbsp;<a title="Carol T. Christ" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Carol_T._Christ">Carol Christ</a>; Dershowitz agreed that the cartoon was anti-semitic.&nbsp;In an editorial on 25 October, Daily Californian editor Karim Doumar stated, "The criticisms we received reaffirms for us a need for a more critical editing eye, and a stronger understanding of the violent history and contemporary manifestations of anti-Semitism."</dd>
<dt>2017</dt>
<dd>In October 2017,&nbsp;<a title="Nigel Farage" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nigel_Farage">Nigel Farage</a>&nbsp;asserted in a&nbsp;<a title="LBC" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/LBC">LBC</a>&nbsp;radio broadcast that the "Jewish lobby" in the United States was more concerning to him than&nbsp;<a title="Russian interference in the 2016 United States elections" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Russian_interference_in_the_2016_United_States_elections">Russian interference in American politics</a>, saying: "There are other very powerful lobbies in the United States of America, and the Jewish lobby, with its links with the Israeli government, is one of those strong voices...There are about 6 million Jewish people living in America, so as a percentage it's quite small, but in terms of influence it's quite big."&nbsp;Farage's remarks were condemned by the&nbsp;<a title="Campaign Against Antisemitism" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Campaign_Against_Antisemitism">Campaign Against Antisemitism</a><span style="font-size: xx-small;">&nbsp;</span>and the&nbsp;<a title="Anti-Defamation League" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Anti-Defamation_League">Anti-Defamation League</a>, which said that Farage's comment "plays into deep-seated&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Antisemetic canard" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Antisemetic_canard">anti-Semitic tropes</a>" and was fuel for extremist conspiracy theories.</dd>
<dt>2017</dt>
<dd>Lecturer Hatem Bazian was denounced by UC Berkeley for retweeting cartoons the school decided had "crossed the line" into anti-Semitism. Bazian apologized and said "the image is offensive and does not represent my views or the anti-racist work that I do."&nbsp;The cartoons were first tweeted by Ron Hughes and later retweeted by Bazian.</dd>
<dt>2017</dt>
<dd>When&nbsp;<a title="Linda Sarsour" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Linda_Sarsour">Linda Sarsour</a>&nbsp;was scheduled to deliver a&nbsp;<a title="Commencement speech" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Commencement_speech">commencement speech</a>&nbsp;at the&nbsp;<a title="City University of New York" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/City_University_of_New_York">City University of New York</a>&nbsp;(CUNY) in June 2017, some American conservatives strongly opposed her selection as speaker.&nbsp;<a title="Dov Hikind" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dov_Hikind">Dov Hikind</a>, a&nbsp;<a title="Democratic Party (United States)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Democratic_Party_(United_States)">Democratic Party</a>&nbsp;state assemblyman in New York, sent Governor&nbsp;<a title="Andrew Cuomo" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Andrew_Cuomo">Andrew Cuomo</a>&nbsp;a letter objecting to the choice of Sarsour as speaker, signed by 100&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Holocaust" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Holocaust">Holocaust</a>&nbsp;survivors.&nbsp;Hikind objected to Sarsour's role based on her previously having spoken alongside&nbsp;<a title="Rasmea Odeh" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Rasmea_Odeh">Rasmea Odeh</a>, who was convicted by an Israeli court for taking part in a bombing that killed two civilians in 1969.&nbsp;Sarsour maintained that she had nothing to apologize for, saying that questions existed about the integrity of Odeh's conviction, that her beliefs had been misrepresented, and that criticism of Israeli policies was being conflated with anti-Semitism. She ascribed the critical reaction to her speech to her prominent role as an organizer for the 2017 Women's March.&nbsp;The university chancellor, the dean of the college, and a group of professors defended her&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Free speech" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Free_speech">right to speak</a>, as did some Jewish groups, including Jews for Racial and Economic Justice.&nbsp;A group of prominent left-leaning Jews signed an open letter condemning attacks on Sarsour and promising "to [work] alongside her for a more just and equal society".&nbsp;Jonathan Greenblatt of the Anti-Defamation League defended Sarsour's&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="First Amendment" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/First_Amendment">First Amendment</a>&nbsp;right to speak despite opposing her views on Israel.&nbsp;A rally in support of Sarsour took place in front of&nbsp;<a title="New York City Hall" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/New_York_City_Hall">New York's City Hall</a>. Constitutional scholar Fred Smith Jr. tied the controversy to broader disputes over&nbsp;<a title="Freedom of speech" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Freedom_of_speech">freedom of speech</a>&nbsp;in America.</dd>
<dt>2017</dt>
<dd>Academy of the Holy Cross in Maryland fired Greg Conte because of his involvement with a white nationalist think tank, Richard Spencer's National Policy Institute.&nbsp;Conte had also written on Twitter that "Hitler did not commit any crimes."</dd>
<dt>2017</dt>
<dd>9 December:&nbsp;<a title="2017 Gothenburg Synagogue attack" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2017_Gothenburg_Synagogue_attack">2017 Gothenburg Synagogue attack</a>&nbsp;takes place in&nbsp;<a title="Gothenburg" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gothenburg">Gothenburg</a>,&nbsp;<a title="Sweden" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sweden">Sweden</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-365" class="reference"></sup></dd>
<dt>2018</dt>
<dd>It was announced that Germany agreed to grant monetary compensation to Jews who were persecuted in Algeria during World War II; this marks the first time for Jews who resided in Algeria between July 1940 and November 1942 to be compensated by the German government.<sup id="cite_ref-367" class="reference"></sup></dd>
<dt>2018</dt>
<dd>On 16 March 2018,&nbsp;<a title="Trayon White" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Trayon_White">Trayon White</a>&nbsp;posted a video on his official&nbsp;<a title="Facebook" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Facebook">Facebook</a>&nbsp;page showing snow flurries falling, alluding to the&nbsp;<a title="Rothschild family" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Rothschild_family">Rothschild family</a>&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Rothschild conspiracy theories" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Rothschild_conspiracy_theories">conspiring</a>&nbsp;to manipulate the weather. In his post, he stated, "Y'all better pay attention to this climate control, man, this climate manipulation ... And that's a model based off the Rothschilds controlling the climate to create natural disasters they can pay for to own the cities, man. Be careful."&nbsp;The comment was widely reported in the Washington media as an endorsement of an&nbsp;<a title="Antisemitism" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Antisemitism">anti-Semitic</a>&nbsp;<a title="Conspiracy theory" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Conspiracy_theory">conspiracy theory</a>.&nbsp;The&nbsp;<em>Washington City Paper</em>&nbsp;reported on 19 March that this was not the first time White alluded to a Jewish conspiracy to control global weather.&nbsp;White later apologized for making the statement,&nbsp;and said he was working with Jews United for Justice to develop a deeper understanding of anti-semitism.</dd>
<dt>2018</dt>
<dd>Austrian foreign minister&nbsp;<a title="Karin Kneissl" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Karin_Kneissl">Karin Kneissl</a>&nbsp;recalled diplomat J&uuml;rgen-Michael Kleppich from Israel after he was photographed wearing a T-shirt with slogans linked to Nazism.</dd>
<dd>2018 April 17:&nbsp;<a title="2018 Berlin anti-semitic attack" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2018_Berlin_anti-semitic_attack">2018 Berlin anti-semitic attack</a>&nbsp;takes place.<sup id="cite_ref-AngelosSemitism_373-0" class="reference"></sup></dd>
<dt>2018</dt>
<dd>In April 2018, Syracuse University permanently expelled&nbsp;<a title="Theta Tau" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Theta_Tau">Theta Tau</a>&nbsp;after video of members surfaced that the university chancellor considered to be "extremely racist, anti-Semitic, homophobic, sexist and hostile to people with disabilities."</dd>
<dt>2018</dt>
<dd><a title="Alice Walker" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Alice_Walker">Alice Walker</a>&nbsp;was asked by a&nbsp;<em><a title="The New York Times" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/The_New_York_Times">New York Times</a></em>&nbsp;interviewer, "What books are on your nightstand?" She listed&nbsp;<a title="David Icke" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/David_Icke">David Icke</a>&rsquo;s&nbsp;<em>And the Truth Shall Set You Free,</em>&nbsp;a book promoting an antisemitic conspiracy theory based on&nbsp;<em><a title="The Protocols of the Elders of Zion" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/The_Protocols_of_the_Elders_of_Zion">The Protocols of the Elders of Zion</a>.</em>&nbsp;Walker described the book as, "A curious person's dream come true."</dd>
<dt>2018</dt>
<dd>Israeli lawmakers&nbsp;<a title="Yuval Steinitz" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Yuval_Steinitz">Yuval Steinitz</a>&nbsp;and&nbsp;<a title="Oren Hazan" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Oren_Hazan">Oren Hazan</a>&nbsp;accused&nbsp;<a title="Jerusalem" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jerusalem">Jerusalem</a>-born actress&nbsp;<a title="Natalie Portman" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Natalie_Portman">Natalie Portman</a>&nbsp;of antisemitism and sought to revoke her citizenship, with Hazan calling her a "little hypocrite liar", after she decided not to travel to Israel and accept the&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="US$" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/US$">US$</a>2 million&nbsp;<a title="Genesis Prize" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Genesis_Prize">Genesis Prize</a>.</dd>
<dt>2018</dt>
<dd>In 2018, media outlets reported on calls for the four co-chairs of the&nbsp;<a title="2018 Women's March" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2018_Women%27s_March">Women's March</a>&nbsp;to resign for failing to denounce Nation of Islam leader&nbsp;<a title="Louis Farrakhan" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Louis_Farrakhan">Louis Farrakhan</a>.&nbsp;<em><a title="The Daily Beast" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/The_Daily_Beast">The Daily Beast</a></em>&nbsp;traced the controversy to February 2018, when&nbsp;<a title="Tamika Mallory" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tamika_Mallory">Tamika Mallory</a>&nbsp;attended a Nation of Islam&nbsp;<a title="Saviours' Day" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Saviours%27_Day">Saviours' Day</a>&nbsp;event hosted by Farrakhan, during which he referred to the "Satanic Jew" and declared that "the powerful Jews are my enemy".&nbsp;<em>The Daily Beast</em>&nbsp;later reported that the Women's March appeared to be losing support.&nbsp;In October 2018, actress&nbsp;<a title="Alyssa Milano" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Alyssa_Milano">Alyssa Milano</a>, who spoke at the 2018 Women's March, told&nbsp;<a title="The Advocate (LGBT magazine)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/The_Advocate_(LGBT_magazine)"><em>The Advocate</em></a>&nbsp;that she refused to participate in the 2019 March unless Mallory and&nbsp;<a title="Linda Sarsour" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Linda_Sarsour">Linda Sarsour</a>&nbsp;condemned what have been described as&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Homophobia in the United States" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Homophobia_in_the_United_States">homophobic</a>,&nbsp;<a title="Antisemitism in the United States" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Antisemitism_in_the_United_States">antisemitic</a>, and&nbsp;<a title="Transphobia" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Transphobia">transphobic</a>&nbsp;comments by Farrakhan.&nbsp;The Women's March released a statement about anti-Semitism, defending Sarsour and Mallory.&nbsp;In November 2018,&nbsp;<a title="Teresa Shook" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Teresa_Shook">Teresa Shook</a>, the co-founder of the Women's March, called for march organizers&nbsp;<a title="Bob Bland" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bob_Bland">Bob Bland</a>, Mallory, Sarsour and&nbsp;<a title="Carmen Perez" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Carmen_Perez">Carmen Perez</a>&nbsp;to resign, saying, "they have allowed anti-Semitism, anti-LBGTQIA sentiment and hateful, racist rhetoric to become a part of the platform by their refusal to separate themselves from groups that espouse these racist, hateful beliefs".&nbsp;The organization's leadership rebuffed calls to step down; Sarsour's initial response alleged that criticisms were motivated by racism and her opposition to Israel. Sarsour later issued a statement that apologized to the march's supporters for its "slow response" and condemned anti-semitism.&nbsp;In December 2018,&nbsp;<a title="Tablet (magazine)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tablet_(magazine)"><em>Tablet</em></a>&nbsp;published an article by&nbsp;<a title="Leah McSweeney" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Leah_McSweeney">Leah McSweeney</a>&nbsp;and&nbsp;<a class="new" title="Jacob Siegel (journalist) (page does not exist)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Jacob_Siegel_(journalist)&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1">Jacob Siegel</a>&nbsp;alleging that during the first meeting between Bland, Mallory, Perez, and others in the days after the&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="2016 US Presidential election" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2016_US_Presidential_election">2016 US Presidential election</a>, Mallory and Perez repeated an&nbsp;<a title="Antisemitic canard" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Antisemitic_canard#Accusations_of_playing_a_major_role_in_the_slave_trade">anti-Semitic canard</a>&nbsp;promoted in Farrakhan's book&nbsp;<em><a title="The Secret Relationship Between Blacks and Jews" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/The_Secret_Relationship_Between_Blacks_and_Jews">The Secret Relationship Between Blacks and Jews</a></em>&nbsp;telling fellow organizer&nbsp;<a title="Vanessa Wruble" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vanessa_Wruble">Vanessa Wruble</a>, who is Jewish, that Jews were leaders in the American slave trade and are especially responsible for subsequent exploitation of racial minorities.&nbsp;Wruble suggested that Mallory and Perez had berated her for her Jewish heritage, saying "your people hold all the wealth."&nbsp;Mallory denied Wruble's account but acknowledged telling "white women" at the meeting, including Wruble, that she "did not trust them."</dd>
<dt>2018</dt>
<dd>The&nbsp;<a title="Echo Music Prize" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Echo_Music_Prize">Echo Music Prize</a>&nbsp;was heavily criticized worldwide when&nbsp;<a title="Farid Bang" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Farid_Bang">Farid Bang</a>&nbsp;and&nbsp;<a title="Kollegah" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kollegah">Kollegah</a>&nbsp;received the award for best hip hop/urban album in April 2018. The nominated album,&nbsp;<em><a class="mw-redirect" title="Jung, brutal, gutaussehend 3" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jung,_brutal,_gutaussehend_3">Jung, Brutal, Gutaussehend 3</a></em>&nbsp;(English: "Young, brutal, handsome 3"), contains the track "0815", in which the artists refer to their muscles as being more defined than those of&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Auschwitz" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Auschwitz">Auschwitz</a>&nbsp;inmates. The duo was even allowed to perform this track during the ceremony, despite heavy protests weeks before the award show. This was much criticized, and as a consequence, the Echo Music Prize was discontinued.</dd>
<dt>2018</dt>
<dd>An Israeli man wearing a yarmulke was attacked in Berlin; the attacker allegedly beat him with a belt and shouted, "Yehudi" &mdash; the Arabic word for Jew. Authorities stated that the man who was assaulted and another man wearing a yarmulke were insulted by three men and then whipped by one. In response to this, thousands of Germans took part in rallies against antisemitism, many of them wearing yarmulkes.</dd>
<dt>2018</dt>
<dd>On 25 February 2018,&nbsp;<a title="Tamika Mallory" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tamika_Mallory">Tamika Mallory</a>&nbsp;attended an anti-Semitic&nbsp;<a title="Louis Farrakhan" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Louis_Farrakhan">Louis Farrakhan</a>&nbsp;speech, where she was directly acknowledged by Farrakhan.&nbsp;Farrakhan made multiple inflammatory comments during his three-hour speech. He claimed that "the powerful Jews are my enemy", that "the Jews have control over agencies of those agencies of government" like the FBI, that Jews are "the mother and father of apartheid", and that Jews are responsible for "degenerate behavior in Hollywood turning men into women and women into men".&nbsp;Mallory was criticized for her support of&nbsp;<a title="Louis Farrakhan" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Louis_Farrakhan">Louis Farrakhan</a>, as well as her support of&nbsp;<a title="Assata Shakur" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Assata_Shakur">Assata Shakur</a>, a former&nbsp;<a title="Black Liberation Army" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Black_Liberation_Army">Black Liberation Army</a>&nbsp;member convicted of murder.<sup id="cite_ref-401" class="reference"></sup></dd>
<dt>2018</dt>
<dd>On 17 April 2018,&nbsp;<a title="Tamika Mallory" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tamika_Mallory">Tamika Mallory</a>&nbsp;criticized Starbucks for allowing the&nbsp;<a title="Anti-Defamation League" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Anti-Defamation_League">ADL</a>, an organization dedicated to fighting anti-Semitism, to participate in a company-wide racial bias training after the arrest of two black men at a Starbucks in Philadelphia, claiming that the "ADL attacks black and brown people".</dd>
<dt>2018</dt>
<dd>Patrick Little, a Republican candidate for the Senate in California, was openly anti-semitic and even called for a United States "free from Jews."</dd>
<dt>2018</dt>
<dd>Paul Nehlen, a Republican candidate for Wisconsin's first congressional district, often made anti-semitic remarks on social media.</dd>
<dt>2018</dt>
<dd>John Fitzgerald, an anti-semite and Holocaust denier, was a Republican candidate for the House of Representatives.</dd>
<dt>2018</dt>
<dd>Walter Stolper of Florida was arrested after attempting to burn down his condo to "kill all the f------ Jews".</dd>
<dt>2018</dt>
<dd><a title="Arthur J. Jones" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arthur_J._Jones">Arthur J. Jones</a>, an American neo-Nazi far-right white nationalist and Holocaust denier,&nbsp;was the Republican candidate for&nbsp;<a title="Illinois's 3rd congressional district" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Illinois%27s_3rd_congressional_district">Illinois's 3rd congressional district</a>.</dd>
<dt>2018</dt>
<dd>Antisemitic graffiti was discovered at Congregation Shaarey Tefilla in Indiana.</dd>
<dt>2018</dt>
<dd>U.S. Magistrate Mark Hornsby of Louisiana ruled that Jews are racially protected under&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Title VII of the Civil Rights Act of 1964" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Title_VII_of_the_Civil_Rights_Act_of_1964">Title VII of the Civil Rights Act of 1964</a>, in a case regarding Joshua Bonadona's claim&nbsp;<a title="Louisiana College" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Louisiana_College">Louisiana College</a>&rsquo;s president, Rick Brewer, refused to approve his hiring because of what he allegedly called Joshua's "Jewish blood."<sup id="cite_ref-410" class="reference"></sup></dd>
<dt>2018</dt>
<dd>Stanford University student Hamzeh Daoud, who posted Facebook messages promising to "fight Zionists on campus", resigned as a resident assistant and said he would begin therapy.</dd>
<dt>2018</dt>
<dd>Antisemitic graffiti was found on the house where&nbsp;<a title="Elie Wiesel" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Elie_Wiesel">Elie Wiesel</a>&nbsp;was born.</dd>
<dt>2018</dt>
<dd>Detention Officers Howard Costner and Jesse Jones of Spalding County were fired because of their online comments expressing sympathy for Hitler and American neo-Nazis.</dd>
<dt>2018</dt>
<dd>Antisemite Steve West won the Republican Missouri House primary election in the 15th District.</dd>
<dt>2018</dt>
<dd>Germany lifted a blanket ban on&nbsp;<a title="Nazi symbolism" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nazi_symbolism">Nazi symbolism</a>&nbsp;in&nbsp;<a title="Video game" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Video_game">video games</a>, including the swastika.</dd>
<dt>2018</dt>
<dd>Antisemitic fliers were discovered near and at five East Bay synagogues.</dd>
<dt>2018</dt>
<dd>The painting&nbsp;<em>Deux Femmes Dans Un Jardin</em>&nbsp;by Pierre Auguste Renoir, which was stolen from the Jewish art collector Alfred Weinberger by Nazis in 1941, was returned to his granddaughter.</dd>
<dt>2018</dt>
<dd>Fliers blaming Jewish people for the sexual assault allegations against&nbsp;<a title="Brett Kavanaugh" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Brett_Kavanaugh">Brett Kavanaugh</a>&nbsp;were posted on the University of California campuses of Berkeley and Davis, and at Vassar College.</dd>
<dt>2018</dt>
<dd>On 27 October 2018,&nbsp;<a title="Pittsburgh synagogue shooting" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pittsburgh_synagogue_shooting">11 people were murdered</a>&nbsp;in an attack on the&nbsp;<a title="Tree of Life &ndash; Or L'Simcha Congregation" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tree_of_Life_%E2%80%93_Or_L%27Simcha_Congregation">Tree of Life &ndash; Or L'Simcha</a>&nbsp;synagogue in&nbsp;<a title="Pittsburgh" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pittsburgh">Pittsburgh</a>,&nbsp;<a title="Pennsylvania" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pennsylvania">Pennsylvania</a>.</dd>
<dt>2018</dt>
<dd>Justin Trudeau, then the Prime Minister of Canada, gave a formal apology on behalf of Canada for its refusal to accept 907 Jewish refugees who, fleeing Nazi Germany, arrived in Canada on the&nbsp;<a title="MS St. Louis" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/MS_St._Louis">MS St. Louis</a>&nbsp;in 1939.</dd>
<dt>2018</dt>
<dd>A Jewish professor, Elizabeth Midlarsky, found swastikas spray-painted on her office walls at Columbia's Teachers College.</dd>
<dt>2018</dt>
<dd>In a Jewish cemetery in Strasbourg, France, antisemitic graffiti was written on tombstones.</dd>
<dt>2018, 23 March</dt>
<dd><a title="Murder of Mireille Knoll" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Murder_of_Mireille_Knoll">Murder of Mireille Knoll</a>.</dd>
<dt>2018 October</dt>
<dd>Vandals overturn headstones and smash vases in a Jewish cemetery in San Antonio, Texas.</dd>
<dt>2018 December</dt>
<dd>Two signs titled "Fake News" and "#MAGA," both frequently expressed by President Donald Trump and his supporters, are planted with arrows beneath them pointing to the marquee for the Holocaust Memorial Museum of San Antonio, Texas.</dd>
<dt>2019</dt>
<dd>Belgium outlawed&nbsp;<a title="Shechita" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Shechita">Shechita</a>.</dd>
<dt>2019</dt>
<dd>Democratic Rep.&nbsp;<a title="Ilhan Omar" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ilhan_Omar">Ilhan Omar</a>&nbsp;drew condemnation from&nbsp;<a title="Nancy Pelosi" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nancy_Pelosi">Nancy Pelosi</a>, the Democratic House leadership, and a number of Jewish organizations for a tweet that was perceived as antisemitic, in which she alleged that American support for Israel was rooted in money spent by pro-Israel lobbying organizations, notably the American Israel Public Affairs Committee. She later apologized for the tweet in a statement.</dd>
<dt>2019</dt>
