<dd><a title="Joan Ryan" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Joan_Ryan">Joan Ryan</a>&nbsp;became the eighth&nbsp;<a title="Member of Parliament (United Kingdom)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Member_of_Parliament_(United_Kingdom)">MP</a>&nbsp;to quit the&nbsp;<a title="Labour Party (UK)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Labour_Party_(UK)">Labour Party</a>&nbsp;and join&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="The Independent Group" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/The_Independent_Group">The Independent Group</a>, citing a "culture of anti-Jewish racism" within the party as the reason for her departure.</dd>
<dt>2019</dt>
<dd>In February, Polish nationalist based in France&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Disruption of Holocaust conference in Paris" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Disruption_of_Holocaust_conference_in_Paris">disrupted The New Polish School of Holocaust Scholarship conference in EHESS, Paris</a>.&nbsp;The Polish&nbsp;<a title="Institute of National Remembrance" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Institute_of_National_Remembrance">Institute of National Remembrance</a>&nbsp;(IPN) which had made social media postings during the conference and sent a delegate,&nbsp;was criticized by French education minister&nbsp;<a title="Fr&eacute;d&eacute;rique Vidal" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fr%C3%A9d%C3%A9rique_Vidal">Fr&eacute;d&eacute;rique Vidal</a>, who said the disturbances were "highly regrettable" and "anti-Semitic". Vidal further stated the disturbances organized by&nbsp;<a title="Gazeta Polska" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gazeta_Polska">Gazeta Polska</a>&nbsp;activists, appeared to have been condoned by the IPN whose representative did not condemn the disruption and which criticized the conference on social media that were further re-tweeted by the&nbsp;<a title="Embassy of Poland, Paris" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Embassy_of_Poland,_Paris">Embassy of Poland, Paris</a>.&nbsp;Agitators stalked conference speakers in Paris, shouting insults such as "dirty Jew" that hark back to interwar antisemitism.</dd>
<dt>2019</dt>
<dd><a title="Ian Austin" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ian_Austin">Ian Austin</a>&nbsp;quit&nbsp;<a title="Labour Party (UK)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Labour_Party_(UK)">Labour</a>&nbsp;over a "culture of extremism, anti-semitism and intolerance" within the party under&nbsp;<a title="Jeremy Corbyn" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jeremy_Corbyn">Jeremy Corbyn</a>.</dd>
<dt>2019</dt>
<dd><a title="Chris Williamson (politician)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Chris_Williamson_(politician)">Chris Williamson</a>, a Labour MP, was suspended by his party over comments that Labour had "given too much ground" when responding to criticism over its handling of antisemitism within its ranks.</dd>
<dt>2019</dt>
<dd>A subway poster in Brooklyn with a picture of&nbsp;<a title="Ruth Bader Ginsburg" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ruth_Bader_Ginsburg">Ruth Bader Ginsburg</a>&nbsp;(who is Jewish) was vandalized with the writing "Die, Jew Bitch!" and a swastika.</dd>
<dt>2019</dt>
<dd>The uptick in violence against Jews in Brooklyn continues with multiple violent attacks.<sup id="cite_ref-436" class="reference"></sup></dd>
<dt>2019</dt>
<dd>The owners of the BerMax Caff&eacute; in&nbsp;<a title="Winnipeg" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Winnipeg">Winnipeg</a>&nbsp;are alleged to have perpetrated an act of fake antisemitism by vandalizing their cafe and fabricating a claim of assault, in similar fashion to the recent&nbsp;<a title="Jussie Smollett" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jussie_Smollett">Jussie Smollett</a>&nbsp;case in Chicago.<sup id="cite_ref-438" class="reference"></sup></dd>
<dt>2019, 4 April</dt>
<dd><a title="Bet Israel Synagogue (İzmir)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bet_Israel_Synagogue_(%C4%B0zmir)">Bet Israel Synagogue</a>&nbsp;of&nbsp;<a title="İzmir" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/%C4%B0zmir">İzmir</a>,&nbsp;<a title="Turkey" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Turkey">Turkey</a>&nbsp;is attacked with a Molotov cocktail.</dd>
<dt>2019</dt>
<dd>The synagogue Chabad, of the city of Poway in California, was the site of an attack on 27 April 2019, in which multiple people were shot during Passover services.&nbsp;</dd>
<dt>2019</dt>
<dd>A synagogue in Halle, Germany,&nbsp;<a title="Halle synagogue shooting" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Halle_synagogue_shooting">was attacked by a lone shooter</a>&nbsp;who failed to gain access to the building. Two doors were damaged and improvised explosives set off. The attacker killed two people nearby.</dd>
<dt>2019</dt>
<dd>A Church of England report was published called "God&rsquo;s Unfailing World: Theological and practical perspectives on Christian-Jewish relations", that encouraged Christians to be repentant for "sins of the past" against Jews, and to challenge current stereotypes and attitudes against them. The report was the first time the Church of England made an authoritative statement about antisemitism.</dd>
<dt>2019</dt>
<dd>On 10 December 2019, a&nbsp;<a title="2019 Jersey City shooting" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2019_Jersey_City_shooting">shooting</a>&nbsp;occurred at a&nbsp;<a title="Kosher foods" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kosher_foods">kosher</a>&nbsp;grocery store located in the&nbsp;<a title="Greenville, Jersey City" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Greenville,_Jersey_City">Greenville section</a>&nbsp;of&nbsp;<a title="Jersey City, New Jersey" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jersey_City,_New_Jersey">Jersey City, New Jersey</a>&nbsp;United States. Five people were killed at the store, including the two attackers and three civilians. A civilian and two police officers were wounded. A Jersey City Police Department detective was shot and killed at a nearby cemetery just before the grocery store attack.<sup id="cite_ref-NJ.com15dec2019_445-0" class="reference"></sup></dd>
<dt>2019</dt>
<dd>Jersey City Mayor Steve Fullop said a trustee of the Jersey City Board of Education, Joan Terrell-Paige, should resign in the wake of her comment after the&nbsp;<a title="2019 Jersey City shooting" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2019_Jersey_City_shooting">2019 Jersey City shooting</a>&nbsp;about Jew "brutes" that according to her have "threatened, intimidated and harassed" black residents.&nbsp;Terrell-Paige further asked whether the public is "brave enough" to listen to the perpetrators' message, and said the local rabbis were selling body parts.<sup id="cite_ref-449" class="reference"></sup></dd>
<dt>2019</dt>
<dd>The&nbsp;<a title="Executive Order on Combating Anti-Semitism" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Executive_Order_on_Combating_Anti-Semitism">Executive Order on Combating Anti-Semitism</a>&nbsp;is an executive order announced by U.S. President&nbsp;<a title="Donald Trump" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Donald_Trump">Donald Trump</a>&nbsp;on Tuesday, 10 December 2019, and signed the next day. The White House initially indicated that the order would define&nbsp;<a title="Judaism" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Judaism">Judaism</a>&nbsp;as a&nbsp;<a title="Nationality" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nationality">nationality</a>&nbsp;instead of a&nbsp;<a title="Religion" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Religion">religion</a>&nbsp;in the&nbsp;<a title="United States" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States">United States</a>, though the order ultimately released was more modest in its reach. The purpose of the order is claimed to be to prevent&nbsp;<a title="Antisemitism" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Antisemitism">antisemitism</a>&nbsp;by making it easier to use laws prohibiting institutional discrimination against people based on&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="National origin" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/National_origin">national origin</a>&nbsp;to punish discrimination against&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Jewish people" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jewish_people">Jewish people</a>,&nbsp;including opposition to policies undertaken by the government of&nbsp;<a title="Israel" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel">Israel</a>.&nbsp;Some American Jews applauded the order, while others objected to defining Judaism as a nationality (as the order was initially indicated to do, though it ultimately did not), claiming that "Trump's reclassification of Judaism mirrored sentiments used by&nbsp;<a title="White nationalism" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/White_nationalism">white nationalists</a>&nbsp;and&nbsp;<a title="Nazi Germany" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nazi_Germany">Nazi Germany</a>" and that "the move appears to question whether Jews are really American".&nbsp;Some decried the order as a political stunt, and called on Trump to more directly address the threat of white nationalism.<sup id="cite_ref-nytimes1_451-1" class="reference"></sup></dd>
<dt>2019</dt>
<dd><a title="Monsey Hanukkah stabbing" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Monsey_Hanukkah_stabbing">Monsey Hanukkah stabbing</a>. Five people were injured in a mass stabbing at the home of a&nbsp;<a title="Hasidic Judaism" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hasidic_Judaism">Hasidic</a>&nbsp;rabbi, which was hosting Hanukkah celebrations, in&nbsp;<a title="Monsey, New York" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Monsey,_New_York">Monsey, New York</a>. The suspect was later apprehended by the police.</dd>
